# 葛仙翁肘后方备急方

**Ge Xianweng’s *Emergency Remedies at the Elbow***

**Original Title:** *Elbow-Carried Emergency Remedies*
**Former Title:** *Elbow-Carried Remedies for Sudden Ills*
**Abbreviated Title:** *Elbow Remedies*

Compiled by Ge Hong of the Jin dynasty, with supplements by Tao Hongjing of the Liang and later Daoist additions from the Jinchang era. Eight juan in total.

**Source of Base Text:** *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, Zhengyi Section.
**Collated Edition:** Ming Wanli-era edition by Liu Zihua, abbreviated as the *Wanli Edition*.

---

### **Ge Xianweng’s *Emergency Remedies at the Elbow*, Juan 1**

**1. Remedies for Sudden Collapse from Malevolent Qi**

Sudden death may occur after prior illness or while resting in bed, with abrupt cessation of breath—all such cases are termed "death from malevolent qi."

**Remedies:**
**Method 1:** Take the heart of a green onion and insert it into the nostril—left for men, right for women—penetrating seven to eight *cun*. If blood emerges from the eyes, it is auspicious. Bian Que’s method is similar, but later involves blowing into the ears. Ge [Hong] states this refers to blowing into the nose, hence it is listed as a separate method.

**Another Method:** Have two people cover their mouths with cloth and blow into the patient’s ears, alternating when exhausted. Alternatively, use a tube to blow, while lifting the shoulders and leaning the body away—do not hover directly over the deceased.

**Another Method:** Pierce the ears with an onion leaf. If blood emerges from the ears or nose, do not be alarmed; absence of blood makes treatment difficult, while its presence is a favorable sign. At this time, lift the patient’s hands and suddenly release them. After a moment, the deceased will raise their hands to grasp at others, and when they cry out in pain, cease the procedure. For men, pierce the left nostril; for women, the right, inserting seven to eight *cun* or more. Highly effective.

It also treats those who have hanged themselves. This aligns with Bian Que’s methods.

**Another Method:** Soak cotton in fine wine, then place it in the deceased’s nostrils, pressing with the hand to force the wine into the nose. Hold their limbs steady to prevent startling them.

**Another Method:** Examine the upper lip’s inner ridge for white spots the size of millet grains, then pierce and remove them with a needle.

**Another Method:** Pour urine over the face several times, and the person will soon speak. This is from Bian Que’s methods.

**Another Method:** Take soap-bean pods the size of large soybeans and blow them into both nostrils; sneezing will restore the flow of *qi*.

**Another Method:** Moxibust the *Chengjiang* point beneath the lower lip’s depression, applying ten cones—highly effective.

**Another Method:** Slit a rooster’s throat and apply its blood to the face; when dry, reapply. Also, encircle the deceased with ashes.

**Another Method:** Use a tube to blow into the lower orifice, having several people take turns. When *qi* flows, the person revives.

**Another Method:** Split open a white dog and press it against the chest. If no white dog is available, a white parrot will also suffice.

**Another Method:** Hold a drake over the deceased’s mouth, sever its head, and let the hot blood drip into the mouth. Simultaneously, use a bamboo tube to blow into the lower orifice, alternating with others when exhausted. When *qi* flows below, the person revives.

**Another Method:** Extract juice from fresh cow or horse dung and pour it into the mouth, ensuring it reaches the throat. If the mouth is clenched, pry it open; if that fails, tap beneath the teeth. If no fresh dung is available, soak dried dung in urine and extract the juice. This is from Bian Que.

**Another Method:** Measure the deceased’s elbow and wrist with a cord—left for men, right for women—then extend the cord from the back down to the base of the spine. Moxibust at this point, then horizontally at half the cord’s length on either side. Apply three cones at each of the three locations, and the person will rise.

**Another Method:** Pinch the *Renzhong* point between the nose and upper lip to rouse them. If unresponsive, roll up the hand and moxibust the crease at the base of the palm, one cone per year of age.

**Another Method:** Moxibust the *Renzhong* point at the base of the nose, applying three cones.

**Another Method:** Moxibust the hairy depression at the base of the big toe’s nail on both feet, applying seven cones. This is Hua Tuo’s method. Some say twenty-one cones.

**Another Method:** Moxibust the navel, applying one hundred cones. Bian Que’s method also states: sever a weasel’s tail, take its blood to drink, and bind the weasel to use as a pillow—the deceased will revive shortly.

Another version: blow *banxia* powder the size of a soybean into the nostrils.

**Another Method:** Grind *nüqing* into a dose of one *qianbi*, open the mouth, place it in the throat, and administer water or bitter wine—the person will revive immediately.

**Note:** The preceding four methods for reviving sudden death and subsequent *shijue* cases all derive from the transmission of the Wei Minister, as recounted by the Orthodox Unity Perfected One. Bian Que received his methods from Master Changsang; this transmission emerged over twenty years after Ge’s time, so it could not have been known to him. These techniques had long circulated, hence references to the King of Chu or the King of Zhao, with variations in sequence and phrasing.

Zhang Zhongjing’s essential formulas include:
- Pound *xie* (Chinese chive) to extract juice and pour it into the nostrils.
- Sever a red rooster’s comb, take its blood, and blow it into the nostrils through a tube.
- Apply the rooster’s comb and blood to the face, encircling it with ashes—the person will rise immediately.
- Boil pig fat the size of a chicken egg in a liter of bitter wine, then pour it into the throat.
- Mix fourteen large soybeans with egg white and wine, then swallow them all.

For sudden death with high fever: boil half a *jin* of alum in three liters of water, then soak the feet up to the ankles.

For sudden death with closed eyes: straddle a cow facing the deceased, pound *xie* to extract juice and pour it into the ears, and blow soap-bean powder into the nostrils—immediately effective.

For sudden death with eyes and mouth open and tongue protruding: moxibust fourteen cones behind the fingernails and toenails, then administer Five-Poison pastes or powders containing *badou*.

For sudden death with limbs flaccid and involuntary voiding: boil a liter of horse dung in seven liters of water, reduce to four liters, and wash the body. Alternatively, take a liter of cow *dong* (thin dung), warm it with wine, and pour it into the mouth.

Moxibust one hundred cones at each of the following points: one *cun* below the heart, three *cun* above the navel, and four *cun* below the navel—the condition will resolve.

For sudden death in children with vomiting and diarrhea of unknown cause: extract juice from a horse dung pellet and have the child swallow it. If no fresh dung is available, boil dried dung in water to extract the juice.

The *Emergency Three-Substance Pill* and *Pei’s Paste* are listed under the emergency medicine section; they are particularly effective for sudden death and can be prepared on the spot.

All cases of sudden death, *zhong’e* (striking by evil), and *shijue* arise from natural *yin-yang* *qi* in heaven, earth, and the human body suddenly becoming obstructed, disconnected, or imbalanced, leading to blockage between upper and lower, or depletion on one side. Even when death seems imminent, revival is possible if the *qi* has not entirely dissipated. At such times, ghosts and spirits may also be involved, so talismans and protective measures can aid recovery.

**Additional Formulas**
Bian Que states: *Zhong’e* and sudden death from ghostly strikes are similar; for those already deceased, these methods may be used in combination.
- Pound fresh *changpu* (calamus) root to extract juice and pour it in—the person will recover immediately.

For *shijue* (corpse-like syncope), where the person suddenly dies but the pulse still stirs, listen for faint murmurs in the ears and warmth in the thighs—this method also treats it.

Sun Simiao’s formula for sudden death: blow soap-bean powder into the nostrils.

**Second Method for Reviving Sudden Death and *Shijue***
*Shijue* is a condition where the person suddenly dies but the pulse still stirs, and a faint whistling sound can be heard in the ears, with warmth in the thighs. Even if the whistling is present and the pulse stirs, it is still classified as *shijue*.

**Revival Method:**
Use a tube to blow forcefully into the left ear three times, then the right ear three times—the person will revive.

**Additional Methods:**

Another method: Pound dried *u** (calamus) into a piece the size of a jujube pit and place it beneath the tongue.

Another method: Moxa the philtrum (renzhong) with seven cones, and moxa the perineum one *cun* below the scrotum with one hundred cones. For women, moxa the midpoint between the two breasts. It is also said: Press the philtrum with the fingernail for a long while, or needle the philtrum down to the teeth—the person will revive immediately. These are all methods transmitted by Master Wei from Bian Que’s techniques, as in the case of Prince Zhao’s affliction.

Zhang Zhongjing also stated: In *shijue*, the pulse stirs but no breath is present; the qi is obstructed and fails to circulate, hence the person lies still as if dead. Insert powdered *u** (calamus) into both nostrils and blow. Have someone place powdered cinnamon beneath the tongue. It is also said that Bian Que’s method was effective for the King of Chu.

Another method: Shave the hair from the left temple in a two-*cun* square, burn it to ash, and pour wine down the throat—the person will revive immediately.

Another method: Measure the arm and wrist with a string—left for men, right for women—then extend the string from the *dazhui* (GV-14) point down along the spine. Moxa the end of the string with fifty cones—the person will revive. This is Bian Que’s secret technique.

Another method: Apply a hot compress to both flanks. Take soot from the stove the size of a bullet, mix it with fermented water, and administer it. After three or four doses, use a tube to blow into the ears, having three or four people take turns. Alternatively, use a small tube to blow into the nostrils, placing dust from the roof beams the size of a bean inside to ensure it enters.

Another method: Burn fourteen strands of a white horse’s tail and one white horse’s front hoof, then mix the ashes with vinegar into pills the size of small beans. Open the person’s mouth and administer two pills, then one pill after a short while.

Another method: Needle *baihui* (GV-20), located five *cun* within the hairline above the nose, inserting the needle three *fen* and reinforcing. Needle the flesh beside the big toe’s nail, three *fen* from the edge, and needle the top of the middle toe three *fen* each. Needle the inner side of the big toe, one leaf of garlic’s width from the tip. Also needle the tip of the styloid process of the ulna on the hand *shaoyin* meridian, one *fen* each.

Another method: Moxa the *danzhong* (CV-17) point with twenty-eight cones.

**Third Method for Reviving Sudden *Kewu* (Visitation by Malevolent Qi)**
*Kewu* is a type of *zhong’e* (strike by evil), often contracted at gates or doorways, causing twisting pain, distension, and fullness in the heart and abdomen, with qi surging into the chest. If not treated immediately, it can also kill. The revival method:

Moxa the *renzhong* (GV-26) point at the philtrum thirty times, pressing firmly beneath the nasal columella. Soak glutinous rice in water, extract one to two *sheng* of its juice, and administer as a drink. If the mouth is locked shut, force it open with an object.

Another method: Pound ink, mix with water, and administer one *qianbi* of the solution.

Another method: Use a bronze or earthenware vessel to hold hot water, placing the vessel on the abdomen. If it cools, remove clothing and press the vessel directly against the skin. If it grows very cold, replace it with hot water. Cease when recovery is achieved.

Another method: Layer three garments over the abdomen, place a bronze vessel atop the clothing, and gradually burn a small amount of thatch inside the vessel. When the thatch is consumed, add more—do not burn too much at once. Cease when recovery is achieved.

Another method: Measure the patient’s mouth with a string, then use this length to mark four points around the navel, each one string’s distance away. Moxa each point three times, igniting all four fires simultaneously. This brings relief.

Another method: Fold the string used to measure the mouth so that one end reaches the area below the heart. Moxa the lower end five times.

Another method: Mix one *fangcunbi* of cinnabar with three *ge* of honey and administer. If the mouth is locked, force the teeth apart to administer.

Bian Que’s method for treating *kewu* includes emergency talismans and a ritual involving *guan* (ablution) decoctions, but as these are not easily practiced by common people, they are not recorded here. This condition corresponds to what is now called *zhong’e* (strike by evil), and it resembles *sudden death by ghostly assault*. Treatments may draw from all these methods.

For those already dead: Pound fresh *changpu* (calamus) root, extract its juice, and have the patient hold it in the mouth—this brings immediate relief.

For *kewu* with a corpse-like stillness and inability to speak: Burn two *jiegeng* (platycodon) roots, grind them to powder, and administer.

Another method: Grind equal parts *xixin* (asarum) and *gui* (cinnamon) into powder and place it in the mouth.

Another method: Mix rooster’s comb blood with cinnabar, form into pellets the size of small beans, and place three or four into the mouth. This brings relief.

If the mouth is suddenly locked and cannot be opened: Grind raw *fuzi* (aconite) into powder, place it in a tube, and blow it beneath the tongue—this brings immediate relief.

Another method: Mix human blood with cinnabar, form into two pellets the size of *wutong* seeds, force the teeth apart, and place them into the throat to swallow.

Hua Tuo’s method for sudden *zhong’e* with shortness of breath and near-death: Moxa the area behind the toenail on the big toes, where the hairs converge, fourteen times on each foot. This brings immediate relief. If not, moxa fourteen more times. The previous method for reviving sudden death (thirty-seven moxa cones) has already been described.

Another essential formula from Zhang Zhongjing: Four *liang* of *mahuang* (ephedra), seventy *xingren* (apricot kernels), and one *liang* of *gancao* (licorice). Boil in eight *sheng* of water, reduce to three *sheng*, and administer in divided doses to swallow. This universally treats all types of *ganwu* (affliction by noxious qi).

Another method: One handful of *jiugen* (leek roots), twenty *wumei* (mume plums), and half a *jin* of *zhuyu* (evodia). Boil in one *dou* of water, then place the patient’s comb into the decoction and bring to a boil three times. If the comb floats, the patient will live; if it sinks, they will die. Reduce the decoction to three *sheng* and administer as a drink.

Another method: One *liang* of *gui* (cinnamon), three *liang* of *shengjiang* (fresh ginger), fourteen *zhizi* (gardenia), and five *ge* of *chi* (fermented soybeans). Pound the ingredients, mix with three *sheng* of wine, warm slightly, strain, and administer in one dose to bring relief.

*Feishi Zouma Tang* (Flying Corpse Galloping Horse Decoction): Two *badou* (croton seeds) and two *xingren* (apricot kernels). Wrap in silk, crush, and place in two *ge* of hot water. Knead with the fingers to extract the juice, then administer immediately. Drink within the time it takes to cook rice—this brings relief. Adjust the dosage as needed to universally treat all types of *feishi* (flying corpse) and *guiji* (ghostly assault).

Other pills and powders are recorded in the *Emergency Remedies* section.

*Ke* (visitation) refers to an external presence, and *wu* (affliction) means to offend—thus, *kewu* describes an external qi offending a person. This is generally a malign qi. Though many recover with treatment, it is a qi borne of ghostly or toxic influences. When encountered suddenly, its power wanes, so it cannot be treated like natural malign qi. Once it enters the body and invades the organs, channels, and collaterals, even after recovery, further treatment is advisable to dispel its lingering influence. Otherwise, it may recur and eventually cause harm, leading to periodic outbreaks.

**Additional Formulas**

From the *Wai Tai Mi Yao*:
For sudden *kewu* (visitation affliction) with suspended corpse syndrome and inability to speak, use equal parts *xixin* (asarum) and *guixin* (cassia heart), placing them in the mouth.

Another formula: Burn two *liang* of *jiegeng* (platycodon), grind to powder, and take with rice water. Also swallow musk the size of a soybean—excellent.

From the *Guang Li Fang*:
For sudden *kewu* near death, finely grind one *qian* of musk, mix with two *ge* of vinegar, and administer—immediate recovery.

**Fourth: Formulas for Sudden Ghostly Assault**
Ghostly assault strikes without warning, as if pierced by human force. The chest, flanks, and abdomen twist with sharp, unbearable pain, unrelieved by pressure. Some immediately vomit blood, or bleed from the nose, or pass blood.

Also called *guipai* (ghostly thrust).

**Formulas for Treatment:**
Moxa one *zhuang* at *renzong* (the philtrum below the nose)—instant cure. If unresolved, add several more *zhuang*.

Another formula: Grind equal parts *shengma* (cimicifuga), *duhuo* (angelica), and *mugui* (cassia bark) into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* with wine—immediate cure.

Another formula: Moxa two *zhuang* one *cun* below the navel.

Another formula: Moxa seven *zhuang* one *cun* above the navel, and at the white flesh of both heels—recovery follows.

Another formula: Steep three pieces of processed mugwort the size of a duck’s egg in five *sheng* of water, boil down to two *sheng*, and consume in one dose.

Another formula: Stir one *sheng* of salt into two *sheng* of water and drink. Also spray cold water on the face, but do not induce vomiting immediately—wait until vomiting occurs, then recovery follows.

Another formula: Stir a pinch of powder into water and drink.

Another formula: Blow pure wine into both nostrils.

Another formula: Sever the head of a white dog, take one *sheng* of its hot blood, and drink.

Another formula: Drip chicken crown blood into the mouth, allowing one swallow. Then split the chicken and press it against the chest until cold, discarding it by the roadside. A black hen is even more effective.

Another formula: Boil one *sheng* of calf dung in three *sheng* of wine and consume. An adult ox may also be used.

Another formula: Burn three *cun* of a scabbard, grind to powder, and drink with water.

Another formula: Burn rat droppings, grind to powder the size of millet grains, and take with a little water if unable to drink, placing it in the mouth.

Other pills and powders are recorded in the *Emergency Remedies* section.

Now, shamans have truly witnessed people suddenly seized by ghosts or spirits—whether disrupting their ranks, colliding with them, or when their spirit is scattered and weak, or burdened by past transgressions. The mild escape, but the severe often die, much like the tales of Yan Jian—this is no fiction. Even if death is fated, one cannot but attempt rescue.

**Additional Formulas**
From the *Gu Jin Lu Yan*:
For demonic possession or *maogui* (cat ghost) illness where the person refuses to name the ghost, pound deer antler shavings into powder, take one *fangcunbi* with water—they will then speak the truth.

**Fifth: Formulas for Sudden Nightmare Unawareness**
If one suddenly falls into a stupor while lying down, do not shine fire upon them—fire will kill them. Instead, bite their heel or the side of the big toe’s nail, and repeatedly spit on their face to revive them.

**Other Formulas for Treatment:**
Grind *zaojiao* (Chinese honey locust) into powder and blow into both nostrils with a tube—they will awaken. This may still work after three or four days.

Another formula: Insert a hair into the nostril—left for men, right for women—twisting it inward.

Another formula: Blow into both ears with a reed tube. Also take fourteen strands of the patient’s hair, twist into a cord, and insert into the nostrils. Cut a rooster’s crown for blood, and blow it into the throat with the tube—highly effective.

Another formula: Grind yellow earth from beneath the stove into powder and blow into the nostrils with a tube.

Grind *xionghuang* (realgar) and *gui* (cassia) into powder and blow into the nostrils—also excellent.

Another formula: Apply well-bottom mud to the eyes, then have the person hang their head over the well. Call their name, and they will awaken.

Another formula: Pound *jiu* (leek) for juice and blow into the nostrils. In winter, dig up the roots, extract juice, and pour into the mouth.

Another formula: Drink salt water, adjusting the amount as needed.

Another formula: Place the person on the ground, draw a line on the earth with a sharp knife from the shoulder—left for men, right for women—encircling the face. Press the knife’s tip into the patient’s nose, entering one *fen*, and hold firmly without moving. The person will speak as if possessed by ghosts or spirits, begging for mercy. Ask: “Who are you? Why have you come?” They will plead to leave. Then erase the drawn line with your finger a few *cun* from the shoulder, allowing them to depart. Do not omit these questions.

Another formula: Cover the patient’s face with an earthen steamer, then have someone swiftly smash it—they will awaken.

Another formula: Hold an ox or horse hoof over the person in a stupor—also effective for sudden death. A black ox is especially good.

Another formula: Grind *xionghuang* (realgar) finely, sift, and blow into both nostrils with a tube. *Gui* (cassia) is also excellent.

Another formula: Grind *wanpu* (calamus) into powder, blow into both nostrils, and place some beneath the tongue.

Another formula: Bind the patient’s elbow with the left cord of a steamer, left for men and right for women. Tightly twist the remaining length, and also bind the feet with hemp. Then inquire about the cause, and loosen the bindings as instructed. Have one person sit at the head to guard, while another calls the patient’s name from inside the door. The seated person responds: “Yes, they are here.” The patient will then revive.

For sudden stupor without awareness, moxa twenty-one *zhuang* at the *jumao* (hairy spot) beneath the big toe.

For those prone to nightmares and evil dreams: Place ash from extinguished fire in the shoes and under the pillow.

Another formula: Wear *xionghuang* (realgar)—left for men, right for women.

Another formula: Moxa twenty *zhuang* at the *jumao* (hairy spot) above both big toes.

Another formula: Place a piece of genuine musk by the head.

Another formula: A tiger-head pillow is especially good.

**Formulas to Ward Off Nightmares:**
Carry *xionghuang* (realgar) the size of a jujube pit under the left armpit—this ensures lifelong freedom from nightmares.

Another formula: Place a square of genuine red felt beneath the pillow.

Another formula: A rhinoceros-horn pillow is excellent; place *qingmuxiang* (costus root) inside the pillow and also wear it on the body.

Another formula: (For) treating prolonged sudden nightmares, write this talisman on paper, burn it until it turns black, mix with a little water, and place it in the mouth of the deceased. Hang a mirror before the deceased’s ear and strike it, calling the deceased’s name—revival will occur within half a day.

For those who lie in nightmare-induced stupor without waking, the hun and po souls wander outside, seized by evil. Though they wish to return, they cannot find their way. Firelight must be avoided, for if illuminated, they will never re-enter. However, those who experience nightmares in lamplight do so because their souls originally departed from brightness but failed to return to the body.

**Additional Formulas**
From the *Qianjin Fang*: To treat ghost-induced stupor, use *zaojia* (Chinese honey locust) powder the size of a *daogui* (a small measure) to revive the dead.

**Formulas for Sudden Affliction by the Five Corpses (Chapter Six)**
The Five Corpses are: *feishi* (flying corpse), *dunshi* (retreating corpse), *fengshi* (wind corpse), *chenshi* (sinking corpse), and *shizhu* (corpse attachment). The formulas recorded here treat all of them. Their symptoms include abdominal pain and distension, breathlessness, upward surging into the heart and chest, lateral attacks on the flanks, or the emergence of lumps, or spasms radiating to the lower back and spine.

A formula to treat them: Moxa three *cun* behind the nipple, fourteen *zhuang*—left for men, right for women. If unresolved, increase the number of *zhuang*. Recovery will follow.

Another formula: Moxa three *cun* below the heart, sixty *zhuang*.

Another formula: Moxa one *cun* below the nipple, on the left or right according to the location of the affliction, increasing the number of *zhuang* until recovery is achieved.

Another formula: With four fingers, press upon the painful area, then moxa the lower edge of the fingers for several *zhuang* until the patient feels pain. Next, pinch the philtrum above the upper lip, then pinch one *cun* below the heart, increasing the number of *zhuang* until recovery is achieved.

Another formula: Crack open a chicken egg, and swallow the white at once. If the mouth is closed, insert it into the throat and shake until it is swallowed—recovery will be immediate.

Another formula: Crack open seven pigeon eggs and swallow the whites at once; do not take a second dose.

Another formula: Roast the root of *li danglu* (Phytolacca acinosa), place it in a pouch, and apply it alternately as a hot compress, replacing it when it cools.

Though the Five Corpses bear distinct names, their patterns are largely similar, with only minor differences. The *feishi* (flying corpse) roams beneath the skin, piercing through the organs and bowels, causing stabbing pain with each onset, its manifestations ever-changing. The *dunshi* (retreating corpse) lodges in the bones and flesh, boring through the blood vessels; each attack renders the patient untouchable, triggered by the sight of a corpse or the sound of mourning. The *fengshi* (wind corpse) courses through the four limbs, with pain shifting unpredictably; each onset brings confusion, provoked by wind or snow. The *chenshi* (sinking corpse) binds the organs and bowels, surging into the heart and flanks; each attack brings excruciating pain, triggered by cold. The *shizhu* (corpse attachment) weighs down the entire body, disturbing the spirit, causing constant disorientation; it worsens with the changing of the seasons, often leading to grave consequences. This last condition has its own treatment, described later as a compress.

All Five Corpses arise from corpse-demons within the body that draw in harm; though the classical arts contain methods to dispel them, these are rarely practiced in the world today. Here, I have compiled the essential techniques from the classics to remedy this neglect.

**Formula:**

Take one *liang* of realgar and one *liang* of garlic, pound them together to form a ball roughly the size of a pellet, then steep it in two *ge* of warmed wine and consume. The condition will resolve in a short while. If it does not, repeat the process. Those already afflicted should keep this remedy on hand.

**Another formula:**
Grind equal parts dried ginger and cinnamon into powder, take a pinch the size of a fingertip, stir-fry until it turns green, then grind again. Mix with water and consume; the condition will resolve.

**Another formula:**
Pound tribulus seeds and form into honey pills. Take two pills the size of a soybean, three times daily.

**Another formula:**
Boil two *sheng* of polished rice in six *sheng* of water until it reaches a single boil, then consume.

**Another formula:**
Simmer eight *ge* of lard in a bronze vessel until slightly bubbling, then add eight *ge* of bitter wine, mix well, and consume in one draught; the condition will resolve.

**Another formula:**
Dig a small pit in the ground, fill it with water, stir thoroughly, then strain and drink the liquid.

**Another formula:**
Take thatch from the four corners of a roof, place it in a bronze vessel, cover the abdomen with three layers of red cloth, set the vessel on the cloth, and burn the thatch until hot. Move the vessel to follow the pain; when the area beneath the donkey itches, the condition will resolve. If the dwelling has a tiled roof, shave wood from the four corner pillars and burn it instead. This method is exceedingly potent and efficacious.

**Another formula:**
Grind together one *chi* of cinnamon, one *liang* of ginger, and three croton seeds into powder, mix with bitter wine to form a paste, and apply to the site of the corpse affliction. The condition will resolve once the paste dries.

**Another formula:**
Chop two *sheng* of *Sapium sebiferum* root, boil to produce a thick decoction, strain, and reduce the liquid to five *sheng*. Add one to two *liang* of water, then consume in doses of five *ge* to one *sheng*. Highly effective.

**Another formula:**
Chop several *hu* of honeysuckle stems and leaves, boil to produce a thick decoction, strain, and reduce the liquid. Consume an amount the size of a chicken egg, two to three times daily. Excellent results.

**Another formula:**
Burn disheveled hair and stir-fry apricot kernels in equal parts, pound into a paste, form into pills, and consume three pills the size of *tong* seeds with wine, five to six times daily.

**Another formula:**
Grind together three parts dragon bone, two parts false hellebore, and one part croton seeds, then mix with well-ripple water to form pills the size of sesame seeds. Consume according to the prescribed method.

**Another formula:**
Dry lacquer tree leaves in the sun, pound into powder, and consume with wine.

**Another formula:**
Thoroughly cook one stove liver, slice, and consume entirely. Garlic paste may also be used.

**Another formula:**
Sever a turtle’s head, burn it to ash, and consume the powder with water in three divided doses. If the flesh-like substance is not fully expelled, the condition may recur.

**Another formula:**
Boil one *fen* of realgar, fifteen gardenia fruits, and one *liang* of peony root in three *sheng* of water until reduced to one and a half *sheng*. Divide and consume in two doses.

**Another formula:**
Burn fourteen gardenia fruits to ash and consume.

**Another formula:**
Grind together one *liang* each of dried ginger and aconite, two *fen* of cinnamon, and thirty croton seeds (with hearts removed, all used raw), sift, mix with honey, and pound ten thousand times. Consume two pills the size of small beans. This remedy treats all conditions without exception.

**For flying corpse entering the abdomen causing piercing pain and death:**
Rhinoceros horn, *shewang*, and the Five Infusion Pills are all excellent remedies, detailed in the major formulas.

**For sudden presence of an object beneath the skin resembling a toad, which later descends into the abdomen like an immobile cup, causing unbearable dragging pain and killing the person within days:**
**Formula:**
Pound together fourteen croton seeds, one *liang* of gentian, one *liang* each of pinellia and *Trichosanthes kirilowii* seeds, and one and a half *jin* of cinnamon. Divide into two cloth pouches, steam until hot, and alternate applying as a compress. The decoction may also be consumed in small amounts. This originally appears in the miscellaneous treatments under the name "yin corpse," and those afflicted often die.

---

**Section Seven: Formulas for Corpse Infusion and Ghost Infusion**

Corpse infusion and ghost infusion, as Ge states, are the "corpse infusion" among the Five Corpses, further compounded by various ghostly harms. The disease manifests in thirty-six to ninety-nine variations, generally causing alternating chills and fever, dribbling discomfort, mental confusion, and indistinct suffering that pervades the entire body. Over months and years, it gradually weakens the patient, leading to death, and after death, it spreads to others, even to the point of annihilating entire households. Upon recognizing these symptoms, one should treat it urgently.

**Formula:**
Take white mulberry bark, dry in the sun, and burn to ash, yielding about two *dou*. Place in a steamer, steam until the vapor permeates, then remove. Pour three to four *dou* of boiling water from a cauldron over the ash, strain, and repeat three times until the liquid is extremely concentrated. Allow to settle, then take two *dou* of the clear liquid to soak two *dou* of red adzuki beans overnight. Dry in the sun, then soak again in the ash liquid until exhausted. Steam the beans until fully cooked, then prepare a broth with mutton or venison and serve with the beans. Begin by consuming one to two *sheng* until satiated. Mild cases resolve with three to four *dou*; severe cases require seven to eight *dou*. As the disease departs, the body will feel a creeping itch. If the root is not fully eradicated, repeat the treatment. Divinely efficacious.

**Another formula:**
Crush fifty peach kernels, boil in water to produce four *sheng* of liquid, and consume in one draught to induce vomiting. If the disease is not fully expelled, repeat after two or three days. If no vomiting occurs, it is not an infusion.

**Another formula:**
Grind together one *liang* of *Asarum forbesii*, one *liang* of stem, half a *liang* of ginseng, fourteen *Trichosanthes kirilowii* seeds, six *zhu* of *Usnea*, and fourteen red adzuki beans into powder. Consume one square *cun* spoonful with warm water at dawn; by evening, one will vomit a hundred kinds of substances. If not fully expelled, consume again later.

**Another formula:**
Dry one otter liver in the shade, pound into powder, and consume one square *cun* spoonful with water, three times daily. If the condition does not resolve, repeat with another liver. Yao states it is divinely efficacious.

**Another formula:**
Grind together one *liang* each of cinnabar and realgar, half a *liang* each of *Podophyllum* and *Aconitum* (or *Stellera*), forty croton seeds (with hearts and skins removed), and two centipedes. Mix with honey to form pills the size of small beans. If the condition does not resolve, consume two pills. This remedy may also be carried for long-term use.

**Master Yao’s Formula:**
Burn human hair to ash, roast apricot kernels until purple, and grind them into a paste. Mix with lard and consume pills the size of *wutong* seeds with wine, three times daily, until resolved.

**Other Major Remedies:**
Hua Tuo’s *Fox-Bone Powder*, *Dragon’s Tooth Powder*, and *Sheep-Fat Pills* are recorded in the comprehensive formulas. Also, the *Huainan Pills* bestowed upon Emperor Cheng are effective against *zhuyi* (possession sickness) that extinguishes households. Women and children are often afflicted by *zhuche* (cart possession) or *zhuchuan* (boat possession), causing heart vexation, confusion, headache, and vomiting. Those with such symptoms should employ the following apotropaic formula:

**Apotropaic Formula:**
Take equal parts of *cheqian* seeds, root bark of *chexia* plum, *shichangsheng*, and *xuchangqing*. Coarsely grind, place half a *ge* in a pouch, and tie it to one’s clothing or head. For *zhuchuan*, if sudden distress arises while boarding, carry this pouch. Alternatively, before entering the boat, carve a piece from the vessel, burn it to ashes, and consume with water.

**Additional Formulas:**

**From *Zimu Milu*:**
To treat *shizhu* (corpse possession), burn tangled hair the size of a chicken egg to ash and consume with water until resolved.

**From *Shiyi Xinjing*:**
For *chuanshi* (consumptive possession), ghostly qi, cough, *xuanpi* (abdominal masses), *zhuqi* (possession qi), or blood and qi blockage leading to gradual emaciation: Take one *liang* of peach kernels, remove skins and tips, crush, and boil in one and a half *sheng* of water. Use the decoction to cook rice porridge and consume on an empty stomach.

---

**Section Eight: Remedies for Sudden Heart Pain**

For sudden heart pain, boil white peach bark and consume the decoction on an empty stomach.

**Another formula:**
Take either cassia powder or dried ginger powder—either may be used alone. Consume one square *cun* spoonful with warm wine, repeating six or seven times in quick succession until resolved.

**Another formula:**
Squeeze five to six *ge* of fresh donkey dung to extract the juice and consume while hot for immediate relief.

**Another formula:**
Take a handful of eastward-growing peach twigs, cut into pieces, and decoct in one *sheng* of wine until reduced to half a *sheng*. Consume in one dose for great efficacy.

**Another formula:**
Consume half a *ge* of raw sesame oil warm for relief.

**Another formula:**
Boil eight *liang* of *huanglian* in seven *sheng* of water until reduced to one and a half *sheng*. Strain and consume five *ge* warm, three times daily.

**Another formula:**
Have the patient sit facing the door. If the patient is male, have a woman offer him a cup of water to drink; if female, have a man offer her a cup. Freshly drawn water is especially effective.

**Another formula:**
Mix one part honey with two parts water and consume for greater benefit.

**Another formula:**
Wrap a piece of worn cloth around a handful of *guan* (washing water residue) the size of a pellet, burn until red-hot, grind to powder, and consume with one cup of wine.

**Another formula:**
Boil one *sheng* of water three times, stir in one *ge* of salt, and drink. If no fire is available, plain water may be used.

**Another formula:**
Hold the breath and endure for several tens of repetitions while pressing the hollow beneath the heart with the thumb to cure.

**Another formula:**
Boil three *sheng* of mature white mugwort in three *sheng* of water until reduced to one *sheng*. Strain and consume in one dose. If afflicted by invading qi, the patient will vomit worm-like substances.

**Another formula:**
Mix one cup of vinegar with one egg, stir well, and consume. Good wine may also be used.

**Another formula:**
Sift hot ashes from beneath the stove to remove charcoal, place in a cloth pouch, and apply to the painful area while still scorching hot. Reheat when cool.

**Another formula:**
Steam or boil soybeans, place in a pouch, and apply alternately to the painful area, replacing when cool.

**Another formula:**
Slice half a *sheng* of fresh or dried ginger, boil in two *sheng* of water until reduced to one *sheng*, strain, and consume in one dose.

**Another formula:**
Moxibust three cones at the tip of the middle finger of the hand.

**Another formula:**
Peel and grind fine high-quality cassia, and consume three square *cun* spoonfuls with warm wine. If unresolved, repeat six or seven times in quick succession. In the absence of cassia, dried ginger powder may be used.

**Another formula:**
Measure the patient’s mouth width, fold the measurement, and apply it below the heart’s depression. Moxibust three cones at the folded end.

**Another formula:**
Draw the Five Phases characters on the ground, gather soil from the center, stir into one *sheng* of water, and consume.

**Another formula:**
Boil two *sheng* of *wuzhuyu*, four *liang* of fresh ginger, one *sheng* of fermented soybeans, and six *sheng* of wine until reduced to three and a half *sheng*. Divide into three doses.

**Another formula:**
Boil one *liang* each of *renshen*, cassia heart, split *zhizi*, roasted *gancao*, and *huangqin* in six *sheng* of water until reduced to two *sheng*. Divide into three doses for remarkable efficacy.

**Another formula:**
Remove skins and tips from seven peach kernels, grind thoroughly when ripe, and consume with water in one dose. Also effective for thirty-year afflictions.

**Another formula:**
Roast two *liang* of *fuzi* and one *liang* of dried ginger, grind, and form honey pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Consume four pills, three times daily.

**Another formula:**
Grind and sift one and a half *liang* of *wuzhuyu*, one *liang* each of dried ginger and cassia heart, two *liang* of *baizhu*, one *liang* each of *renshen*, tangerine peel, *jiao* (with closed mouths and seeds removed, sweated), roasted *gancao*, *huangqin*, *danggui*, and *jiegeng*, and one and a half *liang* of roasted *fuzi*. Mix with honey to form pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Consume three pills daily, gradually increasing to ten or fifteen pills per dose. Take with wine or water, before or after meals as desired. Highly effective.

**Another formula:**
Boil eight *liang* of cassia heart in four *sheng* of water until reduced to one *sheng*. Divide into three doses.

**Another formula:**
Boil three *liang* of *kushen* in one and a half *sheng* of vinegar until reduced to eight *ge*. Divide into two doses. Water may also be used. If boiling is not possible, raw *kushen* may be used.

**Another formula:**
Boil four *liang* of *longdan* in three *sheng* of wine until reduced to one and a half *sheng*. Consume in one dose.

**Another formula:**
Boil five *ge* of *wuzhuyu* and one *liang* of cassia in two and a half *sheng* of wine until reduced to one *sheng*. Divide into two doses for efficacy.

**Another formula:**
Boil two *sheng* of *wuzhuyu*, four *liang* of fresh ginger, one *sheng* of fermented soybeans, and six *sheng* of wine until reduced to two and a half *sheng*. Divide into three doses.

**Another formula:**
Prepare one white chicken as in #14’s culinary method. Boil in three *sheng* of water until reduced to two *sheng*. Discard the chicken and decoct the broth to six *ge*. Add six *ge* of bitter wine and one *qian* of genuine pearl, then decoct again to six *ge*. Add musk powder the size of two soybeans and consume in one dose.

**Another formula:**
Grind one *liang* each of *guixin* and *danggui*, along with fourteen *zhizi*, into powder. Take one *fangcunbi* with wine, three to five times daily. Also treats chronic heart ailments with periodic attacks.

**Another formula:**
Grind two *liang* of *guixin* and one *liang* of *wutou* into powder, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *wuzi* seeds. Take three pills initially, gradually increasing the dose.

**For sudden stabbing heart and abdominal pain:**
Boil two *liang* each of *kushen* and *longdan*, three *liang* each of *shengma* and *zhizi*, in five *sheng* of bitter wine until reduced to two *sheng*. Divide into two doses; induce vomiting for relief.

**For heart *shan* with periodic excruciating pain:**
Grind equal parts of *zhenshewang* and *wuzhuyu* into powder, mix with honey, and form into sesame-sized pills. Take two pills three times daily; avoid hot foods.

**Another formula:**
Moxibustion: apply one hundred cones at *juque* (one *cun* below the *xiphoid process*), and one *cun* to the left and right. Measure the patient’s neck and spine to align the points symmetrically, for a total of six moxa sites.

**For chronic persistent pain with inability to eat or drink, and heaviness in the head:**
Grind six *fen* each of *wutou* and *jiao*, four *fen* of *ganjiang* into powder, mix with honey, and form into pills. Take four soybean-sized pills with wine, gradually increasing the dose.

**Another formula:**
Grind five *fen* of *banxia*, five *fen* of *xixin*, two *fen* of *ganjiang*, three *fen* of *renshen*, and one *fen* of *fuzi* into powder. Mix with bitter wine and form into *wuzida*-sized pills. Take five pills with wine, three times daily.

**For pulling tightness and burning pain below the heart:**
Boil three *liang* each of *guixin* and fresh ginger, along with five *zhishi*, in five *sheng* of water until reduced to three *sheng*. Divide into three doses. May also add two *liang* of *zhu* and half a *jin* of malt sugar.

**For cold-induced pain from heart-lung injury:**
Boil two *liang* of *guixin* and two pig kidneys in eight *sheng* of water until reduced to two *sheng*. Divide into three doses.

**Another formula:**
Form two *liang* of *fuzi* and one *liang* of *ganjiang* into honey pills. Take four *wuzida*-sized pills three times daily.

**For heart impediment and heart pain:**
Stir-fry one *liang* of *shujiao* until yellow, grind into powder, and mix with dog heart blood to form *wuzida*-sized pills. Take five pills five times daily.

**For firm pain below the heart, as large as a bowl with edges like a spinning plate (termed *qi* distention from water retention):**
Roast seven *zhishi*, boil with three *liang* of *zhu* in one *dou* of water until reduced to three *sheng*. Divide into three doses; the mass should gradually soften.

**For shifting accumulations causing intermittent pain below the heart:**
Grind one *sheng* of *wuzhuyu* powder with one pellet of *zhenshewang* the size of a bullet. Mix with egg white to form small pea-sized pills. Take two pills for relief.

**For heart pain with excessive salivation, as if caused by worms:**
Take the heart of any livestock, slice into fourteen pieces, and make crisscross cuts. Dust with one *liang* of *zhendan*, and swallow all at dawn. Adding *xionghuang* and musk enhances efficacy.

**For hunger-induced heart pain (termed *hunger shan*):**
Grind equal parts of *longdan*, *fuzi*, and *huanglian* into powder. Take one *qianbi* three times daily.

**Additional Formulas:**

From *Yaoxing Lun*: For heart pain, *zhong’e* (sudden evil), or pain radiating to the waist and navel. Wrap salt the size of a chicken egg in blue cloth, burn until red-hot, and steep in wine. Consume in one dose to induce vomiting of malign substances.

From *Shiyi Xu*: *Yanhusuo* relieves heart pain; grind into powder and take with wine.

From *Shenghui Fang*: For chronic heart pain with unpredictable attacks, frequent clear-water vomiting, and loss of appetite, decoct two *liang* of *xionghuang* in two *sheng* of good vinegar over low heat until thick. Mix with steamed cake crumbs to form *wutongzi*-sized pills. Take seven pills with ginger decoction.

Another formula: For nine types of heart pain with obstruction, grind one *fen* of *guixin* into powder, decoct in one large cup of wine until reduced to half a cup. Strain and consume warm for immediate effect.

Another formula: For cold *shan* heart pain with reversed cold limbs and inability to eat, grind two *liang* of *guixin* into powder. Take one *qianbi* with hot wine at any time.

From *Waitai Miyao*: For sudden heart pain, grind *ganjiang* into powder and take one *qian* with water.

Another formula: For heart pain, grind *danggui* into powder and take one *fangcunbi* with wine.

From *Bixiao*: For *hui* (roundworm) heart pain, take bear bile the size of a soybean with water for great efficacy.

Another formula: Lightly grill *manli* fish until cooked and feed one or two to the patient; a full meal is even better for permanent relief.

From *Jingyan Fang*: For forty years of unrelieved heart pain, rinse *shumi* and consume the warm liquid as needed.

From *Jingyan Houfang*: For heart pain, grind one *liang* of *jianghuang* and three *liang* of *guirang* into powder. Take one *qianbi* with vinegar decoction.

From *Jianyao Jizhong*: For nine types of heart pain and abdominal or rib-side accumulations with stagnant *qi*, grind two *liang* of *tongzi ganqi* into powder, stir-fry until smoke appears, and grind finely. Mix with vinegar-cooked flour paste to form *wutongzi*-sized pills. Take five to seven pills with hot wine or vinegar decoction at any time.

From *Yao Hezhong*: For sudden heart pain, chew thirty-seven *yuliren* thoroughly and swallow with freshly drawn water. Warm water is even better; pain ceases shortly. Then sip hot saltwater.

From *Bingbu Shouji*: For unbearable heart pain lasting ten or five years, effective immediately. Boil small garlic in strong vinegar and consume until full; do not add salt.

**Ninth Remedy for Sudden Abdominal Pain**
For sudden abdominal pain, write the character for "wind" on the tongue, then draw two intersecting centipedes on paper and swallow it. Another remedy: grind cinnamon into powder and take a three-*cunbi* dose. Vinegar, ginseng, and high-quality dried ginger are also effective. Another remedy: boil two *sheng* of non-glutinous rice in six *sheng* of water for fourteen boilings, then drink. Another remedy: take a large handful of salt, swallow with plenty of water, and induce vomiting to cure. Another remedy: dig a small pit in the ground, fill it with water, stir thoroughly, and drink the liquid. Another remedy: have someone straddle the patient’s abdomen and urinate into their navel. Another remedy: mix one *sheng* of rice flour with two *sheng* of water and drink. Another remedy: have the patient lie prone while someone straddles them, lifting their abdomen with both hands. The patient should relax and allow the helper to raise and lower them about three *chi* from the bed, repeating fourteen times. Then grasp the spine, pressing deeply to draw out the pain from the coccyx to the crown; if not cured, repeat. Another remedy: have the patient rest their head on a one-*chi*-high pillow, tucking their knees to force abdominal *qi* into the chest. Another person should grasp three *cun* above the navel to cure; swallowing *qi* dozens of times is even better. This remedy also treats heart pain, which is latent *qi*.

For sudden onset of various hernias with pulling pain in the lower abdomen and genitals, cold sweats, and near-death agony: grind *shashen* into powder, sift, and take a one-*fangcunbi* dose for immediate relief. Originally listed under miscellaneous treatments as "cold hernia" or "yin hernia," if this fails, take purgative pills or use *Zouma Tang* for relief.

For cold hernia with abdominal pain where food and drink seem to pass unnoticed: boil two *ge* of Sichuan pepper and four *liang* of dried ginger in four *sheng* of water, reduce to two *sheng*, strain, add one *jin* of malt sugar, and simmer to half. Take repeatedly. Another remedy: boil one *sheng* of *banxia*, eight *liang* of cinnamon, and one *sheng* of fresh ginger in six *sheng* of water, reduce to two *sheng*, and divide into two doses.

For intermittent cold hernia with colicky pain: boil three *liang* of *wuzhuyu*, four *liang* of fresh ginger, and two *ge* of fermented soybeans in four *sheng* of wine, reduce to two *sheng*, and divide into two doses. Another remedy: boil one *fuzi* tuber, two hundred Sichuan peppercorns, half a *liang* of dried ginger, ten *banxia* tubers, thirty *dazao* dates, and one *sheng* of non-glutinous rice in seven *sheng* of water until the rice is cooked, strain, and consume one *sheng* per dose until finished. Another remedy: boil one *jin* of *rougui* and half a *sheng* of *wuzhuyu* in five *sheng* of water, reduce to one and a half *sheng*, and divide into two doses. Another remedy: boil two *liang* each of *muli*, licorice, and cinnamon in five *sheng* of water, reduce to one and a half *sheng*, and take in two doses. Another remedy: prepare a black hen as for eating, finely chop seven *jin* of fresh *dihuang*, steam together in a steamer with a copper vessel to collect the juice, and drink from dawn to dusk. This will expel all cold accumulations; then gradually consume white congee. For chronic hernia, take three doses.

**Additional Remedies**
From *Boji Fang*: For disharmony of cold and heat *qi* with loss of appetite or stabbing abdominal pain, grind equal parts *shanzhizi* and *chuanwutou* into powder, form into *wutongzi*-sized pills with wine paste, and take fifteen pills with stir-fried ginger decoction. For small intestinal *qi* pain, take twenty pills with stir-fried *huixiang*, scallions, or wine.

From *Jingyan Fang*: For chronic cold in the original viscera with abdominal pain and deficiency diarrhea, the highly effective *Yufen Dan*: grind five *liang* of raw sulfur and one *liang* of *qingfan* finely, form into mung bean-sized pills with steamed cake, and take five pills on an empty stomach with warm wine, followed by food.

From *Zimu Milu*: For lower abdominal pain with cyanosis or inability to breathe, simmer one *liang* of *kushen* in one and a half *sheng* of vinegar to eight *ge*, and divide into two doses.

From *Shenghui Fang*: For cold hernia with pulling pain in the lower abdomen and genitals and cold sweats, pound one *liang* of *danshen* into powder and take two *qianbi* doses with warm wine.

**Tenth Remedy for Simultaneous Heart and Abdominal Pain**
For distending pain in the heart and abdomen with shortness of breath and near-death or apparent cessation of breath: boil fourteen *zhizi* fruits and seven *ge* of fermented soybeans in two *sheng* of water, first simmering the soybeans to one *sheng* and two *ge*, strain, add *zhizi*, simmer to eight *ge*, strain again, and take half a *sheng*. If not cured, consume the remainder. Another remedy: wash a small garment and drink one to two *sheng* of the water. Another remedy: boil two *liang* of cinnamon in one *sheng* and two *ge* of water, reduce to eight *ge*, strain, and consume at once. If cinnamon is unavailable, dried ginger is also effective. Another remedy: boil twenty-seven *wumei* fruits in five *sheng* of water once, add twenty-seven large coins, simmer to two and a half *sheng*, and consume at once for robust individuals or in two doses for the weak; relief follows immediately. Another remedy: boil two *liang* of *zhuyu*, four *liang* of fresh ginger, and three *ge* of fermented soybeans in four *sheng* of wine, reduce to two *sheng*, and divide into three doses for immediate relief. Another remedy: grind one *liang* of dried ginger and two *liang* of *badou*, form into pills with honey, and take two *xiaodou*-sized pills to induce vomiting or purging for relief.

For treating persistent distending pain in the heart and abdomen:

**Remedy 1:**
Grind two *liang* of *langdu* and half a *liang* of *fuzi* into powder, form into honey pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take one pill on the first day, two on the second, three on the third, then reduce to one pill on the fourth day, and three pills on the sixth day. Maintain a regular dosage of one to three pills thereafter until recovery.

**Remedy 2:**
Grind one *ge* of *wuzhuyu*, four *fen* of dried ginger, and two *fen* each of *fuzi*, *xixin*, and *renshen* into powder, form into honey pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take five pills, three times daily.

Generally, pain in the heart and abdomen—unless caused by *zhong’e* (sudden affliction) or *huoluan* (cholera-like illness)—stems from long-standing accumulations of cold and heat. These remedies may be used for emergency relief, but after recovery, comprehensive treatment should be applied to eliminate the root cause.

**Additional Remedies:**

From *Master Mei’s Prescriptions*:
For firm distension and pain in the heart and abdomen with unbearable distress, even if vomiting and purging have not occurred, boil five *ge* of *guan* in one *sheng* of water until dissolved, consume at once to induce vomiting and expel food; if no vomiting occurs, take again.

From *Sun Zhenren’s Prescriptions*:
For pain in both the heart and abdomen, wrap *jiao* in cloth, apply to the affected area, and heat with fire until the *jiao* sweats; highly effective.

From *Ten Complete Prescriptions*:
For heart and spleen pain, finely chop *gaoliangjiang*, stir-fry, and grind into powder. Take one *qianbi* with rice water for immediate relief.

**Section Ten: Treating Sudden Heart and Abdominal Distress with Fullness**

For sudden heart and abdominal fullness with chest and rib pain so severe it feels fatal:
Immerse hands and feet in scalding hot water, replacing it as it cools.

**Secret Remedy:**
Boil a square inch of green cloth, three *fen* of deer antler, and two *qianbi* of human hair ash in two *sheng* of water until reduced to one and a half *sheng*. Strain and consume entirely.

**Additional Remedies:**
Boil *yiyiren* root thoroughly and take three *sheng* of the decoction.
Boil twenty *bilun* coins in five *sheng* of water for three boils; take three times daily.
Pound *xiangcai* to extract juice and consume one to two *sheng*.
Boiling dried ginger in water is also effective.
Alternatively, use the previous method for heart pain with *zhizi* and *chi* decoction.
Boil one *liang* of *huangqin*, twenty apricot kernels, and one *liang* of *muli* in three *sheng* of water until reduced to one *sheng*; consume at once.

For reversal cold with fullness and constant retching:
Grind two *liang* each of *xiaocao*, cinnamon, *xixin*, dried ginger, and *jiao*, along with two *liang* of blast-fried *fuzi*, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *tong* seeds. Take four pills.

For sudden vomiting and retching:
Moxibustion at one *cun* below the nipple, seven cones, will cure.
Alternatively, moxibustion at the first crease behind the inner edge of the thumbnail on both thumbs, one cone each.
Or, moxibustion at one *cun* below the nail of the middle finger on both hands, one cone each, will cure.

These conditions, though listed under miscellaneous treatments, also fall under the category of phlegm obstruction and *huoluan*. They may be treated according to the methods for *huoluan*. Sudden cases are rare and usually arise as complications of other illnesses—such as from unresolved cold damage, post-*huoluan* depletion and dryness, stagnation after consuming tonics for taxation damage, exposure to cold or heat evil, dietary poisoning, or improper medication. Treatment should address the root cause and not rely solely on these methods.

**Additional Remedies:**

From *Essential Prescriptions Worth a Thousand Gold*:
For abdominal distension and shortness of breath, grind one *liang* of *caodoukou* (remove skin) into powder. Take half a *qian* with unripe papaya and fresh ginger decoction.

From *Doumen’s Prescriptions*:
For chronic qi distension and heart oppression in men and women, with inability to eat due to dietary imbalance and cold-heat conflict causing abdominal fullness:
Roast *houpo* over fire until dry, then repeatedly roast with ginger juice until charred black. Grind into powder and take two *qianbi* with aged rice water, three times daily; highly effective. Also treats regurgitation and stops diarrhea.

From *Tested Prescriptions*:
For qi-induced yellow swelling throughout the body, wheezing, inability to eat, and heart-chest fullness:
Roast non-worm-eaten *zaojiao* (remove skin and seeds) with good vinegar until charred, grind into powder. Take one *qianbi* with seven *badou* (remove oil and membrane), mix with light vinegar and well-ground ink to form pills the size of sesame seeds. Take three pills after meals with aged tangerine peel decoction, three times daily. Increase by one pill every other day until purging occurs. For regular use, aids digestion of alcohol and food.

From *Master Mei’s Prescriptions*:
For abdominal fullness preventing oral medication, wrap roasted fresh ginger in silk and insert into the anus; replace when cool.

From *Sagely Benefit Prescriptions*:
For lung organ congestion with heat and vexation, steam four *liang* of fresh *baihe* with half a cup of honey until soft. Frequently hold a piece the size of a jujube in the mouth and swallow the saliva.

*Volume One of Ge Xianweng’s Handbook of Emergency Prescriptions Concludes*

**Volume Two of Ge Xianweng’s Handbook of Emergency Prescriptions**
**Chapter Twelve: Remedies for Sudden Cholera and Other Acute Conditions**

Cholera generally arises from dietary causes—consuming raw or cold foods mixed with rich, greasy fare, wine, or raw fish—while exposed to wind, damp, or drafts, wearing thin clothing, sitting in the open, or sleeping uncovered. At the first onset, ensure warmth: spread hot coals beneath the patient’s bedding and reduce heat if excessive. Alternatively, steam quilts or clothing, replacing cold layers with warm ones. Another method is to heat the ground, douse it with hot water, cover with a thin cloth, lay a mat over it, and envelop the patient thickly. One may also fill a jar with scalding water to soak the feet up to the knees, or place a copper vessel of hot water on the abdomen, padding it with clothing and replacing it when cool. A heated iron may likewise be applied to the abdomen.

If these measures fail to induce recovery, proceed immediately to moxibustion. Follow the prescribed sequence precisely; do not apply moxa haphazardly. Treat only the afflicted area—never preemptively moxa where no illness exists. Though moxibustion may not yield instant relief, it ensures the patient will not die. Do not discontinue treatment merely because improvement is not immediate.

For cholera, use moxa cones of moderate size, with a modest number of applications. The standard recommends seven cones, though forty or fifty may be applied without harm. Revival often follows the first application.

While classical formulas such as *Li Zhong* pills, *Hou Po* (magnolia bark) with fermented soybean decoction, and *Ban Xia* (pinellia) decoctions to unblock the pulse are effective, the ingredients may be difficult to procure. Here, I outline reliable moxibustion techniques and simple, proven remedies—no less effective than costly medicines. Even in cases where death appears imminent, moxibustion may still revive the patient.

Other remedies, such as *Li Zhong* pills and *Si Shun* or *Hou Po* decoctions, should be prepared in advance each autumn for emergency use.

**Moxibustion for Sudden Cholera:**
- If abdominal pain precedes symptoms, apply fourteen cones to *Tai Cang* (Great Granary), located four *cun* below the heart’s xiphoid process.
- If watery diarrhea occurs first, apply fourteen cones one *cun* beside the navel—left for men, right for women. In severe cases, increase to thirty or forty cones. This point is *Da Chang Mu* (Large Intestine Alarm Point), particularly suited for purging.
- If vomiting precedes symptoms, apply fourteen cones two *cun* below the heart. This also treats unremitting diarrhea.
- For counterflow qi, apply fifty cones to *Ju Que* (Great Gateway), one *cun* below the tip of the xiphoid process.
- For cold reversal in the extremities, apply seven cones to each *San Yin Jiao* (Three Yin Intersection), located three *cun* above the inner ankle’s prominence. Increase if no improvement.
- For muscle spasms, apply six or seven cones to the sole’s depression beneath the big toe (*Yong Quan*, Gushing Spring). Alternatively, apply one cone to the midpoint beneath the big toe for miraculous effect, or seven cones to the nail’s edge on the big toe.
- For spasms entering the abdomen with pain, have four assistants hold the patient’s limbs while applying fourteen cones two *cun* left of the navel. Also moxa the large tendon of the thigh, one *cun* from the groin.
- For hiccups, apply seven cones to the first crease of the wrist (*Xin Zhu*, Heart Governor), aligned with the middle finger.
- For unremitting diarrhea, apply seven cones to *Da Du* (Great Metropolis), at the inner side of the big toe’s base joint, on the border of white flesh.
- For dry heaves, apply seven cones to *Wen Shi* (Interrogator), three *cun* behind the wrist between the tendons. If reversal and vomiting are extreme, moxibustion here restores flow. *The Lesser Compendium* states this revives the dead.
- For simultaneous vomiting and diarrhea, apply seven cones to the outer edge of each nipple, near the abdomen’s white flesh. Increase to fourteen if needed.
- If vomiting ceases but diarrhea persists, apply seven cones to the navel’s center, or fourteen to one *cun* below the navel.
- For vexation and fullness, apply seven cones three *cun* below the xiphoid process (*Wei Guan*, Stomach Duct). Alternatively, place a bowl over the navel and apply fourteen cones atop it.
- For acute pain around the navel, apply twenty-one cones three *cun* below it (*Guan Yuan*, Pass Gate). Highly effective.

**Secret Moxibustion for Reviving the Dead from Cholera:**
Measure the patient’s philtrum with an object, fold it to span from the heart’s *Jiu Wei* (Turtledove Tail) downward, and moxa the measured area—first the center, then the left and right. Next, encircle the spine with an object to align with the heart’s xiphoid process, then apply seven cones one *cun* to either side of the spine. This treats three points each on the abdomen and back.

**Hua Tuo’s Method for Cholera-Induced Death:**
Call the patient’s soul from the rooftop. If all other treatments fail, lay the patient prone with arms extended. Measure the distance between the elbows with a string, then apply one hundred cones along the string’s path on either side of the spine, one *cun* from the vertebrae.

For cases unresponsive to other treatments, moxibustion may be applied to the *Zhou Zhui* (Elbow Vertebra). Tested on hundreds of patients, all rose and sat up immediately after moxibustion. Hua Tuo transmitted this technique to his descendants, who kept it secret through generations.

The above methods are all moxibustion therapies.

**For Cholera with Abdominal Distension, Pain, Restlessness, Fullness, and Shortness of Breath Before Emesis or Purgation:**
- **Formula 1:** Two *sheng* of salt, boiled with five *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; consume in one draught to induce vomiting and achieve cure.
- **Formula 2:** One to two *sheng* of fresh or dried ginger, chopped, boiled with six *sheng* of water for three boils; consume in one draught. If not cured, repeat. If fresh herbs are unavailable, decoct the dregs again.
- **Formula 3:** Drink three *sheng* of fine vinegar; the frail or elderly may consume one to two *sheng*.
- **Formula 4:** Warm one to two *sheng* of wine, add a piece of beeswax the size of a bullet, dissolve, and drink. If no wax, substitute two *fangcunbi* of salt.
- **Formula 5:** Half a *sheng* of cinnamon powder, mixed with two *sheng* of warm liquid; consume entirely.
- **Formula 6:** Boil five to six *sheng* of thick bamboo-leaf decoction and apply hot to areas affected by cramps.
- **Formula 7:** Take a piece of *nan* or camphor wood the size of a palm, shave, boil with three *sheng* of water for three boils, strain, and apply hot.
- **Formula 8:** Consume three *fangcunbi* of dried ginger powder.
- **Formula 9:** Two *sheng* of finely chopped knotweed leaves or stems, boiled with five *sheng* of water for three boils; consume in one draught. Decocted dried perilla or fresh perilla juice is also effective.
- **Formula 10:** One *sheng* of minced garlic, boiled with three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; consume in one draught.
- **Formula 11:** Soak five *sheng* of garlic in warm water, extract the juice, and drink.
- **Formula 12:** Mix human blood with cinnabar and consume two pills the size of *wuzhi* seeds.
- **Formula 13:** One *jin* of sliced fresh ginger, boiled with seven *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; divide into three doses.
- **Formula 14:** Take grime from a weaver’s loom the size of a pigeon’s egg, consume with warm wine to cure.
- **Formula 15:** Drink a small amount of bamboo sap to cure.
- **Formula 16:** Two *liang* of dried ginger, two *liang* of licorice, one *liang* of aconite, boiled with three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; add one *ge* of pig’s bile, mix, and divide into three doses.
- **Formula 17:** Boil a large handful of reed catkins thickly and drink two *sheng* to cure.

**For Cramps:**
- Heat iron until red-hot and cauterize the white flesh near the heel, close to the rear. Apply the iron longitudinally along the foot, pausing to form a sore. Repeat on both feet; shortly, heat will enter the abdomen, cramps will cease, and recovery will follow. A heated knife or shrimp tail may also be used.
- Boil vinegar three times and apply with massage; adding a small amount of powder is especially effective. Bind with cotton padding from below the knee to the foot.
- Burn fourteen gardenia fruits, grind into powder, and consume.
- Equal parts cinnamon and pinellia, ground into one *fangcunbi* of powder, mixed with one *sheng* of water; consume to cure.
- Grind raw soybean powder, mix with wine, and consume one *fangcunbi*.
- Burn centipede fat and apply to the affected area to cure.

**For Cramps Entering the Intestines (as if about to cramp):**
- Boil one *cun* of white chicken droppings with six *ge* of water for three boils; consume in one draught without the patient’s knowledge.
- Boil vinegar with clothing wadding, warm the wadding, and wrap the cramping area.
- Burn three pinches of woven straw rope, consume with wine to cure.
- Consume soot from the bottom of a cauldron with wine to cure.

**For Cramps in the Abdomen:**
Invert the patient so the head is downward until the abdomen is level.

**For Cramps in the Arms, Legs, Chest, or Ribs:**
- Boil one and a half *sheng* of salt with one *dou* of water until scalding hot; soak hands and feet. For cramps in the chest or ribs, wash with the hot liquid.
- For cramps entering the abdomen, invert the patient so the head is downward until the abdomen is level. In severe cases, if the hands pull the genitals and the genitals retract, death is certain; if not yet retracted, inversion may still save the patient.

**For Unremitting Dysentery with Cramps Entering the Abdomen (Near Death):**
Tear one *liang* of fresh ginger, boil with one and a half *sheng* of wine for three to four boils; consume in one draught to cure.

**For Restlessness and Fullness in the Heart and Abdomen After Cholera-Induced Emesis and Purgation:**
Fourteen gardenia fruits, boiled with three *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; add seven *ge* of fermented soybeans, boil to yield one *sheng*, and consume in one draught. For vomiting, add two *liang* of tangerine peel. For restlessness, add one *sheng* of fermented soybeans, one *liang* of licorice, one *sheng* of honey, and two *sheng* of water; divide into five doses.

**For Restlessness and Inability to Lie Still After Cholera-Induced Emesis and Purgation:**
Twenty stalks of scallion whites, twenty jujubes, boiled with three *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; consume in one draught.

**For Intense Thirst After Cholera-Induced Emesis and Purgation (Excessive Drinking is Fatal):**
Boil five *sheng* of millet with one *dou* of water to yield three *sheng*; strain the clear liquid and sip gradually. Avoid other beverages.

**Master Cui’s *Li Zhong* Pill Formula:**
Three *liang* of licorice, one *liang* each of dried ginger, ginseng, and atractylodes, ground and sifted, mixed with honey into pills the size of bullets. If symptoms persist, take another pill. If still uncured, boil one *dou* of warm liquid with pork broth and consume in three to five doses until cured. May also be taken with wine.

**Fourfold Harmony Decoction:**
For unremitting emesis, purgation, dry abdomen, retching, and cold hands and feet. Two *liang* each of dried ginger, licorice, ginseng, and aconite, boiled with six *sheng* of water to yield three and a half *sheng*; divide into three doses. For unremitting diarrhea, add one *liang* of dragon bone.

If abdominal pain is severe, add two *liang* of tangkuei. **Hu Qia**’s version uses one aconite root and one *liang* of cinnamon.

For cholera morbus without vomiting or diarrhea but with sunken pulses in the limbs, cold flesh, sweating, and thirst, recovery follows.

**Magnolia Bark Decoction:**
For vexation, retching, and abdominal distension. Four *liang* of roasted magnolia bark, two *liang* of cinnamon, five roasted *gorgon fruit*, and three *liang* of fresh ginger, boiled with six *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; divide into three doses.

These four decoctions treat all cholera morbus afflictions and should not be left uncompounded.

If cholera morbus presents with particularly severe heart pain, this indicates toxin involvement; treat concurrently with remedies for *zhong’e* (sudden noxious attack).

**Attached Formulas**

**Sun Zhenren’s** treatment for cholera morbus:
Swallow thirty to forty peppercorns with a beverage.

**Doumen Formula** for cholera morbus:
Split a piece of yellow cedar into chips, take a handful, and boil concentratedly in one *zhong* of water to consume.

**Waitai Miyao** for cholera morbus with vexation and agitation:
Burn a clump of tangled hair the size of a chicken’s egg, mix with three *sheng* of salt broth, and consume. If no vomiting occurs, take again.

Another formula for cholera morbus with abdominal pain, vomiting, and diarrhea:
Take three *sheng* of chopped peach leaves, boil with five *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng* and three *ge*; divide into two warm doses.

**Meishi Formula** for cholera morbus with heart pain, diarrhea, and absence of sweating:
Take a large handful of pear leaves and twigs, boil with three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*, and consume.

Another formula for post-cholera morbus vexation and external restlessness:
Twenty stalks of scallion white and twenty jujubes, boiled with three *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; divide and consume.

**Bingbu Shouji’s** remarkably efficacious remedy for saving lives in cholera morbus:
Boil slightly sour fermented water with dried ginger shreds and sip. For summer stomach and bowel discomfort, boil and sip to cure.

**Sun Yonghe’s** treatment for unremitting severe cholera morbus diarrhea:
One aconite root weighing seven *qian*, roasted, skinned, and navel removed, ground into powder. Each dose: four *qian*, boiled with two *zhong* of water and half a *qian* of salt to yield one *zhong*; take warm to cease immediately.

**Jixiao Fang** for unremitting vomiting and diarrhea, or cramps, with frequent limb reversal, vacuity wind, and loss of consciousness. This restores yang: limbs gradually warm, and consciousness returns.
**Yang-Restoring Powder:**
Grind *arisaema* into powder. Each dose: three *qian*, with three Beijing jujubes, boiled in one and a half *zhong* of water to yield eight *fen*; take warm. If consciousness does not return, take again.

**Shenghui Fang** for cholera morbus with cramps near death:
Chop one handful of decayed cattail mat finely, boil with one *zhong* of fermented water to yield juice; consume warm in one dose.

Another formula for liver vacuity cramps:
Chop three *ge* of red knotweed stems and leaves, boil with one *zhong* of water and three *ge* of wine to yield four *ge*; strain and divide into two warm doses.

Another formula for liver wind vacuity cramps entering the abdomen:
Boil half a *jin* of salt in water briefly; hot soaking is excellent.

**Sun Shangyao’s** treatment for foot cramps with pain and spasms:
One *liang* of pine nodes, finely chopped like rice grains, and one *qian* of frankincense. In a silver or stone vessel, stir-fry over low heat until charred, retaining three-tenths of its nature; remove from fire to dispel toxicity, then grind finely. Each dose: one to two *qian*, taken with hot quince wine. Treats all timely cramp disorders.

**Gu Jin Lu Yan Fang** for cholera morbus cramps:
Take a handful of knotweed, remove both ends, boil with two and a half *sheng* of water to yield one and a half *sheng*; consume in one dose.

**Formulas for Cold Damage, Seasonal Qi, and Epidemic Diseases (Chapter Thirteen)**

For cold damage, seasonal qi, epidemic diseases, headache, high fever, and large pulses on the first day:
Take approximately three *sheng* of *zhidui* root and leaves, pound together with one *liang* of cinnabar, boil with one *sheng* of water, strain to yield juice, and consume in one dose; vomiting indicates recovery. For severe cases, consume one *sheng* entirely, cover thickly to induce sweating, and recover.

Another formula:
Pound one *sheng* of garlic to yield two *ge* of juice; consume in one dose. Recovery follows no more than two doses.

Another formula:
Fourteen black plums and five *ge* of salt, boiled with three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; strain and consume in one dose.

Another formula:
Peel the black bark from fresh *zhimu* wood, finely chop one *sheng* of the white inner part, boil with two *sheng* and five *ge* of water, strain, and consume eight *ge* per dose; three doses cure.

Another formula:
Knead twenty-seven *muwanzi* seeds in five *sheng* of water until ripe, strain, and consume all the juice to induce vomiting and diarrhea, curing the illness.

Another formula:
Place one chicken egg in half a *sheng* of cold water, stir to blend, then boil three *sheng* of water to a rolling boil. Pour the egg mixture into the boiling water, stir rapidly to combine, adjust to a warm temperature, and consume in one dose to induce sweating.

Another formula:
Apply cinnabar over the entire body, face the fire, and sit until sweating occurs to recover.

Another formula:
Pound fresh *ranghe* root and leaves together, strain to yield juice, and consume three to four *sheng*.

Another formula:
Boil three *jin* of dried mugwort with one *dou* of water to yield one *sheng*; strain and consume in one dose to induce sweating.

Another formula:
Consume one *sheng* of salt, followed by hot water; abdominal cramping and vomiting should follow. Cover to induce sweating and recover.

Another formula:
Boil one hundred fifty-seven *bishu* coins in one *dou* of water to yield seven *sheng*; consume all the juice. Shortly after, boil again with five *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*, then add two *sheng* of water to combine for three *sheng*. Remove the coins and drink the juice to induce vomiting and expel toxins.

Another formula:
Take a piece of lard the size of a bullet, consume warm, three times daily for three days (nine doses total).

Another formula:
Take thirty black plums, remove the pits, and boil with one *sheng* of fermented soybeans and three *sheng* of bitter wine to yield one and a half *sheng*; strain and consume in one dose.

Furthermore, as cold damage disorders have several types and people cannot distinguish them, a single remedy may address all: if one initially feels headache, feverish flesh, and a surging pulse, within the first or second day, prepare the Scallion and Fermented Soybean Decoction.
Use one handful of scallion whites and one *sheng* of fermented soybeans, boil with three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*, and consume in one dose to induce sweating. If sweating does not occur, prepare again, adding two *liang* of kudzu root and three *liang* of cimicifuga, with five *sheng* of water; decoct to yield two *sheng* and divide into two doses, which will surely induce sweating. If sweating still does not occur, further add two *liang* of ephedra, then grind two *ge* of rice with scallion decoction, boil with one *sheng* of water for a short time, add salt and fermented soybeans, followed by the scallion whites; decoct over fire to yield three *sheng* and divide into doses to induce sweating.

Another formula:
Boil one *sheng* of fermented soybeans with three *sheng* of young boy’s urine to yield one *sheng*; divide into two doses and consume to induce sweating.

Another formula:
