Boil four *liang* of kudzu root with one *dou* of water to yield three *sheng*, then add one *sheng* of fermented soybeans and decoct to yield one and a half *sheng*; consume in one dose. Pound fresh kudzu to extract the juice and consume one to two *sheng*—this is also excellent.

If sweating persists without cessation after three or four days, and the chest feels unwell, inducing vomiting is desired: boil three *sheng* of fermented soybeans with seven *sheng* of water to yield two and a half *sheng*; strain, add one *liang* of honey, and boil again for three bubblings. Consume in one dose and rest quietly to induce vomiting. If recovery does not follow, consume again until recovery.

This esoteric method is transmitted to descendants.

Another formula:
Finely chop three *jin* of fresh rehmannia root, boil with one *dou* of water to yield three *sheng*, and divide into three doses. Alternatively, consume the *Hualu Tusan* or *Kushen Longdan San*.

For cases lasting five or six days or more:
Prepare a large quantity of green bamboo sap, simmer briefly to reduce slightly, and drink frequently; cover thickly to induce sweating.

Another formula:
Boil half a *liang* each of rhubarb, coptis, phellodendron, and gardenia with eight *sheng* of water for six or seven bubblings; add one *sheng* of fermented soybeans and seven stalks of scallion, then boil to yield three *sheng*. Divide and consume—suitable for both elderly and young.

Another formula:
Boil two *liang* of flavescent sophora and two *liang* of scutellaria with half a *jin* of fresh rehmannia in eight *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; divide into two doses. If vomiting or purging of toxins occurs, recovery follows.

For cases lasting six or seven days with extreme heat, heart vexation, delirious speech, visions of ghosts, and a desire to rise and flee:
Boil three *sheng* of dried evodia fruit with two *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; strain, and consume at a moderate temperature. Sweating will bring recovery. This formula is highly reliable and must be used—an esoteric method.

Another formula:
Take one *sheng* of large earthworms, split and remove the contents, then boil in human urine until done; strain and consume. Alternatively, extract fresh juice or decoct in water—both are effective.

Another method:
Extract juice from feces, consuming several *ge* to one or two *sheng*—this is called *Huanglong Tang* ("Yellow Dragon Decoction"), with aged feces being best.

Another formula:
Take a white dog, split it open from the back to collect its blood—more is better. While still warm, apply it thickly to the chest; remove once cooled. This revives those on the verge of death. If no white dog is available, any pure-colored dog may be used.

Another formula:
Remove the black outer layer of paulownia bark, tear it into fine strips, and cut into four-*cun* lengths to form bundles. Boil with five *ge* of wine and one *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; strain and consume in one dose. Vomiting or purging of several *sheng* of green-yellow fluid will bring recovery.

Another formula:
Mix three chicken eggs, a *fangcunbi* of mirabilite, and three *ge* of wine; stir until the mirabilite dissolves completely, then consume.

Another formula:
Boil three *liang* of coptis, two *liang* each of phellodendron and scutellaria, and fourteen gardenia fruits in six *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; divide into two doses. This treats vexation, vomiting, and insomnia.

For those on the verge of death from epidemic qi:
Boil a thousand coins’ worth of coffin wood to make a decoction.

Another method:
Steep one *liang* of flavescent sophora (crushed) in two and a half *sheng* of wine—older formulas use wine to decoct flavescent sophora, reducing it to one and a half *sheng*. Strain, adjust to a moderate temperature, and consume entirely. The patient will experience intense cold and vomit toxins resembling molten glue, then recover.

Another formula:
Boil one hundred coins in one *dou* of water to yield eight *sheng*; grind a *dangmenzi*-sized piece of musk into powder and administer gradually until finished. This may induce sweating or vomiting.

For warm toxin with maculae and severe epidemics difficult to cure—*Heigao* ("Black Paste"):
Chop half a *jin* of fresh rehmannia, combine with one *sheng* of fine fermented soybeans and two *jin* of lard, and boil for five or six bubblings until reduced by one-third. Strain, then add powdered realgar and musk the size of large soybeans; mix well and consume entirely. Toxins will exit through the skin, bringing recovery.

Another formula:
Use a live toad, split its abdomen to remove the intestines, then pound and consume raw. Dried toads from the fifth day of the fifth month, burned to ash, are also effective.

*Heinu Wan* ("Black Slave Pill"), as recorded in *Hu Qia* and *Xiaopin*, is also called *Shuijie Wan* ("Water-Resolving Pill"). Another version adds one *liang* of charred wheat husks, naming it *Mainu Wan* ("Wheat Slave Pill"). The annotations are consistent.

Ingredients:
Two *liang* each of ephedra and rhubarb, one *liang* each of scutellaria and mirabilite, one *liang* of pot-bottom soot, two *liang* of stove chimney soot, and two *liang* of roof beam dust. Pound the ingredients, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of a bullet. Grind one pill in five *ge* of freshly drawn water and consume in one dose. If thirsty, drink water; soon, a chilling sensation will arise, followed by sweating and resolution. If no effect is observed after the time it takes for the sun to move five *chi*, consume another pill. This treats cases of five or six days with intense chest heat and lockjaw, known as "ruined illness," which is otherwise incurable—use this *Heinu Wan*.

Another formula:
Boil four *liang* of indigo plant, two *liang* each of licorice and donkey-hide gelatin, and eight *ge* of fermented soybeans in one *dou* of water. First boil the indigo and licorice to yield three and a half *sheng*; strain, add the fermented soybeans, and boil for three bubblings. Strain again, then add the gelatin and divide into four doses. Consume entirely, then prepare another batch. This is highly effective for cases lasting seven or eight days with unresolved heat after sweating or vomiting, or with intense heat.

Another formula:
Pound two *liang* of rhubarb, two *liang* of licorice, two *liang* of ephedra, thirty apricot kernels, five *ge* of mirabilite, one *liang* of scutellaria, and twenty stir-fried croton seeds; mix with honey to form pills the size of soybeans. Consume three pills to purge toxins. If purging does not cease, use rice water to stop it. Household members attending the patient may also consume this first to purge, preventing contagion. These pills may be prepared in advance.

For resolving muscle layer (heat) on the first or second day:
Boil one *liang* each of ephedra, licorice, cimicifuga, peony, and gypsum, thirty apricot kernels, and three cowrie shells in three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; consume in one dose. Cover to induce sweating, then recovery follows. Consume fermented soybean porridge afterward to replenish deficiency.

Another formula:
Boil two *liang* of ephedra, one *liang* each of scutellaria and cinnamon, and three *liang* of fresh ginger in six *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; divide into four doses.

Alternatively, consume *Gegen Jieji Tang* ("Pueraria Muscle-Resolving Decoction"):
Boil four *liang* of pueraria root, two *liang* of peony, one *liang* each of ephedra, indigo plant, licorice, scutellaria, gypsum, and cinnamon, and four jujubes in five *sheng* of water to yield two and a half *sheng*. Strain and divide into three doses to induce mild sweating.

For cases persisting from three to seven or eight days without resolution, *Xiao Chaihu Tang* ("Minor Bupleurum Decoction") may be administered:
Boil eight *liang* of bupleurum, three *liang* each of ginseng, licorice, and scutellaria, eight *liang* of fresh ginger (or three *liang* of dried ginger if unavailable), five *liang* of pinellia (washed in hot water), and twelve jujubes in nine *sheng* of water to yield two and a half *sheng*; divide into three doses. Cover lightly to induce sweating for half a day, and recovery should follow shortly. If improvement is not observed, prepare another dose.

If heat and excess persist despite sweating, accompanied by fullness, pain, vexation, and delirious speech, *Da Chaihu Tang* ("Major Bupleurum Decoction") may be administered:
Boil half a *jin* of bupleurum, two *liang* of rhubarb, three *liang* of scutellaria, two *liang* of peony, ten pieces of unripe bitter orange, five *liang* of pinellia (washed), five *liang* of fresh ginger, and twelve jujubes in one *dou* of water to yield four *sheng*; divide into four doses. Mild purgation should follow.

These four formulas are of the utmost urgency. If medicine can be obtained promptly, one need not resort to other measures, and death may be averted. All other minor treatments are merely precautionary or for extreme cases.

If the illness is mistreated or fails to resolve after ten days or more, it is termed a "ruined disease," and only *Da Xiao Biejia Tang* ("Major and Minor Turtle Shell Decoctions") should be administered. As this formula requires many ingredients in small quantities, it is not feasible for emergency use and thus is not recorded here.

In all cases of cold damage where sweating is induced, avoid excessive fluid loss. A single dose should produce mild sweating; once the sweat clears, cease further administration. If sweating persists, apply powder and avoid drafts.

When cold damage first manifests with generalized heaviness, lumbar and back pain, unremitting vexation, a floating pulse, a face flushed with brocade-like macules, sore throat, or diarrhea, or with delirious speech and a desire to flee, this is termed "yang toxin." It is treatable within five days; beyond this, death ensues. The following formula is appropriate:
Boil one *fen* each of realgar, licorice, cimicifuga, Chinese angelica, Sichuan pepper, and cinnamon in five *sheng* of water to yield two and a half *sheng*; divide into three doses. Cover to induce sweating. If sweating does not occur, prepare another dose.

If the body feels heavy and the back stiff, with a sensation of being beaten, abdominal pain, epigastric rigidity, shortness of breath, retching, cyanotic lips, a dark complexion, cold limbs, and a pulse that is deep, fine, tight, and rapid, this is termed "yin toxin." It is treatable within five days; beyond this, death ensues. The following formula is appropriate:
Boil two *fen* each of licorice and cimicifuga, one *fen* each of Chinese angelica and Sichuan pepper, and one *liang* of turtle shell in five *sheng* of water to yield two and a half *sheng*; divide into three doses. Cover to induce sweating. If sweating does not occur, prepare another dose by decocting the ingredients again.

For yin toxin with cold mouth and nose, grind one *fen* each of dried ginger and cinnamon into powder and consume with three *ge* of warm wine; this should produce intense heat and lead to recovery.

Yin and yang toxins do not only appear at the onset but may also develop after one or two days. All such cases should be treated with the aforementioned formulas. Most patients with these conditions succumb to the illness.

For heat disease that fails to resolve and leads to severe diarrhea with impending death, administer *Da Qing Tang* ("Major Indigo Decoction"):
Boil four *liang* of indigo plant, three *liang* of licorice, two *liang* of donkey-hide gelatin, eight *ge* of fermented soybeans, and three *liang* of red halloysite in one *dou* of water to yield three *sheng*; divide into three doses. If the decoction is exhausted, prepare another. Administer two doses day and night to achieve recovery.

Another formula:
Boil one *sheng* of fermented soybeans, fourteen gardenia fruits, and one handful of Chinese leek in five *sheng* of water to yield three and a half *sheng*; divide into three doses.

Another formula:
Crush half a *jin* of dragon bone and boil in one *dou* of water to yield five *sheng*. Consume the decoction extremely cold in small sips. If sweating occurs at any point, recovery follows.

Another formula:
Form pills the size of parasol seeds with two *liang* each of coptis and Chinese angelica, one *liang* of dried ginger, two *liang* of red halloysite, and honey. Consume twenty pills, three times during the day and twice at night.

Another formula:
Boil two *liang* of coptis and a piece of processed mugwort the size of a duck egg in two *dou* of water to yield one *sheng*; consume in one dose to achieve immediate cessation. This formula governs all epidemic dysentery.

For all epidemic dysentery, boil three *liang* of coptis, two *liang* each of phellodendron, Chinese angelica, and dragon bone in six *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*. Strain, add seven *ge* of honey, and decoct again to yield one and a half *sheng*; divide into three doses. This is effective.

For epidemic toxin disease with concurrent heat, abdominal pain, and diarrhea, boil half a *liang* each of cimicifuga, licorice, coptis, Chinese angelica, peony, cinnamon bark, and phellodendron in three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*; consumption should yield good results.

For epidemic disease with severe heat diarrhea after four or five days, boil three *liang* each of coptis and phellodendron, three *liang* of dragon bone, and a piece of mugwort the size of a chicken egg in six *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; divide into two doses. Avoid consuming pork and cold water.

For unremitting pus and blood in the stool, boil one *jin* of red halloysite, one *liang* of dried ginger, and one *sheng* of rice in seven *sheng* of water until the rice is cooked. Strain and consume seven *ge* twice daily.

Another formula:
Boil one *jin* of red halloysite and two *liang* of dried ginger in five *sheng* of water to yield three *sheng*; divide into two doses.

For gripping umbilical pain, add one *liang* of Chinese angelica and two *liang* of peony, and increase the water by one *sheng*.

To promote bowel movement when the stool is hard and impacted, boil four *liang* of rhubarb, two *liang* of magnolia bark, and four pieces of unripe bitter orange in four *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng* and two *ge*; divide into two doses. Cease administration once the bowels move.

For constipation lasting over ten days, administer *Chengqi Wan* ("Qi-Regulating Pill"):
Grind two *liang* each of rhubarb and apricot kernels, one *liang* of unripe bitter orange, and one *ge* of mirabilite. Mix with honey to form pills the size of a bullet. Consume with six or seven *ge* of hot water. If the bowels do not move, administer another dose.

For diarrhea with inability to eat, grind one *sheng* of coptis and twenty roasted and dried mume fruits into powder. Melt a piece of wax the size of a chess piece and one *sheng* of honey over a gentle fire until pliable, then form pills the size of parasol seeds. Consume two pills per dose, three times daily.

For distension and fullness in the lower abdomen with inability to urinate, the following remedies may be used:

Grind realgar into fine powder, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of a jujube pit. Insert into the urethral opening to a depth of half an inch. Alternatively, use a bamboo tube to inject into the vagina, causing pain and inducing urination to achieve relief.

Another remedy: Grind three *liang* of talc and one *ge* of *tingli* seeds into powder. Boil in two *sheng* of water until seven *ge* remain, then consume.

Another remedy: Pound fresh scallions and apply thinly to the lower abdomen, replacing them frequently.

For fullness and oppression in the chest and rib-sides, heart blockage, qi urgency, and panting, the following remedy may be used:

Grind one *liang* each of ginseng and *bai zhu*, two *liang* of *zhi shi*, and one *liang* of dried ginger. Mix with honey to form pills. Consume one pill per dose.

If coughing is present, add two *liang* of *gua lou*.
If vomiting occurs, add two *liang* of oyster shell.
Take five or six pills day and night. If not cured, continue administration.

For toxic disease attacking the throat causing swelling and pain, the following remedies may be used:

Slice *shanglu* and roast until hot. Place on a cloth over the throat and press with a heated cloth. Replace when cool.

Another remedy: Take a piece of real cinnabar the size of a fingernail, place in the mouth, and lightly chew to release its juice, allowing it to soak the throat. A slight unusual sensation indicates efficacy.

For toxic disease attacking the eyes afterward, the following remedies may be used:

Boil a wasp’s nest and use the liquid to wash the eyes, six or seven times daily. This is effective.

Another remedy: Soak a green cloth in cold water and apply to the eyes.

If a nebula forms, burn fourteen *chi* beans, grind into powder, and blow into the nose using a tube.

For unremitting vomiting due to cold damage, the following remedies may be used:

Boil one *liang* of licorice, half a *liang* of *shengma*, three *liang* of fresh ginger, and two *liang* of tangerine peel in three *sheng* of water until two *sheng* remain. Consume in one dose to cure.

Another remedy: Grind six *fen* of dried ginger and four *fen* of aconite into powder. Mix with vinegar to form pills the size of parasol seeds. Take three pills per dose, three times daily.

For unremitting hiccups due to cold damage, the following remedies may be used:

Boil three *liang* of licorice and one *sheng* of tangerine peel in five *sheng* of water until three *sheng* remain. Divide and consume, three times daily, until cured.

Another remedy: Wash and dry *banxia*, then grind into powder. Take one *qian* per dose.

Another remedy: Boil one handful of red perilla in three *sheng* of water until two *sheng* remain. Drink gradually.

Another remedy: Grind six *fen* of dried ginger and four *fen* of aconite into powder. Mix with vinegar to form pills the size of parasol seeds. Take three pills per dose, three times daily.

In recent years, there has been an epidemic disease causing sores to erupt on the head, face, and body, spreading rapidly like fire sores, all filled with white pus. If ruptured, new sores form immediately. If not treated promptly, severe cases often result in death. Even after recovery, the scars remain purple-black for over a year before fading. This is caused by virulent toxic qi.

It is said that in the fourth year of Yonghui (653 CE), these sores spread from west to east across the land. Boiling mallow and consuming it with garlic paste was found to halt the condition. Eating it at the onset of symptoms, even with a small amount of rice, is effective.

This disease was acquired during the Jianwu era (25–56 CE) in Nanyang while fighting the barbarians, hence it was called "barbarian sores." Various physicians collaborated on treatments, and the following effective remedies were developed:

Apply high-quality honey to the entire body. Alternatively, decoct *shengma* in honey and consume frequently.

Another remedy: Boil *shengma* thoroughly in water, soak cotton in the liquid, and wash the sores. Soaking in vinegar is even better, though the pain may be unbearable.

Other treatments follow the methods for cold damage, but one must be vigilant against the toxicity.

Using *dihuang* black ointment is also effective.

For epidemic jaundice, the following remedy may be used:

Boil six *liang* of *yinchen*, two *liang* of rhubarb, and twelve gardenia fruits in one *dou* of water. First boil *yinchen* until five *sheng* remain, strain, then add the other ingredients and boil until three *sheng* remain. Divide into four doses. Other treatments for jaundice may also be combined for efficacy.

In recent years, there has also been a "barbarian jaundice" disease. Initially, one feels heaviness and discomfort in the limbs. Soon after, yellowing appears in the eyes, gradually spreading to the face and eventually the entire body. Immediately test the urine with white paper; if the paper turns yellow like turmeric dye, the heat toxin has entered internally, and urgent treatment is required.

At the first sign, prepare *guadi* and red bean powder and blow it into the nose. If several *sheng* of yellow fluid discharge from the nose, recovery is likely.

If the condition has progressed deeply, inspect the underside of the tongue for two prominent white veins. Use a reed knife to incise them, allowing several *sheng* of purple blood to drain, which will provide relief. However, this must be performed by someone experienced in the procedure. Inexperienced incisions may damage the blue veins under the tongue, causing unstoppable bleeding and death.

Alternatively, heat an iron spindle until red-hot and cauterize the veins to scorch them. Combine *guadi* and *badou* into pills and consume to induce discharge of yellow fluid through the stool and urine. After cauterization, avoid all杂食.

It is also said that one may sit on yellow earth to alleviate jaundice, but this must be distinguished from other conditions.

Remedies include:

Boil bamboo and drink the liquid like tea.

Another remedy: Pound fresh *gua* roots, extract the juice, and drink one to two or three *sheng*.

Another remedy: Soak chicken eggs in vinegar overnight and swallow the whites of several eggs.

Another remedy: Cut five *sheng* of bamboo leaves, seven *sheng* of wheat, and three *liang* of gypsum. Grind into powder, wrap in cotton, and boil in one *dou* and five *sheng* of water until seven *sheng* remain. Consume one *sheng* per dose until finished for a cure.

Another remedy: Mix two *sheng* of fresh *ge* root juice, one *sheng* of high-quality *chi*, twenty-one gardenia fruits, and one *sheng* of chopped *yinchen*. Boil in five *sheng* of water until three *sheng* remain, strain, add the *ge* juice, and divide into five doses.

Another remedy: Prepare a golden-footed hen as one would for eating. Consume the meat and broth thoroughly, adding a small amount of salted *chi* for flavor. If not cured, repeat the treatment.

For toxic attack causing swelling and pain in the hands and feet, as if about to sever, the following remedies may be used:

Chop *huzhang* root, boil, and soak the feet in the liquid at an appropriate temperature, stopping when the water reaches just above the ankles.

Another remedy: Soak the feet in rice-straw ash liquid.

Another remedy: Boil *kushen* in wine and soak the feet until cured.

Another remedy: Pound one *sheng* each of salted *chi* and sheep urine until well-mixed, then soak the affected area.

Another remedy: Finely chop five *jin* of *huangbo*, boil in three *dou* of water, and soak the affected area. This also treats swelling and pain in the private parts.

Another remedy: Dig a pit three *chi* deep, just large enough to hold both feet. Heat the pit thoroughly, then pour wine into it. Step into the pit wearing clogs, ensuring the steam is contained and does not escape.

Another remedy: Boil *yangtao* juice and soak the affected area; adding a small amount of salted *chi* is especially effective.

Another remedy: Boil horse dung or sheep dung in water and soak the affected area.

Another remedy: Mix sheep dung with lard and apply to the swelling; this is also effective.

Another remedy: Wrap the swollen area with beef, and the swelling will subside and pain cease.

Another remedy: Pound *changsicao*, extract the juice, and soak the feet in it.

Another remedy: Boil one pig’s trotter with scallions, remove the dregs, add a small amount of salt, and soak the affected area.

For toxic disease causing sores in the lower body, burn a *guan* vessel and insert the ashes deeply as a suppository; no more than three applications are needed.

Another remedy: Apply raw lacquer and insert it with cotton.

Another remedy: Form large moxa cones and apply moxibustion to the lower body—this is a last resort when no other medicine is available.

Another remedy: Take three *sheng* of earthworms, boil in five *sheng* of water until two and a half *sheng* remain, and consume the entire decoction.

Another remedy: Boil peach bark until it reduces to a syrup-like consistency, then combine with cotton for insertion.

Another remedy: Pound water *xingcai*, wrap in cotton, and insert; replace five times daily until cured.

Another remedy: Boil *ju* bark and *hu* bark together until the liquid thickens like malt sugar, then use for insertion.

Another: A thick decoction of boiled peach bark, taken as a drink, is most effective.

Another remedy: Pound *shemei* to extract the juice, take three *ge* three times daily. Soak black plums in water until concentrated, then add honey from cliff bees, and drink frequently.

If the patient’s teeth lose their color, the tongue turns white, or they become excessively drowsy, confused, and insensitive to pain, or if they suffer from diarrhea, urgently treat the lower body. Those who do not recognize this will only address the upper body, neglecting the lower, allowing worms to grow in the lower body. These worms will consume the anus, and when the anus rots to reveal the five viscera, death follows.

Remedy: Take egg white, mix with lacquer, return it to the eggshell, and swallow it while facing upward. This will induce vomiting of the worms, leading to recovery.

Another remedy: Burn horse hooves to ash, grind finely, mix with lard, and apply to cotton for insertion into the lower body several times daily until cured.

Another remedy: Boil fifteen peach kernels, two *sheng* of bitter wine, and one *ge* of salt until six *ge* remain, then consume.

Another remedy: Burn mugwort in a tube to fumigate the lower body, allowing the smoke to enter. Mix a small amount of realgar into the mugwort—this method is used for *xiwen* (stream warmth), hence the inclusion of its treatment.

For incessant diarrhea from an unknown cause: Two *liang* of *wutou*, one *liang* each of *nüwei* and *yunshi*, and two *fen* of *gui*. Form into honey pills the size of *tongzi* seeds, and take five pills with water three times daily.

For sudden pain in the lower body resembling a bird’s pecking: Pound one *sheng* each of red adzuki beans and large beans, place in two pouches, steam until hot, and alternate sitting on them to cure. This was originally recorded in the miscellaneous treatments section and is also caused by toxic *qi* from cold damage.

Thus, while there are many remedies for cold damage—including those using *mahuang*, *gegen*, *guizhi*, *chaihu*, *qinglong*, *baihu*, *sishun*, and *sini*, totaling over twenty essential formulas—the ingredients are difficult to fully prepare. Moreover, diagnosis must be precise, and other comprehensive formulas are recorded elsewhere. Here, only the four most urgently needed formulas are included. The *huanggao* and *chisang* remedies are found in the disease-prevention section and should be prepared in advance; take them at the first sign of illness.

Cold damage (*shanghan*), seasonal epidemics (*shixing*), and warm epidemics (*wenyi*) are three names for the same category of illness, though their origins differ slightly. When one is harmed by cold in winter, or when sweating from strenuous activity exposes one to wind and cold, the illness manifests in summer—this is called *shanghan*. When winter is not very cold, and warm air or westerly winds cause the joints to relax and become susceptible, the illness manifests in spring—this is called *shixing*. When pestilential *qi* and demonic toxins afflict a person in a given year, it is called *wenbing*. Though the diagnostic signs are similar, and refined discourse prefers the general term *shanghan*, common people call it *shixing*. Daoist talismans and inscriptions also distinguish the *five warm* diseases, but ultimately, they share the same path. However, there are differences such as *yangming*, *shaoyang*, *yin* toxin, and *yang* toxin. Cases of *shaoyin* disease that do not involve fever but present with abdominal fullness and diarrhea are the most difficult to treat.

**Attached Formula**
From *The Infallible Remedies*: For seasonal epidemic illness of one or two days’ duration: Take one large *liang* of *mahuang* (remove the nodes), boil in four *sheng* of water, skim off the foam, and reduce to two *sheng*. Remove the dregs, add a spoonful of rice and *chi* to make a thin porridge, and consume one *sheng* while strong. First, prepare hot water and pour over one hundred bowls’ worth over the head, then consume the porridge. Cover thickly to induce sweating; doing this at night is most effective.

**Formulas from *Master Mei’s Remedies***
For unresolved *cold damage* with sweating persisting three or four days, accompanied by chest oppression and vomiting: Take one *sheng* of *chi*, one *ge* of salt, and four *sheng* of water; decoct to one and a half *sheng*, divide and consume—this will induce vomiting.

**Formulas from *Sagely Benevolence Remedies***
For *cold damage* of four days’ duration with persistent vomiting, further vomiting is advisable: Take *kushen* powder, administer two *qian* with wine—recovery follows vomiting.

Another formula for seasonal epidemic *heat toxin* with vexation and restlessness of the heart-spirit: Use half a large spoonful of *lan dian*, mix with one cup of freshly drawn water, and consume.

Another formula for seasonal epidemic with unremitting headache: Take three *liang* of *poxiao*, grind to a powder, mix with raw oil, and apply to the crown of the head.

Another formula for seasonal epidemic with vexing thirst: Take one medium cup of fresh lotus root juice, blend with one *ge* of raw honey, divide into two doses, and consume.

**Formulas from *Victorious Golden Remedies***
For seasonal epidemic *heat disease* with delirious speech and heart vexation: Take *kushen* in any quantity, stir-fry until yellow, and grind to powder. For each dose, take two *qian*, decoct in one cup of water to eight parts, and consume warm. Repeat for three doses—recovery follows whether sweating occurs or not.

**Formulas from *Extensive Relief Remedies***
For *cold damage* of both *yin* and *yang* toxins, *Black Dragon Elixir*: Take one *liang* of imported *liuhuang*, pound with a willow mallet for three days; take one *liang* of *badou* (count the shells), and two *sheng* of a wok. First place the *liuhuang* to cover the wok’s base, then add the *badou*, and cover with more *liuhuang*. Pour in half a *sheng* of strong vinegar, seal tightly with a lid, and further seal the edges with wet paper to prevent steam escape. When the paper dries, remoisten with vinegar. Heat with a gentle flame, keeping watch; when half the *badou* inside crackles, immediately remove the wok from the fire, transfer to a mortar, and pound finely. Add a small amount of rice vinegar and steamed cake, pound again until cool enough to form pills the size of a *chicken’s head*.

For *yin* toxin, decoct forty-nine *jiaomu* grains and two stalks of *cong bai* in one cup of water to six parts, and swallow one pill without chewing.

For *yang* toxin, decoct forty-nine *chi* grains and two stalks of *cong bai* in one cup of water, and swallow one pill without chewing.

**Formulas from *Sun Yonghe’s Remedies***
For *yang* toxin entering the stomach with frequent bloody stool and unbearable pain: Take five large *yujin* roots and one *zaojiazi*-sized *niuhuang*, grind separately, then combine as a powder. For each dose, decoct in one cup of vinegar *jiang* water to three boils, and consume warm.

**Formulas from *Sun Zhao’s Oral Instructions***
For *yin* toxin *cold damage* with reversal cold of the limbs, deep and faint pulse, headache, and lumbar heaviness, also treating *yin* toxin, *ke ni* (hiccup-reversal), and similar conditions: Take equal parts *chuan wutou* and *ganjiang*, grind coarsely, stir-fry until discolored, cool, then grind finely. For each *qian*, decoct in one cup of water with a pinch of salt to half a cup, and consume warm.

Another formula for *yin* excess obstructing *yang* in *cold damage*, where the patient is vexingly hot yet unwilling to drink water: *Thunderbolt Powder* is appropriate. Take one *fuzi*, burn to ash while preserving its nature, grind to powder, and administer with honey water in a single dose—this dispels cold *qi*, allowing *heat qi* to ascend and induce sweating for recovery.

**Formulas from *Sagely Benevolence Remedies***
For *yin* toxin *cold damage* with reversal cold of the limbs, moxibustion is advisable: Take one *sheng* of *wuzhuyu*, mix evenly with wine, fill two silk pouches, steam until extremely hot, and apply to the soles of the feet. Discontinue once *qi* flows smoothly and warmth is evenly restored—this method has been repeatedly verified.

**Tang Dynasty: Cui Yuanliang’s Remedy**
For seasonal epidemic with jaundice, frenzied heart vexation, and delirium: Take one large yellow *gualou*, soak in nine *ge* of freshly drawn water; strain the juice, add half a large *ge* of honey and eight *fen* of *poxiao*, stir until dissolved, and divide into two doses—recovery follows.

**Formulas from *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library***
For seasonal epidemic of four or five days’ duration with *jiexiong* (chest bind), fullness, pain, and high fever: Take one *liang* of *kushen*, slice, decoct in two *sheng* of vinegar to one *sheng* and two *ge*, and consume entirely—recovery follows vomiting. For seasonal epidemic *toxin disease*, only *kushen* and vinegar remedies resolve it, and warming to induce sweating brings recovery.

Another formula for urgent relief of post-epidemic *ou ni* (vomiting-reversal) with inability to retain food: Prepare sheep’s liver as for eating, consume raw and plain—three doses suffice to stop it.

Another formula: Take one chicken egg, boil for three to five boils, remove and soak in water until the exterior is cooked but the interior remains warm, then swallow—effective.

**Formulas from *Sagely Benevolence Remedies***
For seasonal epidemic with *ou ni* (vomiting-reversal) and inability to retain food: Take half a *liang* of *banxia*, soak and wash seven times in hot water to remove sliminess, and one *liang* of fresh ginger; chop together, decoct in one large cup of water to six parts, remove dregs, divide into two doses, and consume warm at any time.

**Formulas from *Master Shen’s Remedies***
For incessant *wa* (belching) in *cold damage*: Wash *banxia* thoroughly, dry, grind to powder, and take one *qianbi* with fresh ginger decoction.

**Formulas from *Essential Relief for the Multitudes***
For unremitting cough and hiccup in *cold damage*, and persistent *yue ni* (hiccup-reversal): Take one *liang* of *xiang* and one *liang* of dried *shi di*, bake dry, grind to powder, and take one *qian* with ginseng decoction at any time.

**Formulas from *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library***
For seasonal epidemic *toxin disease* with nosebleed due to *heat toxin*, where blood descends in several *sheng*: Grind fine *mo* (ink), form pills with egg white the size of *wutong* seeds, and take ten to twenty pills with fresh *dihuang* juice. Repeat after the time it takes to walk five *li*.

Another remedy for *cold damage* of eight or nine to over ten days’ duration with severe vexing thirst, overwhelming heat, and sores in the *sanjiao*, often with diarrhea, gaping mouth, protruding tongue, panting, eye erosion, oral and nasal sores, delirious speech, and loss of recognition: [Formula for] eliminating *heat toxin* and stopping dysentery.

Dragon bone, half a *jin*, crush and boil in one *dou* of water to yield four *sheng*; submerge in a well to chill. Take five *ge* at a time, gradually increasing the dose, and drink freely—especially suitable for the elderly and children.

**Master Mei’s Formulas**: For unremitting dysentery with pus and blood following *heat disease*, with inability to eat: Take white dragon bone powder, one *fangcunbi* mixed with rice broth.

**Dietary Therapy**: For *heat toxin* with bloody stool in *cold damage*: Grind antelope horn to powder and ingest to resolve.

Another remedy for *mounting qi*.

**Imperial Grace Formulas**: For *cold damage* with *fox delusion*, where *toxin* erodes the lower body and the anus becomes like [ ], with unceasing pain and itching: Take half a *liang* of realgar, place in a wide-mouthed jar filled with ash (as for incense burning), ignite the realgar, and when smoke arises, fumigate the afflicted area.

Another formula for *cold damage* with [ ] sores in the lower body: Stir-fry three *liang* of mume flesh until dry, pound to powder, and form pills with refined honey the size of *wutong* seeds. Take ten pills before meals with a decoction of pomegranate root bark.

**Formulas from *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library***: Master Cui’s remedy for *cold damage* with limbs so painful they seem about to detach: Boil sheep dung to obtain juice and pour it over the patient to resolve. Also treats seasonal epidemics with heat and swelling of the scrotum and penis—may also boil *huangbo* and the like to wash the area.

**Master Mei’s Formulas**: For *cold damage* with pea-like sores that have not yet suppurated: Grind *mangxiao*, mix with pig bile, and apply topically for effect.

**Tested Later Formulas**: For seasonal epidemic with pea-like sores or red sores that have not erupted, with vexation, manic agitation, panting, delirious speech, or visions of ghosts and spirits: Grind one *qian* of borneol, gradually mix with pig’s heart blood, and form pills the size of *chicken’s-head fruit*. Take one pill with a *zicao* decoction; soon the heart and spirit will settle, sleep will come, and sores will erupt normally—thereafter, rest and convalesce to recover.

**Drug Properties Treatise** states: *Huzhang* treats great heat with vexation and agitation, stops thirst, disinhibits urination, and suppresses all *heat toxin*. In summer, decoct with licorice—its color becomes amber-like and lovely, fit for storage. When tasted, it is sweet and fine. Place the decoction in a jar, chill in a well until it becomes as cold as water, and store in white porcelain or silver vessels. Sip it like tea; contemporaries call it *cold drink* and hold it in higher esteem than tea. It can break menstrual block in women—pound, steep in wine, and take regularly. Pregnant women must not take it, as it breaks the blood.

**Formulas for Seasonal Epidemic Relapse and Overstrain (Chapter Fourteen)**
For all *toxin diseases* after recovery, within one hundred days, prohibit pork, dog, and mutton, as they harm the blood; also avoid fatty fish, long-stored grease, and dried fish, as they will invariably cause severe dysentery—once diarrhea begins, it cannot be saved. Further prohibit wheat-based foods, garlic, leeks, scallions, raw vegetables, and shrimp [ ], as consuming these often leads to relapse, making treatment difficult and causing repeated outbreaks in subsequent years.

**Formulas for Overstrain After Severe Illness, Early Exertion, or Excessive Eating and Drinking Leading to Mortal Danger**
Burn tortoise plastron and take one *fangcunbi*.

Another formula: Take a small amount of *hufen* with water.

Another formula: Mix three *sheng* of powder with warm water and ingest; cover thickly to induce sweating.

Another formula: Boil one handful of dried perilla in five *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*, and consume entirely. If no dried perilla is available, fresh may be used, adding four *liang* of fresh ginger and one *sheng* of fermented soybeans.

Another formula: Take fourteen double-pointed rat droppings, half a *sheng* of fermented soybeans, and boil in three *sheng* of water until half remains; consume at once. Cover warmly to induce sweating to resolve. Adding one *sheng* of hemp seeds and one *sheng* of water enhances the effect. May also add *zhishi* and a handful of scallion whites.

Another formula: Crush and roast chicken eggshells until yellow-black, grind to fine powder, and take one *ge* with hot water; cover warmly to induce sweating.

Another formula: Boil two *liang* each of *dahuang* and *mahuang*, fourteen *zhizi* kernels, and one *sheng* of fermented soybeans in five *sheng* of water to yield three *sheng*; divide and take twice to induce slight sweating and diarrhea.

Another formula: Thickly decoct *ganpi* and ingest—*lugen* is also excellent.

For relapse due to excessive exertion: Burn cooked rice, sift to powder, and take one *fangcunbi* for effect.

**Formulas for Relapse from Sexual Intercourse, with Swollen Testicles or Retraction into the Abdomen, Abdominal Colic, or Urinary Block**
Burn a woman’s menstrual cloth and take one *fangcunbi*.

Another formula: Take one [ ] egg, strike it thirty-six times, place at the door, and have the patient run until panting; then pierce below the ribs to draw one *sheng* of blood, mix with one *sheng* of wine, and drink. If no [ ] is available, take the blood alone, but avoid cold immediately afterward. Use *jia* [ ].

Another formula: Cover the man with the clothing of the woman with whom he had intercourse for the time it takes to eat a meal to revive.

Another formula: Take the shinbone and blood of *jia* [ ], mix with wine, and drink to resolve.

Another formula: Scrape two *sheng* of green bamboo shavings, boil in three *sheng* of water until it bubbles five or six times, then strain and discard the dregs. Take the bamboo shaving decoction warm. This formula also broadly treats *overstrain relapse*.

Another formula: Grind one *fen* of *fanshi* and three *fen* of *xiaoshi* to powder, mix with barley porridge water, and take one *fangcunbi* at a time—*heat toxin* will exit with urine and stool.

Another formula: Take a large handful of knotweed seeds, crush in water to extract juice, and drink one *sheng*. If dried, thickly extract the juice and ingest. Pound scallion bulbs, mix with bitter wine, and take—also excellent.

Another formula: Extract juice from several *sheng* of earthworms and ingest for effect.

If a recovered man has intercourse with a sick woman, or a recovered woman with a sick man, the healthy partner contracts *yin exchange*, while the sick partner relapses—those who relapse will surely die.

For sudden *yin exchange* disease, whether in men or women with *warm disease*, even if recovered for several decades, if blood vessels remain unharmonized and *heat toxin* lingers, intercourse will transmit the disease, called *yin exchange*, which kills more swiftly than seasonal epidemics—treat urgently.

The patient experiences bodily heaviness, acute heat in the lower abdomen, swelling ascending to the chest, inability to lift the head due to its weight, the growth of *membranous obstructions* in the eyes, and cramping of the knees and shins so severe as to approach death. The following formula may be used:

Take a woman’s undergarment that has touched her private parts, cut a portion, burn it to ash, and ingest one *square-inch spoonful* three times daily. If urination becomes smooth and the genitals show slight swelling, recovery is imminent. A young girl’s undergarment is also effective. If the patient is female, a man’s undergarment may be used instead.

Another formula: Take fourteen *mouse droppings* (pointed at both ends), one handful of indigo, and five *sheng* of water. Boil to reduce to two *sheng* and ingest the entire decoction, then cover warmly to induce sweating.

Another formula: Take twenty-four earthworms and one *dou* of water. Boil to reduce to three *sheng* and ingest in one dose, then induce sweating—this is also effective.

Another formula: Grind four *liang* of dried ginger into powder, mix with hot water, and ingest at once. Cover warmly to induce sweating, and cease once relief is obtained.

Another formula: At the first sign of illness in a man, immediately apply moxibustion to the genitals—thirty-seven cones. If the condition persists, increase to one hundred cones, and recovery will follow. The eyes will remain unharmed, and genital sores will return to normal.

When two men or two women engage in intercourse, they do not transmit *yin exchange* to one another; thus, the term *exchange* refers to the interchange of yin and yang.

To prevent relapse in a convalescent patient, take twenty fingernail clippings from a woman’s hands and feet, along with a one-*chi* length of the lower hem of her undergarment. Burn to ash and ingest with wine or rice broth.

After recovering from a severe illness, even slight exertion may cause nosebleeds. Grind ten parts oyster shell and five parts gypsum into powder and ingest one *square-inch spoonful* with wine three or four times daily. Alternatively, form into honeyed pills the size of *wutong* seeds and ingest accordingly.

After recovering from a severe illness, excessive sweating—including from the eyes—may occur. Use equal parts eucommia bark and oyster shell, ground into powder. Ingest five *spoonfuls* with water before bedtime; if sweating persists, repeat the dose.

Another formula: Grind two *liang* each of licorice and gypsum into powder. Ingest one *square-inch spoonful* with fermented rice water twice daily to resolve the condition.

Another formula: Grind dragon bone, oyster shell, and ephedra root into powder, mix with talcum, and dust the body—this is highly effective.

For post-recovery restlessness, insomnia, eye pain, and vexation:
Take seven *ge* of fermented soybeans and fourteen black plums. Boil the plums in four *sheng* of water until reduced to two and a half *sheng*, then add the soybeans and boil to one and a half *sheng*. Divide into two doses. If black plums are unavailable, use fourteen gardenia fruits instead.

Another formula: Boil four *liang* of coptis, two *liang* of peony, one *liang* of scutellaria, and three small sticks of donkey-hide gelatin in six *sheng* of water until reduced to three *sheng*. Divide into three doses. Two egg yolks may also be added.

Another formula: Take one *dan* of flowing water from a thousand-*li* source, agitate it ten thousand times, then take two and a half *dou*. Wash two *liang* of pinellia, add one *dou* of glutinous rice and four *liang* of poria, and boil to five *sheng*. Divide into five doses.

**Supplementary Formula (from *Master Mei’s Prescriptions*)**:
For post-recovery relapse triggered by intercourse, causing extreme debility, inability to open the eyes, or speechlessness:
Boil thirty gardenia fruits in three *sheng* of water until reduced to one *sheng* and ingest.

---

**Chapter Fifteen: Formulas for Miasma, Epidemics, Warm Toxins, and Pestilence**

**Dried Powder to Ward Off Epidemics**:
Take one *liang* each of hemp seeds, cypress seeds, dried ginger, and asarum, along with half a *liang* of prepared aconite. Grind into powder, and at dawn, have each household member ingest one *square-inch spoonful* with well water. In severe epidemics, take three doses daily.

**Lord Lao’s Divine White Powder**:
Grind one *liang* of atractylodes, three *liang* of aconite, four *liang* of Sichuan aconite, two and a half *liang* of platycodon, and one *liang* of asarum into powder. At dawn, ingest one *qian-spoonful*. If one household prepares this, an entire village will remain free of illness. Carrying it while traveling will dispel pathogenic qi upon encounter. If others fall ill, administer one *square-inch spoonful* with warm wine. For those ill for four or five days, boil one *spoonful* in three *sheng* of water, ingest one *sheng*, and cover to induce sweating.

**Red Powder Formula**:
Grind five *fen* each of moutan bark and prepared gleditsia pods, three *fen* each of asarum, dried ginger, and aconite, two *fen* of cinnamon bark, four *fen* of true pearl, and four *fen* of *zhizhu* into powder. At the first sign of stiffness or malaise, insert a small amount into the nostrils to induce vomiting. Ingest one *square-inch spoonful* with warm wine, cover to induce sweating, and recovery will follow. When traveling at dawn or night or visiting the sick, dusting the body with a small amount is also beneficial. For livestock epidemics, place one *spoonful* under the tongue and administer urine as a wash three or four times daily—highly effective.

**Mountain Miasma Powder**:
To ward off mountain miasma and malignant qi, or when encountering black fog, oppressive vapors, or warm winds from the southwest—all harbingers of epidemics:
Grind five *fen* each of ephedra and Sichuan pepper, three *fen* of Sichuan aconite, and one *fen* each of asarum, atractylodes, saposhnikovia, platycodon, cinnamon bark, and dried ginger into powder. At dawn, ingest one *spoonful* with wine. Particularly effective for those exposed to toxic qi while traveling through mist.

**Taiyi Flowing Gold Formula**:
Grind three *liang* of realgar, two *liang* of orpiment, one and a half *liang* each of alum and *ghost arrows*, and two *liang* of goat horn into powder. Store one *liang* in a triangular crimson pouch, wear it over the heart, and hang it on doorways. On the first day of the month, wrap one *knife-point* of the powder in blue cloth, burn it in the courtyard, and have the sick inhale the fumes to recover.

**Epidemic Warding Pill**:
Grind equal parts realgar, cinnabar, croton seeds, alum, aconite, and dried ginger into powder, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of sesame seeds. At dawn, face the sun and swallow one pill daily for nine days to remain disease-free.

**Common Powder for Warding Off Warm Diseases**:
Grind one *fen* each of true pearl and cinnamon bark, three *fen* of fritillaria (roasted), and three *fen* of egg white (roasted until yellow-black) into powder. Ingest one *square-inch spoonful* on New Year’s Day. If illnesses are prevalent that year, take it on the first and fifteenth of each month. Those already ill will experience significant improvement.

**Tiger-Head Ghost-Killing Formula**:
Five *liang* of tiger skull bone, one and a half *liang* each of cinnabar, realgar, and orpiment, one *liang* each of *podophyllum*, *Gleditsia sinensis*, and *Ligusticum sinense*; grind into powder, mix with beeswax and honey to form pellets the size of bullets, store in a crimson pouch, and tie to the arm—left for men, right for women. Hang one in each corner of the house. On the nights of the new and full moon, burn one pellet in the courtyard at midnight. An alternate formula includes *Acorus calamus* and *Veratrum* but omits tiger skull, *podophyllum*, and *Gleditsia sinensis*; grind into powder and carry on the person.

**Zhao Quan’s Yellow Ointment Formula**:
One *liang* each of rhubarb, aconite, *Asarum*, dried ginger, Sichuan pepper, and cinnamon; eighty croton seeds (remove kernels and husks). Grind finely, soak in bitter wine overnight, then cook with two *jin* of lard rendered in the twelfth lunar month, stirring three times up and three times down. Strain, store in a honeyed vessel. At the first sign of sudden flush or fever, take one pill the size of a *wu* seed; if unresolved, take another. Rubbing the ointment over the body with heated hands hundreds of times is also effective. It treats *zei*-wind* and wandering qi in the skin. Prepare in advance for immediate use.

**Single-Ingredient Remedies**:
- Take the southeast branch of a cypress tree from the southwest corner of a village altar, dry in the sun, grind into powder, and ingest one *square-inch spoonful* for instant recovery.
- On the first *yin* day of the first lunar month, grind *Dysosma versipellis* into powder, store in a triangular pouch, and hang on the door or above the bed for great fortune.
- Grind two *liang* of *Ma-ti-wood* into powder, carry in a crimson pouch—left for men, right for women.
- On the first day of the first lunar month and in the seventh month, swallow fourteen sesame seeds and fourteen small beans. Alternatively, cast fourteen of each into a well.
- Have a woman cast two aconite roots and seven small beans into a well.
- On the Winter Solstice, prepare a red rooster as preserved meat; by the Start of Spring, consume it entirely without sharing.
- On a day in the second lunar month, take a finger-thick root from an eastward-growing mulberry tree and hang it above the door; each person may also carry one.
- Bury a magpie in front of the latrine.
- To prevent contagion of warm diseases, cut a lock of hair to seven inches and secretly place it under the sick person’s mat.
- Measure the walls of the sick person’s room with a string, then tie a knot in it.
- Secretly moxa each corner of the sick person’s bed with one *zhuang* of mugwort without their knowledge.
- Place small beans in a new cloth pouch, submerge in a well for three days, then remove. Men in the household take ten beans; women take twenty.
- Grind the excrement of a *borer* from a peach tree into powder and ingest one *square-inch spoonful*.
- Burn a pinch of dried salted fish head (three fingers’ worth), mix with seven small beans, and grind into powder for ingestion; women use twenty-seven beans.
- Steep fermented soybeans in wine mixed with soil and consume regularly.
- Secretly place a cruc

**Remedies for Malarial Diseases (Section Sixteen)**

For malarial disease: Take fourteen *shimu* (pill bugs) and fourteen fermented soybeans, pound together, and blend. Take two pills when the episode has not yet begun, and one pill when it is about to strike.

Another remedy: Take a handful of sweet wormwood, steep in two *sheng* of water, wring out the juice, and consume it all.

Another remedy: Burn a single clove of *dufu* garlic over white charcoal, grind into powder, and take one *square-inch spoonful*.

Another remedy: On the fifth day of the fifth month, take a slice of garlic, peel and split it open, then carve with a knife to hold one *badou* (croton seed). Remove the heart and skin of the *badou*, place it inside the garlic, secure with bamboo, and roast over fire until hot. Pound into three pills. Take one pill before the episode begins; if it does not cease, take another.

Another remedy: Take one spider, seal it tightly in a reed tube, and tie the tube around the neck. Remove it only after the episode has passed.

Another remedy: At sunrise, face east and bow twice. Then kneel upright, clasp hands toward the sun, and hold your breath. Use ink to mark each ear seven times, then write with cinnabar on the tongue, saying, “Die on the *zi* day.” Bow twice again, leave without looking back, lie down calmly, and refrain from eating. The episode will cease after its time has passed.

Another remedy: Boil a large amount of fermented soybean broth, drink several *sheng* to induce heavy vomiting, and the disease will be cured.

Another remedy: Place one spider in cooked rice, form into a pill, and swallow it.

Another remedy: When the episode is about to begin, pound large *fuzi* (aconite) into powder, mix with bitter wine, and apply to the back.

Another remedy: Take four *shimu* larvae, wrap each in malt sugar, and swallow as pills to immediately cease the episode.

Another remedy: Pound three *liang* of *changshan* (dichroa root) into fine powder, mix with one *liang* of *zhen dan* (cinnabar) and white honey, and pound one hundred times to form pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take three pills before the episode, three at mid-episode, and three before sleep. There is no case where this does not cease the disease; it is consistently effective.

Another remedy: Open the mouth wide, measure the upper and lower lips with a string, then measure from the string to the heart. Moxa one hundred *zhuang* at this measured point below, and moxa fifty *zhuang* at the center of the spine. After the episode has passed, moxa twenty *zhuang*.

Another remedy: Split a large soybean, remove the skin, and inscribe one half with the character for “sun” and the other with “moon.” Hold the “sun” in the left hand and the “moon” in the right, swallow them facing the sun, and do not let others know.

Another remedy: Take three *liang* of *zaojia* (Chinese honey locust), remove the skin and roast, add one *liang* of *badou*, remove the heart and skin, pound together, and form pills the size of large soybeans. Take one pill per dose.

Another remedy: Take one *badou*, remove the heart and skin, and one piece of *shegong* (arrowhead) the size of a *badou*, along with one jujube (peeled). Pound together into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take one pill at the onset of each episode.

Another remedy: Take equal parts *changshan*, *zhimu* (anemarrhena), *gancao* (licorice), and *mahuang* (ephedra), pound into powder, mix with honey, and form pills the size of large soybeans. Take three pills before the episode to ensure it passes completely.

Another remedy: Take three *liang* of *changshan* and half a *liang* of *gancao*, boil in half a *sheng* each of water and wine, and reduce to half a *sheng*. Take one dose before the episode begins, and finish three doses by the time the episode strikes.

Another remedy: Steep three *liang* of *changshan* in three *sheng* of wine for two or three days. At dawn, take three *ge* (a measure), and induce vomiting. Take another two *ge* at the onset of the episode, and it will cease. Aged wine is also effective; in urgent cases, it may be boiled.

Another remedy: Take three *liang* of *changshan* and three hundred grains of *shu* millet, boil in six *sheng* of water, and reduce to three *sheng*. Divide and consume before the episode begins.

Another remedy: If the episodes occur irregularly with heat and vexation in the heart, take two *liang* of *changshan* and one and a half *liang* of *gancao*, boil in six *sheng* of water, and reduce to two *sheng*. Divide into two doses and consume to induce rapid vomiting, then cease. Do not eat or drink.

For chronic malaria that does not cease: Take three *liang* of *changshan*, one *liang* of roasted *biejia* (turtle shell), one *liang* of *shengma* (cimicifuga), one *liang* of *fuzi*, and one *liang* of *wuzeigu* (cuttlefish bone). Steep in six *sheng* of wine near a small fire overnight. Take one *ge* per dose, and take several doses before the episode strikes.

Another remedy: Take one *liang* each of *hualu* (flowering reed) and *zaojia*, roast, and add twenty-five *badou*. Pound together, stir-fry until yellow, and follow the method to pound into pills the size of small soybeans with honey. Take one pill on an empty stomach, one before the episode, and one at the onset. Do not eat or drink.

Another remedy: Take a handful of *niuxi* (achyranthes) stems and leaves, chop, and steep in three *sheng* of wine. Consume until there is a slight wine scent. If the disease does not cease, repeat the process, but do not exceed three doses.

Another remedy: Grind one *square-inch spoonful* of *longgu* (dragon bone) into powder. One hour before the episode, boil in one and a half *sheng* of wine for three boils, then consume while hot. Cover to induce sweating, and it will be effective immediately.

Another remedy: Take three *liang* of *changshan*, half a *liang* of *gancao*, and one *liang* of *zhimu*, pound into powder, and form pills with honey. At the onset of the episode, take ten pills the size of *wutong* seeds. For subsequent doses, reduce to seven or eight pills, then five or six pills, and the disease will be cured.

Another remedy: Two hours before the episode, place a charcoal fire under the bed to warm the spine and feet thoroughly. Cover with blankets, and cease after the episode has passed. This treats cases where cold precedes heat.

Another remedy: Roast *biejia* in advance, pound into powder, and take one *square-inch spoonful* in three doses at the onset of the episode. Moxa with fire, and there is no case where the disease does not cease.

Another remedy: Take three *liang* of *changshan*, pound into powder, and mix with egg white to form pills. Take thirty pills on an empty stomach, thirty pills long after eating, and thirty pills at the onset of the episode. Whether vomiting occurs or not, do not eat or drink from the time of taking the medicine until after the episode has passed.

For warm malaria with loss of appetite: Take two *liang* each of *zhimu*, roasted *biejia*, and *changshan*, three *liang* of *digupi* (wolfberry root bark), one *sheng* of chopped bamboo leaves, and four *liang* of *shigao* (gypsum). Boil in seven *sheng* of water and reduce to two *sheng* and five *ge*. Divide into three warm doses.

Avoid garlic, hot noodles, pork, and fish.

For miasmic malaria: Take three *liang* each of *changshan*, *huanglian* (coptis), and roasted *chi* (fermented soybeans), two *liang* of *fuzi* (aconite, blast-fried). Pound into powder, form honey pills, and take four pills on an empty stomach, three pills at the onset of the episode, swallowing with water. Do not eat from the time of taking the medicine until after the episode has passed.

If accompanied by various dysenteries: Take three *liang* each of *huanglian* and *xijiao* (rhinoceros horn), two *liang* each of *muli* (oyster shell) and roasted *xiangchi* (fermented soybeans), and four *liang* of *longgu* (dragon bone). Pound into powder, form honey pills, and take forty pills twice daily, swallowing with water.

For malaria with no fixed onset: Take two *liang* of *changshan*, one and a half *liang* of *gancao* (licorice), and five *ge* of *chi* (fermented soybeans). Wrap in silk, boil in six *sheng* of water, and reduce to three *sheng*. Take in two doses to induce prompt vomiting.

For malaria of any duration, even up to thirty years: Take three *liang* each of *changshan* and *huanglian*, steep in one *dou* of wine overnight, then boil in an earthenware pot in the morning to reduce to six *sheng*. Take eight *ge* per dose, ensuring three doses before the onset of the episode. If hot, vomiting will occur; if cold, diarrhea will follow. No case will fail to be cured. Half the formula suffices.

For chronic labor malaria unresponsive to various treatments: Take a large handful of fresh *niuxi* (achyranthes), boil in six *sheng* of water, and reduce to two *sheng*. Take one dose on an empty stomach and another at the onset of the episode.

To ward off all malaria: On the day of onset, hold a rooster and make it crow loudly at the same time—no case will fail to be cured.

Another remedy: Before the onset, lie facing south. At the five centers (palms, soles, and crown) and the forehead and tongue—seven places in total—hold the breath and write the character for "ghost."

Incantation method: On the day of onset, hold a stone by the water’s edge and chant in one breath: *"Yuanyuan yuanyuan, xinglu fei nan, zhuoqu nuegui, song yu heguan. Jiji ru lüling."* Cast the stone into the water without looking back.

For all malaria, the *Wumei* (mume) pill formula: Two *liang* of *gancao*, two *liang* each of roasted *wumei* (mume) flesh, *renshen* (ginseng), *guixin* (cinnamon bark), *roucongrong* (cistanche), *zhimu*, and *mudan* (moutan), three *liang* each of *changshan*, *shengma* (cimicifuga), roasted *taoren* (peach kernel, peeled and pitted), and roasted *wudoupi* (black soybean skin). Grind the *taoren* separately and add when forming pills. Pound with a mortar and pestle ten thousand times, form honey pills, and take thirty pills with wine at dawn on the day of onset, forty pills at daybreak, forty pills at the onset, forty pills on an empty stomach on non-onset days, and thirty pills in the evening. No case will fail to be cured. Take slowly. After ten days, eat fatty meat to induce a recurrence.

For visible malaria: Take two parts roasted *bailvti* (white donkey hoof), four parts *dahuang* (rhubarb), three parts *lüdou* (mung beans), two parts *pishuang* (arsenic trioxide), half a part *guangmingsha* (cinnabar), and one part *xionghuang* (realgar). Pound into powder, form honey pills the size of *wutou* seeds, and take two pills with cold water at daybreak on the day of onset. Avoid oil for seven days.

**Additional Formulas**
From *Waitai Miyao*: For unrelenting malaria, take equal parts *ganjiang* (dried ginger) and *gaoliangjiang* (galangal), grind into powder, and take one *qian* per dose, boiled in one *zhongzhan* of water until reduced to seven parts.

From *Shenghui Fang*: For chronic malaria, consumptive malaria, and miasmic malaria, take three *liang* of *biejia* (turtle shell), coat with suet, roast until yellow, remove the rim, and grind into powder. Take two *qianbi* with warm wine at the onset of the episode.

For malaria: Take one hundred *taoren* (peach kernels), remove the skin and tips, grind finely in a mortar without contact with unboiled water, and form a paste. Add three *qian* of *huangdan* (yellow lead oxide) and form pills the size of *wutou* seeds. Take three pills on the day of onset, swallowing with warm wine while facing north. If wine is not consumed, well-drawn water may be used instead. Prepare on the fifth day of the fifth lunar month at noon. Avoid chickens, dogs, and women during preparation.

Another formula: Take any amount of *xiaosuan* (garlic), grind thoroughly, mix with a small amount of *huangdan* until cohesive, and form pills the size of *jitou* (foxnut). Once dry, take one pill with freshly drawn water while facing east. Most effective.

**Chapter Seventeen: Remedies for Sudden Onset of Manic-Depressive Illness**

For sudden manic illness: Moxa three cones at the center of the penis. Recovery follows when urination becomes unobstructed.

Another remedy: Moxa three cones on the penis and fourteen cones at the seam below the scrotum.

Another remedy: Moxa three cones on each nipple, seven cones at the base of the big toe where the hairs converge, and seven cones at the base of the little toe.

Another remedy: Take one *sheng* of *tingli* (lepidium seed), pound three thousand times, hang a white dog upside down, strike it with a stick to draw blood, and mix with the *tingli* powder. Take one pill the size of a hemp seed, three doses to cure.

Another remedy: Steep three *sheng* of *langdang* (henbane) seeds in five *sheng* of wine, remove and dry, repeating until the wine is exhausted. Pound into powder and take one *qianbi* three times daily. Do not exceed the dose, as it may worsen mania.

Another formula from *Xiaopin*: The *Langdang* powder for manic-depressive illness. Take three *sheng* of *langdang* seeds, grind into powder, steep in one *sheng* of wine for several days, remove, pound, mix with the original liquid, strain, and simmer over hot water until it can be formed into pills. Take three pills the size of small beans three times daily. The face and mouth will feel tight, and there may be a sensation of insects moving in the head, with redness appearing on the forehead, hands, and feet—these are signs of impending recovery. If not observed, continue until the formula is finished.

Another remedy: Grind *fangkui* (ledebouriella) and take one to two *daogui* with warm wine. Numbness and slight insensitivity of the body indicate efficacy.

Another remedy: Burn the rope of a person who died by hanging and take three pinches of the ash.

Generally, for manic illness: When an episode occurs, the patient falls to the ground, foams at the mouth, loses consciousness, and upon being forcibly lifted, behaves wildly, even soiling themselves. Such cases are difficult to treat.

For sudden mania: Burn a toad, pound into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* three times daily with wine.

Another remedy: Lay the patient on the ground and pour cold water on their face continuously for an entire day.

For sudden raving or ghostly speech: Insert a needle slightly under the toenail of the big toe to stop the symptoms.

Another remedy: Bind the patient’s two hands tightly together with a steamer’s belt, then apply moxibustion to both flanks. Grasp the elbow tips and cauterize both points simultaneously, seven cones each. After a short while, the demon will speak its name and beg to leave. Gently question it, then untie the hands.

Generally, when mania erupts, the patient may run wildly or claim exalted status, calling themselves divine or sacred. In all such cases, apply moxibustion extensively to achieve lasting recovery. If the patient instead weeps, moans, or sighs, this indicates demonic possession rather than mania, and should be treated according to methods for demonic afflictions.

*The Effective Remedies of Recent Times* states: Burn paper used in silkworm rearing to ash, and take with wine or water to cure wind-induced mania.

**Additional Remedies**
*From the *Doumen Prescriptions*:* To treat epilepsy, apply moxibustion to the perineum at the midpoint between the anus and scrotum, one cone per year of age.

*From the *Thousand Gold Prescriptions*:* For wind-induced epilepsy and all manner of illnesses, boil four *sheng* of hemp seeds in six *sheng* of water over high heat until the seeds split. Strain and reduce to seven *ge*, then take on an empty stomach at dawn. The patient may experience episodes, remain silent, or speak excessively—do not be alarmed. Simply massage their hands and feet until they calm. Three doses will bring recovery.

Another remedy: For sudden onset of manic possession—where the patient tears their hair, screams wildly, and attempts to harm others without regard for fire or water—form *ku shen* (sophora root) into pills the size of firmiana seeds with honey. Take ten pills per dose with mint decoction.

*From the *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library*:* For wind-induced epilepsy with pulling pain in the flanks, episodes of vomiting, and tinnitus like cicadas, remove the heart and peel of *tian men dong* (asparagus root), dry in the sun, grind to powder, and take one *fangcunbi* with wine. Prolonged use also promotes longevity.

*From the *Extensive Beneficial Prescriptions*:* For heat-induced wind epilepsy, thoroughly grind *lan long jiao* (decayed dragon’s horn) and take two *ge* of the thick juice before meals, twice daily.

*From the *Proven Later Prescriptions*:* For adults and children suffering long-term wind epilepsy, throat-constricting coughs, or full-body wind rashes with sudden drooling: This remedy induces minimal vomiting, only expelling saliva. For children, administer one *zi*. Grind *gua di* (melon stalk) to a fine powder without limit. Adults take one *zi*; those under fifteen or the elderly and weak take half. Administer in the morning with well-flower water, and have the patient hold a piece of rock sugar in their mouth. After a while, saliva will flow like water. In chronic cases, once all saliva is expelled, a piece resembling a saliva cloth will float on the water like a mirror. When the saliva is fully drained, consume congee for a day or two. If vomiting becomes excessive and the patient weakens, drink a cup of musk decoction to stop it. Finely chop musk and take with warm water.

Formerly, the Minister of the Court of Imperial Sacrifices suffered from dizziness and took this remedy, expelling saliva with success.

*The Miscellaneous Records of Emperor Ming* states: During the Kaiyuan era, a renowned physician named Ji Peng could diagnose illness by observing a patient’s complexion and speech, without needing to take their pulse. The emperor, having heard of him, summoned him to the palace to examine a concubine who, every afternoon, would laugh, sing, weep, and scream as if mad, yet could not stand. Ji Peng observed her and said: “This must have resulted from overeating followed by sudden exertion, causing her to collapse.” He administered a cloud-mother decoction, had her sleep deeply, and upon waking, her suffering was gone. When asked, she recounted: “During the grand celebration for Princess Taihua’s birth, the palace hosted a grand musical performance. I was the lead singer and, fearing my voice would not be clear and sustained, ate a full bowl of pig’s trotter stew before performing. After singing a long piece, I felt intense heat in my chest. While playing on the terrace, I fell from a height. It was a long while before I regained consciousness, and since then, I have suffered from madness and been unable to stand.”

**Chapter Eighteen: Remedies for Sudden Fright, Demonic Possession, and Confusion**

For palpitations due to heart deficiency: Grind equal parts *ma huang* (ephedra) and *ban xia* (pinellia), form into honey pills, and take three pills the size of soybeans, twice daily, gradually increasing the dose. Wash *ban xia* to remove slipperiness and dry before use.

For distress caused by shock, sorrow, or terror—such as sudden loss of wealth, or pent-up frustration leading to mental disarray, erratic behavior, and restlessness: Combine two *liang* each of *long gu* (dragon bone), *yuan zhi* (polygala), *fu shen* (poria spirit), *fang feng* (saposhnikovia), and *mu li* (oyster shell); seven *liang* of *gan cao* (licorice); and seven *da zao* (jujubes). Boil in eight *sheng* of water, reduce to two *sheng*, and divide into two doses. Prepare daily until recovery.

Another remedy: Four *liang* each of *fu ling* (poria) and *gan di huang* (dried rehmannia); three *liang* each of *ren shen* (ginseng) and *gui* (cinnamon); two *liang* of *gan cao*; one *sheng* of *mai men dong* (ophiopogon), with the heart removed; six *liang* of *ban xia*, washed to remove slipperiness; and one *jin* of *sheng jiang* (fresh ginger). Boil in one *dou* of water with the blood and liver of a black hen, reduce to three *sheng*, and divide into four doses—three during the day and one at night. During treatment, eat lightly and avoid rich foods. Three doses will bring recovery.

Another remedy: Prepare a white rooster as for eating, cut four *liang* of *zhen zhu* (pearl) and four *liang* of *xie bai* (Chinese garlic chives), and boil in three *sheng* of water until reduced to two *sheng*. Fast overnight, then consume the entire chicken and broth at dawn.

Other calming and mind-stabilizing pills are recorded in the major prescriptions.

For sudden demonic possession with confusion and chills: Apply moxibustion to the *ren zhong* point below the nose and at the base of the thumbnail on both big toes and thumbs, seven cones each. If symptoms persist, increase to fourteen cones.

This method originally appeared in the miscellaneous treatments.

For women who communicate with demonic entities, speaking or laughing alone, or experiencing sorrow and confusion: Grind one *liang* of *xiong huang* (realgar) and mix with two *liang* of melted pine resin. Stir with a tiger’s claw until the size of a bullet, then burn in a fire basket at night. Have the woman sit over it, covering herself tightly with a blanket, leaving only her head exposed. If not cured after one attempt, repeat up to three times, after which the demon will sever ties on its own.

Another remedy: Grind one *liang* each of *xiong huang*, *ren shen* (ginseng), and *fang feng* (saposhnikovia) with one *sheng* of *wu wei zi* (schisandra). Sift and take one *fangcunbi* with well water at dawn. Three doses will bring recovery.

The master would insert five needles into the topknot of the patient’s hair. For those with manic illness, a vessel of water was prepared, covered with three layers of new red cloth, and a large knife laid horizontally atop it. Assuming a solemn demeanor, the master would call the patient forth. The afflicted would invariably attempt to rise and flee, but the master would not permit it. Instead, he would take a mouthful of water and spray it upon the patient, then exhale sharply while gazing intently—repeating this three times until the patient was thoroughly drenched. Wiping away the water, he would flick the patient’s forehead near the hairline with his finger and ask, “Do you wish to be cured?” The patient would refuse to answer, so the master would repeat the flicking twice seven times before receiving a response. Then, using a staff-like needle, he would pierce the area beneath the nose, beside the philtrum near the nostrils, leaving the needle in place. He would next insert needles into the hollows before both ear roots, again leaving them in place. Finally, he would measure one *cun* upward from the bridge of the nose into the hairline and insert a needle horizontally, then pierce straight upward from the nose into the same point. Only after these procedures would he thoroughly question the patient. Once the patient awoke in clarity and remorse, the treatment would cease.

For men or women who frequently dream of intercourse with spirits, leading to confusion and disorientation: Saw deer antler into fine shavings and take three pinches with wine, three times daily.

**Attached Remedies**
Zhang Zhongjing’s remedy for palpitations below the heart: *Ban xia* and *ma huang* pills. Grind equal parts of the two ingredients into powder, form into honey pills the size of small beans, and take three pills each time, three times daily.

*Jian Yao Ji Zhong Fang*: For unsettled heart *zang*, fright palpitations, and forgetfulness—upper diaphragm wind-heat transforming into phlegm. Grind one *liang* each of white quartz and cinnabar into powder. Take half a *qian* each time after meals and before bed, mixed with gold or silver-infused water.

For guest heat in the heart, qi obstruction between the bladder and ribs, constant morning sorrow, and unease with palpitations: Take two large *jin* of *sha cao* root, slice and roast until fragrant, then place in a raw silk pouch. Steep in three large *dou* of ash-free clear wine. In spring, soak for one day before drinking; after the tenth month, soak for seven days, keeping the vessel in a warm place. Drink one cup on an empty stomach, three or four times day and night, ensuring the wine’s influence remains continuous. Adjust dosage as needed. For those who do not drink wine, take ten *liang* of *sha cao* root, five *liang* of *gui xin*, and three *liang* of *wu yu*, grind into powder, and form into honey pills with one thousand pestle strikes, each the size of a *wu* seed. Take twenty pills on an empty stomach with wine or ginger-honey decoction, gradually increasing to thirty pills until recovery.

**Chapter Nineteen: Remedies for Sudden Wind Stroke and Acute Conditions**
For sudden wind stroke with suffocating confusion and near-death: Moxibustion at the transverse crease beneath the big toe, one cone per year of age. Another remedy is the *Xu Ming* decoction.

If the poison is acute and mobility impaired, with inner sinew tension: Moxibustion at the inner ankle. For outer sinew tension: Moxibustion above the outer ankle, twenty cones.

For swelling and numbness due to deficiency: Grind two parts *bai lian* and one part *fu zi* into powder. Take half a *dao gui* each time, up to three doses daily.

If the eyes roll upward with the pupils obscured: Moxibustion behind both outer canthi, three cones.

For inability to recognize people: Moxibustion at the tips of the floating ribs, seven cones each (the floating ribs are the curved ends of the lower ribs).

For inability to speak: Moxibustion on the second or fifth vertebra, fifty cones.

Another remedy for speechlessness appears in a later chapter.

Another remedy: Boil one *sheng* each of fermented soybeans and *zhu yu* in five *sheng* of water until two *sheng* remain. Sip gradually.

For upward-rolling eyes, lockjaw, and acute abdominal pain: Moxibustion at the first transverse crease below the scrotum, fourteen cones.

Another remedy involves consuming medicinal pastes.

For those who rage, attempt to stab or kill others, or contemplate suicide, ceaselessly cursing and speaking in ghostly tongues: Moxibustion at the red flesh at the corners of both lips, one cone each.
