Also moxa the creases of both elbows, five cones each, and the space between the shoulder blades, three cones. Repeat the moxibustion three times over three days. This is Cang Gong’s secret method. Additionally, moxibustion at the seam beneath the scrotum, thirty cones.

Other remedies for manic possession appear elsewhere.

For those who become manic: Take axle grease the size of a chicken egg, heat it in bitter wine, and stir until dissolved. Consume the entire mixture.

For heart vexation, confusion, abdominal fullness and pain, or intermittent loss of consciousness: Take five *sheng* of soot from beneath a cauldron, grind and sift, then mix with eight *sheng* of cold water. Strain and drink the entire liquid. If the patient’s jaw is locked, force it open and administer the liquid through a bamboo tube to ensure it is swallowed. The patient will recover immediately—this method is highly effective.

For opisthotonos with arched back, loss of limb control, and near-death from vexation: Mix five *sheng* of clear wine with one *sheng* of chicken droppings, grind and sift, then whisk a thousand times. Adults take one *sheng* three times daily; children take five *ge*. Recovery will follow.

For unbearable pain throughout the head and body, with disorientation and near-death from vexation: Take head filth the size of a large soybean and swallow it. Additionally, fill two pouches with steamed soybeans and alternate applying them as hot compresses to the painful areas. If soybeans are unavailable, steam mouse burrow soil and apply similarly.

For acute abdominal pain: Roast half a *jin* of salt until exhausted, place it in the mouth, then drink two *sheng* of hot water to induce vomiting. Recovery will follow.

Another remedy: Slice six parts *fu zi* and three *liang* of fresh ginger, boil in two *sheng* of water until one *sheng* remains, and divide into two doses.

For loss of limb control: Burn green cloth to produce smoke and fumigate the affected area using a small-mouthed vessel.

Another remedy: Boil three *sheng* of fermented soybeans in nine *sheng* of water until three *sheng* remain, and divide into three doses.

Another: Lightly roast one *sheng* of fermented soybeans, place in a pouch, and steep in three *sheng* of wine for three nights. Drink warm, enough to induce mild intoxication.

For localized spasms, numbness, and loss of control: Roll a handful of dried mugwort leaves into a ball, place it beneath a clay steamer, and seal all but one opening. Position the painful area over the open hole and burn the mugwort beneath it until the skin blackens. Recovery will occur within an hour.

Another remedy: Shave rotten wood into shavings, boil in water until thick, and while scalding hot, steep the painful area—effective.

For clenched jaw that will not open: Take five *sheng* of soybeans, roast until yellow-black, steep in five *sheng* of wine, and extract the liquid. Force the mouth open with an implement and pour the liquid in, then induce sweating.

Another remedy: Four *liang* of *duhuo*, two *liang* of cinnamon, boiled in two *sheng* of wine and water to yield one and a half *sheng*. Divide into three doses, administer while the mouth is open, then have the patient lie warmly covered and apply moxibustion to induce sweating.

For rigidity of the body with inability to bend, stretch, or turn: Cut yellow-white *huai* bark into pieces, boil in six *sheng* of wine and water to yield two *sheng*, strain, and administer in small doses at an appropriate temperature.

Another remedy: Scrape one *sheng* of *zhi* tree bark, steep in one *sheng* of wine overnight, and consume from five *ge* to one *sheng*. When the wine is finished, prepare more—recovery will follow.

For facial distortion with deviated mouth: Apply moxibustion to the horizontal crease at the corner of the mouth. Remove the moxa as soon as heat is felt—do not burn completely, as excessive application will overcorrect. If the left side is distorted, moxa the right corner; if the right side is distorted, moxa the left.

Another method: Moxa a single cone on the upper joint of the middle finger—if the distortion is to the right, moxa the left finger. Additional moxibustion methods for deviated mouth follow later.

Another remedy: Take powdered *kongqing* and place it in the mouth—swallowing it will immediately restore normality. (Identical to Yao’s method.)

Another remedy: Rub spider eggs on the tense cheek near the jaw until the mouth returns to normal—stop when alignment is achieved. Alternatively, warm the eggs by the fire before rubbing.

Another remedy: Grind equal parts oyster shell, alum, aconite, and yellow earth from a stove, mix with the blood of a three-year-old rooster’s comb, and apply to the tense side. Hold water nearby; when the mouth begins to realign, promptly wash off the medicine. Do not reapply once corrected.

Another remedy: Apply a mixture of turtle shell and *wutou*—remove immediately when the mouth begins to realign.

For cold extremities, clear fluid vomiting, and writhing with cries: Take one *liang* of cinnamon, break into pieces, boil in three *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*, strain, and consume the entire dose at an appropriate temperature.

For joint pain: Grind eight *liang* of cattail pollen with one *liang* of roasted aconite. Take one *qian* initially, three times daily, gradually increasing to one *fangcunchi*.

For painful, restless joints that resist bending or stretching, with pain upon touch, shortness of breath, sweating, or swelling: Two *liang* of aconite, four *liang* of cinnamon, three *liang* of *zhu*, and two *liang* of licorice, boiled in six *sheng* of water to yield three *sheng*. Divide into three doses—recovery follows sweating.

For sudden wind strike with profuse cold sweating like water: Grind equal parts gypsum and licorice, and take one *fangcunchi* with wine. Repeat the dose when the sun has moved one *zhang*.

For gradual wind strike with loss of limb control: Boil three *sheng* of fermented soybeans in nine *sheng* of water to yield three *sheng*, and divide into three doses. Prepare twice daily. Alternatively, steep in wine and consume.

If suddenly struck by wind-induced paralysis, with the body unable to control itself, speechlessness, and confusion rendering one unable to recognize others, the marrow fat of an aged leopard cat is most essential—this is found in the *Emergency Remedies* section.

**Additional Formulas for Head Wind and Headache**
From *Tested Formulas*: To treat acute wind strike with eyes closed, clenched jaw, and no way to administer medicine, use this powder. Dip the middle finger into the powder and rub the teeth thirty to forty times, focusing on the molars on both sides—the mouth will open on its own, allowing medicine to be given. Named *Opening the Pass Powder*: Grind *tiannanxing* into powder, mix with borneol in equal parts, and prepare on the fifth day of the fifth lunar month at noon. For the afflicted, administer from one *zi* to half a *qian*.

From *Concise Aid for the Multitudes*: For wind strike with clenched jaw and foaming saliva.
Use one *zhi* of *zaojiao*, remove the skin, coat with lard, and roast until yellow. Grind into powder and take one *qianbi* with warm wine at any time. If the pulse is strong and large, adjust the dose to two *qianbi*. If the jaw remains locked, rub the teeth with a white plum—the mouth will open, allowing the medicine to be administered to induce vomiting of wind saliva, leading to recovery.

To treat wind strike with loss of consciousness and tightly clenched jaw.
Use one *liang* of *lilu*, remove the root, boil in a strong decoction of *fangfeng*, bathe, dry, cut finely, and stir-fry until slightly brown. Grind into powder and take half a *qian* with warm water, inducing vomiting of wind saliva as the effect. If no vomiting occurs after walking two *li*, administer again. Also treats gallbladder wind toxin, disharmony of deficiency and excess, and excessive drowsiness.
Use one *liang* of raw *suanzaoren* and two *liang* of *jinting* wax tea, coat with fresh ginger juice, and roast until slightly scorched. Grind into powder and take two *qian* each time, boiling in seven *fen* of water to yield six *fen*, and consume warm at any time.

From *Sun Shangyao’s Remedies*: To treat sudden wind strike with a drunken stupor, bodily heaviness, limbs unresponsive, or falling without falling, or a slanted mouth with slight drooling—if left untreated even briefly, it becomes a grave illness, thus harming the person. This condition arises from wind saliva congesting the upper diaphragm, obstructing the flow of *qi*. The *Emergency Salvation Thin-Saliva Powder* is recommended:
Four *ting* of pig’s tusk *zaojiao* (must be plump and unblemished, with black skin removed), one *liang* of *jin fan* (clear and lustrous), grind both together, sift into fine powder, and grind again into a fine preparation. For the afflicted, administer half a *qian*; for severe cases, three *zi*. Mix with warm water and administer. It does not cause violent vomiting but only gently thins the saliva, allowing one to two *sheng* to be expelled, restoring clarity. Follow with gradual treatment—do not rush into aggressive therapy, lest it harm the patient’s life. Its repeated efficacy cannot be fully described.

From *Master Mei’s Formulas*: To treat flaccid wind paralysis, with dragging limbs, slanted mouth and eyes, slurred speech, and unsteady gait.
The *Divinely Effective Black Dragon Elixir*: Five *liang* each of *chuanwu* (with skin and navel removed) and *wulingzhi*. Grind into powder, add borneol and musk, and grind finely. Form into pills the size of a bullet with water. For each dose, first dissolve one pill in fresh ginger juice, then mix with warm wine and consume. Take twice daily, on an empty stomach and before the evening meal. For one person, thirty pills suffice—after five to seven pills, one can lift the hands and move the feet; ten pills allow self-sufficiency.

From *Sagely Benefit Formulas*: To treat all wind illnesses. If taken over time, it lightens the body, sharpens the eyes, darkens the beard, and preserves youthful appearance.
Use the *nanzhu* tree: in spring and summer, take the branches and leaves; in autumn and winter, take the root bark. Select and finely chop five *sheng*, boil in five *dou* of water to yield two *dou*, strain, and simmer the liquid in a clean pot until it thickens like syrup. Store in a porcelain bottle and take one spoonful with warm wine, three times daily.

Another formula, with miraculous efficacy against wind.
Use one *jin* of *mutianliao*, remove the skin, and finely chop. Place in a raw silk bag and steep in two *dou* of good wine. After seven days in spring and summer, or fourteen days in autumn and winter, open and consume. Take one cup each on an empty stomach, at noon, and in the early evening, adjusting the dose for the elderly and young. For long-term use, take only one cup each morning.

Another formula for wind-induced slanted mouth.
Crush seven *badou*, remove the skin, and apply the paste: if the mouth slants left, apply to the right palm; if right, apply to the left palm. Place a cup of warm water over the palm—the mouth will straighten. Wash off the medicine and repeatedly pull the middle finger.

Another formula for wind-induced vertigo.
Use two *liang* of cicada moltings, lightly stir-fry, and grind into powder. Take one *qianbi* with warm wine at any time.

From *Essential Formulas Worth a Thousand Gold*: To treat wind strike with facial distortion, clenched jaw, and an immobile tongue.
Boil *guixin* in wine to extract the juice, soak a cloth, and apply to the affected area—the condition will correct. If the left side is slanted, apply to the right; if the right, apply to the left. Consistently effective.

Another formula for wind stroke persisting for three years.
Finely chop one *jin* of pine needles, boil in one *dou* of wine to yield three *sheng*, and consume in one dose to induce sweating—immediate recovery.

Another formula for sudden wind strike with facial swelling.
Pound apricot kernels into a paste and apply.

Another formula for head and facial wind, with eye and nasal congestion, dim vision, and cold tears.
Grind three *sheng* of apricot kernels into powder, boil in water for four to five cycles, and wash the head until cold sweat is induced. Repeat three times for recovery.

From *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library*: To treat sudden wind strike with slanted mouth.
Grind five *liang* of *zaojiao* (skin removed) into powder, mix with three-year-old vinegar, and apply: if the mouth slants left, apply to the right; if right, apply to the left. Reapply as it dries—recovery follows.

Another formula for hemiplegic wind and all wind disorders.
Cut one large *sheng* of mulberry twigs—use this year’s fresh, tender branches—boil in one large *dou* of water to yield two large *sheng*. In summer, chill the decoction in a well to prevent souring. Take one cup daily on an empty stomach. When the first batch is finished, decoct and consume again. Lifelong adherence prevents hemiplegic wind. For wind prevention, consuming one large *sheng* is optimal.

Another formula for wind-induced sensations of insects crawling over the body.
Boil one *dou* of salt in one *shi* of water until reduced by half. Clarify, then wash the body three to five times with the warm liquid—effective for all wind disorders.

From *Master Ge’s Formulas*: To treat wind strike with cold damage, lockjaw, and loss of consciousness.
Stir-fry one *sheng* of white chicken droppings until yellow and extremely hot. Mix with three *sheng* of wine, strain, and consume the liquid.

From *Supplement to the Thousand Golden Prescriptions*: For heat wind with sweating and heart vexation, mix mica with water and consume. Recovery follows after no more than two doses.

From *Formulas from the Satchel*: For wind-induced head and brain pain unbearable to endure, apply a massage ointment.
Pound burdock stems and leaves to extract two *sheng* of thick juice. Combine with one *sheng* of ash-free wine and a spoonful of salt crystals. Simmer over fire until thickened into an ointment, then massage onto painful areas. The wind toxin disperses and ceases. Also treats seasonal head pain. When massaging, apply force until heat is generated—rapid efficacy follows. In winter, when leaves are unavailable, roots may be substituted.

From *Tested Later Formulas*: For wind strike and congestion, grind washed, clean *xuanfuhua* (inula flower) into powder, mix with refined honey, and form pills the size of *wutong* seeds. At bedtime, take five to ten pills with tea.

Another formula to resolve wind-heat, disperse accumulated heat and wind congestion, promote digestion, transform *qi*, guide blood, and thoroughly resolve congestion.
Grind four *liang* of rhubarb and four *liang* of morning glory seeds (half raw, half parched) into powder. Mix with refined honey to form pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take ten pills with tea; if mild purgation is desired, take fifteen. Suitable for winter use—does not disturb the person.

From *Collected Verified Formulas*: For wind-heat with heart agitation, dry mouth, raving speech, generalized high fever, and various poisonings, use *Dragon Brain Sweet Dew Pills*.
Burn half a *jin* of *hanshuishi* (calcium sulfate) for half a day. Bury in a clean earthen pit, cover with a basin, and mound wet soil around it. After one night, retrieve and add two *liang* each of licorice powder and *tianzhu huang* (bamboo silica), plus two *fen* of *longnao* (borneol). Form into pills the size of longan seeds with glutinous rice paste. Dissolve in honey water and consume.

From *Heart Mirror of Dietary Medicine*: For wind strike with heart and lung wind-heat, loss of limb control, wind impediment with unbearable symptoms, flaccid sinews and vessels, disorientation, and vexation.
Cut one *jin* of bear meat and prepare as salted, cured jerky following standard methods. Consume on an empty stomach.

Another formula for wind-induced spasms, contractures, hemiplegia, and obstructed blood and *qi*.
Refine four *liang* of wild goose fat, strain, and take one spoonful daily on an empty stomach with a cup of warmed wine.

The same text states: For pervading wind with unbearable pain in all joints day and night.
Grind half a *liang* of *moyao* (myrrh) into powder. Roast three *liang* of tiger brain bone in *su* (refined butter) until yellow, then pound and sift into powder. Mix thoroughly with the *moyao*. Take two *qian* with warm wine, three times daily—highly effective.

From *Imperial Grace Formulary*: For pervading wind with unbearable pain in all joints.
Roast one tiger skull in *su* until yellow, then crush and place in a silk bag. Steep in two *dou* of clear wine for five nights. Drink warmed as desired—wondrously effective.

From *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library*: For pervading wind with unbearable sour pain in all joints.
Refine thirty *jin* of pine resin fifty times (or at least twenty times if fifty is unfeasible). Warm three *sheng* of refined *su* and blend with three *sheng* of pine resin, stirring until extremely thick. On an empty stomach, take one *fangcunbi* (spoonful) with wine, three times daily. Consume thin rice porridge frequently. Avoid blood, raw or cold foods, sour items, and fruits for one hundred days—recovery follows.

From *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library*: *Pine Node Wine* for pervading wind with limb pain as if dislocated.
Steep twenty *jin* of pine nodes in five *dou* of wine for fourteen days. Take one *ge* (cup), five or six times daily.

From *Doumen’s Formulas*: For *White Tiger Wind* of any duration, even chronic cases unresponsive to treatment with unbearable pain.
Finely cut and dry-fry an unspecified quantity of *nao* (borneol), *she* (musk), *feng* (maple bark), and *liu* (willow bark). Steep in wine and consume until intoxicated—immediate recovery. The mistletoe growing on maple trees is particularly effective; its leaves can also be used to refine *pishuang* (arsenic powder)—especially potent.

From *Tested Later Formulas*: For *White Tiger Wind* with migrating pain and hot swelling in both knees.
Roast one *liang* each of tiger shin bone in *su* and black aconite (parched, skin and navel removed) into powder. Take two *qianbi* with warm wine, twice daily.

From *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library*: For scrofula wind and three-year cases.
Grind cuttlefish bone with vinegar and apply after first scrubbing the skin until red.

Another formula for scrofula wind: Grind sulfur with vinegar and apply—immediate cessation.

From *Imperial Grace Formulary*: For scrofula wind, grind sheep’s sorrel root on raw iron with good vinegar, scraping continuously to collect the liquid. Apply to the affected area. If unresolved, add a small amount of sulfur, grind together, and reapply.

From *Collected Verified Formulas*: For white patches on the neck and face that spread gradually like tinea but without sores, apply eel fat. First, scrub the affected area until dry and painful, then apply the fat. One application cures; severe cases require no more than three.

From *Imperial Grace Formulary*: For white patches, burn snake slough into powder, mix with vinegar, and apply—excellent.

Another formula: For wind-stroke with vexing heat and itchy skin sores, use four liang of *tigho* (clarified butter). Take one #36 spoonful mixed with wine per dose.

From *Collected Verified Formulas*: For wind qi lodged in the skin causing unceasing itch.
Grill wasp nests and mix equal parts with cicada slough, grind into powder, and take one *qianbi* with wine, two or three times daily.

Another formula: Equal parts cicada slough and *bohe* (mint), grind into powder, and take one *qianbi* with wine, three times daily.

*Miscellaneous Records of the Northern Dream* states: A court official consulted Physician Liang, who diagnosed him: "Your wind illness is severe; return home at once." The official then saw Zhao E, a veterinarian from Fuzhou, who examined him and likewise declared the illness critical. "There is but one method," he said. "Try eating crisp pears—any quantity, chewed or juiced. After ten days at home consuming only crisp pears, he recovered fully."

From *Essential Prescriptions Worth a Thousand in Gold*: For head wind and headache, stir-fry three *sheng* of soybeans until silent, then place in a twelve-*sheng* jar with nine *sheng* of clear wine. While the beans are still hot, add them to the wine, seal with honeyed mud for seven days, then take warm.

Master Sun’s formula for head wind pain: Wash the head with fermented soybean decoction and avoid wind—immediate relief.

From *Supplement to Essential Prescriptions Worth a Thousand in Gold*: For head wind, pound *tinglizi* (pepperweed seeds), steep in hot water, strain the juice, and wash the head.

Another formula for head wind and hair washing: Boil two *sheng* of *wuzhuyu* (evodia fruit) in five *sheng* of water until reduced to three *sheng*, then soak cotton and wipe the hair roots.

From *Imperial Grace Formulary*: For head wind pain that flares before windy or rainy weather.
Grind one *liang* of *guixin* (cassia heart) into powder, mix with wine into a paste, and apply to the crown and temples.

Chen Cangqi’s *Supplement to Materia Medica* states: For unbearable headache, blow *xiaoshi* (saltpeter) powder into the nostrils—immediate cure.

*Rihuazi* states: For headache, mix *juemingzi* (cassia tora seeds) with water and apply to the temples.

Another formula: Make a pillow of *juemingzi*—superior to black beans—for head wind and improving vision.

From *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library*: For splitting headache, boil two *liang* of *danggui* (Chinese angelica) in one *sheng* of wine until six *ge* remain, and take in two doses.

From *Sun Zhao’s Oral Instructions*: For headache.
Equal parts roasted *fuzi* (aconite) and calcined *shigao* (gypsum), ground into powder, with a small amount of *nao* (borneol) and *she* (musk) added. Take half a *qian* with tea or wine.

From *Doumen Formulas*: For sudden headache, grind silk-less silkworm pupae into powder and take two *qianbi* with warm water—immediate relief.

Another formula: For one-sided headache, finely slice *jingxiong* (Sichuan lovage), steep in wine, and take—excellent.

From *Extensive Relief Formulas*: For one-sided headache, *Zhiling Powder*: Equal parts *xionghuang* (realgar) and *xixin* (asarum), ground finely. Use less than one *zi* per dose—blow into the right nostril for left-side pain, left nostril for right-side pain—immediate effect.

From *Tested Later Formulas*: For peerless one-sided headache, grind *bibo* (long pepper) into powder. Have the patient hold warm water in the mouth; for left-side pain, inhale one *zi* through the left nostril; for right-side pain, inhale through the right—effective.

From *Collected Verified Formulas*: For one-sided or general headache, grind one *liang* of *gujingcao* (pipewort) into powder, mix with white flour, spread on paper, and apply to the painful area. Replace when dry.

Another formula for one-sided headache: Use one *xieke* (clam shell) of fresh radish juice. Lie supine and drip into the nostril—left pain, left nostril; right pain, right nostril; both sides, both nostrils—divinely effective.

From *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library*: For head wind with bran-like white scales.
Carve a firm *chumu* (paper mulberry) wood pillow and replace every sixty days.

**Chapter Twenty: Formulas for Sudden Wind-Induced Aphonia and Inability to Speak**

For sudden loss of speech: Boil melon seeds in vinegar, wrap the neck for a full day and night—relief.

Another formula: Boil soybeans, reduce the juice to a syrup, and hold in the mouth. Or simply boil thickly and drink.

Another formula: Boil *chi* (fermented soybeans) juice and take gradually. Stir half a *sheng* of fine wine into the juice and divide into three doses.

Another formula: Peel fresh, high-quality *gui* (cassia), grind, and take three pinches under the tongue, swallowing the juice.

Another formula: Chop *gu* (millet) branches and leaves, boil in wine, strain the foam, and drink as needed.

For sudden loss of voice with choked sound: Boil five *liang* of *jupi* (tangerine peel) in three *sheng* of water until one *sheng* remains, strain, and take all at once.

Another formula: Boil *kuzhuye* (bitter bamboo leaves) thickly and take—relief.

Another formula: Pound *ranghe* (edible canna) root, mix with wine, strain, and drink the juice. (Originally in Miscellaneous Treatments.)

Another formula: *Tongcao* (rice-paper plant pith), *ganjiang* (dried ginger), *fuzi* (aconite), *fushen* (poria with hostwood), half a *liang* each; *fangfeng* (saposhnikovia), *gui* (cassia), *shigao* (gypsum), two *liang* each; *mahuang* (ephedra), one and a half *liang*; *baizhu* (atractylodes), half a *liang*; *xingren* (apricot kernels), thirty pieces. Grind all into powder, form into honey pills the size of soybeans, and take seven pills per dose, gradually increasing. All these treat wind-stroke. Many other formulas use bamboo sap decoctions, but though this prescription is small, it targets the ailment precisely—if one dose fails, take another.

Another formula: Needle one *cun* and five *fen* beside the *dachui* point, then needle below and retain the needle.

Another formula: Grind *fanshi* (alum) and *gui* (cassia) into powder, wrap in cotton like a date, and place under the tongue to induce salivation.

Another formula: Heat a horse’s bit iron until red, quench in one *sheng* of vinegar, mix with a broken egg, and drink.

For sudden cold-induced hoarseness: One *liang* of *gancao* (licorice), two *liang* of *gui* (cassia), two *liang* of *wuweizi* (schisandra), thirty *xingren* (apricot kernels), eight *liang* of sliced fresh *jiang* (ginger). Boil in seven *sheng* of water until two *sheng* remain, and take in two doses.

Additional Formulas
From *Proven Later Formulas*:
For wind-stroke with loss of speech: One *liang* of *duhuo* (pubescent angelica), sliced, simmered in two *sheng* of wine until one *sheng* remains; five *ge* of soybeans, stir-fried until crackling. Pour the hot medicinal wine over the beans, cover for a long while, then take three *ge* warm. If the condition persists, take again.

Another formula for wind-stroke with loss of speech, wheezing in the throat like a saw, and foaming at the mouth:
Take one *fen* of *lilu* (black false hellebore) and one *tiannanxing* (arisaema rhizome). Remove the outer skin of the *tiannanxing* and hollow out a small pit on the navel side. Fill the pit with one *rongdou* of aged vinegar, then heat all sides over a fire until yellow. Pound together, grind to an extremely fine powder, and form into pills with raw honey the size of red beans. Take three pills each time with warm wine.

From *Sagely Benefit Formulas*:
For wind-stroke with loud voice but impaired throat:
Take two *liang* of *ranghe* root (mioga ginger), grind, and press to extract the juice. Mix with one large cup of wine, stir evenly, and take half a cup warm at any time.

Formula Twenty-One: For Wind-Toxin Leg Weakness with Fullness and Upward Qi
The disease of *jiaoqi* (leg qi) first arose in Lingnan and gradually spread to Jiangdong. It strikes without warning—sometimes with slight pain or numbness, sometimes with mild swelling in both shins, or sudden weakness upon standing, or numbness in the lower abdomen, or alternating chills and fever—all its signs. If not treated immediately, it ascends into the abdomen, then erupts as qi and kills.

To treat this, decoctions, wines, massages, and ointments are commonly used. As there are many effective remedies (#37), not just one formula, here I select only those of singular efficacy, supplemented with moxibustion.

Take one *sheng* of fine fermented soybeans, steam three times and sun-dry three times. Soak in three *dou* of good wine for three nights until drinkable, adjusting the quantity to the patient’s capacity. For prevention, administer without waiting for symptoms: boil the fermented soybeans in wine and take. When leg weakness shows slight improvement, further prepare other formulas and apply moxibustion.

Next, the *Du Huo* Wine formula: five *liang* each of *du huo* (pubescent angelica) and raw, sliced *fuzi* (aconite), steeped in one *dou* of wine for three nights. Begin with one *ge* per dose, increasing until mild numbness is felt.

Another formula: two *jin* of *bai fan shi* (alunite) or *zhongru* (stalactite powder), three *liang* of *fuzi*, and three *sheng* of fermented soybeans, steeped in three *dou* of wine for four to five days. Drink gradually. If qi stagnation is present, add two *sheng* of *suzi* (perilla seed).

Another formula: grind three *liang* of fine sulfur into powder. Boil five *sheng* of cow’s milk with five *sheng* of water, add the sulfur, and reduce to three *sheng*. Take three *ge* per dose. Alternatively, boil sulfur directly in milk without water. If cow’s milk is unavailable, sheep’s milk may be used.

Another method: reduce three *sheng* of cow’s milk by half, then take five *ge* with one *liang* of sulfur powder. After ingestion, cover thickly to induce sweating, avoiding drafts. Take another dose midday and one at dusk. If sweating occurs, do not repeat; simply rest and recover. If unresolved, repeat after several days. For long-term use, it may be decocted into pills.

Northerners find this sulfur remedy highly effective for leg disorders, provided the sulfur is of the finest quality. It should be prepared in advance.

If the shins are swollen such that pressing leaves an imprint, force the patient to drink two to three *sheng* of black calf’s urine to promote urination and gradually reduce swelling. Use a copper vessel, and fresh urine is best. If no black calf is available, a pure yellow one may suffice.

Another formula: grind *qianniuzi* (morning glory seeds), mix with honey into pills the size of small beans, and take five pills to promote urination. They may also be swallowed whole. The seeds are black, resembling *qiouzi* kernels, and are sold in markets.

Another formula: crush *sanbai* root and take with wine.

Another: boil black soybeans in water or wine and drink the broth.

Another: eating small red beans is also beneficial.

Another: grind raw *huma* (sesame), mix with wine, and take to cure the condition.

Another: boil three *sheng* of black soybeans in one *dou* of water to nine *sheng*, add nine *sheng* of clear wine, and reduce again to nine *sheng*. Drink gradually; urination will relieve the swelling.

Formulas such as *Feng Yin*, *Bai Ji*, *Zhu Li*, and *Du Huo* decoctions, as well as *Ba Feng*, *Shi Hu*, and *Gou Ji* powders, are detailed in comprehensive medical texts.

*Jin Ya* Wine is most essential for treatment; its formula is recorded here: four *liang* each of *shujiao* (Sichuan pepper), *yinyu* (skimmia), *jin ya* (golden teeth), *xixin* (asarum), *wang cao* (lithospermum), *gan dihuang* (dried rehmannia), *fangfeng* (saposhnikovia), *fuzi* (aconite), *difu* (kochia), *shuodi* (glossy privet), and *shengma* (cimicifuga); three *liang* of *renshen* (ginseng); one *jin* of *qianghuo* (notopterygium); and five *liang* of *niuxi* (achyranthes). Cut the fourteen ingredients, steep in four *dou* of wine for seven days, and drink two to three *ge* per dose, gradually increasing. It also treats speechlessness and bent legs with excellent results. *Cezi* Wine is also effective.

For rural or impoverished households, these remedies may be brewed: *baqia* (smilax), pine nodes, and pine needles are all beneficial. Wash and chop one *hu* of *baqia*, boil in three *hu* of water to nine *dou*, strain, and use the liquid to soak yeast and cook rice, brewing as one would wine. When ready, drink freely, preparing three to five *hu* at once. If using pine nodes or needles, follow the same method; the liquid should be as concentrated as possible.

For those with bent legs, unable to walk for years, or suffering from lumbar and spinal contracture and abdominal tightness, three to five doses will restore health.

If brewing is impractical, *shanglu* (pokeweed) by the water’s edge is also effective.

Moxibustion points are numerous, but as not all may be known, I record only the essentials. Begin from the upper body; moxibustion on the legs alone risks trapping qi and causing danger.

First, moxa *Dazhui*: the prominent vertebra at the nape. Apply moxa to the point above it. If qi stagnation is present, first moxa *Baihui* with fifty cones—this point lies in the depression atop the head.

Next, moxa *Jianjing* on both shoulders with one hundred cones each. The point lies in the depression near the head on the shoulders; press with fingers to locate the center.

Next, moxa *Danzhong* with fifty cones. This point lies between the breasts, at the junction of the sternum and ribs, where pressing elicits a subtle qi sensation. Some say it is the single point at the center of the chest.

Next, moxa *Juque*, located one *cun* below the tip of the xiphoid process, measured by the patient’s finger-width. Moxibustion at these five upper points suffices to treat qi stagnation. Moxibustion at *Baihui*, *Fengfu* (#40), *Weiguan*, and the five *zang* transport points is even better, depending on the urgency of the condition. All points are recorded in moxibustion manuals and cannot be fully listed here.

Next, moxa *Fengshi* with one hundred cones. This point lies on the outer thigh; stand upright, let the hands hang naturally, and press the thigh where the middle finger rests—this is the point, where pressing feels appropriate.

Next, moxa *Zusanli* with two hundred cones. Have the patient place their hand horizontally below the knee, fingers together (a measure called *yifu*). The point lies one *yifu* below the kneecap, at the outer edge of the shinbone, where pressing reveals a depression.

Next, moxa *Shang Lian* with one hundred cones, located one *yifu* below *Zusanli*.

Next, moxa *Xialian* with one hundred cones, located one *yifu* below *Shang Lian*.

Next, moxa *Juegu* with two hundred cones. This point lies slightly more than three *cun* above the outer ankle; align the fingertip with the upper edge of the ankle bone, then bend the finger to measure four *cun*—this is the point. It roughly aligns with *Xialian*, forming two distinct points in the interstice. These eighteen points below are all essential points. For the remaining points—*Futu* and *Dubi*—when applying the prescribed number of cones, it is not necessary to complete them all at once; rather, spread the treatment over three days to fulfill the total.

**Alternative Formula:**
Steep two *jin* of *Konggongnie* and five *liang* of *shihu* in two *dou* of wine, then consume.

**Appended Formulas:**

*From the* **Doumen Fang***:*
To treat sudden wind-toxin, swelling, tightness, and acute pain: Take one *jin* of willow bark, chop it, and boil it in wine until hot. Wrap it in silk and apply it to the swollen area. When it cools, reheat and replace it. This method is highly effective.

*From the* **Shenghui Fang***:*
To treat migratory wind-toxin pain: Grind small mustard seeds into powder, mix with egg white, and apply as a poultice.

*From the* **Jingyan Hou Fang***:*
To treat wind-toxin bone-marrow pain: Grind two *fen* of *shaoyao* and one *liang* of roasted *hugu* into powder, place in a silk pouch, and steep in three *sheng* of wine for five days. Take two *ge* per dose, three times daily.

*From the* **Shiyi Xinjing***:*
To dispel all wind-damp impediment and tetany of the limbs: Grind three *liang* of *cangerzi* into powder, decoct in one and a half *sheng* of water until seven *ge* remain, strain, and sip.

Also, to treat muscle spasms, chronic wind-damp impediment, downbearing *qi*, expelling pathogenic *qi* from the bones, harmonizing the intestines and stomach, dispersing water swelling, and—with prolonged use—lightening the body and augmenting *qi* and strength: Take one *sheng* of *yiyiren*, grind into powder, and for each dose, boil two *sheng* of water with two spoonfuls of the powder to make a congee. Consume on an empty stomach.

Also, to supplement deficiency, dispel wind-damp impediment: Warm one cup of wine, mix in two large *liang* of *tihu*, and take one spoonful of the mixture.

*From the* **Jingyan Fang***:*
To treat pain beneath the skin anywhere on the body: Grind *heshouwu* into powder, mix with ginger juice to form a paste, apply to the painful area, and wrap with silk. Then, heat the sole of a shoe over fire and press it against the area. This method is highly effective.

*From Sun Zhenren’s Formula:*
To treat *jiaoqi* and counterflow *qi*: Prepare *kuai* from one large red crucian carp and consume one or two portions at once for relief.

*From the* **Qianjin Yi***:*
To treat *jiaoqi* surging upward to the heart: Boil two *liang* of alum in one *dou* and five *sheng* of water for three to five boilings, then soak and wash the feet. This is highly effective.

*From the* **Guangli Fang***:*
To treat *jiaoqi* causing vexation, agitation, and loss of consciousness: Boil one *sheng* of soybeans in three *sheng* of water to make a thick decoction, then consume half a *sheng* at once. If symptoms persist, take another half *sheng* to stabilize the condition.

Su Gong states: For those suffering from *jiaoqi*, eat to satiety in the morning as desired, eat lightly after noon, and fast in the evening. If hungry, consume fermented soybean congee. If digestion is poor and symptoms resemble impending cholera:
Take two *liang* of *gaoliangjiang*, crush it, and boil in three *sheng* of water until one *sheng* remains. Consume it all at once to resolve the condition. Wait until extremely hungry, then eat a full portion of thin congee. This remedy is most effective when taken in large quantities. If *gaoliangjiang* is unavailable, substitute one *liang* of ginger, boil it thoroughly in one *sheng* of clear wine, and consume it with the dregs. Though not as effective as *gaoliangjiang*, it still yields significant results.

The *Tang Bencao* notes: For *jiaoqi*, soak the affected area in a thick decoction of *hongcao* for prolonged relief.

*From the* **Jianyao Jizhong***:*
To treat *jiaoqi* with persistent leg swelling: Take one *liang* of black *fuzi*, remove the skin and navel, grind into powder, and mix with fresh ginger juice to form a paste. Apply to the swollen area, and when the paste dries, reapply with fresh mixture until the swelling subsides.

**Chapter Twenty-Two: Formulas for Acute Onset of *Fu San* Toxicity**

When consuming Five Minerals *Huming Gengsheng* or *Zhongru* Cold-Food Powder, improper regulation or dosage may provoke acute onset of illness, manifesting in myriad ways. If symptoms arise suddenly rather than gradually, they are due to the potency of the powder. Immediate intervention is required. For all external pains or abnormalities in the limbs or body, wash the affected area with cold water hundreds of times. If heat surges, soak a cloth in water and apply it as a compress. Alternatively, soak a cold stone in water and use it to press the area. Drink warm wine and walk leisurely.

For all internal pains or abnormalities in the heart and abdomen—such as vexation, oppression, or confusion—act swiftly. If cold, drink warm wine in one or two *sheng* increments, gradually increasing the amount. If slight relief is felt, consume more cold food. Heart pain is most urgent; if the flesh is cold and the mouth is clenched, force open the teeth and administer hot wine for relief.

For abdominal masses, heat accumulations, or other complex conditions, purge immediately. Boil fourteen *zhizi* and five *ge* of *chi* in two *sheng* of water until one *sheng* remains, then consume it all at once. If heat is severe and sores have erupted, add two *liang* of *huangqin*. If accumulations persist and appetite is poor with aversion to cold, purge again. Prepare the following powder: half a *sheng* of fine *dahuang* powder, half a *sheng* of *mangxiao*, two *liang* of *gancao*, and one *fen* each of *banxia*, *huangqin*, and *yuanhua*. Grind into powder and store in an airtight container. To administer, boil twenty *dazao* in eight *sheng* of water until soft, then strain to obtain four *sheng* of liquid. Add five *fangcunbi* of the powder, stir well, and heat the mixture three times (raising and lowering it over the fire). Divide into three doses and consume one in the morning. If bowel movements occur, the remaining doses may be omitted. If relief is not felt, take another dose.

After purging, prepare wine congee and consume two *sheng*, followed by watery gruel. Do not delay eating, as an empty stomach may allow heat to enter, which can be fatal.

After purging, always keep the following emergency formula on hand: one *ge* each of *dahuang* and *tingli*, thirty *xingren* and *badou*, ground and mixed with honey into pills the size of *hudou*. Take two pills daily.

Those who experience diarrhea should reduce the dosage; those with abdominal fullness should increase it. There are many formulas for decoctions, powders, pills, and medicinal wines, but the key lies in maintaining coolness and allowing frequent bowel movements—only seeking free flow. The limbs should be kept in regular motion, and one must not miss meals or become hungry, nor consume spoiled rice, rotten fish, or meat. Additionally, one should avoid hot foods and drinks, heavy clothing, approaching fire, braving summer heat on long journeys, or excessive exposure to wind and cold.

Generally, the body should be in a robust state to tolerate these methods well. If illness has already manifested, one must forcibly endure the treatment. The medicines taken should primarily be those that resolve toxins and are cooling in nature.

When taking powders, if the illness seems to have subsided, discontinue use. After twenty or thirty days, resume as needed. If stagnation remains unresolved, leading to vexing heat, it is due to improper dosage—one should then follow the prescribed methods for prevention and treatment.

This method is most often employed by the wealthy and carefree, while those who are poor and toil rarely experience adverse reactions, as their bodies are accustomed to cold and labor. However, in cases of critical danger, these few principles are briefly recorded here for urgent reference. The rest are detailed in the major formulas.

**Additional Formulas**

**From *The Sagely Benefit Formulas*:**
For treating the activation of alchemical minerals (rushi) causing congestion, heat, heart vexation, and blood vomiting: Pound fresh *cirsium* (thistle) to extract its juice, take three *ge* per dose, add a small amount of honey, stir well, and consume.

*The Dietary Therapy* states: If heat from cinnabar or minerals erupts, cook *zizania* (wild rice) roots with crucian carp into a thick soup and eat it—after two or three servings, recovery will follow.

**Formula Twenty-Three: For Sudden Upward Qi and Coughing**

**For sudden upward qi with wheezing and near-collapse:**
Pound leeks to extract their juice and drink one *sheng*; an immediate cure will follow.

**Another formula:**
Finely slice three *sheng* of mulberry root bark, three *liang* of fresh ginger, and half a *sheng* of *zanthoxylum* (Sichuan pepper). Boil in seven *sheng* of water and five *sheng* of wine until reduced to three boils, strain, and consume the entire decoction. Once one *sheng* enters the mouth, the qi will descend. *A formula not transmitted in the *Thousand Gold*.*

**Another formula:**
Two *sheng* of *zanthoxylum* and three *liang* of fresh ginger, boiled in seven *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*; divide into three doses.

**Another formula:**
Four *liang* of *ephedra*, two *liang* each of cinnamon and licorice, and fifty apricot kernels—roast, pound into powder, and take one square *cun* spoonful with warm water, three times daily.

**Another formula:**
Grind *ginseng* into powder and take one square *cun* spoonful, five or six times daily. For coughing due to qi, regardless of duration, this formula brings immediate relief.

**For qi-induced coughing:**
Equal parts aged tangerine peel, cinnamon bark, and apricot kernels (tips and skins removed, roasted)—pound and form into honey pills. Take twenty pills after meals with tea, avoiding raw scallions. *Transmitted by Attendant Secretary Shi.*

**For sudden reversal of qi with upward surging, pain and fullness in both flanks, and near-collapse:**
Heat water until scalding, then soak both feet and hands, changing the water frequently. This is called *bentun* (rushing piglet) disease, arising from sudden fright, terror, or sorrow. The qi surges downward, then violently strikes the heart, chest, and navel, causing a pounding sensation. If left untreated, it can be fatal. Most formulas require many ingredients and even the killing of a piglet, but this single decoction suffices.

Two *liang* each of licorice and ginseng, two *liang* of cinnamon bark, one *sheng* of *zanthoxylum*, one *jin* of fresh ginger, and one *sheng* of *pinellia*—boil in one *dou* of water to yield three *sheng*, divided into three doses. This medicine should be prepared in advance; when the illness strikes, compound it urgently.

**Another formula:**
Two *liang* of *ephedra* and one *liang* of apricot kernels—roast until yellow, pound into powder, and take one square *cun* spoonful with wine, several times daily, until cured.

**For sudden qi depletion where breathing fails to recover, with shoulders heaving and gasping:**
Three *liang* of dried ginger—crush, steep in one *sheng* of wine, and take three *ge* per dose, three times daily.

**Another formula:**
Measure the length from the base of the thumb to the crease at the heart, then moxa three cones at this point for a cure.

**Another formula:**
Three *liang* of *ephedra*—first decoct to remove froth—with two *liang* of licorice, boiled in three *sheng* of water to yield one and a half *sheng*, divided into three doses.

**To prevent recurrence after recovery:**
Take these two ingredients, roast fifty apricot kernels, and form into honey pills. Take four or five pills the size of *tung* seeds, three times daily, until cured.

**Another formula:**
Two *liang* of *ephedra*, one *liang* each of cinnamon and licorice, and forty apricot kernels—boil in six *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*, divided into three doses.

These three formulas may also be prepared as *xiaotoubei* decoctions. For those with qi blockages, the medicines can be pounded into powders and taken regularly. For those with excessive cold, add three *liang* of dried ginger. For those with copious phlegm, add three *liang* of *pinellia*.

**For severe exertion from running or rushing, leading to panting and fatigue, followed by drinking cold water, which triggers upward qi and fever:**
Use three *jin* of bamboo leaves and three *liang* of tangerine peel, boiled in one *dou* of water to yield three *sheng*. Strain and divide into three doses; one dose every three days is effective.

**For extreme heat exhaustion or eating hot cakes followed by excessive cold water, which fails to disperse in the throat and instead generates qi, causing wheezing and panting:**
Equal parts rhubarb, dried ginger, and croton seeds—grind into powder and take half a *qian* spoonful. If vomiting or diarrhea occurs, recovery will follow. If stagnation persists in the heart, chest, or diaphragm, causing discomfort:

Two parts *melon pedicel*, three parts *asarum*, and one part ginseng—pound, sift, and take one *qian* spoonful with hot water, two or three times daily, until effective.

**For lung atrophy with coughing, spitting of frothy saliva, a warm sensation in the heart, vexation, and thirstlessness:**
Five *liang* of fresh ginger, two *liang* each of ginseng and licorice, and eleven jujubes—boil in three *sheng* of water to yield one and a half *sheng*, divided into two doses.

**Another formula:**
Two *liang* of licorice—boil in three *sheng* of water to yield one and a half *sheng*, divided into two doses.

**Another formula:**
Pound fresh *asparagus* to extract one *dou* of juice, mix with one *dou* of wine, one *sheng* of malt sugar, and four *ge* of *aster*—simmer in a copper vessel over a water bath until it can be formed into pills. Take one pill the size of an apricot kernel, three times daily.

**Another formula:**
Two *liang* of licorice, three *liang* of dried ginger, and twelve jujubes—boil in three *sheng* of water to yield one and a half *sheng*, divided into two doses.

**For sudden onset of cold-induced upward qi:**
Three *liang* of dried perilla leaves and four *liang* of aged tangerine peel—boil in four *sheng* of wine to yield one and a half *sheng*, divided into two doses.

**For sudden coughing:**
One part soot from beneath a cauldron and seven parts fermented soybeans—pound into pills the size of *wu* seeds and take fourteen pills.

**Another formula:**
Prepare a black chicken as for eating, steep in good wine for half a day, then remove the chicken and drink the wine. *Alternatively, boil a white chicken in one* dou *of vinegar to yield three* sheng*, divided into three doses. Eat the chicken meat, but avoid salt for best results.*

**Another formula:**
Moxa one point between the fifth and sixth vertebrae below the *dazhui* (GV-14) point, once for each year of age. *Also treats upward qi.*

**Another formula:**
Moxa the junction of dark and light flesh beneath both nipples, one hundred cones each, and the condition will resolve. *Also treats upward qi.* Moxa one point on the chest opposite the nipples, with cones corresponding to the patient’s age.

**Another formula:**
Take three *sheng* of peach kernels, remove the skins, pound them, and place in a vessel. Seal tightly and steam for the duration of one cooking cycle. Then remove, dry in the sun, and store in a silk bag. Place the bag in two *dou* of wine for six or seven days. Drink four to five *ge* at first, gradually increasing to one *sheng*.

**Another formula:**
Grind six *liang* of malt sugar and six *liang* of dried ginger into powder. Boil two *liang* of fermented soybeans in one *sheng* of water for three boilings, discard the dregs, dissolve the malt sugar, then add the dried ginger. Divide into three doses.

**Another formula:**
Mix malt sugar with fresh ginger shavings and steam beneath three *dou* of rice. Form into pills the size of a bullet, and take ten times day and night.

**Another formula:**
Finely chop two pig kidneys, add three *liang* of dried ginger powder, and boil in seven *sheng* of water to yield two *sheng*. Take gradually, then cover to induce sweating.

**Another formula:**
Roast and eat the heart of a black chicken. *Excellent.*

**Another formula:**
Combine and decoct equal parts fresh ginger juice and *bai bu* (*Stemona*) juice. Take two *ge*.

**Another formula:**
Steep four *liang* of *bai bu* root in one *dou* of wine for two nights, warm over a fire, and take one *sheng* twice daily.

**Another formula:**
Grind two hundred Sichuan peppercorns into powder, roast two hundred apricot kernels, and remove the pits from one hundred jujubes. Pound together until thoroughly blended, then form into pills the size of jujubes. Take gradually.

**Another formula:**
Pound three *liang* of fresh ginger to extract the juice, add three *liang* of dried ginger shavings and one *sheng* of peeled, roasted apricot kernels. Pound together into pills and take three pills, five or six times daily.

**Another formula:**
Boil one *sheng* of *yuan hua* (*Genkwa*) in three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*. Discard the dregs, add fourteen jujubes, and simmer until the liquid is absorbed. Consume once daily for three days.

**Another formula:**
Roast and pound one *liang* of *ting li* (*Lepidium*), and boil three jujubes in three *sheng* of water to yield one *sheng*. Discard the jujubes, add the *ting li*, and simmer to yield five *ge*. Adults divide into three doses; children into four.

**Hua Tuo’s Five-Cough Pill:**
Take equal parts roasted *zao jia* (*Gleditsia*), dried ginger, and cinnamon. Pound and form into honey pills the size of *tong* seeds. Take three pills, three times daily.

**Another formula:**
Grind one part pine shavings, two parts cinnamon, and two *liang* of roasted *zao jia* (remove skin and seeds). Form into honey pills the size of *tong* seeds. Take fifteen pills; children take five pills, once or twice daily.

**Another formula:**
Grind white clamshells from rooftops into powder and take one *fangcunbi* with wine.

**Another formula:**
Grind *fu san shi* (*pumice*) into powder and take, or form into honey pills.

**Another formula:**
Thinly slice one pig’s *□*, boil in vinegar, and consume entirely. No more than two doses required.

**Another formula:**
Boil two *liang* of *yuan hua* in two *sheng* of water for four boilings. Discard the dregs, add one *jin* of white sugar, and take a dose the size of a jujube. Avoid salty or sour foods. *Also treats chronic cough.*

**For chronic cough and upward qi lasting ten or twenty years, unresponsive to all other treatments:**
Steep three pig *□* and one hundred jujubes in three *sheng* of wine for several days. Take two to three *ge* at first, increasing to four or five *ge*. The condition will resolve shortly.

**Another formula:**
Place a live tortoise in a pit and urinate on it until submerged. After the tortoise dies, leave it for three days, then remove and burn to ash. Mix the ash with one *sheng* of fine wine to form a dry meal. Consume all at once, and shortly afterward, a large vomit will expel the cough sac, effecting a cure. Children may take half a *sheng*.

**Another formula:**
Prepare three live tortoises as for eating, remove the intestines, and boil in five *sheng* of water to yield three *sheng*. Use this liquid to steep yeast and ferment four *sheng* of glutinous rice as usual. Drink two *sheng* to finish the batch. This will permanently resolve the condition.

**Another formula:**
Remove the head of a bat, burn until charred, grind into powder, and take with a drink.

**Attached Formulas**

**Sun Zhenren’s Formula for Cough:**
Burn *zao jia*, grind into powder, and take two *qianbi* with fermented soybean broth.

**Ten Complete Salvation Formulas for Cough:**
Take one large *tian nan xing* (*Arisaema*), roast until cracked, and grind into powder. For each dose, take one large *qian*, boil in one *zhan* of water with three slices of fresh ginger until reduced to five *fen*, and take warm on an empty stomach at midday and before bedtime.

**Qie Zhong Fang’s Cough-Soothing Lozenge:**
Take one *liang* of *ting li* seeds from Caozhou, roast on paper until black. Add one *liang* each of *zhi mu* (*Anemarrhena*) and *bei mu* (*Fritillaria*). Grind together, then mix with half a *liang* of jujube pulp and one and a half *liang* of melted rock sugar. Form into pills the size of bullets. For each dose, wrap one pill in fresh silk and hold in the mouth, slowly swallowing the saliva. Severe cases require no more than three pills. *Modern physicians also frequently use this formula.*

**Cui Zhiti’s Fumigation Method for Chronic Cough:**
Each morning, take a portion of *kuan dong hua* (*Tussilago*) the size of a chicken egg, mix with a little honey to moisten, and place in a one-*sheng* iron pot. Use a clay bowl with a drilled hole, inserting a small bamboo tube (a brush handle will suffice). The tube should be slightly long, and the bowl and pot should fit snugly. Seal the joint with mud to prevent air leaks. Place charcoal beneath the pot. After a short time, smoke from the *kuan dong hua* will emerge from the tube. Hold the tube in the mouth and inhale the smoke, swallowing it. If chest discomfort arises, lift the head and pinch the tube to prevent smoke leakage. Inhale until the smoke is exhausted. Perform this once every five days. On the sixth day, eat a full meal of mutton noodles, and the condition will resolve permanently.

**Sheng Jin Fang’s Golden Millet Pill for Chronic, Sudden, or Consumptive Cough:**
Grind one *liang* of *ci huang* (*orpiment*) finely. Use paper-mud to seal a small box, ensuring the mud is not too thick, and let dry. Place the powdered *ci huang* inside, seal the box with water-mixed *chi shi zhi* (*halloysite*), and apply an additional layer of mud. Once dry, place the box on the ground and surround it with charcoal the size of *tanzi* bullets to form a mound. Ignite the charcoal from above, using a flatiron to cover the top, and let the fire gradually intensify. When one-third of the charcoal has burned, check if the *tanzi* pieces are uniformly red. If so, remove the fire and let cool. Open the box to retrieve the medicine, which should resemble a mirror’s surface—bright and red. Grind finely in a mortar, then mix with a water-soaked *bing* cake center to form pills the size of millet grains. Take three to five pills with licorice water, then rest for a while. *Excellent.*

**Cui Yuanliang’s *Remedies from the Sea*:**

A singularly effective formula for coughs: Take a fine pear, remove its core, and pound to extract one teacup of juice. Add forty Sichuan peppercorns, bring to a single boil, then strain. Immediately add one large *liang* of black maltose, dissolve completely, and slowly hold in the mouth to swallow. It will take effect at once.

Meng Shen states: For sudden coughing, take one pear and pierce fifty holes in it. Insert one Sichuan peppercorn into each hole, wrap in dough, and roast in hot ashes until done. Allow to cool, remove the peppercorns, and eat the pear.

Another formula: Remove the core of a pear, fill with *su* (ghee) and honey, wrap in dough, and roast until done. Eat.

Another formula: Stew pear flesh in *su* until tender, allow to cool, and eat.

Another formula: Pound one *sheng* of pear juice, one *liang* of *su*, one *liang* of honey, and one *sheng* of rehmannia juice. Simmer over a gentle fire and slowly hold in the mouth to swallow.

For all cough treatments, wait until the breathing has settled before eating, as consuming while hot will cause harm. Those with cold-induced coughs are beyond remedy. In such cases, prepare a mutton broth with noodles, eat to satiety, then lie down briefly.

**From the *Qianjin Fang*:**
To treat coughing with counterflow *qi* in children and adults: Take three *sheng* of apricot kernels, remove skins and tips, and stir-fry until yellow. Pound into a paste, add one *sheng* of honey, and divide into three portions. Mix one portion with the apricot kernels, pound to the proper consistency, then add the next portion, and pound again until smooth. Finally, add the last portion and pound thoroughly. Take before meals, holding in the mouth to swallow the juice.

**From *Yang’s Obstetrics and Pediatrics*:**
A formula for urgent fullness in the chest, making it difficult to sit or lie down: Take one large *liang* of turtle shell, roast until yellow, and grind finely into powder. Steep one handful of *dengxin* (rush pith) in two *sheng* of water, decoct to five *ge*, and take one *qianbi* before meals. After meals, take one *qianbi* with honey water.

**From Liu Yuxi’s *Transmitted Reliable Formulas*:**
Li Ya’s remedy for all coughs and counterflow *qi*: Use dried ginger—only the finest from Taizhou—along with *zaojia* (Chinese honey locust), roasted and peeled, selecting plump, unperforated pods. Also use *guixin* (cassia bark), choosing the purple, pungent variety, peeled. Pound each ingredient separately, sift, then weigh equal parts (quantity as desired). Combine, pound and sift again, then blend with refined white honey. Pound twenty to thirty times. Take three pills per dose, slightly larger than *wutong* seeds. Take whenever coughing occurs, three to five times daily, without regard to meals. Avoid onions, oil, salt, fish, and hot wheat noodles. The effect is divine.

Liu was in Huainan on the same staff as Li. Li often dispensed medicine without revealing the formula. When criticized for stinginess, Li explained: “Most people with coughs take cold medicines. If they saw this formula’s hot, drying ingredients, they would refuse to take it. That is why I only provide the medicine, and it proves effective.” Trials confirmed its reliability.

**From *Concise and Effective Remedies for the Multitudes*:**
To treat lung *qi* panting and coughing: Take two *liang* of *madouling* (birthwort fruit), using only the inner seeds and discarding the husk. Add half a *liang* of *su*, mix well in a bowl, and stir-fry over a slow fire until dry. Add one *liang* of roasted licorice, grind both into powder, and take one *qian* per dose. Decoct in one cup of water to six *fen*, and sip warm. Alternatively, hold the powder in the mouth and swallow the saliva.

For phlegm-induced coughing with urgent panting: Take one and a half *liang* of *jiegeng* (platycodon root), grind into powder, and decoct in half a *sheng* of boys’ urine to four *ge*. Strain and take warm.

Yang Wenwei’s formula for phlegm-induced coughing and chest congestion: Select a large, plump *guālóu* (trichosanthes fruit), cut open, clean the seeds, crush, and scrape the peel. Slice finely and dry by baking. Take forty-nine *banxia* (pinellia rhizomes), wash ten times in hot water, crush, and dry by baking. Grind into powder, then simmer with the *guālóu* pulp and water used to wash it until it forms a paste. Grind finely into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take twenty pills with ginger decoction.

**From the *Master Shen’s Formulas*:**
For chronic cough with counterflow *qi*, bodily swelling, shortness of breath, fullness, inability to lie flat, and constant frog-like croaking: *Baiqian* decoction governs this. Take two *liang* of *baiqian* (willowleaf swallowwort rhizome), three *liang* each of *ziwan* (tatarian aster root) and washed *banxia*, and seven *ge* of *daji* (euphorbia root). Slice, steep in one *dou* of water overnight, then decoct the next day to three *sheng*. Divide into three doses. Avoid mutton and maltose for best results.

**From *Master Mei’s Formulas*:**
For chronic *xiā* coughing with wheezing and sleeplessness: Grind *baiqian* into powder and take two *qianbi* with warm wine.

Another formula for counterflow *qi* coughing with wheezing, gasping, and sticky phlegm: Soak indigo leaves in water for a long time, pound, and extract one *sheng* of juice. Take on an empty stomach in one dose. Shortly after, grind apricot kernels to extract juice and cook porridge to eat. Rest for one or two days, then repeat the treatment until phlegm is fully expelled.

**From the *Military Ministry’s Handbook*:**
For coughing with counterflow *qi*, shortness of breath, and chest rattling in children and adults, with coughing up of foul, purulent phlegm: Take one *ge* of *danzhuli* (bamboo sap) three to five times daily. Adults may take one *sheng*.

**From the *Sagely Benefit Formulas*:**
To treat sinew and vessel damage with urgent counterflow *qi* and coughing: Take twenty jujubes, remove pits, and simmer in four *liang* of *su* over a low fire until the *su* is fully absorbed. Hold one jujube in the mouth at a time and swallow slowly.

**From the *Tested Later Formulas*:**
To suppress panting and dissolve phlegm: Take forty-nine pig trotter nails, wash and dry thoroughly. Place half a *zi* each of *banxia* and alum into each nail, seal in a jar to prevent smoke from escaping, and calcine until red-hot. Remove from fire, grind finely, and add one *qianbi* of musk. For those with upper panting and coughing, take with glutinous rice water. Children take half a *qian*. Most effective.

**From the *Divine Garden Formulas*:**
To treat coughing with urgent counterflow *qi*, panting, coughing of blood, and spitting of blood: Take high-quality ginseng, pound into powder, and administer three *qianbi* per dose, mixed with egg white. Take at the fifth watch, then lie down without a pillow, supine. A single dose often suffices; for chronic cases, take again. Avoid raw, salty, pickled, or fermented foods, soy sauce, wheat-based dishes, and overindulgence in food or drink. Convalesce well.

Xi Yan once treated deficiency with internal heat, coughing of pus and blood, and dry mouth and throat, where cold-natured medicines could not be taken. Take four *liang* of fine astragalus and one *liang* of licorice, grind into powder, and take three *qian* per dose, infused like tea or added to porridge or gruel.

**From Du Ren’s Formulas:**
To treat heat in the upper burner with sores in the mouth, tongue, and throat, and coughing of pus and blood: Take one *liang* of platycodon and two *liang* of licorice, grind into powder, and administer two *qian* per dose. Decoct in one cup of water until six-tenths remain, strain, and take warm after meals, sipping slowly. Also treats lung congestion.

**From the *Tested Formulas*:**
For severe coughing, or fresh blood in sputum: Take one *jin* of mulberry root bark, soak in a rice-washed pot for three nights, scrape off the yellow outer layer, and slice finely. Add four *liang* of glutinous rice, dry over a low fire, then grind together into powder. Take one to two *qian* per dose, mixed with rice water.

**From the *Doumen Formulas*:**
To treat lung rupture with incessant coughing of blood: Take a large piece of *hai xi* paste, roast over fire until charred yellow, then coat with *su* and roast again, repeating until fully permeated. Grind into powder, dissolve three large *qianbi* in hot water, and administer. The bleeding will cease. (This refers to *shui jiao*, highly effective.)

**From the *Heart Mirror of Dietary Medicine*:**
To address counterflow *qi*, coughing, chest and diaphragm fullness, and panting: Take three *liang* of peach kernels, remove skins and tips, grind with one *sheng* of water to extract juice, and cook with two *ge* of polished rice into congee. Consume.

Also, to treat all lung ailments with incessant coughing of pus and blood: Take five *jin* of fine *su*, melt and clarify three times, then allow to congeal. The resulting *tihu* (purest essence) will yield one *ge* per dose, which is curative.

Also, to address chronic counterflow *qi*, coughing, copious phlegm, panting, and spitting of pus and blood: Take one *ge* of radish seeds, grind, decoct in water, and take before meals.
