**Section Fourteen: Formulas for Sudden Generalized Swelling and Fullness**

**For sudden swelling and fullness, with the entire body and face grossly enlarged:**
Take one large carp and three *sheng* of undiluted wine, simmer until the wine is fully absorbed, then consume the fish. Do not add vinegar, salt, fermented beans, or other ingredients. No more than two or three doses are needed for recovery.

Another formula: Moxibust three cones on the white flesh below the inner ankle. Effective.

Another formula: Take one *dou* of soybeans, cook thoroughly, strain, and drink the broth while eating the beans. A few doses will suffice; red beans are especially effective.

Another formula: Mix egg yolk and white, apply to swollen areas, and reapply as it dries.

Another formula: Chop apricot leaves, decoct until concentrated, and soak the affected area while hot. May also be taken internally.

Another formula: Take ten kernels from within plum pits, grind thoroughly, and mix with three *ge* of polished rice. Decoct in four *sheng* of water to make congee, reducing to two *sheng*, and consume. For subsequent doses, increase the number of kernels.

Another formula: Take one *sheng* of soybeans, decoct in five *sheng* of water until two *sheng* remain, discard the beans, add eight *sheng* of wine, and further decoct to nine *sheng*. Divide into three or four doses. After swelling subsides, avoid excessive drinking if thirsty.

Another formula: Take three *sheng* of ox urine in one dose; swelling will lessen. If unresolved, take again.

Another formula: Take one *jin* of *zhanglu* root, peel and slice thinly, decoct until soft, discard the dregs, and add one *jin* of mutton, scallions, fermented beans, and salt, prepared as a meal. Consume freely. After swelling subsides, this may still be taken regularly. Alternatively, pound *zhanglu* and mix half with rice to steam into cakes for consumption.

Another formula: Take one pig kidney, divide into seven pieces, dust with one *fen* of *gansui* powder, and roast until cooked. Consume one piece daily for four to five days until bowel sounds and increased urination are noted. If not, continue until finished. Remove the skin before eating, and consume entirely for best results. Do not eat salt. If incomplete, repeat the course.

Another formula: Slice two *sheng* of *zhanglu*, steep in three *sheng* of wine for three nights, and take five *ge* to one *sheng* three times daily. This formula treats all types of fullness, whether from deficiency *qi*, wind-cold *qi*, or water-damp *qi*.

**For swelling that enters the abdomen, causing severe fullness and distress, impairing food intake:**
Take two *liang* each of *daji* and *wuzhi* powder, grind, mix with honey, and form pills the size of *tong* seeds. Take two pills at dawn; as swelling gradually recedes, continue until resolved, then cease.

Another formula: Take ten *liang* of *tingli* seeds, three *liang* of *jiaomu*, three *liang* of *fuling*, and two *liang* of *wuzhuyu*, grind, mix with honey, and form pills the size of *tong* seeds. Take ten pills three times daily.

Another formula: Take one carp weighing five *jin*, decoct in two *dou* of water until one and a half *dou* remain, discard the fish, and add five *liang* of *zejie*, three *liang* of *fuling*, and three *sheng* of sliced mulberry root bark. Further decoct to four *sheng*, and divide into four doses. Urination will increase, and swelling will gradually subside.

Another formula: Peel and roast *zaojia* until yellow, chop three *sheng*, steep in one *dou* of wine, and decoct in a stone vessel until boiling. Take one *sheng* three times daily, preparing a new batch when finished.

If swelling is localized to a specific area, mix ash with water and apply. Reapply as it dries.

Another formula: Grind red beans and hemp seeds together, and apply to swollen areas.

Another formula: Boil *badou* in water, then dip a cloth in the liquid to wipe the affected area. Yao states: Take thirty *badou* seeds, crush with their husks, decoct in five *sheng* of water until two *sheng* remain, and wipe the swollen area five times daily. The swelling will diminish upon application. Avoid contact with the eyes and genitals. This treats sudden swelling of the body resembling bloating.

For general swelling: Chop scallions, boil until soft, and soak the affected area two to four times daily.

Another formula: Steep one *sheng* of *tusizi* in five *sheng* of wine for two or three nights, then take one *sheng* three times daily until cured.

If swelling begins in the feet and gradually ascends, entering the abdomen proves fatal. The following formula treats this: Boil one *hu* of small beans until thoroughly soft, yielding four to five *dou* of liquid. Soak the area below the knees in the warm decoction twice daily until the swelling fully subsides. If the swelling has already entered the abdomen, do not soak; instead, consume only the boiled small beans, avoiding rice, fish, and salt. Drink the small bean decoction exclusively. In the absence of small beans, soybeans may be substituted. This condition is critical, with only one in ten surviving—treatment must be administered urgently.

Another formula: Shave paulownia or tung wood, boil to extract the juice, and soak the affected area while drinking a small amount. Adding small beans enhances efficacy.

Another formula: Finely chop one fresh pig’s liver and consume it at once. Do not consume with salt. Vinegar may be used for improved results.

Another formula: Drink boiled *chi* decoction and apply the dregs to the feet.

**Additional Formulas:**
From *Beiji Fang* (Emergency Remedies): For sudden full-body swelling, pound elm bark into flakes, mix with rice to make porridge, and consume to promote urination.

From *Yangshi Chanru* (Yang’s Obstetrics and Pediatrics): For generalized swelling with inhibited urination, grind five *liang* of *zhuling* into powder, decoct in three *ge* of water, and take one *fangcunbi* dose, increasing to two if needed.

From *Shiyi Xinjing* (Heart Mirror of Dietary Medicine): For qi panting, puffy swelling, and scanty urination, take one *liang* of apricot kernels, remove the tips and skins, stir-fry, grind, and cook with rice into a thick porridge. Consume two *ge* on an empty stomach.

*Ge Xianweng Zhouhou Beiji Fang*, Volume Three, concludes.

**Ge Xianweng’s *Zhouhou Beiji Fang*, Volume Four**
**Chapter Twenty-Five: Remedies for Sudden Onset of Massive Abdominal Water Disease**

At the onset of water disease, swelling first appears above the eyes like the back of an old silkworm moth, with discoloration flanking the head’s vessels. The inner thighs grow cold, the shins become full, and pressing leaves an indentation. When turning the abdomen, a sound of shifting nodes is heard—these are its signs.

If left untreated, the body gradually swells, and the abdomen becomes fully distended. Pressing causes the flesh to rebound—by this stage, the disease has taken hold, though it may still be treated. Such conditions often arise from depletion following major illness, after diarrhea, in women post-childbirth, or when water intake is not promptly dispersed. The Triple Burner is afflicted, urination obstructed, and gradual accumulation binds together, eventually flowing into the channels and network vessels.

**Remedies:**

1. Take one *sheng* of *tingli* (tingli seeds), stir-fry, and pound in a mortar. Slit open a live male mandarin duck, mix its blood and head with the *tingli*, and pound ten thousand times. Form into pills the size of parasol-tree seeds, starting with five and gradually increasing to ten. Avoid salt. Regularly consume rice with adzuki beans and drink adzuki bean broth; snakehead fish is also beneficial.

2. Another formula: One *liang* each of *fangfeng* (saposhnikovia), *gancao* (licorice), and *tingli* (tingli seeds). Pound and mix with bitter wine to form pills the size of parasol-tree seeds. Take three pills, three times daily. Continue until the swelling subsides.

3. Another formula: Six *fen* of *xionghuang* (realgar), three *fen* of *shexiang* (musk), and two *fen* each of *gansui* (kan-sui), *yuanhua* (genkwa), and *renshen* (ginseng). Pound and mix with honey to form pills the size of soybeans. Take two pills, increasing to four. Recovery will follow.

Another formula: Soak two *sheng* of *tingli* seeds in five *sheng* of spring wine overnight. Take one *ge* at a time; urination will become unobstructed.

Another formula: One *liang* of *tingli* and twenty apricot kernels, stir-fried until yellow. Pound and divide into ten doses. Once urination is restored, recovery will follow immediately.

Another formula: *Hu Qia’s* "Mercury Pills," highly effective for water swelling and promoting urination. As attested by Yao.

One *sheng* each of *tingli* and *jiaomu*, six *liang* of *mangxiao*, and ten *liang* of mercury. Boil the mercury in water for three days and nights, then combine and pound sixty thousand times. Form into pills the size of soybeans. Take three daily, increasing by one pill each day up to ten, then restart from one. After recovery, consume beef and mutton to restore strength, and drink in moderation.

Another formula: Gather and finely chop a large quantity of *ke* tree bark. Boil into a thick decoction and reduce until it can be formed into pills. Take three pills the size of parasol-tree seeds, then another after a short while. Water will be expelled. Later, take three pills three times daily. This tree is also called *munu* and is used by southerners to build boats.

Another formula: Equal parts genuine *suhexiang* (storax), mercury, and white lead, mixed with honey into pills. Take two pills the size of soybeans three times daily. Water will be expelled; regulate diet and rest well. If *suhexiang* is unavailable, omit it.

Another formula: Take twenty ripe castor beans, remove the skins, and grind. Mix with water to make three *ge* of liquid. Take once daily. Around midday, vomiting and diarrhea will expel accumulated water and fluids. If incomplete, take thirty beans three days later. If still incomplete, repeat the process. After recovery, regulate intake of fluids and salty foods.

Another formula: One *sheng* of adzuki beans and one white chicken, prepared as for eating. Boil in three *dou* of water until fully cooked. Consume the solids and drink the broth, gradually finishing all.

Another formula: Take a green-headed male duck and boil in five *sheng* of water until one *sheng* of broth remains. Drink gradually until finished. Cover thickly to induce sweating; this is beneficial.

Another formula: Swallow ten egg yolks from swallows’ eggs at once.

Another formula: Roast mole crickets until fully cooked and eat ten daily.

Another formula: For cases where only the abdomen is swollen, with fluid movement and gurgling sounds, and the skin turns black—this is called *water gu*. Take ninety *badou* (croton seeds), remove skins and hearts, and sixty apricot kernels, remove skins and tips. Stir-fry until yellow, pound together, and form into pills the size of small beans. Take one pill with water as needed. Wine may also be consumed; this is beneficial.

Another formula: Finely pound *guishan* (Chinese lobelia) and extract its juice. Drink an amount the size of a chicken egg to expel water, then treat the *water gu* again. Alternatively, grind hemp seeds into juice and drink.

Another formula: Boil thirty *jin* of *cimicao* (motherwort) and three *dan* of its seeds to obtain one *dan* of liquid. Strain and further reduce over heat until it can be formed into pills. Take three to five or six pills the size of *zaojia* seeds. Water will be expelled through urination; then consume thin rice porridge for nourishment.

Another formula: One large handful of white cogon grass roots and three *sheng* of adzuki beans. Boil in three *sheng* of water until dry, remove the grass roots, and eat the beans. Water will be expelled through urination.

Another formula: Ten *jin* each of *shuweicao* (common club moss) and *mabiancao* (European verbena). Boil in one *dan* of water to obtain five *dou* of liquid. Strain, further reduce, and mix with starch to form pills. Take two pills the size of soybeans, increasing to four or five. Avoid fatty meats and cold, raw foods.

For swelling and fullness: One handful of white mulberry tree bark, boiled in two *sheng* of water to obtain five *ge*. Grind two large white areca nuts into powder, add to the decoction, and boil for three to five more bubbles. Once done, add a small amount of *hongxue* (red snow) and consume. Also, under the section on swelling and fullness, formulas include drinking cow urine, *zhanglu* (pokeweed), mutton stew, and fragrant soft candies. The major formulas for the ten types of water swelling are recorded in a separate volume.

If water is only in the skin and not yet in the abdomen, take diaphoretic medicines to induce sweating for recovery. However, guard carefully against wind and cold. If only the abdomen is swollen and purgatives are ineffective, needle two *cun* below the navel, inserting several *fen* to drain the water. Stop when the puncture closes and the abdomen reduces.

**Attached Formulas**

From Li Jiang’s *Bingbu Shouji Fang*: A remedy for water disease, regardless of duration or severity, even with adverse pulses. One large *liang* each of *daji* (euphorbia), *danggui* (Chinese angelica), and *jupi* (tangerine peel). Chop and boil in one large *sheng* of water to obtain seven *ge*. Consume at once; two to three *dou* of water will be expelled. Do not be alarmed by the severity; recovery will follow after no more than two doses. Avoid toxic foods for one year. After water is expelled, take again to prevent recurrence. This formula originates from Zhang Shangke.

From *Waitai Miyao*: For water qi. Peel and chop white *zhanglu* (pokeweed) roots into pieces the size of small beans, one large cupful. Boil in three *sheng* of water to obtain one *sheng*. Once thoroughly cooked, add one large cup of millet and cook into porridge. Consume on an empty stomach. If taken twice daily, excessive purging may occur; once daily ensures mild purgation. Avoid mixed foods.

Another remedy for water disease with swelling: Take one very large carp, remove the head, tail, and bones, retaining only the flesh. Boil with two *dou* of water and one large *sheng* of adzuki beans. Reduce to two *sheng* of liquid, strain through cloth, and consume at once. If unable to finish, divide into two doses, warming the second. After consumption, diarrhea will follow; recovery occurs once purging ceases.

Another formula: For sudden swelling and fullness. There was a case of sudden foot and leg swelling, gradually ascending to the knees, making walking impossible. Eventually, the head and face swelled, and the entire body became bloated and distended. Take the white pulp of a bitter gourd, shape into pieces the size of soybeans, wrap in dough, and boil briefly. Consume seven on an empty stomach. By midday, a *dou* of water will be expelled. For three days, water will continue to drain, leading to significant emaciation and recovery. Maintain dietary caution for three years.

The bitter gourd must be of fine quality—smooth, unblemished, with fine and orderly veins. If not, it is toxic and should not be used.

From *Sheng Hui Fang*: To treat ten types of water retention in near-death cases, use half a *jin* of badger meat, sliced, with three *ge* of polished rice, three *sheng* of water, and cook into a porridge with scallions, Sichuan pepper, ginger, and fermented soybeans; consume.

Another formula: For ten types of water disease with swelling, fullness, panting, and inability to lie down, take five mole crickets, dry and grind into powder, and take half a *qianbi* to one *qian* before meals, mixed with hot water. When urination becomes unobstructed, the treatment is effective.

From *Shi Yi Xin Jing*: To treat ten types of water disease in near-death cases, take one green-headed duck, prepare as for eating, finely chop, and cook with rice and the five flavors into a very soft porridge; consume on an empty stomach.

Another formula: For water qi distension, swelling, and scant, difficult urination, take one white duck, remove feathers and intestines, wash thoroughly, and stuff with half a *sheng* of rice, ginger, and Sichuan pepper. Sew shut, steam according to method, and consume when done.

From *Yang Shi Chan Ru*: To treat bodily swelling, water qi urgency, and inability to lie down, take one large handful of *Prunus japonica* kernels, pound into powder, mix with wheat yeast, and form into cakes. Consume, and the bowels will promptly move, relieving qi and restoring health.

From *Mei Shi Fang*: To treat water swelling with inability to sit or lie down, and swelling of the head, face, and entire body, take mulberry branches growing eastward, burn to ash, leach with water, and use the liquid to cook red adzuki beans. Consume on an empty stomach until full, then eat when hungry until all are finished; do not consume rice.

Another formula: For water swelling and scant urination, drink one *sheng* of yellow ox urine. Within a day and night, urination will become unobstructed, and recovery will follow. Do not consume salt.

Another formula: For water beneath the heart, take three *liang* of *Atractylodes macrocephala* and five *liang* of *Alisma*, slice, decoct in three *sheng* of water until reduced to one and a half *sheng*, and divide for consumption.

From *Qian Jin Yi*: To treat inhibited urination and stagnant bladder water qi, dry *Spirodela polyrhiza* in the sun, grind into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* once or twice daily; effective.

From *Jing Yan Fang*: A proven formula transmitted by the Pei family of Hedong for water swelling and sudden swelling: Pound three *liang* of *Lepidium* six thousand times until pasty, then add four *liang* of *Stephania tetrandra* powder. Take a green-headed duck, decapitate it over the mortar, allowing the blood to drip in. Once the blood is fully drained, mix in the duck’s head and pound another five thousand times. Form into pills the size of *Firmiana* seeds. For severe cases, take ten pills on an empty stomach with plain hot water; for milder cases, take five. Take frequently, stopping after five days. This medicine promotes urination with miraculous efficacy.

From *Wei Zhou Du Xing Fang*: To treat water swelling that begins in the feet and ascends to the abdomen, which is fatal, cook one *dou* of red adzuki beans until extremely soft, take four to five *sheng* of the liquid, and soak the area below the knees in the warm broth. If the swelling has entered the abdomen, consume only the adzuki beans without other foods; this will also cure. Li Jiang’s *Bing Bu Shou Ji Fang* also records this method, which has proven effective.

**Section Twenty-Six: Formulas for Sudden Abdominal Masses**

For sudden, violent masses in the abdomen resembling stone, with stabbing pain and day-and-night wailing, if left untreated, death occurs within a hundred days. Formula: Steep two *jin* of *Achyranthes* in one *dou* of wine, seal tightly in hot ashes to warm and extract the flavor. Consume from five *ge* to one *sheng*, adjusting according to strength.

Another formula: Use *Sambucus* root in the same manner; even better.

Yao notes: *Achyranthes* wine is divinely effective.

Another formula: Take a large quantity of *Phytolacca* root, steam and pound it, then spread on new cloth placed over the abdomen (not directly on the skin). Replace when cool; do not cease day or night.

Another formula: On the fifth day of the fifth month, take ten *jin* of bottle gourd (peeled), one *chi* and two *cun* of cinnamon, and a duck-egg-sized lump of yellow earth from a stove. Pound together, mix with bitter wine, and apply to the afflicted area with cloth. Recovery occurs within three applications.

Another formula: Burn *Poncirus* wood to ash, leach with water to obtain eight *sheng* of liquid, and use to brew one *hu* of rice into wine. Begin with half a *ge*, gradually increasing to one or two *sheng* if no effect is observed. All cases are cured before finishing one batch. This ash is also used in dyeing crimson; the leaves are used in brewing wine. *Poncirus* is pronounced *zhi ren*.

Generally, masses develop gradually. If suddenly noticed and already large and firm, they are difficult to treat. Abdominal masses and accumulations impair eating and lead to emaciation. Treatments often employ potent medicines like *Xian Bing*, *Yu Hu*, and the Eight Toxins. Here, only simple and accessible remedies are selected.

Take *Polygonum cuspidatum* root (avoid those whose shadow falls on water), gather over a *dan* in weight, pound thoroughly, and decoct to extract juice for making pills. Cook five to six *sheng* of glutinous rice into porridge, mix with the medicine, and consume at midday after applying the medicine. Recovery follows.

Another formula: Take one *sheng* of the root, pound a thousand times, steep in wine, and consume three times daily, starting with a small amount. This wine treats masses better than many potent medicines.

Another formula: Burn one *dan* of silkworm droppings with mulberry firewood to ash, leach with water five times, and place a one-*chi*-long live softshell turtle in the liquid to cook until thoroughly done. Remove bones, shred finely, and decoct further until pills can be formed. Take seven pills the size of *Firmiana* seeds, three times daily.

Another formula: Pound two *liang* of *Aconitum* and three hundred Sichuan peppercorns into powder, mix with egg white, and form into pills the size of hemp seeds. Begin with one pill, gradually increasing to the size of soybeans, with a maximum of three pills per dose.

Another formula: Take one large pig’s heart, cut open and remove blood, pound into powder, and add five grains of realgar, five *Shexiang* *musk* grains, and one hundred *Croton* seeds (remove hearts and skins, use raw). Sew the heart shut, place in a small copper vessel with good wine, and decoct until the heart is submerged and nearly dissolved. Add up to three *sheng* of wine as needed, decoct until the mixture can be formed into pills the size of hemp seeds. Take three pills, three times daily.

If the wine is exhausted yet the mixture remains undissolved, remove and pound it with honey to form pills—this is effective.

Another formula: Take half a *jin* of *Rhei Radix et Rhizoma* (rhubarb) powder, three *liang* of *Natrii Sulfas* (mirabilite), and one *jin* of honey. Combine and decoct over a gentle heat until the mixture can be formed into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take ten pills, three times daily.

**For treating turtle-like accumulations lodged beneath the heart, where the head and feet can be felt by hand and shift intermittently:**
Take a pair of white hens, fast them for one night, then the next morning feed them with fried rice cooked in lard. Collect their droppings, regardless of quantity, mix with urine in a copper vessel, and heat over a fire until dry. Pound into powder and take one *fangcunbi* spoonful, four to five times daily, until the accumulation is fully resolved. Continue feeding the hens to collect droppings until recovery is complete, then slaughter and consume the hens alone.

**For treating an object beneath the heart, large as a cup, preventing food intake:**
Take two *liang* of *Descurainiae Semen* (tingli seed), stir-fried, two *liang* of *Rhei Radix et Rhizoma* (rhubarb), and four *liang* of *Euphorbiae Helioscopiae Herba* (zeqi). Pound, sift, and form into honey pills, pounding a thousand times. Take two pills the size of *wutong* seeds, three times daily, gradually increasing the dose.

Formulas for *xian*-like accumulations, *bingzhe*-ghost accumulations, and other such pills are recorded separately in the major formulas.

**For treating qi bind beneath the ribs:**
Take two *liang* of *Euphorbiae Ebracteolatae Radix* (langdu), one *liang* of *Inulae Flos* (xuanfuhua), and two *liang* of *Aconiti Radix Lateralis Praeparata* (prepared fuzi). Pound, sift, and form into honey pills. Take two pills the size of *wutong* seeds, gradually increasing to three pills.

**Moxibustion method for accumulations:**
Use a copper vessel holding about two *sheng*, fill with fish oil to a depth of two to three *cun*, and prepare six or seven large moxa cones. Ignite the cones to warm the oil, cover the accumulation with heavy paper, and apply the vessel to press and warm it. Continue day and night without pause; replenish the oil as it depletes.

Another formula: Crush three *sheng* of *Zanthoxyli Pericarpium* (zhuyu), mix with wine, and boil until cooked. Wrap in cloth and apply to the accumulation. Replace when cool, and continue until the accumulation shifts away. Persist in warming until it fully resolves.

Alternatively, use fine *Zanthoxyli Pericarpium* powder mixed with egg white and *Aconiti Kusnezoffii Radix* (shegong) for oral intake.

Another formula: Take one *sheng* of yellow earth from a stove, pound thoroughly, then add more and pound again. Moisten with bitter wine until damp, apply to one side of a cloth, and place over the afflicted area. Replace when dry until the accumulation resolves.

**For treating women with accumulations beneath the navel, large as a cup or *sheng*, obstructing menstruation, causing intermittent pain, diarrhea, emaciation, and weakness—this is qi *jia*. If the mass feels firm and unyielding upon palpation, it is a flesh accumulation and incurable; if not, it may be treated.**
Take one *jin* of *Toxicodendri Resina* (dried lacquer) powder and thirty *jin* of fresh *Rehmanniae Radix* (dihuang). Pound the *dihuang* to extract its juice, then decoct the lacquer powder in the juice until it can be formed into pills. Take three pills the size of *wutong* seeds after meals, three times daily, until resolved.

**Additional Formulas**

From *Waitai Miyao Fang*:
**For treating chronic accumulations in the heart and abdomen, or sudden-onset accumulations:**
Grind *Cinnabaris* (zhusha) finely and mix with rice to form a red paste. Take a rooster, starve it for three days, then feed it the red rice. Secure the rooster to a board and collect its droppings. Dry in the sun, grind into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* to two *qian* spoonfuls with warm clear wine, three times daily. For severe cases, take up to six doses day and night. If one rooster’s droppings are insufficient, feed another until enough is collected. Discontinue upon recovery.

Another formula: **For treating accumulations in the abdomen from fish, meat, or other toxins:**
Burn five *sheng* of dog feces to ash, wrap in silk, and steep in five *sheng* of wine for two nights. Strain and divide into ten doses, taking two daily initially, then three daily until finished. The accumulation will be expelled according to the ingested substance.

From *Qianjin Fang*:
**For treating undigested fish or raw meat lodged in the chest and diaphragm, leading to accumulations:**
Pound *Verbenae Herba* (mabiancao) to extract one *sheng* of juice and drink. Ginger water may also be used; the accumulation will dissolve immediately.

Another formula: **For treating flesh accumulations with insatiable cravings for meat:**
Drink three *sheng* of white horse urine on an empty stomach. The patient will vomit the flesh; if it does not emerge, death will follow.

From *Yaoxing Lun*:
**For treating *zheng* and *pi* diseases:**
Grind equal parts *Trionycis Carapax* (bie jia), *Chebulae Fructus Pericarpium* (helile skin), and *Zingiberis Rhizoma* (dried ginger) into powder and form into pills. Take thirty pills on an empty stomach, twice daily.

During the reign of Emperor Ming of the Song, a palace woman suffered from lower back pain radiating to the heart, causing fainting during attacks. Xu Wenbo examined her and diagnosed a *jia* accumulation. He administered oil, inducing her to vomit a hair-like substance three *chi* long, with a head resembling a snake that writhed. It was hung up to drain completely, leaving only a single strand of hair.

From *Shengjin Fang*:
**For treating qi outside the membranes and qi masses:**
Grind *Corydalis Rhizoma* (yanhusuo) into powder without limit. Take one pig’s pancreas, cut into pieces, roast until cooked, and dip in the powder to consume.

**Chapter Twenty-Seven: Formulas for Cold Accumulations, Food and Drink Stagnation, and Bindings in the Heart and Abdomen**

**For treating cold accumulations in the abdomen, food and water stagnation, phlegm retention beneath the heart, fullness and distension in the ribs, gurgling upon palpation, and counterflow harming food intake:**
Take one large toad, remove its skin and internal organs, and dismember it. Use one *sheng* of *Natrii Sulfas* (mangxiao) for adults, seven *ge* for average individuals, and five *ge* for the weak or emaciated. Add six *sheng* of water, decoct to four *sheng*, and take one *sheng* per dose. If no purgation occurs after the first dose, take another *sheng*. Once purgation occurs, administer every nine or ten days.

Another formula: Take eight *liang* of *Zanthoxyli Pericarpium* (zhuyu), one *sheng* of *Nitrum* (xiaoshi), and one *jin* of fresh ginger. Decoct with five *sheng* of wine to four *sheng*. Take one *sheng* per dose; if no pain occurs, discontinue. Do not take a second dose. After purgation, provide good convalescent care.

Another formula: Take eight *liang* of *Rhei Radix et Rhizoma* (dahuang) and four *liang* of *Descurainiae Semen* (tingli seed), both stir-fried, and four *liang* of *Natrii Sulfas* (mangxiao), stir-fried until dry. Pound thoroughly and form into honey pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take three pills after meals, gradually increasing to five pills.

Another formula: Take three *liang* of *Euphorbiae Ebracteolatae Radix* (langdu), one *liang* of *Aconiti Radix Lateralis Praeparata* (fuzi), and three *liang* of *Inulae Flos* (xuanfuhua). Pound, form into honey pills, and take three pills the size of *wutong* seeds before meals, three times daily.

Another formula: Take thirty *Crotonis Fructus* (badou), remove the kernels, and twenty *Armeniacae Semen* (xingren), stir-fry both. Add six *fen* of *Platycodonis Radix* (jiegeng), four *fen* of *Veratri Radix et Rhizoma* (lilu), and three *fen* of *Gleditsiae Fructus* (zaojia), all roasted. Pound thoroughly, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *hudou* beans. Take one pill before meals, twice daily. For purging, take two pills. With prolonged convalescent care, full recovery may be achieved in a hundred days.

Another formula: Take two *liang* of *Fritillariae Bulbus* (beimu), two *liang* of *Platycodonis Radix* (jiegeng), one *liang* of *Alumen* (fanshi), and one *liang* of *Crotonis Fructus* (badou), removing kernels and skin for raw use. Pound a thousand times, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take two pills per dose; reduce dosage slightly after recovery.

Another formula: Take one *liang* of *Poria* (fuling) and three *liang* of *Zanthoxyli Pericarpium* (zhuyu). Pound, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take five pills, three times daily.

Another formula for sudden retention of undigested food and lingering fluids causing abdominal distress: Take three *liang* each of *Rhei Radix et Rhizoma* (dahuang), *Poria* (fuling), and *Natrii Sulfas* (mangxiao), and one *fen* of *Crotonis Fructus* (badou). Pound, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take two pills per dose; discontinue if no pain occurs.

Another formula: Take two *liang* of *Zanthoxyli Semen* (jiaomu) and one *liang* of *Crotonis Fructus* (badou), removing skin and kernels, stir-fried. Pound and form into pills the size of *sesame seeds* with jujube paste. Take two pills; discontinue when pain subsides.

Another formula: Take one *Crotonis Fructus* (badou), remove kernel and skin, stir-fry, along with fourteen *Zanthoxyli Semen* (jiaomu) and sixteen *Sojae Semen Praeparatum* (chi). Pound together to form pills. Take two pills to induce vomiting and diarrhea. If incomplete, take two more pills. Purging with *Sishen Wan* is also effective.

*Zhonghou Hei Wan* is the foremost remedy for all accumulations, congealed phlegm, and sores. Take four *fen* each of *Platycodonis Radix* (jiegeng) and *Cinnamomi Cortex* (gui), eight *fen* of *Crotonis Fructus* (badou) with kernels and skin removed, five *fen* of *Armeniacae Semen* (xingren) with skin removed, and twelve *fen* of *Genkwa Flos* (yuanhua), all stir-fried until purplish. First pound the three ingredients into powder, then pound *Crotonis Fructus* and *Armeniacae Semen* into a paste. Combine and pound two thousand times, forming pills the size of *hudou* beans. Take one pill to induce purgation, increasing to two or three pills as needed. For infants ten days old with convulsions, administer one or two pills the size of millet grains. For any abdominal discomfort or perceived bodily distress, take immediately; one or two bouts of purgation will bring relief.

*Sulphur Pills*, extremely warming, treat severe internal cold where even in summer one cannot remove clothing. Take equal parts of *Sulphur* (liuhuang), *Alumen* (fanshi), *Zingiberis Rhizoma* (ganjiang), *Zanthoxyli Pericarpium* (zhuyu), *Cinnamomi Cortex* (gui), *Aconiti Radix* (wutou), *Aconiti Radix Lateralis Praeparata* (fuzi), *Zanthoxyli Pericarpium* (jiao), *Ginseng Radix* (renshen), *Asari Radix et Rhizoma* (xixin), *Gleditsiae Fructus* (zaojia), and *Angelicae Sinensis Radix* (danggui), adjusting quantity as needed. Pound, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take ten to twenty pills, three times daily. For cold-induced diarrhea, add *Halloysitum Rubrum* (chishizhi) and *Fossilia Ossis Mastodi* (longgu) for immediate relief.

*Lusuxing Wan* treats severe cold accumulations. Take three *liang* each of *Alumen* (fanshi), *Zingiberis Rhizoma* (ganjiang), *Cinnamomi Cortex* (gui), *Platycodonis Radix* (jiegeng), roasted *Aconiti Radix Lateralis Praeparata* (fuzi), and *Gleditsiae Fructus* (zaojia). Pound, sift, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds with honey. Take ten pills with wine, increasing to fifteen pills.

Supplementary formulas.

From *Waatai Miyao*: Formula for Masses (Pĭ).
Ten *liang* of *Rhei Radix et Rhizoma* (dahuang), pound, sift, mix evenly with three *sheng* of vinegar, and two spoonfuls of white honey. Simmer until pliable for pill-making, forming pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take thirty pills with fresh ginger decoction, adjusting to induce purgation; reduce dosage for milder cases.

From *Shenghui Fang*: Formula for *Fu Liang* Qi Lodged Beneath the Heart, Congealing and Unresolved.
Use two *liang* of *Persicae Fructus Immaturus* (taonu), ground to powder. Take two *qianbi* on an empty stomach, mixed with warm wine.

From *Jianyao Jizhong*: Formula for Long-standing Cold Accumulation with Inability to Eat, Persistent Vomiting, and Cold in the Stomach.
Five *liang* of *Pinelliae Rhizoma* (banxia), washed, ground to powder. For each dose, take two *qian* of powder with one *liang* of white flour, kneaded with water and cut into dice-shaped pieces. Boil in water until the flour is cooked, then consume with fresh ginger and vinegar.

**Chapter Twenty-Eight: Formulas for Phlegm-Rheum and Obstructions in the Chest and Diaphragm**

Formula for Sudden Splitting Headache, Neither from Cold Strike nor Wind Strike.
Four *fen* of *Fu Yue Xia Mo* (soot from beneath a cauldron), three *fen* of *Aconiti Radix Lateralis* (fuzi), and one *fen* of *Cinnamomi Cortex* (gui). Pound, sift, and take one *fangcunbi* with cold water to induce vomiting.
An alternate formula omits *gui*.
Another formula: equal parts *Sophorae Flavescentis Radix* (kushen), *gui*, and *banxia*. Pound, sift, mix with bitter wine, and apply topically; pain will cease.
Another formula: thirty *Mume Fructus* (wumei), a three-finger pinch of salt, and three *sheng* of wine. Boil to reduce to one *sheng*, strain, and consume in one draught to induce vomiting; this cures the condition. Originally listed among miscellaneous treatments, this ailment arises from phlegm reversal and qi surging upward in the chest and diaphragm, termed "reversal headache." Vomiting provides immediate relief.
Alternatively, cook rice into a thick gruel of two to three *sheng*, adjust to lukewarm temperature, and drink entirely. After a short while, induce vomiting; once vomiting ceases, drink again. Repeat several times. In severe cases, continue until bile is vomited. This method is harmless and immediately effective.

Formula for Copious Phlegm in the Chest, Headache with Loss of Appetite, and Stagnant Phlegm upon Drinking Alcohol.
Two *liang* of *Dichroae Radix* (changshan), one *liang* of *Glycyrrhizae Radix* (gancao), one *liang* of *Usneae Herba* (songluo), and twenty-one *Trichosanthis Fructus* (guadi). Boil in one and a half *sheng* each of wine and water to reduce to one and a half *sheng*. Initially take seven *ge*; induce vomiting. If vomiting is incomplete, divide the remainder into two doses. Later, take *Pinelliae Decoction* (Banxia Tang).

From *Hu Qia*: Named *Fen Ge Tang* (Powder-Barrier Decoction).
One *liang* of *Alumen* (fanshi) and two *sheng* of water, boiled to reduce to one *sheng*. Add half a *ge* of honey and consume in one draught. If vomiting does not occur shortly after, drink a small amount of hot water.

Another formula: three *liang* each of *Asari Herba* (duheng) and *songluo*, and thirty *guadi*. Steep in one *sheng* and two *ge* of wine for two nights, strain, and take five *ge* warm. If vomiting does not occur after the first dose, take another in the evening.

Another formula: one *liang* of *guadi* and four *liang* of *Phaseoli Semen* (chixiaodou), ground to powder. Mix with three *ge* of warm water and consume, then lie down quietly. If vomiting is desired but does not occur, take another dose.

Another formula: first prepare one *sheng* of boiling water, then add one *sheng* of cold water, naming it "raw-cooked water." Consume three *ge* of salt, followed by this water. After a short while, vomiting will commence; manually induce it. If incomplete, take another two *ge* of salt and two *sheng* of water afterward. Alternatively, take more water; vomiting will not recur.

Another formula: four *liang* of *changshan* and half a *liang* of *gancao*. Boil in seven *sheng* of water to reduce to three *sheng*, then add half a *sheng* of honey. Take one *sheng*; if vomiting does not occur, take another dose. Honey may be omitted.
Consuming one of these formulas monthly prevents phlegm-fluid afflictions.
There is also *Xuanfu Wuyin* (Five Drinks with *Inulae Flos*), found in the major formulas.

For Chest Obstruction with Cold, Shortness of Breath, and *Bi* (stifling sensation).
*Bi* is pronounced *fubi*.
Two *liang* of *gancao*, three *liang* of *Poria* (fuling), and fifty crushed *Armeniacae Semen* (xingren). Boil in one *dou* and three *sheng* of water to reduce to six *sheng*, divided into five doses.

Another formula: four *liang* of *gui*, two *liang* each of *Atractylodis Macrocephalae Rhizoma* (bai zhu) and *gancao*, and roasted *fuzi*. Boil in six *sheng* of water to reduce to three *sheng*, divided into three doses.

For Concretions in the Diaphragm, Perceived as Persistent and Unyielding.
One *liang* of *Veratri Nigri Radix et Rhizoma* (lilu), roasted and ground to powder, and half a *liang* of *Crotonis Fructus* (badou), husked and stir-fried. First pound *badou* into a paste, then add *lilu* powder and pound ten thousand times. Form into honey pills the size of sesame seeds. Take one to two or three pills.
The disease of the diaphragm is termed *gaohuang* (vital region). Decoctions and pills pass through directly, while acupuncture and moxibustion cannot reach it. Thus, pills are made for oral retention, allowing the qi and efficacy to permeate and fumigate. There is a *Wuge Wan* (Five Diaphragm Pills) formula:
Ten parts of *Ophiopogonis Radix* (maidong), deseeded, ten parts of roasted *gancao*, six parts each of *Zanthoxyli Pericarpium* (jiaomu), *Polygalae Radix* (yuanzhi), roasted *fuzi*, *Zingiberis Rhizoma* (ganjiang), *Ginseng Radix* (renshen), *gui*, and *Asari Radix et Rhizoma* (xixin). Pound, sift, and form into pills the size of a bullet with high-quality honey. Retain one pill in the mouth, gradually swallowing its juice, three pills daily. This governs shortness of breath, chest fullness, hardness beneath the heart, and cold qi.
There are over ten formulas for this condition, most being similar. This pill is the most effective. Though its ingredients are numerous, it does not align with the names of the five diaphragms—*youge* (worry diaphragm), *qige* (qi diaphragm), *huige* (anger diaphragm), and *hange* (cold diaphragm)—each with distinct diagnostic signs. In the major formulas, there is also *Qiqi Fang* (Seven Qi Formula), largely similar with minor differences.

**Supplementary Formulas**

From *Shenghui Fang*: Formula for Phlegm Reversal Headache.
Take the flesh of ten *wumei*, two *qian* of salt, and one *zhongzhan* of wine. Simmer to reduce to seven *fen*, strain, and take warm at any time; vomiting is beneficial.

Another formula: Formula for Cold Phlegm-Rheum with Nausea.
One *liang* of *Piperis Longi Fructus* (bibo), ground to powder. Take half a *qian* before meals, mixed with clear rice gruel.

Another formula: Formula for Phlegm Congestion with Retching, Chest Fullness, and Inability to Eat.
One *liang* of *Magnoliae Officinalis Cortex* (houpo), coated with fresh ginger juice and roasted until yellow, then ground to powder. Take two *qianbi* at any time, mixed with rice gruel.

From *Qianjin Yifang*: On treating phlegm-rheum with spontaneous vomiting of water. When cold drinks are consumed excessively, the spleen and stomach become weakened in qi, unable to digest food and drink. Whatever enters the stomach transforms into cold water and is incessantly vomited. **Red Halloysite Powder** governs this. Take one *jin* of *red halloysite*, pound and sift, and take one *fangcunbi* with wine or water as preferred. Gradually increase to three *bi*; upon finishing one *jin*, one will never again vomit clear water, nor suffer from diarrhea, and the five viscera will be fortified, rendering the person robust and healthy. There was a case of phlegm-rheum unresponsive to various remedies, which was cured by this formula.

From *Imperial Pharmacy Formulary*: **True Ancestor’s Elixir**, bestowed by Emperor Zhenzong upon the Grand Chancellor Gao, dispels phlegm, clears the eyes, and stimulates appetite. Take ten *liang* of *Sichuan lovage rhizome* (chuanxiong), selecting the firm and small pieces, soak in a clay pot with millet water for three days, changing the water daily, then slice and dry in the sun. Grind to powder and divide into two portions. To each portion add one *fen* each of musk and borneol, and half a *liang* of *raw rhinoceros horn*, boiled in a double boiler. Knead with honey into pills the size of small marbles. Chew and swallow one pill with tea or wine.
- For phlegm, add half a *liang* of *cinnabar*;
- For thoracic congestion, add one *fen* each of *cow-bezoar* and *water-floated iron powder*;
- For dizziness and blurred vision, add one *fen* of *asarum*;
- For facial paralysis, add one *fen* of *blast-fried arisaema*.

Another formula for thoracic congestion with wind-phlegm: Take any quantity of *pinellia*, soak in sour juice overnight, then wash five to seven times in warm water to remove the foul odor. Dry in the sun, pound to powder, and mix with fermented millet water into cakes. Dry in the sun, then grind to powder again. For every five *liang*, add one *qian* of *raw borneol*, grind evenly, and use thick fermented millet water to form pills the size of *chicken’s heads*. Store in a gauze bag in a well-ventilated, shaded place to dry. Take one pill with good tea or peppermint decoction.

From Wang’s *Boji*: For disharmony of the triple burner qi, thoracic congestion, dizziness, blurred vision, copious phlegm and saliva, and mental lethargy. **Diaphragm-Freeing Pill**: Take four *liang* of *pharbitis seed*, half raw and half parched, and two *liang* of *Gleditsia sinensis* (unworm-eaten, coated with butter and roasted). Grind to powder, boil with fresh ginger juice, and form into pills the size of *tung seeds*. Take twenty pills with *schizonepeta* decoction.

From *Tested Later Formulas*: For head wind transforming phlegm. Take any quantity of *Sichuan lovage rhizome*, wash clean, soak, slice thinly, and dry in the sun or bake. Pound to powder and form into pills with refined honey the size of small marbles. Chew and swallow at any time with tea or wine.

Another formula for wind-phlegm: Take one *fen* of *curcuma* and ten *fen* of *veratrum*, grind each to powder, mix evenly, and take one *zi* with a cup of warm fermented millet water. First dissolve a small amount in the water, then swallow the rest, rinsing the mouth with the remaining water. Follow with food to press it down.

From *Waitai Miyao*: For all wind-phlegm, wind cholera, indigestion, and constipation. Take three *myrobalan* fruits, pound to powder, and take all at once with wine three to five times; effective.

From *Shengjin Fang*: For wind-phlegm. Take seven *white stiff silkworms* (straight ones), grind finely, and administer with one *chabiao* of ginger juice mixed with warm water.

Another formula for wind-phlegm: Grind *radish seeds* to powder and take one spoonful with warm water. After a while, phlegm and foam will be vomited. For paralysis and slack wind, follow this emetic with a purgative, then take a qi-harmonizing powder to recover.

From *Doumen Fang*: For thoracic congestion and stagnation, dispelling phlegm and opening the stomach. Wash *pinellia* clean, bake dry, and pound to powder. Mix with fresh ginger juice into cakes, wrap in damp paper, and bake over a slow fire until fragrant. Boil one cake the size of a marble in two cups of water with half a *qian* of salt, reducing to one cup. Take warm to dispel thoracic congestion and counterflow, strongly suppress phlegm toxin, and treat damage from alcohol and food; highly effective.

**Formula Twenty-Nine for Sudden Thoracic Impediment Pain**
Thoracic impediment causes the heart to feel firm, stuffy, and suddenly painful, with the muscles suffering from numbness and tightness as if stabbed, preventing bending or stretching. The skin over the chest is painful to the touch, with thoracic fullness, shortness of breath, coughing-induced pain, vexation, spontaneous sweating, or pain radiating to the back and spine. If left untreated, it can be fatal within days.
- **Treatment Formula**: Take *realgar* and *croton seed*; pound the *realgar* finely, sift, add *croton seed*, and pound thoroughly. Form into pills the size of small beans. Take one pill; if ineffective, gradually increase the dose.
- Another formula: Pound *immature bitter orange* and take one *fangcunbi* three times daily and once at night.
- Another formula: Take one large *trichosanthes fruit*, slice, and combine with half a *sheng* of *Chinese chive*. Boil in seven *sheng* of white wine, reducing to two *sheng*, and take in two divided doses. Alternatively, add four *liang* of *pinellia* (washed in hot water to remove sliminess).
- Another formula: Boil half a *jin* of *tangerine peel*, four *immature bitter oranges*, and half a *jin* of *fresh ginger* in four *sheng* of water, reducing to two *sheng*, and take in two divided doses.
- Another formula: Take equal parts *immature bitter orange* and *cinnamon*, pound to powder, and take one *fangcunbi* with *tangerine peel* decoction three times daily. A divine formula from *Zhang Ji*.
- Another formula: Take one *fen* each of *cinnamon*, *aconite*, and *dried ginger*, and two *fen* each of *ginseng*, *asarum*, *evodia*, and *fritillaria*. Pound together, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of small beans. Take three pills three times daily.
- If the condition relapses after recovery: Pound five *jin* of *leek roots*, extract the juice, and drink to cure.

**Supplementary Formulas**
*Du Ren’s* treatment for chest and diaphragm pain radiating to the back, abdominal fullness and distension with obstructed qi, and phlegm cough.

**Trichosanthes Root Formula**
Remove the pulp from *trichosanthes* (大栝楼), take the seeds, stir-fry until ripe, grind separately, then combine with the seed husks. Mix with wheat-flour paste to form pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take fifteen pills with rice broth.

**Formula Thirty: Sudden Stomach Reversal with Retching and Vomiting**
*Ge’s* formula for sudden incessant dry retching:
Crack open a chicken egg, discard the white, and swallow several yolks—this will cure it.

Another formula: Pound *kudzu root*, extract the juice, and take one *sheng*.

Another formula: Some say to take one *sheng* of warm sugarcane juice, three times daily.

Another formula: Take one *sheng* of fresh ginger juice.

Another formula: Moxa the point between the two tendons on the posterior wrist, called *Wenliu*, seven cones on each side. Moxa *Xinzhu* (尺泽) on the *Heart Governor* channel—also effective.

Another formula: Two *liang* each of *licorice* and *ginseng*, four *liang* of fresh ginger. Boil in six *sheng* of water, reduce to two *sheng*, and divide into three doses.

**Formula for Sudden Retching, Vomiting, and Counterflow Cold of the Limbs**
Take half a *jin* of fresh ginger (peeled and sliced) and four *liang* of *tangerine peel* (broken into pieces). Boil in seven *sheng* of water, reduce to three *sheng*, strain, and take one *sheng* at a suitable temperature, three times daily.

Another formula: Cut *yingyu* vine to release its sap, collect in a vessel, and drink one *sheng*. Fresh *kudzu* vine is especially effective.

**Formula for Sudden Uncontrollable Retching**
Drink several *sheng* of freshly drawn well water—highly effective.

Another formula: The condition arises from qi stagnation between the eyebrows and the bridge of the nose.

Another formula: Insert a small object about one *fen* deep into each nostril, then place *soap bean* inside to induce sneezing—this will cure it.

Another formula: Simply hold the breath and tilt the head back.

Another formula: Boil two *sheng* of fine *fermented soybeans* to extract the juice and drink it.

Another formula: Boil *fragrant perilla* (香苏) and *licorice* (激) to make a decoction, and take one to two *sheng*—effective.

Another formula: Grind three *sheng* of *non-glutinous millet* into powder and take with well-drawn water—effective.

Another formula: Use one *jin* of *loquat leaves* (wipe off the fuzz, then roast), boil in one *dou* of water, reduce to three *sheng*, and take. *Reed rhizome* is also effective.

**Formula for Frequent Vomiting After Eating**
Burn two *liang* of *deer antler* to ash, combine with one *liang* of *ginseng*, grind into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* three times daily. *Yao* concurs.

**Formula for Sudden Persistent Nausea**
Half a *jin* of *Chinese scallion* (薤白), one *liang* of *evodia*, half a *sheng* of *fermented soybeans*, one *ge* of rice, four *jujubes*, two *immature bitter oranges*, and a salt pellet the size of a bullet. Boil in three *sheng* of water, reduce to one and a half *sheng*, and divide into three doses.

Another formula: Simply chew *cardamom seeds* or *areca nut*—also effective.

**Formula for Stomach Reversal Where Food Cannot Be Retained and Is Immediately Vomited**
Four *liang* of *rhubarb*, two *liang* of *licorice*. Boil in two *sheng* of water, reduce to one and a half *sheng*, and divide into two doses.

**Formula for Belching Sourness or Acid Reflux After Eating**
One *liang* of *ginseng*, half a *jin* of *evodia*, six *liang* of fresh ginger, twelve *jujubes*. Boil in six *sheng* of water, reduce to two *sheng*, and divide into two doses.

For incessant hiccups: Wash *pinellia*, dry, and grind into powder. Take one *bi*—this will immediately stop it.

Another formula: Six *fen* of dried ginger, four *fen* of *aconite* (roasted). Grind, mix with bitter wine, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take three pills three times daily—effective.

**Supplementary Formulas**
*Zhang Zhongjing’s* formula: *Major Pinellia Decoction* for stomach reversal and vomiting.
Three *sheng* of *pinellia*, three *liang* of *ginseng*, one *sheng* of white honey. Add one *dou* and two *sheng* of water, decoct while stirring one hundred and twenty times, then reduce to three and a half *sheng*. Take one *sheng* warm, twice daily. Also treats phlegm-rheum in the diaphragm.

Another formula: For vomiting, hiccups, inability to retain food, dizziness, and palpitations—*Pinellia Decoction with Poria*.
One *sheng* of *pinellia*, half a *jin* of fresh ginger, three *liang* of *poria*. Slice, boil in seven *sheng* of water, reduce to one and a half *sheng*, and divide into warm doses.

*Qianjin Fang*: For stomach reversal where food is immediately vomited.
Pound *millet* into powder, mix with water to form pills the size of *wutong* seeds—seven pills. Boil thoroughly, then swallow slowly with vinegar. The condition will resolve once the pills descend. Wheat flour may also be used.

Another formula: For dry hiccups with cold counterflow of the hands and feet—eat fresh ginger. This is the sagely medicine for vomiting.

**Formula for Epigastric Fullness and Hardness, Inability to Eat, and Chest Hiccups**
Eight *liang* of fresh ginger (finely sliced), boil in three *sheng* of water, reduce to one *sheng*. Five *ge* of *pinellia* (washed to remove sliminess), boil in five *sheng* of water, reduce to one *sheng*. Combine the two decoctions, reduce to one and a half *sheng*, and take in small doses.

Another formula: For dry retching—take one cup of goat’s milk on an empty stomach.

*Doumen Fang*: For stomach reversal.
Take one large *aconite* tuber, place on a brick, and heat from all sides until it cracks. Soak in fresh ginger juice, then heat again until dry, repeating until the ginger juice is nearly exhausted (about half a bowl). Grind into powder and take one *qian* with *millet* broth. The condition will resolve in no more than three doses.

*Jingyan Fang*: *Powder for Vomiting and Stomach Reversal*.
One large *aconite* tuber, one *jin* of fresh ginger (finely minced). Boil and grind into a fine paste, then take with rice broth.

Another formula: For persistent vomiting in men or women where porridge, food, or medicine cannot be retained—*Effective Rubbing Pill* for this condition.
Use *flying squirrel droppings* (五灵脂), selecting only the pure, high-quality kind (free of soil or stones). Grind into powder, mix with dog bile, and form into pills the size of *chicken’s head* seeds. For each dose, take one pill, grind finely with hot ginger wine, then dissolve in a small amount of ginger wine. Prepare warm porridge in advance. With the left hand, administer the medicine to the patient (without letting them rinse their mouth), then immediately use the right hand to feed them the porridge—do not give too much.

Another formula: *Azure Radiance Elixir*, for immediate relief of vomiting and retching.
Take four *liang* of northern yellow lead (sifted), mix with half a *sheng* of fine rice vinegar, and place in a small pot. Simmer until dry, then heat with three *cheng* of charcoal fire until glowing red. Allow to cool, grind into fine powder, and form into millet-sized pills with cooked millet. Take seven pills with a decoction of fermented grains, without chewing, in a single dose.

From Sun Zhenren’s *Dietary Prohibitions*: For vomiting.
Take one white areca nut (roasted), one *fen* of tangerine peel (baked), grind into powder, and decoct in one *zhong* of water until half remains. Take the decoction.

From *Guangji Formulas*: For vomiting and retching with inability to eat.
Take two *liang* of chebulic myrobalan peel (remove pits, stir-fry), grind into powder, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take twenty pills on an empty stomach, twice daily.

From *The Heart Mirror of Food and Medicine*: For weak spleen and stomach *qi*, undigested food, vomiting, and regurgitation with inability to retain liquids.
Take half a *sheng* of millet, pound finely, mix with water, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Boil until cooked, add a pinch of salt, and swallow with the broth on an empty stomach.

From *The Golden Casket and Jade Case Formulas*: For the five types of dysphagia, *qi* stagnation in the heart and diaphragm, vexation, and vomiting with inability to eat.
Take five *liang* of reed rhizome (chopped), decoct in three large *zhong* of water until two *zhong* remain. Strain and take warm at any time.

From *The Outer Terrace Secret Essentials*: For regurgitation.
In my youth, I suffered from this ailment—every time I ate cakes, porridge, or soup, I would soon vomit it all back. During the Zhenguan era, the imperial physicians Xu and his brothers, as well as the renowned doctors of the Chai and Jiang families, were summoned to treat me. They exhausted their skills, yet none could cure me. I grew increasingly emaciated, and death seemed imminent. Then, a guard mentioned: "Drinking donkey urine is highly effective." I took two *ge* at dawn, and afterward, only half of my food was vomited. At dusk, I took another two *ge*, and by the first watch of the night, when I ate porridge, the vomiting ceased. By noon the next day, I reported this to the palace, where five or six others suffering from regurgitation were also cured after taking it together. This remedy is slightly toxic—do not exceed the dosage. Collect fresh, warm urine and take two *ge*. For severe cases of seven days or more, it works well. Many have since been cured with this method.

Another formula: For vomiting.
Take three *liang* of hemp seeds, pound, stir-fry, and extract the juice with water. Add a pinch of salt and consume. Instantly effective. Highly praised by Advisor Li.

Another formula: For chronic coughing fits with forty or fifty consecutive coughs.
Take half a *ge* of fresh ginger juice and one spoonful of honey, decoct until thick, and take warm. Three doses will bring immediate relief.

Another formula: For coughing.
Take four *liang* of fresh ginger (crushed), two *liang* of *lanxiang* leaves, one *qianbi* of pepper powder, and four *liang* of salted flour. Wrap the mixture in dough, bake into a flatbread, and consume on an empty stomach. No more than two or three doses are needed for efficacy.

From *Sun Shangyao’s Formulas*: For all types of hiccups.
Take two *liang* of tangerine peel (soaked in hot water to remove the pith, chopped), decoct in one *sheng* of water until five *ge* remain, and take hot in one dose. For greater effect, add one *liang* of *zhike* (remove pith, stir-fry) and decoct together.

From *Master Mei’s Formulas*: For stomach regurgitation, where food eaten in the morning is vomited in the evening, or food eaten in the evening is vomited in the morning, or vomiting occurs shortly after eating.
Mix seven *sheng* of sugarcane juice with one *sheng* of fresh ginger juice. Divide into three doses.

Another formula: For acid reflux.
Take four *liang* of areca nut and two *liang* of tangerine peel, grind finely into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* on an empty stomach with raw honey water.

From *The Military Ministry’s Handbook*: For acid reflux, where sour *qi* rises like strong vinegar.
Take one *ge* of evodia fruit, decoct in three *zhong* of water until seven *fen* remain, and take in one dose. Even if the decoction is strong, it must be consumed. Recently, a man whose heart felt as if stung by a bee took this formula and remained free of symptoms for twenty years.
