**Chapter Thirty-One: Sudden Onset of Jaundice and Various Yellow Diseases**

**Formulas for Jaundice:**
Take five *sheng* of turnip seeds, pound and sift, and take one *fangcunbi* three times daily. Recovery occurs within ten days.

Another formula: Burn human hair and take one *qianbi* three times daily.

Secret formula for jaundice.

Another formula: Pound fresh wheat seedlings, mix with water, and extract the juice. Take three *sheng*, with small wheat being superior to barley. Take six or seven *ge* per dose, three or four times daily. This treats alcohol-induced jaundice.

Another formula: Roast *lilu* in ashes until slightly discolored, pound, sift, and take half a *qianbi*. Mild vomiting may occur, but no more than a few doses are needed. This is a secret formula.

Another formula: Take two *fen* each of small beans, glutinous rice, and white chicken droppings, pound, sift, and divide into three doses. Yellow fluid will be discharged. This universally treats yellowing of the face and eyes, bringing immediate relief.

There are five types of jaundice: yellow jaundice, grain jaundice, alcohol jaundice, female jaundice, and taxation jaundice.

**For yellow sweat:** When the body and limbs are slightly swollen, the chest is full, and no sweat is produced—or sweat appears like the juice of *huangbo*—caused by sudden immersion in water after profuse sweating.
Take one *jin* of hot lard, consume warm, three times daily. When diarrhea occurs, gradual improvement follows.

Another formula: Take fifteen gardenia fruits, three *gualou* seeds, and three *fen* of *kushen*, grind into powder, soak two chicken eggs in bitter wine until soft, mix the yolks and whites with the powder, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take ten pills five or six times daily. If heat is relieved without vomiting, the condition will resolve on its own.

Another formula: Take one yellow hen, prepare it, and stuff with three *jin* of chopped fresh rehmannia root. Secure tightly, place in a copper vessel, and steam until thoroughly cooked. Extract the juice and take it twice.

Another formula: Take a handful of fresh cogongrass roots, finely chop, and cook with one *jin* of pork into a thick soup; consume it all.

Another formula: Burn oak bark into powder and take one *fangcunbi* spoonful, three times daily.

Another formula: Take one *chi* of licorice, fifteen gardenia fruits, and fifteen *fen* of *huangbo*; boil in four *sheng* of water until reduced to one and a half *sheng*, then divide into two doses.

This formula also treats warm diseases with jaundice.

Another formula: Take six *liang* of *yinchen*, boil in one *dou* and two *sheng* of water until reduced to six *sheng*, strain, add two *liang* of rhubarb and fourteen gardenia fruits, then boil until reduced to three *sheng*; divide into three doses.

Another formula: Take a handful of ephedra, boil in five *sheng* of wine until reduced to two and a half *sheng*, consume entirely to induce sweating and recovery. If the condition transforms into jaundice, death often follows; administer urgent treatment. Pound *tugua* root to extract juice and take one *sheng* in a single dose, up to three doses. When sweating occurs, the illness will be expelled through urine; if not, take more.

For grain jaundice—characterized by dizziness after eating, restlessness, and yellowing—caused by eating excessively while famished, which agitates the stomach *qi*, the following formula is used: Take four *liang* of *yinchen*, boil in one *dou* of water until reduced to six *sheng*, strain, add two *liang* of rhubarb and seven gardenia fruits, then boil until reduced to two *sheng*; divide into three doses. Recovery follows the passing of yellow urine.

Another formula: Grind three *liang* of *kushen* and one *ge* of gentian into powder, form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds with ox bile, and take five pills with fresh wheat juice, three times daily.

For wine jaundice—marked by heart vexation, swelling of the feet and shins, yellow urine, and red or dark-yellow patches upon drinking—caused by heavy intoxication followed by wind exposure and water immersion, the following formula is used: Take two *liang* of astragalus and one *liang* of magnolia bark, grind into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* spoonful with wine, three times daily.

Another formula: Take one *liang* of rhubarb, five *zhishi* fruits, seven gardenia fruits, and six *ge* of fermented soybeans; boil in six *sheng* of water until reduced to two *sheng*, then divide into three doses.

Another formula: Burn equal parts of *yuanhua* and *jiaomu* into powder and take half a *qian* once or twice daily.

For female taxation jaundice—characterized by yellowing of the body and eyes, fever, aversion to cold, fullness and tension in the lower abdomen, and difficulty urinating—caused by excessive exertion, intense heat, and intercourse followed by water immersion, the following formula is used: Grind equal parts of *xiaoshi* and *fanshi* into powder and take one *fangcunbi* spoonful with barley porridge, three times daily, to induce slight sweating. Yellow fluid will be expelled through urine.

Another formula: Take a bundle of tangled hair the size of a parrot’s egg and half a *jin* of lard; simmer until the hair dissolves completely, then divide into two doses.

**Additional Formulas**

From *Waitai Miyao*: For treating jaundice. Boil willow branches in one *dou* of water until reduced to a thick half-*sheng* of juice, then consume entirely.

Another formula: For yin jaundice where sweat stains clothes yellow and saliva is yellow. Pound turnip seeds into powder and take one spoonful at dawn with well water, twice daily, increasing to two spoonfuls until effective. Each night, soak a small piece of cloth in urine and mark the date; when the color fades to white, recovery is complete. No more than five *sheng* should be consumed.

*The Illustrated Canon* states: For jaundice and fox delusion disease, *Zhuling* Powder is the primary remedy. Grind equal parts of *zhuling*, *fuling*, and *zhu* into powder and take one *fangcunbi* spoonful with water.

*Dietary Therapy* states: For heart urgency and jaundice. Steam *baihe*, mix with honey, and consume; powdered form is especially effective. The red variety, called *shandan*, is inedible.

For treating jaundice: Take one large *liang* of *qinjiao*, finely chop, divide into two portions, and steep each in half a *sheng* of fine wine. Squeeze out the juice, discard the dregs, and take on an empty stomach in two doses. If diarrhea occurs, cease further doses. Those who tolerate wine well respond more readily. This formula, used by Cui Yuanliang, has proven highly effective in treating patients. *Qinjiao* must be fresh, high-quality, and net-veined.

From *Classified Essentials of the Cold Damage Canon*: For treating jaundice in men and women where medical treatment has failed, with yellowing of the ears and eyes, indigestion, abdominal distension, heat-generated yellow coating in the stomach, and dry stool causing the illness. Take one small *sheng* of rendered lard, warm, and consume in a single dose, three times daily. Recovery follows the passing of dry stool.

Another formula: For jaundice unresponsive to all remedies. Boil a donkey’s head until tender, consume with ginger relish, and drink the broth as desired.

Another formula: For jaundice where the body and eyes resemble gold. Avoid exposure to women, chickens, or dogs. Take a handful of eastward-growing peach roots, cut as fine as chopsticks or hairpins, boil in one large *sheng* of water until reduced to one small *sheng*, then consume warm on an empty stomach. After three to five days, the yellow will disperse like thin clouds, though the eyes recover last. Full restoration takes a hundred days. After the body’s yellow fades, occasional sips of clear wine may hasten the clearing of eye yellow; without it, recovery is slower. Avoid hot noodles, pork, and fish. This is a secret formula from Xu Zicai’s family.

From *Zhengyuan Guangli Fang*: For jaundice with heart vexation, heat, dry mouth, and yellowing of skin and flesh. Boil twelve *fen* of *qinjiao* in one large *sheng* of cow’s milk until reduced to seven *ge*, strain, and take warm in two doses. This formula originates from Xu Renze.

**Formulas for Sudden Onset of Lumbar and Hypochondriac Pain (Chapter Thirty-Two)**

**Ge Family’s Formulas for Sudden Lumbar Pain with Inability to Bend or Straighten:**
Stand upright and lean against a small bamboo stalk. Measure from the person’s sole to the navel, cut the bamboo to this length, then measure from the navel to the center of the spine. Moxibust the point at the top of the bamboo, applying cones equal to the patient’s age. After treatment, conceal the bamboo to prevent others from obtaining it.

**Alternative Formula:**
Burn a six-inch piece of deer antler, grind to powder, and take with wine. Deer velvet is especially effective.

**Another Formula:**
Roast one turtle shell, grind to powder, and take one *fangcunbi* after meals, three times daily.

**Another Formula:**
Grind eight *fen* of cinnamon, four *fen* of tree peony, and two *fen* of aconite into powder. Take one *daogui* with wine, twice daily.

**For Kidney Qi Deficiency and Debility with Lumbar and Spinal Pain, or Exposure to Wind and Damp Leading to Cold Invasion:**
If untreated, the condition may spread to the legs and knees, causing hemiplegia, cold impediment, or flaccid weakness. Treat promptly with the following formula:
Four *fen* of *duhuo*, one large aconite (roasted), eight *fen* each of *duzhong*, *fuling*, and *guixin*, six *fen* each of *niuxi*, *qinjiao*, *fangfeng*, *xiongqiong*, and *shaoyao*, five *fen* of *xixin*, and ten *fen* of dried rehmannia. Cut the ingredients, decoct in nine *sheng* of water until reduced to three *sheng*, and take warm in three divided doses on an empty stomach. After walking eight or nine *li*, take another dose. Avoidances as before. Consume three doses in succession.

**For Various Lumbar Pains, Including Kidney Deficiency and Cold with Lumbar Pain and Impotence:**
Grind equal parts of roasted *ganqi* (until smoke ceases), *bajitian* (with hearts removed), *duzhong*, and *niuxi*, along with eight *fen* each of *guixin*, *gouji*, and *duhuo*, ten *fen* each of *wujia pi*, *shanzhuyu*, and dried *shuyu*, and six *fen* of *fangfeng*, and four *fen* of aconite. Form into honeyed pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take twenty pills with wine on an empty stomach, twice daily, gradually increasing the dose until efficacy is achieved. Highly effective.

**For Hypochondriac Pain as if Struck:**
Stir-fry half a *sheng* of soybeans until charred, then boil in one *sheng* of good wine until bubbling. Drink to intoxication.

**Another Formula:**
Combine equal parts of *yuanhua* and chrysanthemum with half a *jin* of *zhizhu* flowers. Place in a cloth pouch, steam until hot, and apply as a compress to the painful area. Replace when cool.

**Another Formula:**
Moxibust seven cones one *cun* above the coccyx, then moxibust seven cones one *cun* to the left and right of this point.

**For Chronic Hypochondriac Pain with Occasional Flare-Ups:**
Grind ten *fen* of dried rehmannia, five *fen* each of licorice and *ganqi*, five *fen* of water, and a one-*chi* piece of cinnamon. Sift and take one *bi* with wine, three times daily.

**Another Formula:**
Collect *difuzi* in the sixth or seventh month, dry in the shade, grind to powder, and take one *fangcunbi* five or six times daily.

**For Lumbar Pain with Blood Stagnation:**
Grind approximately three *sheng* of *duzhong*, mix with vinegar, and apply to the painful area. Reapply when dry. Also, moxibust three cones at the white flesh border of the heel.

**For Acute Lumbar Sprain:**
Chew fresh *gegen* and swallow the juice; the more consumed, the better.

**Another Formula:**
Pound fresh rehmannia to extract three *sheng* of juice, decoct to two *sheng*, add one *sheng* of honey, and mix with one *sheng* of the decoction. Take three times daily. If unresolved, repeat the dose.

**Another Formula:**
Moxibust seven cones at the *yaoyan* point. Acute lumbar sprain resembles sudden lumbar strain with difficulty turning.

**For Persistent Lumbar Cold as if Wearing a Coin Belt:**
Decoct two *liang* each of licorice and dried ginger with four *liang* each of *fuling* and *baizhu* in five *sheng* of water until reduced to three *sheng*. Divide into three doses. The *Xiaopin* states: "This formula is warming."

**For Sudden Hypochondriac Pain as if Struck:**
Use a string to measure the distance between the nipples, then fold the string and measure from the nipple to the painful hypochondrium. Moxibust thirty cones at the folded point beneath the string. This method originally appeared in the *Miscellaneous Treatments* section.

**Yinjü’s Effective Formula for Lumbar and Back Pain:**
Cut one *jin* of *duzhong*, steep in two *dou* of wine for ten days, and take three *ge* per dose.

**Supplementary Formula from the *Qianjin Fang* for Lumbar and Leg Pain:**
Stir-fry one *sheng* of fresh sesame until fragrant, grind, and sift. Take one small *sheng* daily until one *dou* is consumed, ensuring permanent relief. May be taken with wine, honey water, or broth.

**From the *Xu Qianjin Fang* for Lumbar and Knee Pain from Injury:**
Roast *lurong* (quantity as available) with butter until purple, grind to powder, and take one *qianbi* with warm wine.

**From the *Jingyan Fang* for Lumbar and Leg Pain:**
Wash one *jin* of *weilingxian*, dry, steep in good wine for seven days, grind to powder, and form into *tongzi*-sized pills with flour paste. Take twenty pills with the medicated wine.

**From the *Jingyan Hou Fang* for Miraculous Lumbar Pain Relief:**
Grind *poguzhi* to powder and take three *qianbi* with warm wine.

**Another Formula for Kidney Deficiency with Lumbar and Leg Weakness:**
Store fresh chestnuts in a bag, hang to dry, and consume over ten at dawn, followed by pork kidney porridge.

**Another Formula for Chronic Lumbar and Knee Cold Pain or Numbness and Weakness in Men:**
Wash and weigh one *liang* of *tusizi* and one *liang* of *niuxi*, steep in a silver vessel with wine covering them by one *cun* for five days, dry in the sun, and grind to powder. Mix with the original steeping wine and a small amount of fresh wine to form a paste, then roll into *wutong* seed-sized pills. Take twenty pills with wine on an empty stomach.

**From the *Waitai Miyao* for Lumbar Pain:**
Roast a yellow dog’s hide and wrap it around the painful lumbar area until thoroughly warmed. Repeat for relief. Xu Boyu’s formula is identical.

**From the *Doumen Fang* for Lumbar Pain:**
Cut half a *liang* of rhubarb and half a *liang* of fresh ginger into small pieces, stir-fry in a pan until yellow, add two bowls of water, and consume at the fifth watch. By dawn, the patient will pass dark, liver-like blood clots from the lumbar region into a basin, after which the pain will cease.

Another formula for heavy lumbar pain:
Grind *binglang* (areca nut) into powder and take one *qian* with wine.

**From the *Meishi Fang* for Sudden Lumbar Pain with Inability to Turn:**
Take one deer antler, five *cun* in length, and two *sheng* of wine. Burn the antler until red-hot, then steep it in the wine overnight. Drink the infusion.

**From Cui Yuanliang’s *Haishang Fang* for Cold Wind Qi in the Lumbar and Legs:**
Cut two large *liang* of rhubarb into pieces the size of *weiqi* stones, stir-fry with a small amount of *su* (ghee) until the *su* is fully absorbed. Take care not to scorch the rhubarb, as this will diminish its potency. Grind into powder and sift. Each day, on an empty stomach, boil three *ge* of water with two coin-sized slices of fresh ginger for over ten simmers. Remove the ginger, then take two *qian* of rhubarb powder, place it in a separate bowl, and mix with the ginger decoction. Consume in one draught. If any ginger decoction remains, sip it slowly until finished. This will purge copious cold pus and foul matter, and the ailment will be cured upon cessation.

Ancient physicians used potent medicines to attack illnesses, always adjusting dosages according to the patient’s strength and condition—they did not apply them indiscriminately. When Yao Sengyuan first served at court, Emperor Wu of Liang developed a fever and wished to take rhubarb. Sengyuan advised, “Rhubarb is a swift-acting purgative; Your Majesty is advanced in years and should not use it lightly.” The emperor disregarded his counsel and nearly collapsed. Later, Emperor Yuan suffered from a thoracic and abdominal ailment. All the physicians insisted that mild medicines should be used gradually to harmonize and unblock. Sengyuan, however, declared, “The pulse is surging and replete—this indicates retained food. Without rhubarb, there is no hope of recovery.” The emperor followed his advice and recovered.

From this, we see that modern physicians often use a single potent medicine to treat myriad illnesses. When they happen to cure a condition, they deem the formula miraculous, yet when they err, they never acknowledge their misapplication of the medicine. Such practitioners are legion—how can one not take heed!

**Cultivating the True Formulae: Divine Immortal Recipes**

**Cuscuta Seed Elixir**
Take one *dou* of cuscuta seeds and one *dou* of wine; steep for a long while, then strain and dry in the sun. Repeat the steeping until the wine is exhausted. Each dose consists of two *qian*, taken with warm wine, twice daily. Afterward, consume three to five spoonfuls of rice porridge to aid absorption. After twenty-one days, increase the dose to three *qian* per serving. This elixir bestows a radiant complexion, and after three years, the old shall revert to youth. It also treats lumbar and knee ailments, dispels wind, and with prolonged use, extends lifespan.

**Formula Thirty-Three: Remedy for Debilitation, Emaciation, and Inability to Endure Labor**
For those with a long-standing predisposition to overwork, whose suffering manifests upon exertion—causing pain throughout the body, joints, and skin, or inducing heat and tendon tension—proceed as follows:
Take a one-*chi* length of root from the southeast side of a white *zhe* tree. Scrape off the outer bark, retaining the inner layer. Burn it to ashes or finely chop and pound it. Take three *fangcunbi* with wine, then cover thickly to induce sweating. Administer thrice daily. If wine is unavailable, use fermented grain water instead.
*(Note: The white *zhe* is a thornless variety of *zhe*.)*

**Formula for Sudden Prolonged Insomnia**
At dusk, heat a new cloth over fire and use it to warm the eyes.

**Additionally, steam large soybeans, then alternate filling pillows with them. When the pillow cools, replace it with a warm one. Sleeping through the night with a pillow of hot soybeans will bring immediate relief.**

**These two remedies originally appeared in the Miscellaneous Treatments section. Both address depletion from overwork. Though not immediately critical, if left untreated, such conditions gradually consume the person. Later efforts to restore health require several times the effort, so these methods are recorded here in brief.**

**For men and women suffering from chronic depletion due to overwork, or those who fail to recover after severe illness—manifesting as heaviness in the limbs, aching bones and muscles, shortness of breath, panting upon movement, or tension in the lower abdomen, stiffness in the back and waist, palpitations, dry throat and lips, pallor, loss of appetite, debility of yin and yang, melancholy, excessive sleep, and prolonged inactivity—if untreated for years or even a hundred days, they gradually grow emaciated, the qi of the five viscera depletes, and recovery becomes difficult.**

**Decoction Formula:**
Two *liang* of licorice, three *liang* of cinnamon, four *liang* of peony, five *liang* of fresh ginger (dried ginger may be substituted), and twenty-one jujubes. Boil in nine *sheng* of water until reduced to three *sheng*. Strain, add eight *liang* of maltose, and divide into three doses. Prepare another dose every other day.
*For enhanced efficacy, add two* liang *each of astragalus and ginseng.*
*If phlegm congestion or loose stools occur, omit the maltose.*

**Another Formula:**
Prepare one black hen as for cooking. Stuff its belly with one *jin* of sliced fresh rehmannia and two *sheng* of maltose. Secure tightly, place in a copper vessel, and steam with five *sheng* of rice until done. Consume the meat and broth without salt. Repeat thrice monthly.
*Yao comments: "Divinely effective." Also stops night sweats.*

**Another Formula:**
One *liang* of licorice, four *liang* of white atractylodes, four *liang* of ophiopogon, two *liang* of oyster shell, and twenty jujubes. Boil in eight *sheng* of water until reduced to two *sheng*. Take in two doses.

**Another Formula:**
Three *liang* each of astragalus, lycium root bark, and fresh ginger; two *liang* each of licorice, ophiopogon, and cinnamon; and three *ge* of raw rice. Boil in nine *sheng* of water until reduced to three *sheng*. Divide into four doses.

**Another Formula:**
Slice one sheep kidney and one *sheng* of atractylodes. Boil in one *dou* of water until reduced to nine *sheng*. Take one *sheng* two or three times daily, finishing in one day. In winter, divide into two days, taking twice daily.

**Additional formulas include the Center-Fortifying Kidney-Draining Decoction and various pill recipes.**

**Rehmannia Pill:**
Four *liang* of dried rehmannia, two *liang* each of poria, dioscorea, cinnamon, moutan, and cornus, and one *liang* each of aconite and alisma. Grind into powder, form into phoenix-tree-seed-sized honey pills. Take seven pills thrice daily, increasing to ten pills.
*This is Zhang Zhongjing’s Eight-Ingredient Kidney Qi Pill, which treats depletion and insufficiency, severe fluid retention, lumbar pain, lower abdominal tension, and urinary difficulty.*
*For long-term use, omit aconite and add schisandra.*

**For Severe Wind-Cold:**
One *sheng* each of sophora, coptis, calamus, plantago seed, honeysuckle, and lycium fruit. Grind, form into phoenix-tree-seed-sized honey pills. Take ten pills thrice daily.

**Kidney Qi Bolus Formula and Powder Recipes:**

**Bolus Formula:**
One *jin* of atractylodes, half a *jin* of cinnamon, four *liang* each of dried rehmannia, alisma, and poria. Grind, sift, and take one *fangcunbi* with water, two or three times daily.

**Another Formula:**
Two *jin* of fresh rehmannia and one *jin* of wheat flour. Grind, stir-fry until dry, sift, and take one *fangcunbi* with wine thrice daily.

**Appended Formulas**

**Lycium Berry Wine:**
Tonifies depletion, promotes muscle growth, enhances complexion, strengthens the body, and dispels taxation heat.
Steep five *sheng* of fresh lycium berries in two *dou* of good wine. Crush, mix well, and infuse for seven days. Strain and drink, beginning with three *ge* and adjusting to taste.
*Agrees with* Wai Tai Mi Yao*.*

**Dietary Therapy:**
*Tonifies depletion, treats lung taxation, quenches thirst, and dispels wind-heat.*
Use asparagus: remove skin and heart, cook with honey, and consume after meals. For superior results, dry in the sun and form into honey pills. Also excellent for facial washing.

**Another Formula:**
Mix sparrow egg white with powdered aconite and cuscuta to form pills. Take five pills with wine on an empty stomach.
*Treats male impotence, female vaginal discharge, urinary difficulty, eliminates hernial masses, abscesses, and swelling, and restores the qi of the five viscera.*

**Empirical Formula:**
*Warms essence-qi and benefits primordial yang.*
Grind equal parts of white dragon bone and polygala into powder. Form into phoenix-tree-seed-sized honey pills. Take thirty pills with cold water before bedtime.

**Another Formula:**
*Eliminates night sweats and genital sweating.*
Apply powdered oyster shell to sweaty areas.

**Later Empirical Formula:**
*Treats five taxations and seven injuries, yang-qi debility, and weak lumbar and legs.*
Prepare a stew with one pair of sheep kidneys (remove fat and membranes), one *liang* of cistanche (soaked in wine overnight, peeled, and sliced). Cook as usual with scallions, salt, and seasonings. Consume on an empty stomach.

**Another Formula:**
*Treats five taxations and seven injuries in men and women, chronic cold in the lower origin, blackens hair, dispels all wind diseases, relieves limb pain, preserves complexion, and strengthens qi.*
Soak one *jin* of psoralea in wine overnight, dry, then stir-fry with one *sheng* of black sesame until the sesame pops. Sift out the sesame, grind the psoralea into powder, and form into phoenix-tree-seed-sized pills with vinegar-cooked wheat paste. Take twenty pills in the morning with warm wine or salted water.

**Another Formula: "Firm Yang Elixir"**
Take two *liang* of dodder seeds, soak in wine for ten days, rinse with water, dry by baking, and grind into powder. Add one *liang* of eucommia bark (honey-toasted and pounded), then mix with powdered Chinese yam cooked in wine to form a paste. Roll into phoenix-tree-seed-sized pills. Take fifty pills on an empty stomach with wine.

*From* **Shi Yi Xin Jing**: *To strengthen men, invigorate yang, and relieve cold in the legs and knees.*
Soak one *jin* of epimedium in one *dou* of wine for three days; drinking it is excellent.

*From* **Yu Yao Yuan**: *Treats wind-dampness in the feet and knees, deficiency sweating, lack of strength, frequent pain, and genital sweating.*
Burn alum into ash, grind finely, and take one spoonful. Steep in boiling water and rinse the painful areas.

*From* **Wai Tai Mi Yao**: *To supplement deficiency taxation, replenish marrow, promote muscle growth, brighten complexion, and induce robust health.*
Toast deer antler glue, pound into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* with wine, three times daily.

**Another [formula] for bone steaming:**
Take 120 peach kernels (remove skins, discard double kernels, retain the tips), pound and form into pills. At dawn, take all with well-flower water in one dose. Afterward, drink wine to intoxication and consume water—more is better. Take another dose every other day. Avoid meat for one hundred days.

**Bone steaming is also called "internal steaming."** The term "internal" signifies external cold with internal heat clinging to the bones. Its root lies within the five viscera and six bowels. Symptoms may include dry, lusterless skin, gradual thinning of the limbs, and swollen feet during steaming episodes.
Grind gypsum into a fine powder (like milk), mix with water, and take one *fangcunbi* twice daily until the body feels cool.

*From* **Cui Yuanliang’s Hai Shang Fang**: *Treats bone steaming and ghostly qi.*
Take five *dou* of boys’ urine (settled) and five *dou* of green wormwood (harvested in the eighth or ninth month, with seeds, finely chopped). Combine the two, place in a large cauldron, and boil vigorously to reduce to three *dou*. Strain, clean the cauldron thoroughly, return the liquid, and simmer gently to reduce to two *dou*. Add ten pig gallbladders, simmer to one and a half *dou*, then remove from heat and cool. Store in a new ceramic vessel. Before each dose, toast and grind two to three *liang* of licorice, mix with the decoction, and pound one thousand times to form pills. Take twenty pills on an empty stomach with rice porridge, gradually increasing to thirty pills.

**Formula Thirty-Four: Treating Spleen-Stomach Deficiency and Inability to Eat**

**For sudden food illness resembling cold damage, where the patient only desires to lie down—untreated for seven or eight days, it may prove fatal:**
Locate the sunken areas on either side of the spine and moxa each depression at both ends with seven cones; this will cure it.

**For undigested fish or raw meat lodged in the chest and diaphragm, unvomitable and unpassable, risking concretion:**
Take *puxiao* the size of half a chicken egg and one *liang* of rhubarb. Chop the two ingredients, boil in two *sheng* of wine to reduce to one *sheng*, strain, and consume entirely; it will dissolve immediately. If *puxiao* is unavailable, substitute *mangxiao*; either may be used.

**For indigestion from raw or cold foods, or exposure to wind while lightly clothed, or lying down immediately after eating, causing vexation, fullness, and pain in the heart and abdomen, or prolonged non-digestion:**
Heat the ground until scorching, spread a thin mat of *wan* grass, lie down facing east, and cover to induce sweating; this will cure it immediately.

**For post-meal fullness, vexation, and drowsiness with abdominal distension:**
Toast flour until fragrant, pound, and take one *fangcunbi*. Fresh barley flour is even better; if unavailable, *mi* (coarse grain) may suffice.

**These four entries originally appeared in the "Wei Ye" section, all pertaining to dietary and spleen-stomach matters. When stomach qi is full and strong, food-related ailments will never arise. Dietary care should first address the root, hence the subsequent enumeration of methods.**

**For abdominal deficiency-cold, inability to eat, and undigested food, leading to emaciation, weakness in the limbs, and the onset of myriad illnesses:**
Take ten *jin* of fresh rehmannia, pound to extract juice, and mix with three *jin* of fine flour. Dry in the sun, then re-mix with juice until exhausted. After meals, take half a *ge*, three times daily, gradually increasing to three *ge*.

**Another formula:**
Toast half a *jin* of flour, five *sheng* of wheat bran, five *ge* of fermented soybeans, and two *sheng* of apricot kernels until yellow and fragrant. Pound, sift, and form into pills the size of bullets. Take one pill, gradually increasing the dose.

**Another formula:**
Pound half a *jin* each of rhubarb and peony root into powder, add half a *jin* of *mangxiao*, and mix with three *jin* of honey. Simmer in a copper vessel over a water bath to form phoenix-tree-seed-sized pills. Take seven to ten pills.

**Another formula:**
Pound one *jin* of yeast, ten *liang* of dried ginger, and one *ge* of evodia, then mix with honey to form pills the size of bullets. Take three times daily.

**Another formula:**
Toast two *jin* of atractylodes and one *jin* of yeast until yellow, pound, and form into phoenix-tree-seed-sized pills with honey. Take thirty pills, three times daily.
For severe cold, add three *liang* of dried ginger.
For abdominal pain, add three *liang* of Chinese angelica.
For emaciation, add two *liang* of licorice.
Maintain long-term care, gradually employing the yeast-atractylodes method.

**For postpartum water retention in the heart region, requiring purgation:**
**For spleen-stomach qi deficiency, preventing food from descending and leading to anorexia:**
Pound and sift three *sheng* of hemp seeds with roasted soybeans (fragrant and yellow). Take one to two *fangcunbi* before meals, four to five times daily; this is excellent.

**For post-meal drowsiness causing "grain taxation," with heavy, fatigued limbs, taciturnity, and increased symptoms after eating:**
Toast one *sheng* of barley bran and one *liang* of Sichuan pepper, add three *liang* of dried ginger, pound into powder, and take one *fangcunbi* three to four times daily.

**Additional Prescriptions**

From *The Heart Mirror of Food as Medicine*:
**For cold spleen-stomach qi preventing food intake, weakness, and lack of strength—Hútú Soup:**
Finely chop half a *jin* of crucian carp, prepare as raw fish slices, and steep in boiling fermented black soybean broth. Add powdered black pepper, dried ginger, dill, and tangerine peel. Consume on an empty stomach.

From *Recent Prescriptions*:
**For chronic spleen-stomach deficiency-cold leading to anorexia, prolonged emaciation, and consumptive weakness:**
Use Wenzhou white dried ginger as the sole ingredient. Boil in fermented rice water until thoroughly permeated, then remove, moisten, and dry. Pound and sift, then cook with aged granary rice into a porridge. Form into *tongzi*-sized pills. Take thirty to fifty pills per dose, as needed; the effect is divine.

From *Dietary Therapy*:
**For stomach qi deficiency with wind-heat preventing food intake:**
Mix half a chicken-egg shell’s worth of fresh ginger juice, a small amount of fresh rehmannia juice, and one spoonful of honey with three *ge* of water. Consume in one dose; immediate relief follows.

From *Tested Prescriptions*:
**For intolerable intermittent pain in the spleen’s original qi:**
Stir-fry one *liang* of evodia fruit with one *liang* of peach kernels until the evodia turns charred black. Discard the evodia, remove the peach kernels’ skins and tips, and grind finely. Stew three scallion stalks until soft, soak in wine, and divide into two warm doses.

From *Later Tested Prescriptions*:
**For promoting spleen-stomach food intake:**
Pound two *liang* of fennel seeds and four *liang* of fresh ginger evenly together. Store in a clean vessel, cover with damp paper, and leave overnight. The next day, stir-fry in a silver or stone vessel over gentle heat until yellow and crisp. Grind into powder, form into *wutong*-sized wine pills, and take ten to fifteen pills per dose with tea or wine.

From *Arcane Essentials from the Imperial Library*:
**For chronic qi distension:**
Consume one *sheng* of black ox urine warm on an empty stomach, once daily. Discontinue once the qi disperses.

---

**Prescription Thirty-Five: For Sudden Famine, Starvation, and Near-Death Exhaustion**
Grain is the sustenance of life; deprivation for several days can prove fatal. While *The Divine Farmer’s Classic* describes methods to stave off hunger, medical texts seldom address such techniques, likely because they border on the realm of immortals and transcend common practice. Thus, in years of famine, corpses lie strewn across the roads—truly lamentable.

Here, I record only the most accessible methods. If stranded in a desolate wilderness, fallen into a ravine, deep well, or ancient tomb, with no hope of rescue, one must drink water and practice qi absorption. The method is as follows:

Close the mouth, stir the tongue against the upper and lower teeth to generate saliva, and swallow it. Three hundred and sixty swallows per day are ideal; with practice, one may reach a thousand, naturally eliminating hunger. Initial fatigue may arise for three to five days, but thereafter, strength gradually returns.

Other methods, such as consuming the six *wu* hours of the twelve Earthly Branches, are omitted here, as one in dire straits may struggle to discern directions or time.

If water is available but no vessel, cup it in the left hand and recite: *"By the grace of the attending officials, true famine strikes. The correct red-yellow path avoids passing beneath city walls. Physicians, take heed for yourselves."* Conclude by tapping the teeth three times, then tapping the left hand three times with the right hand. Repeat this thrice, then drink. If a cup is later obtained, store water in it, hold it in the left hand, and tap it with an object in the right hand as before. Drinking three *sheng* daily will prevent hunger and restore health.

If able to traverse mountains and marshes:
Gather pine or cypress leaves, finely chop, and consume two *ge* with water, two to three *sheng* at midday. Alternatively, dig and wash white cogon grass roots, chop, and consume. These three substances may be sun-dried, pounded on stone, and taken in *fangcunbi* doses to sustain for a day.

If soybeans are available, roast until hot, then consume with water until sated; this provides relief for ten days. Red small beans are also effective. Roast both beans until yellow, grind into powder, and consume one to two *sheng* to sustain for ten days.

Among herbs, *atractylodes*, asparagus root, *ophiopogon*, Solomon’s seal, and fritillaria may be eaten raw or cooked, alone or together. Tree fungi, sandalwood, and white elm bark also stave off hunger.

In times of famine when grain is scarce and life depends on medicinal aid:
Take one *dou* of rice, wash thoroughly, steam and sun-dry it a hundred times, then pound. Consume once daily with water for thirty days; thereafter, one may abstain from food entirely while traveling three hundred *li* daily.

Another method: Soak one *dou* of non-glutinous rice in three *sheng* of wine, remove and sun-dry, then soak again until the wine is exhausted. Consume gradually, drinking when thirsty, to sustain for thirty days. One *hu* and two *sheng* suffice for a year.

There is also the *Guard the Center Pill* method. The above methods using rice and beans are easily obtained and prepared, harmonizing with grain qi to preserve strength without depletion. However, those of impure constitution may struggle with prolonged medicinal reliance; if possible, alternate with grains.

Refer to my *Grain Prescriptions* for further details.

**Additional Prescriptions**

From *Imperial Grace Formulary*:
**Method for Grain Abstinence and Immortal Ascension:**
Pound pine nuts into a paste, mix three *qian* with wine, and consume thrice daily to eliminate hunger. Drink water when thirsty, avoiding other foods. After a hundred days, the body becomes light, capable of traveling five hundred *li* daily.

From *Leisure Talks of a Rustic*:
**Master Fuhu’s Pine Resin Refinement Method:**
Boil ten *jin* of pine resin in water five times to remove bitterness. For each *jin* of refined resin, mix with four *liang* of poria powder. Take one *daogui* each morning with water to abstain from food for a year, extending lifespan with a light, clear body.

From *Baopuzi*:
During the reign of Emperor Cheng of Han, a hunter in the Zhongnan Mountains encountered a person without clothing, their body entirely covered in black hair, leaping over gullies and ravines as if flying. Stealthily observing their whereabouts, the hunters surrounded and captured them, discovering it was a woman. When questioned, she said: "I was a palace woman of Qin. When the eastern rebels arrived, the King of Qin surrendered and fled. Startled, I ran into the mountains. Starving and on the verge of death, an old man taught me to eat the leaves and seeds of pine and cypress. At first, they were bitter and astringent, but later I grew accustomed to them and no longer felt hunger. I no longer suffered from cold in winter or heat in summer." This woman was from the Qin era, and by the time of Emperor Cheng, over three hundred years had passed.

*Wanxian Weng’s Handbook of Emergency Prescriptions*, Volume Four, concludes here.

*Ge Xianweng’s Handbook of Emergency Prescriptions*, Volume Five:
**Chapter Thirty-Six: Remedies for Carbuncles, Breast Abscesses, and Various Toxic Swellings**

**Hidden Recluse’s Effective Remedies:**
For *yangju* sores with itching worms: Grind eight *fen* of *fuzi* (aconite) and two *fen* of *lilu* (veratrum) into powder and apply. The worms will emerge naturally.

**Ge’s Remedies for Breast Abscesses, Various Carbuncles, Back Boils, and Breast Swellings:**
Moxibustion over the affected area, one hundred cones.
Another remedy: Stir-fry *zifen* (millet powder) until black, mix with egg white, and apply to the carbuncle. Pierce a small hole in the silk cloth covering to vent toxic *qi*. Replace when dry. Wondrously effective.
Another remedy: Pound the soot from the bottom of a cauldron, mix with egg yolk, and apply. Adding a small amount of *chi* (fermented soybeans) enhances the effect.
Another remedy: Grind *huangbo* (phellodendron bark) into fine powder, sift, mix with egg white, and apply thickly. Replace when dry. Heals well.
Another remedy: Burn deer antler, grind into powder, mix with bitter wine, and apply. Excellent.
Another remedy: Grind deer antler on a stone with water, collect the turbid liquid, and apply to the carbuncle. Replace when dry. The swelling dissipates immediately.
Another remedy: Grind *banxia* (pinellia) into powder, mix with egg white, and apply. Also effective when ground with water.
Another remedy: The wondrously effective "water-ground" method, from the *Minor Treatises*.
Another remedy: Mix *zhuyu* (evodia) with vinegar, or pound ginger or garlic and apply. Both are effective.

**For All Malignant Toxic Swellings:**
Take one large handful of *manjing* (turnip) root (if unavailable, substitute *longkui* root), one *liang* of *rutouxiang* (frankincense, clear and bright), one *liang* of *huanglian* (coptis, from Xuanzhou), forty-nine apricot kernels (remove tips), and three to four *qian* of white willow wood. Chop finely, pound three to two hundred times, and form into cakes three to four *fen* thick. Apply to the swelling, replacing when dry. The swelling disperses immediately. Then apply a medicated plaster to the sore for best results.

**Ge’s Remedy for Dozens of Carbuncles:**
Burn cow dung, grind into powder, mix with egg white, and apply. Replace when dry. Wondrously effective.
Another remedy: Grind deer antler, *gui* (cinnamon), and chicken droppings separately, then burn and combine. Mix with egg white and apply, replacing when dry.
If the carbuncle has already formed pus and requires rupture:
Burn one feather from each wing of a white chicken and ingest. It will perforate. (Yao’s method concurs.)
Another remedy: Swallow one *yiyiren* (coix seed). Do not take more.
Another remedy: Mix *que shi* (sparrow droppings) with bitter wine and apply to the head of the carbuncle, the size of a small bean.

**Ge’s Remedy for Consolidating a Formed Carbuncle to Prevent Further Growth:**
Apply powdered small beans. Mixing with egg white is even better. It will heal.
Another remedy: Mix *yuanhua* (genkwa) powder with glue and apply. Replace when dry. The carbuncle liquefies.

**For Unremitting Pus and Blood with Acute Pain After Rupture:**
Take ten layers of fresh *baiqiu* (white catalpa) leaves and apply to the wound. Secure loosely with cloth.

**For Breast Swelling:**
Grind two *fen* each of *guixin* (cinnamon heart) and *gancao* (licorice), and one *fen* of *wutou* (aconite, prepared) into powder. Mix with bitter wine, apply to paper, and cover the swelling. The pus will liquefy. Wondrously effective.

**Ge’s Remedy for Women’s Breast Carbuncles and Malignant Swellings:**
Pound boiled *liugen* (willow root bark) thoroughly, warm over fire, place in a silk pouch, and apply as a compress. Replace when cool. Highly effective.
Another remedy: Boil a wooden rice pestle until bubbling, wrap in silk, and apply to the breast. Use two *ya* (tooth-shaped) compresses, alternating dozens of times. Yao states it is wondrously effective.

**Breast Carbuncle Remedy:**
Take two *fen* each of *dahuang* (rhubarb), *lancao* (orchid grass), and *fulonggan* (yellow earth from beneath a stove), and two *fen* of fresh ginger. First, pound and sift the first three ingredients, then combine with ginger and pound again. Mix with vinegar and apply. The breast pain will cease. Extremely effective. Liu Juanzi omits the ginger.
Another version uses four *fen* of fresh ginger in equal parts. Elsewhere, it is recorded that using crucian carp yields immediate results.

The *Xiaopin* states this formula is excellent.

**Yao’s Breast Carbuncle Remedy:**
Take one *fen* each of *dahuang* (rhubarb), moistened rat droppings, and *huanglian* (coptis). Grind the first two ingredients into powder, then pound the rat droppings again. Mix with millet porridge water and apply around the breast. The pain will cease, and the condition will heal. If millet is unavailable, polished rice may be used instead.

Another remedy: Apply cow or horse dung, both effective. These methods resolve the swelling.

**Jealousy Breast Formula from the *Xiaopin*:**
Grind equal parts of *huangqin* (scutellaria), *bailian* (ampelopsis), and *shaoyao* (peony) into powder, sift, and take one *qianbi* with fermented grain water, five times daily. If the right breast is swollen, consume milk from the left breast; if the left breast is swollen, consume milk from the right breast. This will disperse the root of the swelling. Yao’s formula is identical and guarantees a cure.

**Yao’s Remedy:**
Pound fresh *dihuang* (rehmannia) and apply; replace when warm. Red beans are also effective.

Another note: If hundreds of treatments fail and the swelling remains hard and purple, use the earlier willow root bark method—heat until warm and apply to the swelling. It will heal overnight.

**General Note:**
If breast milk is not expelled and congeals internally, it is called "jealousy breast," which is more urgent than carbuncle.

**Xu Yu’s Remedy for Painful Breast Nodules:**
Take three *liang* each of *dahuang* (rhubarb) and *huanglian* (coptis). Boil in five *sheng* of water until reduced to one *sheng* and two *ge*. Divide into three doses; purgation will bring immediate healing.

**Ge’s Sudden Toxic Swelling Remedy:**
Peel and finely pound a large *wujing* (turnip) root, mix with bitter wine to a paste, boil briefly, stir rapidly, and apply to the swelling. Wrap with silk and replace two or three times daily. The seeds are also effective.

Another remedy: Burn cow dung into ash, mix with bitter wine, and apply. Replace when dry.

Another: Mix lime with water and seal the swelling.

Another: Grind *shengma* (cimicifuga), *qingmuxiang* (aristolochia), or *zitan* (red sandalwood) with bitter wine and apply. Excellent results.

Another: Pound water pepper thoroughly and apply.

**For Swelling That Has Entered the Abdomen:**
Take one *liang* each of *shexiang* (musk), *xunluxiang* (frankincense), *qingmuxiang* (aristolochia), and *jishexiang* (clove). Boil in four *sheng* of water until reduced to two *sheng*. Divide into two doses.

**For Stubborn Hard Swellings:**
Pound equal parts of *wuzhuyu* (evodia) and *xiaosuan* (garlic) and apply. Red garlic is also effective.

Another remedy: Pound crucian carp and apply.

**For Wind Swelling with Itching (Rising When Pressed or Hidden Rashes):**
Simply press and rub the area vigorously several times daily; it will resolve.

Another: Grind *gui* (cinnamon) or *duhuo* (angelica) with bitter wine and apply repeatedly. Excellent results.

**For Sudden Swelling on the Body or Face (Like Inflation):**
Crush thirty *badou* (croton seeds) with their skins, boil in five *sheng* of water until reduced to three *sheng*, strain, and dip cotton to wipe the swelling. It will vanish immediately—avoid contact with the mouth.

**For Sudden Red, Painful, Narrow, Elongated Swelling (Called *Yong*):**
Take five *liang* of deer antler, one *liang* of *bailian* (ampelopsis), four *liang* of *muli* (oyster shell), and one *liang* of *fuzi* (aconite). Grind, sift, mix with bitter wine, and apply to silk. Replace when dry.

**For Stone-like Carbuncle (Hard as Rock or Large Nodules, Unchanged in Color, or Stone Carbuncle That Does Not Resolve):**
Burn eight *liang* of deer antler to ash, take two *liang* of coarse, yellow *bailian* (ampelopsis), and one *jin* of whetstone (burn until red). Grind all into powder, mix with bitter wine to a thick paste, and apply to the carbuncle. Reapply when dry until resolved. Administer *lianqiao* (forsythia) decoction internally.

**Yao’s Method:**
Burn the stone until extremely red, then quench in five *sheng* of bitter wine. Repeat until the wine is reduced by half. Pound the stone and mix with the medicine. Use the remaining wine first; if insufficient, add more.

**Yao’s Note:**
If the swelling is extremely hard with a root, it is called "stone carbuncle." Moxibustion with one hundred cones should be applied to the top; the stone will fragment and emerge. If it does not, increase the moxa.

**General Warning:**
Carbuncles, deep-rooted sores, tumors, stone carbuncles, tendon nodules, and scrofula must never be treated with needles or cupping. Such methods often lead to disaster.

**For Unruptured Carbuncles:**
Grind *wancao* (sweet flag) into powder, mix with egg white, and apply thickly to paper. Replace when dry; the pain will subside.

**For Severe, Throbbing Carbuncle Swelling:**
Grind *dahuang* (rhubarb), sift, mix with bitter wine, and apply to the swelling. Replace when dry; within three applications, the swelling will reduce, no pus will form, and it will resolve. Extremely effective.

**For Unformed Carbuncle Pus:**
Apply earwax from a cow; it will heal immediately. If necrotic flesh remains, use a flesh-dissolving remedy, then apply ointment for healing.

**Flesh-Dissolving Formula:**
Take equal parts of white charcoal ash and *dihui* (reed ash), boil to a paste. Do not prepare in advance—it loses efficacy after ten days. Also effective for removing moles.

**General Carbuncle Formula:**
Soak *gualou* (trichosanthes) root and red adzuki beans in bitter wine for five days, then dry, roast, and grind into powder. Mix with bitter wine, apply to paper, and affix to the swelling. Effective.

**Hidden Resident’s Effective Formula for Resolving Carbuncles:**
Grind two parts *bailian* (ampelopsis) and one part *lilu* (veratrum) into powder, mix with wine to a paste, and apply three times daily. Highly effective.

**For Bone-Exposing Sores:**
Grind two *fen* each of *huanglian* (coptis) and *muli* (oyster shell) into powder. First wash with salted wine, then apply.

**Ge’s Sudden *Biaoju* Sores (Clustering Like Grains on Hands, Feet, or Shoulders, Oozing Fluid):**
Roast and pound *wujing* (turnip), wrap, and apply while rolling over the sores day and night without ceasing.

**For Deep-Rooted Sores at the Fingertips (Red-Black, Difficult to Treat):**
Follow major formulas; simple remedies are insufficient.

**For Chronic Bone Carbuncles (Oozing Fluid When Pressed, Unhealed for Years):**
Heat maltose and apply to the sore, then press a fresh crucian carp onto it. After the time it takes to cook rice, scrape and inspect—small worms will emerge. Wash and reapply the medicine until the worms are gone; healing will follow.

**Yao’s Formula on *Biaoju* (Flame Carbuncle):**
*Biaoju* arises suddenly in the flesh as a dark nodule, the size of a bean or grain. In severe cases, it may grow as large as a plum, appearing red, black, white, or green. The lesion contains a core with deep roots, and after a brief period, the surrounding area swells entirely. The blisters turn dusky, purplish-black, capable of rotting sinews and bones. If the toxin enters the viscera, it may prove fatal. In the South, it is called *tuozhu* (clinging toxin). Where it afflicts thick flesh, excise it, then cauterize with red-hot iron three times until charred like charcoal. Alternatively, apply moxibustion directly on the dark core, one hundred cones for best effect. In early spring, layer *suanmo* leaves around the lesion to prevent spread. Drink juices of *kuigen* (mallow root), *xijiao* (rhinoceros horn), and *shengma* (cimicifuga) to purge internal and external heat. The treatment follows the method for *dandu* (cinnabar toxin).

**Liu Juanzi’s Yellow Qi Paste for Suppurating Carbuncles (Draining Pus and Blood, Promoting Flesh):**
*Huangqi* (astragalus), *shaoyao* (peony), *dahuang* (rhubarb), *danggui* (angelica), *xiongqiong* (ligusticum), *duhuo* (angelica pubescens), *baizhi* (angelica dahurica), *xiebai* (Chinese chive), each one *liang*; *shengdihuang* (fresh rehmannia), three *liang*. Chop the nine ingredients, simmer in two and a half *sheng* of lard, stirring thrice up and thrice down. When the paste forms, strain and discard the dregs. Apply to the sore, massaging the surrounding area, three times daily.

**Decoction for *Danyong* (Cinnabar Carbuncle) at Onset (Spreading and Enlarging, Including Minor *Dan Tuo* in Children):**
*Shengma* (cimicifuga), *huanglian* (coptis), *dahuang* (rhubarb), *xiongqiong* (ligusticum), each two *liang*; *huangqin* (scutellaria), *mangxiao* (mirabilite), each three *liang*; *danggui* (angelica), *zhigancao* (honey-fried licorice), *lingyangjiao* (antelope horn), each one *liang*. Chop the nine ingredients, boil in one *dou* and three *sheng* of water to five *sheng*, strain, return to the pot, and stir in *mangxiao* with a wooden stick until a paste forms. Adjust temperature, spread on cloth, and apply to the swelling. Repeat until the swelling dissipates. This is Wang Lian’s secret formula from Ganlin—take care to avoid the genitals.

**Hu Powder for *Biaochuang* (Flame Sores, Spreading with Copious Discharge):**
Roast *hufen* (lead powder), *zhigancao* (honey-fried licorice), *qianru* (rubia), and *huanglian* (coptis), each two *fen*. Grind into powder, sift, and dust onto the sore thrice daily. Highly effective.

**Paste for All Carbuncle Sores:**
Wax, *luanfa* (human hair), *fanshi* (alum), *songzhi* (pine resin), each one *liang*; lard, four *liang*. First melt the hair, then add alum when the hair dissolves. When the alum dissolves, add pine resin; when the resin dissolves, add wax; when the wax dissolves, add lard. Apply to the sore.

**Red Dragon Skin Decoction for Washing Putrid, Festering Sores:**
Chop three *sheng* of *hushupi* (oak bark), boil in one *dou* of water to five *sheng*. Use cold in spring and summer, warm in autumn and winter. Wash breast sores and all putrid sores, then apply paste.

**Rhubarb Decoction for Early Pain in *Fabei* (Carbuncle on the Back):**
*Dahuang* (rhubarb), *zhigancao* (honey-fried licorice), *huangqin* (scutellaria), each two *liang*; *shengma* (cimicifuga), two *liang*; *zhizi* (gardenia), one hundred pieces. Boil the five ingredients in nine *sheng* of water to three and a half *sheng*. Drink until several bowel movements occur, then stop. If no movement, take again.

**Mu Zhansi Powder for *Fabei* (Back Carbuncle), *Faru* (Breast Carbuncle in Women), and *Changyong* (Intestinal Carbuncle):**
*Muzhansi* (aralia), *zhihoupo* (honey-fried magnolia bark), *zhigancao* (honey-fried licorice), *xixin* (asarum), *gualou* (trichosanthes), *fangfeng* (saposhnikovia), *ganjiang* (dried ginger), *renshen* (ginseng), *jiegeng* (platycodon), *baijiang* (patrinia), each one *liang*. Grind into powder, take one *fangcunbi* with wine, seven times by day and four by night—more is better. If the affliction is above, vomiting occurs; if below, pus and blood discharge. This pertains to *changyong* (intestinal carbuncle), where the swelling is painless. Long-term use treats all carbuncles and hemorrhoids. If the sore has already ulcerated, healing is swift. No *fabei* (back carbuncle) is incurable, and the swelling resolves unnoticed. For prolonged use, omit *baijiang* (patrinia), which is especially effective for *faru* (breast carbuncle), postpartum conditions, and abdominal masses in women. All are Liu Juanzi’s formulas.

**Liu Juanzi’s Mu Zhansi Powder for Dissolving Pus in Carbuncles:**
*Muzhansi* (aralia), *guixin* (cinnamon bark), *renshen* (ginseng), *xixin* (asarum), *baijiang* (patrinia), *ganjiang* (dried ginger), *zhihoupo* (honey-fried magnolia bark), *zhigancao* (honey-fried licorice), *fangfeng* (saposhnikovia), *jiegeng* (platycodon), each one *liang*. Grind into powder, take one *fangcunbi*. Upon swallowing, one feels it flow into the sore. If the carbuncle has been cauterized but not ulcerated, it may be taken. If the sore has not ulcerated, omit *baijiang*. Occasionally, this formula may reduce a carbuncle to water.

**Bailian Paste for Unresolved *Yong* Swellings, Scrofula, and Nodules:**
*Bailian* (ampelopsis), *huanglian* (coptis), *dahuang* (rhubarb), *huangqin* (scutellaria), *wangcao* (lithospermum), *chishizhi* (red halloysite), *wuzhuyu* (evodia), *shaoyao* (peony), each four *fen*. Grind, sift, and mix with egg white into a paste. Spread on old cloth and apply, leaving a small opening. Replace when dry. Heals.

**For Life-Threatening *Fabei* (Back Carbuncle):**
Take a winter melon, cut off the top, and place it over the sore. When the melon rots, cut it away and replace. Before the melon is exhausted, the sore will have contracted—then nourish with paste.

**Alternative Formula:**
Grind *fulonggan* (furnace earth) into powder, mix with wine, and apply thickly to the sore. Replace when dry; recovery follows swiftly.

**Another Formula:**
Toast *wutongziye* (paulownia leaves) on a griddle until charred, sift through silk, mix with honey, and apply. Replace when dry.

**Miscellaneous Effective Formulas for *Yong* Swellings (Treating Heat Swellings):**
Pound *jiazi* (mustard seeds) with *baiye* (cypress leaves) and apply—universally effective. Wild mustard is even better.

**Another Formula:**
Grind *xiaojiezi* (small mustard seeds) into powder, mix with vinegar into cakes, and apply to swellings or scrofula. Check frequently; stop when the swelling subsides to avoid damaging flesh. Effective for *mafugu* (horse bone carbuncle).

**Another Formula:**
Burn human feces into ash, mix with vinegar into a paste, and apply to the swelling. Replace when dry—highly effective.

**Another Formula:**
Take yellow *xionghuang* (realgar) and *cihuang* (orpiment), heat until red, then douse with strong vinegar. Reheat and douse again until the stones soften like mud. Scrape and apply to the swelling; if dry, mix with vinegar. This is a great secret.

**Method to Resolve Swellings with Moxibustion:**
Slice a single garlic clove crosswise to a thickness of one *fen*, place on the swelling’s head, and apply moxa cones the size of *wutongzi* (paulownia seeds), one hundred cones. If no reduction is felt, repeat frequently—more is better. Avoid excessive heat; if pain is felt, lift the garlic. Replace charred garlic with fresh. Do not burn the skin or flesh. If the body is dry, moxibustion is unnecessary.

I have once suffered from a large swelling below the lower abdomen, and moxibustion cured it. Whenever I use this method, it proves highly effective.

**Another Formula:**
Take the kernel from the head of fresh ginseng [text unclear], or mix magnetite powder with vinegar and apply.

**Another Formula:**
Apply licorice [text unclear] to this swelling—do not ingest the plantain seed.

**Another Formula:**
Apply chicken-intestine herb.

**Another Formula:**
Apply white *bai lian* (ampelopsis) powder—also effective.

**For Hot Swellings and Boils:**
Apply roasted glue repeatedly, ten or more times a day, and it will resolve. Especially effective for treating boils in children, with divine results each time.

**For All Toxic Swellings with Unbearable Pain:**
Knead dough into a round piece the size of a coin, fill it with Sichuan peppercorns, cover the swelling’s head with the dough cake, and apply moxibustion until the pain penetrates—this will immediately stop the pain.

**Another Formula:**
Pound castor bean and apply—immediate relief.

**For Wind-Toxin Swellings on Palms and Soles:**
Mix equal parts ground Sichuan pepper and salt with vinegar, and apply—it will resolve.

**For Carbuncles with Foul, Rotten Flesh:**
Apply white *lan ru* (Solanum) powder. When the flesh is gone, stop and apply other ointments. If flesh does not regenerate, apply astragalus powder. *Lan ru* and astragalus halt all malignant flesh. If the flesh persists, use seven heads of red-skinned *lan ru* ground into powder—take half a *qianbi* and mix with three *qianbi* of white *lan ru* powder to apply. This is Yao’s formula, and it heals.

**For Malignant Vessel Disease:**
Suddenly, red vessels resembling earthworms appear on the body. This arises from evil wind entering the collaterals in spring or winter, causing blood stasis. Take *Five Fragrances and Forsythia Decoction*, lance to remove blood, and apply *Red Sage Ointment*—it will heal after some days. When I crossed mountains and ridges, I suffered from this and regularly took *Five Fragrances Decoction*, applying mung beans to reduce the swelling. The following are all Yao’s formulas.

**For Malignant Nodule Disease:**
Suddenly, nodules like plums or apricots appear in the flesh, or small ones like soybeans, with sharp pain moving beneath the skin, accompanied by fever and chills. This disease arises abruptly; if the toxin enters the abdomen, it can kill. This affliction is common in the south. Take *Five Fragrances and Forsythia Decoction* and apply mung beans—it will resolve immediately. For children, applying *Red Sage Ointment* is also effective.

**For Malignant Flesh Disease:**
Suddenly, flesh like red adzuki beans protrudes from the body, growing into shapes like cow or horse udders or rooster combs. Take *Rhaponticum Decoction* internally, and externally cauterize with a heated iron, three times daily, until slightly charred. Apply *Cimicifuga Ointment*.

**For Qi Pain Disease:**
Suddenly, a localized pain like a blow appears in the body, unbearable and wandering, flaring up intermittently. When the pain subsides, the area feels cold as if touched by frost or snow. This arises from sudden cold injuring the body during winter warmth extending into spring. First take several doses of *Five Fragrances and Forsythia Decoction*. Also, boil willow bark in white wine and apply warm compresses. Where red spots appear, lance to remove blood.

**Five Fragrances and Forsythia Decoction:**
Treats malignant flesh, malignant vessels, malignant nodules, scrofula, wind-binding swellings, and qi pain.
*Costus root, eaglewood, clove* (each 2 *liang*), *musk* (0.5 *liang*), *frankincense* (1 *liang*), *belamcanda rhizome, Chinese knotweed, cimicifuga, pubescent angelica, mistletoe, roasted licorice, forsythia* (each 2 *liang*), *rhubarb* (3 *liang*), *bamboo sap* (3 *sheng*). Boil the thirteen ingredients in 9 *sheng* of water until reduced by half, add 3 *sheng* of bamboo sap, and divide into three doses. Highly effective.

**Rhaponticum Decoction:**
Treats carbuncles, cinnabar toxins, swellings, and malignant flesh.
*Rhaponticum, white ampelopsis, scutellaria, white swallowwort, roasted immature orange fruit, cimicifuga, roasted licorice, peony, ephedra* (nodes removed, each 2 *liang*), *rhubarb* (3 *liang*). Boil the ten ingredients in 1 *dou* of water to yield 3 *sheng*. If no herbs are available, use rhubarb to purge—also effective. For cinnabar toxins, lance to remove blood.

**Red Sage Ointment:**
Treats malignant flesh, malignant nodules, scrofula, wind-binding, and all vessel swellings.
*Red sage, elder* (each 2 *liang*), *gentian, pubescent angelica, aconite, bletilla, achyranthes, chrysanthemum, saposhnikovia* (each 1 *liang*), *artemisia leaf, azalea flower, Sichuan pepper* (each 0.5 *liang*). Chop the twelve ingredients, soak in 2 *sheng* of bitter wine overnight, then simmer with 4 *jin* of lard until the wine evaporates. Do not overcook. Strain and apply to affected areas five times daily. Spread on old cloth and apply. This ointment may also be taken internally—consume sparingly after a thorough bowel movement. (Same as *Xiaopin*.)

**Cimicifuga Ointment:**
Treats cinnabar toxins, hot swellings, and sores.
*Cimicifuga, white ampelopsis, rhaponticum, mirabilite* (each 2 *liang*), *scutellaria, immature orange fruit, forsythia, snake’s tongue herb* (each 3 *liang*), *gardenia* (20 pieces), *elder root* (4 *liang*). Chop the ten ingredients finely, place in a vessel, soak in 3 *sheng* of water for half a day, then simmer with 5 *sheng* of lard until the water evaporates. Strain and apply five times daily. For urgent cases, decoct in water. Extremely effective.

**Ge’s Formula for Sudden Toxic Swellings with Acute Pain:**
Boil willow bark in wine until hot and apply as a compress—the pain will cease.

**Appended Formulas:**

**From *Sheng Jin Fang*:**
Treats brain abscesses, back carbuncles, deep-rooted boils, hot boils, and malignant sores.
Finely chop a rabbit’s head from the twelfth month, place in a jar, and seal tightly—the longer it is stored, the better. Spread thickly on cloth and apply to hot, painful areas, changing frequently like ice. It will heal.

**From *Qian Jin Fang*:**
Treats back carbuncles and deep-rooted swellings, whether ulcerated or not.
Mix 3 *sheng* of fermented soybeans with a little water, pound into a paste, and form into cakes 0.3 *cun* thick. If the swelling has an opening, do not cover it; place the soybean cake over the opening and apply moxibustion with mugwort until warm. Maintain warmth without burning the flesh.

**Appended Formulas:**

If the swelling is hot and painful, change the compress urgently—the ailment will abate, and the patient will soon recover. Apply twice daily.

If moxibustion is used and pus begins to flow from a preexisting sore, the condition will improve.

**From *Waizhai Miyao*:**
Treats impending back carbuncles (with chills and shivering as if about to erupt) or existing sores and swellings.
Dissolve **3 liang** of **xiao shi** (borax) in **1 sheng** of warm water until dissolved, then cool. Take an old green cloth, fold it three times, cut to fit the affected area’s size and shape, dampen it, and apply. Replace immediately when it grows hot. Frequent changes will swiftly heal the condition.

**From *Jiyan Fang*:**
Treats back carbuncles.
Take **100 live snails**, place them in a clean **1 sheng** jar with **1 bowl of fresh-drawn water**, seal, and leave overnight until dawn. Remove the snails and discard them. The water will resemble saliva—mix with **zhen ge powder** (real oyster powder) in any quantity, apply to the sore, and brush with a chicken feather. Repeat **10+ times daily** until the heat and pain subside, at which point the sore will heal.

**From *Cui Yuanliang’s Haishang Fang* (Secret Method for Back Carbuncles):**
Li Beihai says: This formula was divinely revealed and is supremely secret.
Grind **3 large liang of licorice root**, sift the powder, and mix with **9 liang of barley flour** in a large dish until evenly blended. Add a small amount of high-quality ghee, knead thoroughly, and shape into cakes slightly larger than the sore. Apply hot to the swelling, covering with oil paper and old paper to allow ventilation. Replace when cool. If pus forms, it will drain naturally; if no pus forms, the swelling will dissolve internally.
**Note:** While using this remedy, the patient must consume **astragalus gruel**—this is most effective.

Another method:
Lightly roast **1 large liang of licorice root**, grind it, and steep in **1 large sheng of water**. Place a small knife horizontally across the container and leave it exposed overnight. At dawn, stir to emulsify the liquid and drink the froth. This treats all sores, swellings, and back carbuncles with remarkable efficacy.

**From *Mei Shi Fang*:**
Treats all deep-rooted boils and back carbuncles, or those affecting the breasts. If untreated in the early stages (when only slightly red), death will follow swiftly.
**Formula:** Pound **ramie roots** and apply. Change frequently.

**From *Shenghui Fang*:**
Treats **fishing-eye sores** (intertrigo-like lesions) and **attached-bone carbuncles**.
Burn **dog skull** and fumigate the affected area.

Zhang Wenzhong’s method for treating **stone-like carbuncles** (hard, non-purulent):
Pound **raw *zhanglu root*** and rub it on. Replace when dry, stopping when the area softens.

**From *Zimu Milu*:**
Treats **deep-rooted boils, hemorrhoids, fistulas, and infantile measles**.
Boil **hawthorn root** and use the juice to wash the area.
Another method: Powder **silkworm larvae** and apply.

**From *Xiaopin Fang*:**
Treats early-stage carbuncles.
Mix **powdered red adzuki beans** with vinegar and apply. This also dissipates the swelling.

**From *Bozhi Fang*:**
Treats all unruptured swellings with pain, causing them to dissolve internally.
Pound **raw rehmannia root** into a paste, spread it on cloth to match the swelling’s size, sprinkle **wood aromatic powder** on top, then add another layer of rehmannia. Apply to the swelling. No more than **3–5 applications** are needed.

Dayuzi says: To dissipate toxic swellings, apply **powdered *juemingzi* (decorticated *mucuna pruriens*)** mixed with water.

**From *Shiliao* (Dietary Therapy):**
Treats swellings.
Simmer **bitter melon root** in **bitter wine** until dry, grind and sift, then mix with bitter wine and spread on paper for application. Those with **metallic constitutions** should also ingest it.

Yang Wenwei’s method for treating **unruptured carbuncles**:
Powder **bitter melon root and red adzuki beans** equally, mix with vinegar, and apply.

**From *Qian Jin Fang*:**
Treats all malignant swellings where treatment was delayed and pus has formed.
Burn **hawthorn thorns** into ash, dissolve in water, and drink. The next morning, the head will clear.
Another method for **cold sores** where the wound does not close:
Burn **rat skin** into ash, finely powder, and seal over the sore.

Sun Zhenren says: Treats **multiple carbuncles**.
Burn **cow dung** into ash, mix with **egg white**, and apply. Replace when dry.

**From *Sun Zhenren’s Shiji*:**
Treats all **heat-toxin swellings**.
Mix **raw *zhanglu root*** with a little salt and apply. Change twice daily.

**From *Jiyan Fang*:**
Treats swellings.
Take **willow branches** the thickness of a toe and **3 chi long**, **20 stems**, boil until scalding. Wrap the swelling in old cloth and bathe with the hot liquid—immediate relief follows.

Another method for treating **carbuncles and all unruptured swellings** (to draw out toxins):
Powder **white abalone shell**, mix with water, and apply. Reapply when dry.

**#3 Method:** Treats **toxic heat** with **foot swelling and pain threatening amputation**.
Soak in **alcohol-cooked *ku shen*** (sophora root).

**From *Waizhai Miyao*:**
Treats carbuncles and swellings.
Mix **flying squirrel liver** with garlic into a paste, apply on cloth, and affix. Replace when dry.

Another method for **all swellings, ruptured or unruptured**:
Soften **white glue** in water to match the swelling’s size, cut a hole at the top, and affix. If pus has formed, the glue will draw it out completely. If no pus exists, the swelling will dissolve.

Another method:
Burn **crucian carp** into ash, mix with vinegar, and apply to all swellings until healed.

Another method for treating **heat-toxin diseases** attacking the hands and feet, causing swelling and pain threatening amputation:
Soak in **xanthium fruit juice**.

Another method:
Boil **horse manure** and use the juice to soak the area.

**From *Zhouhou Fang*:**
Treats **toxic attacks on hands and feet**, causing swelling and pain threatening amputation.

**From *Jingyan Houfang*:**
Treats all **carbuncles without visible heads**.
Swallow **1 pumpkin seed** with fresh-drawn water. The swelling will rupture within moments. For multiple swellings, ingest **2 seeds**, adding one more for each additional site. The method is verified.

Another method for treating **all carbuncles** that have already formed pus but fear needling to break them, ensuring rapid drainage:
Take the **first feather** from beneath a white rooster’s wing—one stalk from each side—burn to ash, grind, and administer with water.

From *Mei Shi Fang*:
Apply **sparrow dung** to the head; it will soon rupture. **Male sparrow dung** is superior; firmness indicates maleness.

**Note:** Realgar has long been used to treat **carbuncles and abscesses**. In *Zhou Li · Yang Yi* (Physician of Ulcers), it states:
*"In treating carbuncles and abscesses, the Five Toxins are used to attack them."* Zheng Xuan’s commentary explains:
*"Modern medical prescriptions include Five Toxin medicines, made by mixing yellow *huangdi* (瓦), stone gall, cinnabar, realgar, *yushi* (誉石), and magnetite, then burning them for three days and nights. The rising smoke is collected with chicken feathers and applied to the wound. Rotten flesh and bone will then be expelled entirely."*

Thus, the scholar-official Yang Yi once recorded:
*"When Zhishu Guan was young, a carbuncle formed on his cheek, spreading to the jaw and outer ear, swelling like an overturned bowl. It ulcerated, draining pus and blood incessantly, causing unbearable pain. After countless treatments over a year without improvement, someone advised him to follow Zheng’s method. After preparing and applying the burned medicine, within moments, the rotting bone—including two teeth—drained out, and he recovered fully, remaining healthy afterward."* This confirms the swift efficacy of ancient prescriptions in treating disease.

The *huangdi* (瓦) used in this process resembles the glazed tiles sold in markets today. In modern alchemy, yellow glazed tiles (*huangzhen*) are still employed, as recorded in antiquity. *Huangdi* is pronounced *wǔ*.

From *Mei Shi Fang*:
For **postpartum lactation failure**, where milk accumulates and forms a carbuncle, apply crushed *pu gong yao* (蒲公草) to the swelling, changing it three or four times daily. Commonly called *pu gong ying* (蒲公英), though the name is corrupted from *púgōngyīng* to *púgōngguō* in speech. The juice may also be ingested by boiling it.

Another method for treating **jealous milk carbuncles**:
Crush cloves into powder and administer with water, one *fangchén* dose.

Another method for treating **cracked nipples**:
Apply crushed clove powder topically.

From *Qian Jin Fang*:
For **jealous milk**:
Mix **house dust** with vinegar and apply it. This also treats **scrotal swelling**.

From *Ling Yuan Fang*:
For **initial breast abscesses**, where swelling and hardness form, threatening pus drainage, one dose suffices:
Take **true birch bark from the north**, boil in *wugui* (無灰) wine, and administer one *fangchén* dose. Rest afterward until recovery.

From *Sheng Hui Fang*:
For **persistent breast carbuncles**:
Use **half a *jin* of wheat flour**, toast until golden, mix with vinegar into a paste, and apply to the breast. It will dissolve immediately.

From *Chan Bao*:
For **breast and carbuncle swellings**:
Take **chicken dung powder**, administer one *fangchén* dose, repeating three times at short intervals. It will heal.

*Mei Shi Fang* also treats **cracked nipples** with the same method.

From *Jian Yao Ji Zhong*:
For **female breast carbuncles** where pus does not drain, forming internal abscesses (**jealous milk**):
Burn **wild bee combs** to ash, grind, and take two *qian* per dose with one *zhongshao* cup of water, decocting until reduced by four parts. Strain, warm, and ingest.

Another method for treating **blocked lactation** (*chui nai*):
**Du Sheng San** (独胜散):
Take **half *liang* of white cloves**, grind into powder. Administer one *qian* dose with warm wine, without regard to time.

From *Zi Mu Mi Lu*:
For **blocked lactation** with **chills and high fever**:
Soak **pork lard** in cold water, apply as a poultice, changing when it warms. Immediate effect.

From *Yang Yan Nan Xing Fang*:
For **unbearable pain from blocked lactation**:
Use **baked *chuan shan jia* (穿山甲), *mu tong* (木通), and raw *zi ran tong* (自然铜)**, each one *liang*. Grind into powder. Take two *qian* per dose with warm wine, without regard to time.

*Shi Yi Xin Jing* states:
For **blocked lactation without itching or pain**, where the breast hardens like stone:
Take **one *liang* of green tangerine peel**, boil in water to remove the white pith, dry, and grind into powder. Take two *qian* doses with warm wine, without regard to time.

Burn **bamboo leaves**, mix with the yolk of an egg, and apply—it will heal.

**Alternative Method:**
Burn **snake skin**, grind into powder, and apply with **pork fat**.

**Alternative Method:**
Boil **willow leaves** or **willow bark**, wash the carbuncle with the decoction (adding a little salt)—this also treats **facial carbuncles**.

**Another Method for Facial Carbuncles:**
Take **one *sheng* of pork fat from the twelfth month**, **hair clippings the size of an egg**, and **one live crucian carp**. Simmer until fully dissolved, then add **two *liang* of realgar (*zhong huang*) and *ku shen* powder**, and **one *ku* of *fu zi*** (processed). Grind and let congeal, then apply to all carbuncles—none will fail. (*From Hu Xie’s* method for **scabies, carbuncles, and tinea**—highly effective.)

For **carbuncles with protruding malignant flesh**:
Grind **prickly ash berries (*wu mei*)** into powder and apply. Alternatively, grind **sulfur (*liu huang*)** and apply with saliva to dry it.

For **carbuncles with crusting, itching, and pain**:
Pound **hyacinth beans (*ban dou*)** into a paste and seal over the carbuncle—when the crust falls off, it will heal. (A recent method.)
