**Chapter Thirty-Nine:** Methods for Treating **Painful Tinea, Scabies, Lacquer Carbuncles, and All Malignant Carbuncles**

(*From Xiao Pin*):
**Method for Scabies, Tinea, and Malignant Carbuncles:**
**Mercury (*shui yin*), alum (*fan shi*), snakeweed seed (*she chuang zi*), and rhubarb (*huang lian*)**, each two *liang*. Grind and sift all four, then mix with **seven *he* of pork fat from the twelfth month** (including the mercury). Stir vigorously ten thousand times until the mercury disappears and the fat solidifies. Apply to carbuncles, including **children’s scalp sores**—highly effective.

**Gong Qingxuan’s Addition:**
Add **one *liang* of *zhu ru*** (evodia fruit).

**Method for All Carbuncles (Divinely Verified):**
**Realgar (*xiong huang*), rhubarb (*huang lian*), and pine resin (*song zhi*)**, each two *liang*; **ash from burnt hair** the size of a marble. Melt the four ingredients with **pork fat and pine resin**, pound while hot, and apply thinly to carbuncles—extremely effective.

**Another Method for Malignant Carbuncle Powder:**
**Mercury (*shui yin*), rhubarb (*huang lian*), and barite (*hu fen*)**, each two *liang**, roast until yellow, then sift. Dust onto carbuncles. For **dry carbuncles without pus**, mix with saliva.

For **malignant carbuncles on a child’s body:**
Use **bamboo shoot juice** to wash the carbuncle, then apply **bamboo shell powder**—it will heal.

For **carbuncles resembling burning flesh that self-destruct:**
Roast **barite (*hu fen*)** until black, then mix equal parts with **phellodendron (*huang bai*)** and **rhubarb (*huang lian*)**. Sift and dust onto the carbuncle.

For **sudden malignant carbuncles:**
Grind **cocklebur (*cang er*)** and **peach bark (*tao pi*)** into powder and place inside the carbuncle—excellent.

For **malignant carbuncles on the head:**
**Barite (*hu fen*), mercury (*shui yin*), and white pine resin (*bai song zhi*)**, each two *liang**; **four *liang* of pork fat from the twelfth month**. Melt the resin, then mix with the mercury and barite. Apply twice daily. (*From Hu Xie’s* method for **children’s head and facial carbuncles**. Adding **two *liang* of rhubarb (*huang lian*)** also treats **alopecia from carbuncles**.)

**Realgar Plaster for Malignant Carbuncles:**
**Realgar (*xiong huang*), orpiment (*ci huang*), and mercury (*shui yin*)**, each one *liang*; **two *liang* of pine resin (*song zhi*)**; **half a *jin* of pork fat**; **hair clippings the size of an egg**. Combine and simmer, strain, then add mercury. Apply to carbuncles twice daily.

**Effective Method: Realgar Meat Powder for Malignant Carbuncles:**
**Six *fen* of realgar (*xiong huang*), two *fen* each of *zhu ru* (evodia) and alum (*fan shi*)**. Grind into powder and apply to carbuncles twice daily.

**Method for Removing Facial Acne (Most Effective):**
**Eight *fen* of rhubarb (*huang lian*), five *fen* each of glutinous rice and red adzuki beans (*chi xiao dou*), one *fen* of *wu zhu yu* (evodia fruit); **six *fen* each of barite (*hu fen*) and mercury (*shui yin*)**. Grind the rhubarb and others, then sift. First, grind the mercury on the palm until extremely fine, mix with the medicine, and dilute with **raw sesame oil** to the desired consistency. Wash the carbuncle, dry it, and apply. This treats all carbuncles—divinely verified and not to be passed on.

**Gan Family’s Pine Resin Plaster (For Hot Carbuncles with Foul Pus, Preventing Scarring):**
**Pine resin (*song zhi*), white benzoin (*bai jiao xiang*), and **aloeswood (*xun lu xiang*)**, each one *liang*; **one and a half *liang* each of *dang gui* (angelica) and beeswax (*la*); one *liang* of licorice (*gan cao*)**; **half *he* each of pork fat and sheep kidney fat**; **half *he* of raw rehmannia (*sheng di huang*) juice**. Grind the pine resin and others into powder, mix with the fats and rehmannia juice, simmer over low heat until yellow, then add the wax, strain, and apply to the carbuncle. Highly effective. (This is half the original secret recipe.)

**Rehmannia Plaster (For All Disseminated Carbuncles; Preventing Scarring, Removing Pus, and Regenerating Flesh—Secret Method):**
**One *sheng* of rehmannia juice (*di huang zhi*), two *liang* of pine resin (*song zhi*), one *liang* of aloeswood (*xun lu xiang*), and **sheep kidney fat and cow tallow**, each the size of an egg**. First, simmer the rehmannia juice with the pine resin and aloeswood until dissolved, then add the sheep fat and tallow, along with **half an egg-sized piece of beeswax**. Combine and simmer over low heat until the water evaporates and the plaster forms. Strain and apply to cloth, then affix to the carbuncle, changing once or twice daily. For **chronic cases**, add **one piece of dried tangerine peel (*ju pi*)** and **hair clippings the size of an egg**—it will heal in ten days.

**Secret Method for Regenerating Flesh:**
For **women’s carbuncles on the cheek**, which recur annually after healing, apply the **Gan Family’s secret plaster**—it will never return.

**Gan Family’s Highly Effective Method:**
**Two *liang* of alum (*fan shi*), roasted until all liquid is gone**; **one *liang* of barite (*hu fen*)**; **one and a half *liang* of mercury (*shui yin*)**. Grind and sift, then sift the alum and barite separately. First, warm a piece of pork fat in a porcelain dish, grind the mercury until fully dissolved, then add more pork fat, along with the alum and barite. Mix until thick and pasty. Wash the facial carbuncle and apply. Additionally, roast the barite until yellow, then apply this powder thinly over the plaster—it will heal in several days. (The Gan Family’s method is highly effective.)

**Method for Treating Scabies Carbuncles (All below the waist are classified as scabies—these are caused by parasitic worms; the worms die, and the condition heals immediately):**
Take **one bowl of vinegar dregs**, **one bowl of hemp seeds (*ma zi*)**, and **one *shao* each of white sand and salt**. Mix and apply as a poultice. When dry, reapply. First, wash the area with warm water, dry it, and apply the poultice **once or twice**—it will heal.

「孔如针穴，皆虫食，大验。
**Method for Treating Smallpox Pockmarks and Scabies Carbuncles (All are caused by parasitic worms—highly effective):**
Take **pounded croton seed (*ba dou*)** until fine as a needle’s hole, and apply it—all are caused by worms, and this method is highly effective.

**Remedies for Stubborn Ulcers (Those that persist for thirty years):**
Take **one liang each of rhubarb (*da huang*), scutellaria (*huang qin*), and coptis (*huang lian*)**, ground into a powder. Clean the ulcer by washing, then apply the powder three times daily—none will fail to heal.
Alternatively, **phellodendron bark (*huang bo*)**, graded by quality, is also excellent.

**Ge Family’s Method for Treating White Alopecia (Alopecia Areata):**
Slaughter a pig and immediately take its abdomen, remove feces, and while still warm, apply it inverted over the head. In moments, the worms will emerge into the abdomen. If not all are expelled, repeat the process until no worms remain, then cease.

**Another Method:**
Grind **prickly ash (*li lu*)** into powder, mix with **December pig fat (*zhe yue zhu shao*)**, and apply. For **May *Lian Lu* grass (*Lian Lu cao*)**, burn it into ash, mix with fat, and apply—all must first be washed with warm water before applying.

**Another Method:**
Take **sheepfoot root (*yang ti jiao gen*)**, preferably a single root, and avoid exposure to wind, sunlight, or contact with women, chickens, or dogs. Grind it with **three-year-old vinegar** into a paste, wipe the alopecia clean, and apply. If made into powder and applied, it is even better.

**Yao Family’s Method:**
Prepare **mutton (*yang rou*)** as one would make jerky, roast until fragrant, and while still warm, apply it inverted over the affected area—it will heal within three to four days.

**From *Sacred Benevolent Prescriptions* (*Sheng Hui Fang*):**
**Method for Treating Wind-Itch Scabies (Generalized itching forming ulcers):**
Take **one sheng of silkworm excrement (*can sha*)**, boil in **two dou of water**, reduce to **one dou two sheng**, strain, and bathe while warm—it will heal.

---

**From *The Thousand Gold Formulas* (*Qian Jin Yi*):**

**Appropriate to Avoid Wind.**
**Method for Treating All Itch from Dan Poison (*Dan Yin*):**
Boil **fermented milk (*lào rù*)** with salt until hot, and rub it on the affected area—**itch will vanish beneath the hands.**

**Another Method for Treating Severe Wind Itch in Adults and Children:**
Take **one sheng of Chinese wolfberry (*zhu yú*)**, five sheng of wine, boil to extract **one sheng**, soak a cloth in the liquid, and wipe the body. **Pei Yu initially treated wind-heat skin conditions, where itch spread across the body and formed ulcers.**
Take **equal parts burdock seed (*niú bàng zǐ*)** and duckweed (*fú píng*), adjust with **mint decoction (*bó hé tāng*)** and take **two qián**, twice daily.

**From *Later Experiential Prescriptions* (*Jing Yan Hou Fang*):**
**Method for Treating Lung Toxin Ulcers (*Fei Du Chuang*)**, resembling severe wind conditions (*Dà Fēng Jí*):**
Apply **Green Cloud Powder (*Lǜ Yún Sǎn*)**.
Take **high-quality mulberry leaves (*sāng yè*)**, wash them clean, and steam them overnight until fully cooked. Dry them in the sun, grind into a fine powder. Adjust with water and take **two qián**, daily.

**From *Prescriptions from the Armchair’s Rear* (*Zhǒu Hòu Fāng*):**
**Method for Treating Sudden Onset of Damp-Rot Ulcers (*Jìn Yǐn Chuāng*),** spreading with pus and turning lethal if untreated.
Apply **rooster comb blood (*jī guān xuè*)**—**itch will subside.**
**Another Method for Treating Sudden Onset of Moon-Eclipse Ulcers (*Yuè Shì Chuāng*)** in adults and children:
At the **full moon**, collect **rabbit feces** and the **inner contents of toads' abdomens (*xiā mā wáng*)**, burn them together into ashes, grind into a powder, and apply to the ulcers—**itch will subside.**

**From *Collected Verified Prescriptions* (*Jí Yàn Fāng*):**
**Method for Treating Moon-Eclipse Ulcers (*Yuè Shì Chuāng*):**
Take **two liǎng of tiger skull bone (*hǔ tóu gǔ*)**, crush it, mix with **one sheng of pig fat (*zhū zhī*)**, and simmer into a paste. When the paste turns **yellow**, apply it to the ulcers—**itch will subside.**

**From *Sacred Benevolent Prescriptions* (*Shèng Huì Fāng*):**
**Method for Treating Reverse-Bloom Ulcers (*Fǎn Huā Chuāng*):**
Take **one jīn of horseweed (*mǎ chǐ xiàn*)**, burn into ashes, finely grind, and apply with **pig fat (*zhū zhī*)**—**itch will subside.**

**Another Method for Treating All Fleshy Ulcers (*Chuáng Ròu*):**
Where **flesh protrudes like ants’ hills, several inches high (*rú yǐ chū shù cùn*)**:
Take **one liǎng of sulfur (*liú huáng*)**, finely grind, and apply thinly to the protruding flesh—**it will immediately shrink.**

**From *Ghost’s Bequeathed Prescriptions* (*Guǐ Yí Fāng*):**
**Method for Treating All Fleshy Ulcers (*Chuáng Ròu Chū*):**
Burn **black dates (*wū méi*)** into ashes, grind into a powder, and apply—**the malignant flesh will vanish at once, most miraculous.**

**From *Simple and Essential Prescriptions for Saving the Masses* (*Jiǎn Yào Jì Zhòng Fāng*):**
**Prescription for Applying to Ulcers:**
Take **four liǎng of turmeric (*huáng yào zǐ*)**, grind into a powder, and apply with **cold water**. Reapply when dry—**itch will subside.**

**From *The Army Medical Manual* (*Bīng Bù Shǒu Jí*):**
**Method for Treating Heat Ulcers (*Rè Chuāng*)** caused by ingestion of **Dan Poison (*Dān Shí*)**, where pain is unbearable:
Wrap **paper rings** around the swollen area, fill the center with **saltpeter (*xiāo shí*)**, and pour water over it with a spoon. Once the heat subsides, **pain will cease.**

**Method for Treating Head Ulcers (*Tóu Chuāng*)** and all heat ulcers (*Rè Chuāng*):**
First, cleanse with **a small amount of vinegar (*cù*)** mixed with water to remove the scabs. Then, wash with **warm water** until dry. Take **centipede powder (*bǎi cǎo shuāng*)**, finely grind, mix with **a little talc (*ní fěn*)**, and apply with **raw oil (*shēng yóu*)**—**itch will heal immediately.**

**Method for Treating Malignant Ulcers (*È Chuāng*):**
A **Tang-era record** of this case states:
In the **Jiangzu region**, there was once a merchant whose **left arm developed an ulcer resembling a human face**, yet without other suffering. When the merchant playfully dripped wine into its mouth, the face turned **red**, and when food was given to it, the ulcer could **consume it**. If too much was eaten, the arm swelled, and if nothing was eaten, the entire arm **became paralyzed**. A skilled physician instructed him to test all possible medicines—**metals, minerals, herbs, and trees**—but none caused discomfort until **fritillary bulb (*bèi mǔ*)** was administered. The ulcer **frowned and closed its mouth**, and the merchant rejoiced, saying: *“This medicine can cure it!”*
He then **pierced the ulcer’s mouth with a small reed tube**, administered the medicine, and in **a few days**, a scab formed—**the wound healed**, though its nature remained unknown. **Careful consideration reveals:** this was not a **golden ulcer (*Jīn Chuāng*)** as described in *The Classic of Materia Medica* (*Běn Jīng*).

**Method for Treating Sudden Onset of Leprosy (*Lài Bìng*),** where skin becomes **numb**, or **itches persistently like crawling insects**, or **vision is obscured as if by hanging threads**, or **itch turns red and black—**this must be treated **urgently** with **barbarian wine (*mán yí jiǔ*)**, the best quality.

**Method for Treating White Leprosy (*Bái Lài*):**
Take **five jīn of sophora root (*kǔ cān*)**, and **three dǒu of wine**, steep them, and **drink without cessation**. Additionally, take the **root bark of sophora (*kǔ cān pí gēn*)**, grind into powder, and take orally—**effects verified.**

**Another Method:**
Take **one thousand stalks of mugwort (*ài cǎo*)**, boil them thickly, and use the liquid to steep **fermented grains (*qū*)** into wine. **Drink regularly until intoxicated**—**Ma Tong’s prescription.**

**Ma Tong’s Prescription:**
Take **one whole large viper (*dà shǎn shé*)**, chop it carefully without injury, and steep in wine—**one dǒu for large individuals, five shēng for smaller ones**. Warm with **chaff fire (*jiāng huǒ*)**, let it settle, then extract **one cùn of the viper**, mix with **pig fat rendered in the twelfth lunar month (*là yuè zhū gāo*)**, and apply to the ulcers—**itch will subside.**
This also treats **rat-bite ulcers (*shǔ lián*)** and all malignant ulcers (*È Chuāng*).

**Another Method:**
Take **two jīn of sophora root (*kǔ cān*)**, **two liǎng of honeybee nest (*lù fēng fāng*)**, **two jīn of fermented grains (*qū*)**, and **three dǒu of water**, steep the medicine overnight, strain, and ferment with **two shēng of glutinous millet (*shǔ mǐ*)** until ready. **Drink gradually, three times daily.**
**One variation adds** the **root bark of sophora (*kǔ cān pí*)**—**even more effective.**

**Supplementary Prescriptions:**

**From *Sacred Benevolent Prescriptions* (*Shèng Huì Fāng*):**
**Method for Treating Severe Wind Conditions (*Dà Fēng Jí*),** where **bones and flesh rot away**, **every joint aches acidly**, **eyebrows and hairline fall out**, and **the body itches persistently**:
Take **one jīn of horseweed (*mǎ xiān hāo*)**, finely chop, and **parch-roast into a powder**. Before each meal and at night, take **two qián**, adjusted with **warm wine**.

**Another Method for Treating Severe Wind Conditions (*Dà Fēng Jí*),** to **regrow eyebrows and hairline**:
Take **one jīn of Chinese juniper leaves (*cè bǎi yè*)**, **steam nine times and dry in the sun nine times**, pound and sift into powder. Refine with **honey**, form pills the size of **Chinese catalpa seeds (*wú tóng zǐ*)**, and take **three times daily, one at night**, with **five to ten pills in warm water**. After **one hundred days**, **new growth will appear**.

**Another Method for Treating Severe Wind (*Dà Fēng*),** where **hair on the head and face falls out**:
Take **mulberry twig ash (*sāng zhàng huī*)**, wash with **hot water** to extract the juice, and bathe the face. Then, take **soybean water (*dà dòu shuǐ*)** to grind into a paste, and **apply with horseweed ash (*mǎ xiān hāo huī*)**—**the efficacy is even better**. Next, use **boiled water with green beans (*lǜ dòu*)**, remove the skin, and take the **clean beans**—**do not exceed ten doses**. **Bath the head every other day**, and **wash the face daily**.

**Another Method for Treating White Leprosy (*Bái Lài*):**
Take **unlimited amounts of horseweed (*mǎ biān cǎo*)**, grind into powder, and before each meal, take **one qián**, adjusted with **schizonepeta and mint decoction (*jīng jiè bó hé tāng*)**.

**From *Dietary Therapy* (*Shí Liáo*):**
**Method for Treating Leprosy (*Lài Bìng*):**
Take **one jīn of white honey (*bái mì*)** and **two jīn of fresh ginger (*shēng jiāng*)**, pound to extract the juice. First, weigh **equal amounts** into a **wok**, then place **the honey in the wok**, melt it, and weigh **five jīn liǎng**. Next, add **the ginger juice to the honey**, simmer with **gentle fire** until the ginger juice is fully consumed. Weigh the honey again—**one jīn liǎng**—and **rest immediately**. The medicine is now complete.

**For a Leprosy Sufferer of Thirty Years:**
At dawn, take a pill the size of a large date (*zǎo*), **one dose**, three times daily. **Alcohol may be taken freely** as a beverage.

**Avoid:** raw cold foods, vinegar, slippery substances, and foul-smelling items. **Its benefits are vast**, and **it has saved countless lives**—too numerous to recount all.

**From *Secret Essentials of the Outer Chamber* (*Wàitái Mìyào*):**
**Treatment for Severe Wind-Related Illness (*Èfēng Jí*):**
Take **pine resin (*sōng zhī*)**, refine it, and drop it into **cold water twenty times**. Form into pills with honey, and take **two liǎng** on an empty stomach, **three times daily**. For those with a **collapsed nasal septum (*bí zhù duàn lí*)**, this will correct it in **three hundred days**. **Avoid salt and sexual activity**.

**From *The Master Who Embraces Simplicity* (*Bàopǔ Zǐ*) says:
**Zhào Qú** suffered from leprosy for many years, and no physician could cure him. His family then **brought provisions** and fled to a **mountain cave** to seek help. Zhào lamented his misfortune, **weeping bitterly**.

After a month, a **Daoist immortal (*xiān rén*)** passed through the cave and saw him. Moved by pity, the immortal inquired into his condition. Zhào, recognizing the stranger as an extraordinary being, **knocked his head in reverence** and **confessed his plight**, begging for his life. The immortal then took a **medicine from his pouch** and gave it to him, instructing him on its use.

In **over a hundred days**, his sores healed, his complexion brightened, and his skin became smooth. When the immortal returned to check on him, Zhào **repaid his gratitude** for saving his life and **begged for the recipe**. The immortal replied: *"This is pine resin; there is an abundance of it there. You may refine and take it. With prolonged use, your body will grow lighter, your strength will multiply a hundredfold. You will traverse perilous heights and cross treacherous depths without fatigue, live to a hundred years with teeth unfallen and hair unsilvered, and at night, you will often emit a radiant glow—bright as a mirror."*

**From *The Transmission of Divine Responses and Immortals* (*Gǎnyìng Shénxiān Zhuàn*) says:
**Cuī Yán**, a soldier in the **Left Attendant Cavalry Corps (*Zuǒ Qīn Jì Jūn*)**, fell ill one day. His **two eyes grew dim**, and he could no longer **discern figures** even at close range. His **eyebrows and hair fell out**, his **nose bridge collapsed**, and his skin developed **sores like scabies (*xiǎn*)**—all deemed **incurable afflictions**. His family **despaired of his survival**.

He then **sought refuge in the Luó Valley of Yángzhou**. While there, he **encountered a wandering Daoist (*dào liú*)** who emerged from the valley. The Daoist **did not reveal his name or lineage** but gave him a prescription:
Take **one to two jīn of soapberry thorns (*zào jiǎo cì*)**, burn them to **ash**, then **steam and dry** them thoroughly. Grind into powder, and **boil a strong decoction of rhubarb (*dà huáng*)**. Take **one qián** with the decoction before meals for **one decennial period (*shùn*)**. His **temple hair will regrow**, his skin will **brighten and become supple**, and his condition will be cured. His **eyesight will double**, surpassing the norm.

After obtaining this remedy, the Daoist **retired into the mountains**, leaving no trace of his whereabouts.

**From *The Chronicle of Court and Field* (*Zhāoyě Huìzǎi*) says:

「In **Shangzhou**, there was a person afflicted by **great wind** (*dàfēng*), whom his family despised. They built a thatched hut for him in the mountains, where a black snake (*wūshé*) fell into his wine jar (*jiǔ géng*). The patient was unaware, but after drinking the wine, his condition gradually improved. Only when the jar’s bottom still contained the snake’s bones did he realize its cause.

**Daoist Caution** (*dào jǐn*) notes: According to **Li Zhao’s *History Supplement*** (*Guóshǐ Bǔ*), Li Zhou’s younger brother suffered from **wind** (*fēng*), and someone suggested that **snake wine** (*shéjiǔ*) could cure it. Thus, he sought a black snake, placed it alive in a jar, and fermented it with **malted barley** (*qū niè*). For several days, the snake’s cries never ceased. When the wine was ready, its aroma was intense, and he drank it fully. In moments, it all transformed into water, leaving only the snake’s **hair and scales** (*máo fā*). The account in *Zhāoyě Huìzǎi* is likely too extreme to be taken lightly.

**Treatment for Sudden Onset of Verminous Fistulas** (*chú dé chóngshǔ zhūliú fāng*)—**Fourth Remedy for Afflictions of the Scrotum** (*dì sìshíyī fāng*)

**Bo Ge** (*Gě Shì*) says: All swellings have their corresponding **pathogenic factors** (*xiāngzhǔ*), and patients should examine the original remedy.

Most often, it appears on both sides of the head, with **clustered nodules** (*lěilěi yǒu hé*).

**Bo Ge’s Remedy**: For **verminous fistulas** (*shǔliú*) where the **nodules** (*hé*) are painful and not yet suppurated (*wèi chéng nóng*), apply **cypress leaves** (*bó yè*), sprinkle with **refined salt** (*fá yán*), and **moxibust** (*wēn*) until the heat penetrates downward—it will then dissolve.

**Bo Ge’s Remedy**: If one suddenly contracts **verminous fistulas** (*shǔliú*) with **afflictions of the scrotum** (*yīnzhǒng*) yet no sores have formed but the area is already hot, use the following remedy quickly: Pound **black rooster’s feet** (*wū jī zú*) or **plantain herb** (*chēqián cǎo*), and apply it. If the **nodules** (*hé*) have already formed and **pus and blood** (*nóng xuè*) are discharging, smear with **hot pig dung** (*rè niú shǐ*), three times daily.

Another remedy: Take **white fresh skin** (*bái xiān pí*), boil and consume one *sheng* (升), causing the vermin to be vomited up.

Another remedy: Take one **cat or weasel** (*māo lí*), prepare it as a soup (*zuò gēng rú shí fǎ*), and ingest it on an empty stomach (*kòng xīn jìn zhī*)—the vermin will die and exit.

Or, swallow it raw—its efficacy is even greater.

Another remedy: Extract a **vermin** (*shǔ*) from the center of a fistula, one as large as a **chicken egg** (*jī zǐ dà*), and with **three-year-old pig fat** (*sān suì làyuè zhū zhī*) from the **twelfth lunar month** (*làyuè*), decoct it until the vermin’s **bones, flesh, and hair** (*gǔ ròu yú fā*) are completely dissolved. Apply half to the sore and consume the other half with wine (*jiǔ fú*)—the vermin will exit through the wound.

**Bo Ge’s Remedy**: A **secret method** (*mì bù chuán zhī fǎ*)—**Liu Xun’s Remedy for Verminous Fistulas** (*Liú Xún shǔliú fāng*).
Use **tortoise shell** (*guī ké*), **roasted licorice root** (*zhì gān cǎo*), **cinnamon bark** (*guì xīn*), **realgar** (*xióng huáng*), **dried ginger** (*gān jiāng*), and **roasted weasel bones** (*zhì lí gǔ*), divide them equally, pound into a powder, mix with **honey** (*mì*), and apply to the wound—it will never fail. First, **moxibust** (*jiǔ*) to create the wound, then apply the medicine effectively.

Another remedy: **Five升 of oak bark** (*zhà mù bái pí*), combined with **one斗 of wine** (*yī dǒu jiǔ*), decoct together. Remove the bark when done, and reduce the liquid to **two升** (*èr shēng*). Consume it all, and the **old stagnant flesh** (*sùròu*) will emerge—it will then heal.

Another remedy: **Fistula sores with seated flesh** (*liúchuāng zuò ròu gāo*).
Use **white mulberry bark** (*kuàngshù bái pí*), **vermin flesh** (*shǔròu*), and **angelica root** (*dāngguī*), each **two liǎng** (两); **leek white** (*xiè bái*), **three liǎng**; **raw rehmannia root** (*shēng dìhuáng*), **five liǎng**; and **three升 of three-year-old pig fat** (*sān suì zhū zhī*). Decoct into a plaster (*jiān gāo chéng*), apply it to the wound, and cover the **orifice** (*kǒng*) to promote new flesh growth.

**Bo Ge’s Remedy**: If the sores are numerous but the **orifices** (*kǒng*) are small, it is **ant fistula** (*mǐliú*). The remedy: Burn **dried carp scales** (*bǐng lí jiǎ*), mix with **pig fat** (*zhū gāo*), and apply.

Another remedy: Burn **twenty-one spiders** (*zhīzhū*), and use the ashes effectively.

Another remedy for **fistulas** (*liú fāng*): Decoct **peach leaves** (*táo yè*) and **peach branches** (*táo zhī*), cleanse and wash the wound, and insert the decoction into the **orifice** (*kǒng*)—this is a highly verified remedy.

**Bo Ge’s Remedy**: If the **fistula** (*liú*) affects the **mouth** (*kǒu lǐ*), take **white mulberry root** (*kuàngshù gēn*) from the **eastern journey** (*dōngxíng*), finely grind it, boil in water, and use the clear liquid to **rinse the mouth** (*hán zhī*). Spit repeatedly (*shù tǔ*), but do not swallow.

**Flesh Fistula Remedy** (*ròuliú fāng*): Pound **sophora bark** (*huái bái pí*) into pills (*dǎo wán*), wrap them in **cotton** (*mián*), and insert into the **lower abdomen** (*xiàbù zhōng*). Apply externally—it works.

**Verminous Fistula Remedy** (*shǔliú fāng*): **Andromeda root** (*shínán*), **raw rehmannia root** (*shēng dìhuáng*), **orpiment** (*cíhuáng*), **poria** (*fúlíng*), and **scutellaria root** (*huánglián*), each **two liǎng**. Make into a powder (*wéi sǎn*), and apply to the wound twice daily.

Another remedy: **Alum** (*fánshí*), **three fēn** (分), burn it; **leopard-spotted cat** (*bān māo*), **one fēn**, roast it, remove its **head and feet** (*tóu zú*), pound and mix with **vinegar** (*cù*). Consume **half a chǐ** (匕), and in moments, the **verminous creature** (*liú chóng*) will exit through the **urine** (*xiǎobiàn*).

**From *The Simplified Abbreviated Prescriptions* (*Shān Fán Fāng*).**

**Additional Remedies** (*Fù fāng*)

**From *The Prescriptions for Emergencies at One’s Elbow* (*Zhǒuhòu Fāng*)**: Treating **wind fistula** (*fēngliú*).
Use **one honeycomb** (*lù fēng fáng*), roast until it turns **yellow and red** (*huáng chì sè*), grind into powder (*wéi mò*). Each dose, take **one qián** (钱), mix evenly with **three-year-old pig fat** (*làyuè zhū zhī*), and apply to the wound.

**From *The Thousand-Gold Prescriptions* (*Qiān Jīn Fāng*)**: Treating **verminous fistula** (*shǔliú*).
Take **one chicken egg** (*jī zǐ*), cook in **rice gruel** (*mǐ xià*), simmer for half a day (*bàn rì*). Remove the egg yolk (*qǔchū huáng*), and simmer until it turns **black** (*fú rèn zhī*). First, wipe the wound with the egg yolk liquid (*shì*), dry it, and insert the medicine into the **orifice** (*kǒng*). Three applications will cure it.

**From *The Thousand-Gold Supplement* (*Qiān Jīn Yì*)**: Treating **ant fistula** (*mǐliú*).
Take **twenty-one dried carp scales** (*cì lí jiǎ*), grind into powder (*wéi mò*), mix with **pig fat** (*zhū gāo*), and apply.

**From *The Sacred Benevolence Prescriptions* (*Shèng Huì Fāng*)**: Treating **mole cricket fistula** (*zhōugū liú*).
Burn **valonea leaves** (*qì yè*) into ashes (*wéi huī*), finely grind them (*xì nián*), and soak **valonea leaves** (*qì yè*) in **used rice water** (*zāi bié*) to wash the wound (*qǔ xǐ liú*). Wipe it dry, and insert a small amount of ash into the **orifice** (*liú zhōng*).

Another remedy: For treating **all fistulas** (*yīqiè liú*).
Refine **pine resin** (*sōng zhī*) into a powder (*liàn chéng sōng zhī wéi mò*), pack it into the **orifice** (*tián liú kǒng*) until full (*lìng mǎn*), and apply three to four times daily.

**Treatment for Sudden Scrotal Swelling and Pain** (*dì sìshí'èr fāng*)—**Fourth Remedy for Afflictions of the Scrotum** (*dì sìshí'èr fāng*)

**Bo Ge’s Remedy**: For **sudden scrotal swelling** (*nánzǐ yīn chú zhǒng*) and pain in men (*fāng*), **moxibust** (*jiǔ*) the **second joint** (*dì èr jié*) of the **big toe** (*zú dà zhǐ*) at its **horizontal crease** (*héng wén lǐ*), with **five moxa cones** (*wǔ zhuàng jiā*). **Bo Ge** (*Yáo Yún*) says: The **root of the big toe** (*zú dà zhǐ běn*), with **three moxa cones** (*sān zhuàng*).

Another remedy: Pound the **kernel of peach pits** (*táo hé zhōng rén*), decoct it into a powder (*wéi mò*), and consume with wine (*jiǔ fú*) like a **small shot pellet** (*rú tán wán*).

**Bo Ge** (*Yáo Yún*) says: No more than **three doses** (*bùguò sān*).

Another remedy: **Yellow earth from the hearth** (*zào zhōng huáng tǔ*), grind into powder (*wéi mò*), mix with **chicken egg yolk** (*jī zǐ huáng*), and apply.

**Snake couch grass** (*shé chuáng zǐ*), ground into powder (*wéi mò*), mixed with **chicken egg yolk** (*jī zǐ huáng*), and applied—this is also effective.

Another remedy: Pound **chervil roots** (*wújīng gēn*) or **horsewhip grass** (*mǎbiān cǎo*), and apply—both are effective.

**Bo Ge** (*Yáo Yún*) agrees.

Another remedy: Take **six rooster spurs** (*jī hé liù mǔ*), burn them, and mix equally with **snake couch grass powder** (*shé chuáng zǐ wéi mò*). Consume together (*héng fú*), and apply a small amount near the **testicles** (*ruǎn zuǒ*)—this is excellent.

**Bo Ge’s Remedy** omits **snake couch grass** (*wú shé chuáng zǐ*).

For **children’s scrotal hernias** (*xiǎo’ér yīn shàn*), when they flare up with **swelling and pain** (*fā shí zhǒng tòng*), follow **Xian Eng’s previous moxibustion method** (*yī xiān’ēng qián jiǔ fǎ*), and **moxibust** (*jiǔ*) the **affected side** (*suí zuǒ yòu*). It will improve.

If the pain is **sharp as a stab** (*suí tòng rú cì*), **moxibust** accordingly (*fāng*).」

For **scrotal hernia** (*yīn shàn*), simply consume the dried juice of **raw *yègān*** (*shēng yègān zhī qǔ xià*), or take it in pill form (*yī kě fú wán yào xià zhī*). **Bo Ge** (*Yáo Yún*) states: **"Walking Horse Decoction"** (*zuò wǒmǎ táng*) is also mentioned in the **Corpus of the Dead** (*shī zhù zhōng*).

When a **scrotal hernia** (*yīn shàn*) suddenly retracts into the abdomen (*yīn huán zú suō rù fù*), causing severe pain as if near death (*jí tòng yù sǐ*), it is called **scrotal hernia**. **Wolfsbane** (*lángdú*) four *liǎng*, **Siler root** (*fángfēng*) two *liǎng*, and **Aconite** (*fùzǐ*) three *liǎng*—burned and made into honey pills (*mì wán*)—should be taken, three pills per dose (*fú sān wán*), the size of **Chinese hackberry seeds** (*tóngzǐ dà*), three times daily (*rì yè sān dù*).

When **sudden pain occurs in the penis** (*yīn jīng zhōng zú tòng bù kě rěn*), take **realgar** (*xiónghuáng*) and **alum stone** (*fánshí*) each two *liǎng*, and **licorice root** (*gāncǎo*) one *chǐ* (a cubit) or five *shāng* (a pint)—boil to reduce to two *shāng*, then strain and apply (*zhì*).

**Bo Ge** (*Yáo Yún*) states: This cures cases as large as a **fighting bowl** (*dǎ dòu zhě*).

**Ge Shi’s Remedy** for **male genital ulcers** (*nánzǐ yīn chuāng sǔn làn*):

Boil **yellow berberine bark** (*huángbài*) and wash the ulcer (*quán chuāng xiǎo zhī*). Alternatively, apply **white honey** (*bái mì*) to it. Another remedy: Take **yellow berberine bark** (*huánglián*) and **yellow berberine root** (*huángbài*) in equal parts, grind into powder (*wéi zhī*), and boil with **fat pork juice** (*zhǐ zhū ròu zhī*) to apply to the ulcer until dry (*zhì chuāng qì*), then dust with powder (*fěn zhī*).

**Bo Ge’s Remedy**: Honey-fried licorice powder (*mì jiān gāncǎo wéi*), applied to the ulcer. For cases where the **penile head swells** (*yīn tóu zhǒng*) and the **ulcer near the neck is near rupture** (*xiàng xià chuāng yù duàn*), apply **pork juice** (*zhū ròu zhī*) after straining (*zhì*). Following **Bo Ge’s method** (*yī Yáo fāng*), the result is miraculously effective (*jiù shén xiào*).

For **penile ulcers nearing exhaustion** (*yīn shì yù jìn zhě*), take **toad dung** (*xiāmá*) and **rabbit dung** (*tùshǐ*) in equal parts, grind into powder (*fèn*), and apply to the ulcer (*bó chuāng shàng*).

When **penile itching with discharge** (*yīn yǎng zhī chū*) occurs, chew **raw yellow soybean** (*shēng dàdòu huáng*), and apply to the ulcer. This also cures **urine scald ulcers** (*niào huī chuāng*).

**Bo Ge’s Remedy** for **penile itching with new ulcers** (*yīn yǎng shēng chuāng*):

Chew **sesame seeds** (*húmá*), and apply to the ulcer.

**Ge Shi’s Remedy** for **penile scrotal damp itching with peeling skin** (*yīn náng xià shī yǎng pí bō*):

Take **14 *wūméi*** (*wūméi shí sì mǔ*), **40 coins** (*qián sì shí wén*), and **a pinch of salt** (*sān zhǐ cuō yán*), along with **one *shāng* of sour wine** (*kǔ jiǔ yī shāng*), and soak together in a **copper vessel** (*yú tóng qì nèi zǒng zhì jiǔ rì*), washing daily (*rì xǐ zhī*).

Another remedy: Boil **sophora bark** (*huáipí*) or **yellow berberine bark juice** (*huángbài zhī*) and **cinnamon leaf juice** (*xiāng yè zhī*)—both are effective (*bìng liáng*).

For **penile ulcers with pus discharge resembling a mortar** (*rén yīn shēng chuāng, nóng chū jiù fāng*), take **high-chang alum** (*gāochāng bái fán*) one small *liǎng*, grind finely (*dǎo xì*), and mix with **equal parts of hemp** (*má rén děng fèn*), pulverize (*yán*), and refine **one *gē* of pork fat** (*liàn zhū zhī yī hé*). In a **porcelain vessel** (*yú cí qì zhōng*), blend all into a paste (*hé jiǎo rú gāo*). Then, cut **white sophora bark** (*huái bái pí qiē*), make a decoction (*zuò táng*), and wash the ulcer (*yǐ xǐ chuāng*). Pat dry (*shì lìng gān*), apply the paste (*jí qǔ gāo tú shàng*), and finally affix **strychnine leaf** (*qiū yè tiē shàng*)—no more than three applications (*bù guò sān*).

There are **two types of penile ulcers** (*yīn chuāng yǒu èr zhǒng*). The first: **ulcers with pus discharge resembling a mortar** (*zuò jiù nóng chū*), called **penile erosion ulcers** (*yīn shì chuāng*). The second: **ulcers that are simply hot** (*dàn yì zuò chuāng*), called **heat ulcers** (*rè chuāng*). If the ulcer is due to **heat** (*ruò shì rè*), take **one *liǎng* of yellow berberine bark** (*huángbài yī liǎng*) and **one *liǎng* of scutellaria root** (*huángqín yī liǎng*), cut, and make a decoction (*zuò táng*) to wash it (*xǐ zhī*). Then, take **coptis rhizome** (*huánglián*) and **yellow berberine bark** (*huángbài*), grind into powder (*zuò wéi fú zhī*).

For **female genital ulcers** (*nǚzǐ yīn chuāng*), grind **sulfur** (*liúhuáng wéi*), and apply to the ulcer (*fú shàng*).

**Bo Ge** agrees (*Yáo tóng*).

---

**Further Treatments:**
Burn and pulverize **almonds** (*xìngrén*), apply as a poultice (*fú zhī*).

Another prescription: grind **realgar** (*xiónghuáng*) and **alum stone** (*fánshí*) each into **two *fēn*** of powder, and **musk** (*shèxiāng*) into **half *fēn***, mix and apply (*dǎo fú*). Bo Ge agrees (*Yáo tóng*).

If there is **pain in the genital region** (*ruò yīn zhōng tòng*):
Take **alum stone** (*fánshí*) **two *fēn***, parch and reduce, and **rhubarb root** (*dàhuáng*) **one *fēn***, and **licorice root** (*gāncǎo*) **half *fēn***, grind into powder (*zuò wéi*), wrap in cotton (*mián guǒ*) like a date (*yú*), and insert to relieve pain (*dǎo zhī*), until improvement (*qǔ chà*).

If **fleshy polyps protrude** (*ruò yǒu xīròu tū chū*):
Use **three *shēng* of bitter wine** (*kǔjiǔ*), soak **five *méi* of *wūméi* (glossy privet fruit)** (*wūméi*) for **three days** (*sān rì*), then wash the affected area (*yǐ xǐ zhī*). Repeat **three to four times daily** (*rìyè sān sì dù*).

If **itching or scratching causes pain and suffocation** (*ruò kǔ yǎng pò zhī tòng mèn*):
Take **fresh pork liver** (*zhūgān*), roast until hot (*zhì rè*), and place inside the genital region (*nèi yīn zhōng*). A **worm** (*chóng*) will soon attach itself to the liver (*dāng yǒu chóng zhuó gān*). Then remove it.

**Prescription for Infant Baldness** (*xiǎo ér tū fāng*):
Take **whitehead root** (*báitóu'éng gēn*), pulverize (*dǎo*), and apply (*fú*) overnight (*yī xiǔ*). Alternatively, it may be applied as a poultice (*zuò wéi chuāng*) for **twenty days** (*èrshí rì*), until cured (*qù*).

**Moxibustion for Genital Edema** (*jiǔ tuí*):
Apply moxibustion (*jiǔ*) directly to the edema (*tuí*).

Another method: apply moxibustion (*jiǔ*) to the **penile shaft** (*jīng shàng*).

Another method: apply moxibustion (*jiǔ*) to the **white vessel on the lower abdomen** (*bái xiǎo fù mài shàng*), and to the **three central points of the big toe** (*jiǔ jiǎo dà zhǐ sān zhōng*), using **one strong moxa cone** (*jiǔ yī zhuàng*).

Another method: apply moxibustion (*jiǔ*) to the **small toe** (*xiǎo zhǐ tóu*), aligning it with the edema (*tuí*) on either side (*suí tuí zuǒyòu zhuó jiǔ*).

**Prescription by Yao Shixian** (*Yáo Shì fāng*):
Take **willow branches** (*yángliǔ zhī*) as thick as the **big toe** (*dà zhǐ*) and **three *chǐ* long** (*sān chǐ*), **twenty branches** (*èrshí méi*), boil in water (*shuǐ zhǔ*) until extremely hot (*jìng rè*). Cover the swollen area (*zhǒng chù*) with old paper (*gù zhǐ*) and felt (*zhān*), then repeatedly press (*gēng qǔ*) with the hot willow branches (*zhǔ zhī*). Continue until improvement (*qǔ chà*), then stop (*zhǐ*).

**Prescription for Testicular Edema** (*luǎn tuí*):
Pulverize **ripe peach kernels** (*shú táo rén*), and apply (*fú zhī*). It also treats **female genital edema** (*nǚ rén yīn zhǒng*), replacing the poultice (*zuò*) when it dries (*zào*).

---
**From *Xiao Pin* (小品):**
**Peony Powder** (*Mǔdān sǎn*) – **Prescription for Edema with Excessive *Qi* and Distension** (*liáo tuí piān dà qì zhàng fāng*):
**Peony root** (*mǔdān*), **Siler divaricatum root** (*fángfēng*), **cinnamon twigs** (*guìxīn*), **parched broad beans** (*biàn dòu*), and **iron filings** (*tiě jīng*), each in equal parts (*fēn děng*), mix and grind finely (*hé dǎo xià*). Take **one *fāngcùn* spoonful** (*fāngcùn shì*) for adults, or **one *dāo guī*** for children (*xiǎo ér yī dāo guī*), and cure in **twenty days** (*èrshí rì*). Excellent results (*dà liáng*).

For **infants** (*yīng ér*), mix with **breast milk** (*rǔ shì*) to the consistency of **large soybeans** (*dà dòu*), and administer (*yǔ zhī*). Without medication (*bù yòng yào fǎ*), this method reliably cures edema (*liáo tuí bì chà fāng*).

Have the patient hold **a *nuò* rice cake** (*nuò mǐ bǐng zǐ*) and **one hundred *jiǎ* prickly ash thorns** (*zào jiǎ cí yī bǎi gè*), then sit at a **community shrine** (*zuò shè chù*). First, distribute the **prickly ash thorns** (*zào jiǎ cí*) equally among the shrine attendees (*shè rén*), shrine officials (*shè guān*), and elders (*sān lǎo yǐ xià*), giving each **one needle** (*yī zhēn*). Then, show the rice cake (*bǐng zǐ*) to the crowd, stating from head to tail (*cóng tóu zhì wěi*), that the officials and elders (*shè guān yǐ xià*) have begged for **needle-pounding** (*qǐ zhēn chuí*). Ask the crowd: *"What is being pounded?"* (*chuí hé wù?*). The patient replies: *"The crowd's leader"* (*chuí rén kuí*). After completely encircling and exhausting the needles (*zhōu zā zǒng biàn qì*), return the rice cake to the home (*bǐng què dào jiā*), dry it (*bǐng gān*), and store it (*shōu*). The edema will then **unconsciously dissipate** (*tuí bù jué zì sàn*), never to return (*yǒng chà*), with **miraculous efficacy** (*jí shén xiào*).

---
**From *Qian Jin Fang* (千金方):**
If a **man’s genital region is cold** (*yǒu rén yīn lěng*), due to **shame causing cold *qi*** (*cán jiàn lěng qì rù*), leading to **scrotal distension and fear of death** (*yīn náng zhǒng mǎn kǒng sǐ*), with **day-and-night pain and suffocation** (*rìyè téng mèn bù dé mián*):
Take **fresh chili peppers** (*shēng jiāo*), select the **plumpest** (*zé zhī lìng*), wrap them in cloth (*yǐ bù pò guǒ zhe*), and place them over the **scrotum** (*huán náng*), making a layer **half-*cùn* thick** (*lìng hòu bàn cùn*). Soon, the **hot *qi*** (*rè qì*) will spread widely (*dà tōng*). Replace the poultice **twice daily** (*rì zài yì zhī*), until improvement (*qǔ chà*).

Another prescription from *Wài Tái Mì Yào Fang* (外台秘要方):
Boil **great burdock root** (*dà jiè gēn*) into its juice (*zhī*), and administer (*fú zhī*). The condition will immediately improve (*lì chà*).

From *Méi Shī Fang* (梅师方):
**Treatment for Sudden Testicular Distension and Pain** (*zhì zú wài shèn piān zhǒng téng tòng*):
Grind **rhubarb root** (*dàhuáng*) into powder (*wéi*), mix with **vinegar** (*cù*), and apply (*fú zhī*). Replace when dry (*fú zhī zào*).

Another prescription: grind **cinnamon twigs** (*guìxīn*) into powder (*wéi*), mix with water (*shuǐ*), and apply **one *fāngcùn* spoonful** (*tiáo fāngcùn shì*).

Another prescription from *Méi Shī Fang* (梅师方):
**Treatment for Sudden Testicular Pain** (*zhì zú wài shèn piān téng*):
Mix **prickly ash thorns** (*zào jiǎ cí*) with **its bark** (*pí*) into powder (*wéi*), adjust with water (*shuǐ tiáo*), and apply (*fú zhī*). Effective (*liáng*).

From *Chū Yú Shì Fang* (初虞世方):
**Treatment for Genital Edema with Undetermined Location and Pain** (*zhì shuǐ □ piān dà shàng xià bù dìng téng tòng*):
Take **oyster shell** (*mǔlì*)—**no limit on quantity** (*bù xiàn duō shǎo*)—fix with **salt mud** (*yán ní*), and **three *jīn* of charcoal** (*tàn*), calcine until the fire is exhausted (*jiān lìng huǒ jìn*), cool (*lěng*), then take **two *liǎng* of the residue** (*tàn*), and **one *liǎng* of dried ginger** (*gān jiāng*), parch (*páo*), grind into fine powder (*yòu wéi xì fú*). Mix with **cold water** (*lěng shuǐ*), adjust to the desired consistency (*xī shòu děng suǒ*), and apply to the affected area (*fú bìng chù*). If **urination improves** (*xiǎo biàn lì*), the condition will heal (*jí qù*).

---
**From *Jīng Yàn Fang* (经验方):**
**Treatment for Male Genital *Qi* Injury and Related Distension** (*zhì zhàngfù běncáng qì shāng, pángguāng lián xiǎo cháng děng qì*):
Take **golden bell fruit** (*jīn líng zǐ*) **one hundred** (*yī bǎi*), soak in **warm water** (*wēn táng*), peel (*qù pí*), and **croton seeds** (*bā dòu*) **two hundred** (*èr bǎi*), crush slightly (*chuí wēi pò*), and **fermented wheat bran** (*fú*) **two *shēng*** (*liǎng*). Mix in a **copper pot** (*tóng guō*) and roast (*chǎo*). Stop when the **golden bell fruit turns red** (*jīn líng zǐ chì shú wéi dù*). Cool (*fàng lěng*), remove the seeds (*qǔ chū qù hé*), and grind into powder (*wéi fú*). Take **three *qiǎn* per dose** (*měi fú sān qiǎn*), mixing with **hot wine or vinegar water** (*fēi shí rè jiǔ, cù táng tiáo bìng dé*). The **wheat bran and croton seeds** (*fú, bā dòu*) are not to be used (*bù yòng*).

---
**From *Wài Tái Mì Yào* (外台秘要):**
**Treatment for Urinary Bladder *Qi* Distension** (*zhì pángguāng qì jí, yí xià qì*):
Use **artemisia capillaris** (*wúyīng*)—pound (*dǎo*), mix with **powdered salt** (*shí wéi fú zhī*), both in equal parts (*èr wù fēn děng*)—wrap in cotton (*mián guǒ*) like a date (*yú*), and insert into the **lower abdomen** (*xià bù*). Alternatively, it may **discharge turbid urine** (*xià shuǐ è zǐ*), or **reduce distension** (*xià qì*), both excellent (*jiā*).

Another method: **treat genital dampness** (*yīn xià shī*):
Take **one *shēng* of *hào zhūyú* (turmeric)** (*hào zhūyú*), boil with **three *shēng* of water** (*shuǐ*), until **three boiling points** (*sān fèi*), remove dregs (*qù zǐ*), and wash (*xǐ*). If **itching improves** (*yǎng chà*), the condition will resolve (*qì*).

Another method: **treat genital ulcers** (*yīn tóu shēng chuāng*):
Use **honey to roast licorice root** (*mì jiān gāncǎo*), and apply (*fú zhī*). The condition will improve (*chà*).

---
**From *Qian Jin Fang* (千金方):**
**Treatment for Male Genital Ulcers** (*zhì zhàngfù yīn tóu*):
Grind **cuttlefish bone** (*wūzé yú gǔ*) into powder (*wéi*), apply as a paste (*fén fú zhī*). Effective (*liáng*).

Another prescription from *Qian Jin Yì Fang* (千金翼方):
Take **one *méi* of **softshell turtle shell** (*biē jiǎ*), burn until charred (*shāo*), mix with **egg white** (*jī zǐ bái*), and apply (*fú zhī*). Effective (*liáng*).

**From *Ge Xianweng’s Emergency Handbook for Arm’s Reach Use*, Volume Six**
**Prescriptions for Treating Red, Painful, Dim, and Pierced Eye Ailments (No. 43)**
*Hua Tuo’s Prohibited Prescriptions*

Instruct the patient to use two fingers to gently press the afflicted eye, then recite aloud:
*"Chīchī, the house is narrow and cramped—no room for lodgers!"*
The ailment shall depart immediately.

**From the *Injury by Cold* Treatments (Appendix):**
**Maos’ Prescriptions**
For cold tears welling in the eyes, with redness and itching:
Boil **three parts rhubarb (huánglián)**, **two parts canarium (ruìrén)**, and **four parts dried ginger (gānjiāng)** in **one sheng of breastmilk (rǔshì)**, soaking overnight. Simmer gently, reduce to **three ge**, strain, and apply **one grain-sized portion** to the inner canthus.

**For Injured or Ruptured Pupils:**
Apply **two drops of cow bile daily**, shielding from wind.
If the **black pupil is ruptured**, the condition shall improve.

**Additional Prescriptions**

**From the *Fàn Wāng Prescriptions*:**
For cold tears welling in the eyes, unable to open with sharp pain:
Take salt the size of a large soybean, place it in the eye, then blink repeatedly to expel the salt. Rinse the eyes several times with cold water—this shall cure the ailment.

**From the *Bó Jì Prescriptions*:**
For wind-toxin ascending, causing swollen, itchy, and dry eyes with unbearable pain—sometimes with red, ulcerated upper or lower eyelids, or with floating cataracts and encroaching opaque growths—**Divine Wind-Dispelling Powder** is highly effective.
**Fivefold Myrobalan (wǔbèizi)**, 1 liang; **Climbing Honeysuckle Seed (mànjīngzi)**, 1.5 liang. Grind into a powder. For each dose, take 2 qián with 2 bowls of water, simmer in a copper or stone vessel until reduced to 1 bowl. Strain, then apply warm to wash the eyes. Retain the dregs for a second dose, then repeat the decoction and washing. This greatly clears the eyes, relieving dryness and itching.

**From the *Jiǎnyào Jìzhòng*:**
For liver deficiency causing eye pain, persistent cold sensations, and aching sinews—along with photophobia and fear of daylight—**Liver-Nourishing Powder** is prescribed.
**Summer-Thorned Sophora (xiàkūcǎo)**, ½ liang; **Mugwort (xiāngfùzi)**, 1 liang. Grind into a powder. Take 1 qián per dose, mixed with aged tea, without regard to time.

**From the *Shènghuì Prescriptions*:**
For severe eye itching, redness, and dryness, apply **dog bile** into the eyes.
Another prescription: For wind-induced red eyes, take **10 dried Earthworms (dìlóng)**, parched and ground into powder. Before sleep, mix with cold tea and take 2 sháo.

Another prescription: For cold-toxin from injury by cold attacking the eyes, causing white cataracts, use **2 liang of cuttlefish bone (wūzéiyú gǔ)**, excluding the large skin, ground into powder. Add a small amount of **camphor (lóngnáo)**, further refining until fine. Apply three to four times daily, using a small portion each time.

Another prescription: For chronic internal cataracts, grind **Plantain Seed (chēqiánzi)**, **Dried Rehmannia (gāndìhuáng)**, and **Ophiopogon (màimén'dōng)** in equal parts into a powder. Form into honey pills the size of **Chinese catalpa seeds (wútóngzi)**, and take as needed—highly effective.

For eye ailments, **rhubarb (huánglián)** is often used, but **Sheep Liver Pills** are particularly miraculous.
Take **1 large liang of rhubarb powder**, one **white sheep’s liver**, remove the membrane, and grind together in a mortar until extremely fine. Knead with multiple hands into pills the size of **Chinese catalpa seeds (wútóngzi)**. Take seven pills with warm water after each meal, repeating for five doses. This treats all eye diseases, cataracts, and blindness caused by green or blue afflictions. **Avoid pork and cold water.**

Sùyǔxī remarks: There was a man named **Cuī Chéngyuán**, who, while serving in office, pardoned a condemned prisoner. Years later, he fell ill and died by his own hand. One night, suffering from internal cataracts and blindness, as he sat alone sighing in the dead of night, he heard a rustling sound from the veranda. Asked who it was, the voice replied: *"I am the prisoner you once spared—I have come to repay this kindness."* The man then revealed this prescription before passing away. Following its use, his eyesight returned within months.

Thus the prescription was passed down to the world.

Another prescription: the modern physician’s eye-washing decoction.
Take equal parts of **dang gui (Chinese angelica)**, **sháo yào (white peony)**, and **huáng lián (coptis)**, finely ground. Brew with **snow water** or **sweetened water** into a thick infusion, and wash the eyes while hot—if it cools, rewarm and wash again. This greatly benefits the eyes. It treats **wind-toxicity**, **red-eye**, and **flowery cataracts**, all of which it governs.

Its principle states: All eye diseases arise from stagnant blood and vessels, so **blood-moving herbs** are combined with **huáng lián** to treat them. Blood, when heated, flows freely—that is why the wash must be applied while hot. Those who use it will find miraculous results.

Another prescription: for **crow’s-eye disease** (presbyopia), regardless of age.
Take **two liáng of cāng zhú (atractylodes)**, pound and sift into a powder. Each dose: **one qián**. At any time, take a fresh **sheep’s liver**, slit open with a bamboo knife, sprinkle the powder inside, bind tightly with hemp string, and boil in **a large bowl of fermented rice water** until done. The patient first inhales the steam, then—once the medicinal vapor has dissipated—ingests the liver. *(From *Jiǎn Yào Jì Zhòng*)* For children’s **crow’s-eye disease**. *(From *Méi Shī Fāng*)* To treat **yellowed, dim vision** where objects are unseen.
Slice **qīng yáng (green sheep’s) liver**, eat with **diluted vinegar**. Boiling it is also effective.

Another prescription: for **eyeballs that suddenly protrude one or two inches**.
Drench the eyes with **freshly drawn water**, changing the water repeatedly, until the eyeballs return on their own.

*(From *Cuī Yuàn Liàng’s Sea-Coast Prescriptions*)* Three names: **Xīguó cǎo (Western Herb)**, **Bìléngqié (Bilva)**, and **fùpénzi (Chinese mulberry)**.
To treat **dim vision**, **cold tears**, **persistent weeping**, **green/blue blindness**, and **epidemic dimness**, take **Xīguó cǎo**, dry it under the sun, pound until thoroughly pulverized, wrap in thin cotton, and soak in **human breast milk** for the duration of an eight- or nine-*lǐ* walk. Apply to the eyes while lying supine—within three or four days, vision will return as in youth. **Avoid alcohol, oil, and wheat flour.**

*(From *Qiān Jīn Fāng*)* To treat **children’s black, cloudy cataracts** with pain and dryness.
Burn **one liáng of bèi chǐ (oyster shell)** into ash, grind into a fine powder, mix with a small amount of **long náo (camphor)**, and apply. This is supremely effective.

Another prescription: for **permanent clear vision**.
Take **one dàn of hú mǎ (sesame seeds)**, steam them thirty times, grind into a powder, and take with wine—**one shāng daily**.

Another prescription: an ancient remedy for **clear vision and black hair**.
Soak **huái zǐ (sophora seeds)** in **ox bile** for **one hundred days** in the shade, then swallow **one seed after meals**. In ten days, the body feels light; in thirty, gray hair turns black; in one hundred, one attains **spiritual penetration**.

*(From *Sūn Zhēn Rén’s Food Taboos*)* To treat **eye cloudiness**.
Take **one dà liáng of máng xiāo (mang Xiao, saline soda)**, place in a copper vessel, and refine over intense heat. Once cooled, sift through fine silk and apply to the **inner eye corners** before sleep each night. This is supremely effective.

*(From *Jīng Yàn Fāng*)* **Bái Lóng Sǎn (White Dragon Powder)** to **dissolve cataracts and restore vision**.
Take **mǎ yá xiāo (tooth coral, calcined)**, wrap in thick paper, press firmly, and carry in the breast pocket against the flesh for **one hundred twenty days**. Remove, grind into a powder, mix with a small amount of **long náo (camphor)**, and refine finely. For those with **long-standing eye films** causing dimness and blurred distance vision—even if the pupil remains unbroken—this will cure them.

Each application uses **two mǐ of the powder**, applied to the eyes.

Another prescription: for **internal and external cataracts**.
Take **four liáng of cāng zhú (atractylodes)**, soak in **rice-wash water for seven days**, changing the water daily, then scrape off the blackened skin, slice finely, and fry with **one liáng of qīng yán (green salt)** until yellow. Remove the salt.

Take **two liáng of mù dì (spikemoss)**, soak in **a child’s urine overnight**, rinse with water, and dry in the sun. Combine and grind into a powder. Take **one qián sháo** daily at any time, mixed into **vegetable dishes**.

*(From *Jīng Yàn Hòu Fāng*)* To treat **dim vision from exhaustion**.
Harvest **màn jīng huā (rocket flower)** in the third month, dry in the shade, and grind into a powder. Take **two qián sháo** with **well-water** on an empty stomach. Long-term use grants **longevity** and allows **nighttime reading**.

*(From *Wài Tái Mì Yào*)* To treat **eye films and protruding flesh**.
Take the **whitest alunite**, place **one grain-sized piece** on the **film or protruding flesh**, and cold tears will flow. Wipe with cotton until the foul discharge is exhausted. The ailment will improve daily, the film will thin, and recovery will follow. **Only the purest alunite may be used.**

Another: **Bǔ Gān Sǎn (Liver-Tonifying Powder)** to treat **thirty-year blindness**.
Collect **jí lí zǐ (spiny cocklebur seeds)** on the **seventh day of the seventh month**, dry in the shade, and pound into a powder. Take **one fāng cùn sháo** after meals with water.

Another: to **cure blindness**.
Take **one pig’s gallbladder**, boil into pill form the size of **glutinous millet grains**, insert into the eyes. After a meal’s time, it is effective.

Another prescription: for **severe cataracts**.
Take the **white skin of a pig’s gallbladder**, dry in the sun, twist into a small cord the thickness of a **hairpin shaft**, burn into ash, and—once cooled—apply the ash directly to the cataract. **Three to five applications** will suffice.

Another prescription: to **lighten the body, tonify qi, and sharpen vision**.
Take **one shēng of wú jīng zǐ (rape seeds)**, boil in **nine shēng of water** until the liquid is exhausted, dry daily for three cycles, then grind into a powder. Take **one fāng cùn sháo** three times daily with water.

*(From *Dòu Mén Fāng*)* To treat **fire-eye (conjunctivitis)**.
Burn **moxa**, cover with a bowl as smoke rises, wait until the smoke condenses into soot on the bowl’s underside, then dissolve the soot in warm water to wash the eyes. This is immediately effective. Adding **huáng lián (coptis)** enhances the result.

*(From *Guǎng Lì Fāng*)* To treat **eye protrusions and protruding flesh**.
Take **seven fresh xìng rén (apricot kernels)**, remove the skins, chew finely, and—while still warm—wrap the saliva on a cotton swab to apply to the protruding flesh. **Four or five applications** will suffice.

*(From *Yào Xìng Lùn*)* It is said: **Rubbing teeth with salt on an empty stomach**, then spitting into water to wash the eyes, allows **nighttime reading of small text**. This is effective.

**On the Blindness of Gu’s Nurturing Sister**
Gu’s sister, who had lost her sight, was once treated by Gu himself. He refused to wear his cap or eat until he obtained a **viper’s gallbladder**—a remedy for her affliction. Though he searched exhaustively, he found none. A boy then presented him with a single *gē* (合) measure of the substance, which proved to be the very gallbladder. As the boy departed, he transformed into a **green crow** (青乌) and vanished. The sister’s vision was immediately restored.

---
**Section 47: Treatments for Sudden Deafness and Related Ailments**

**Bo Ge’s Sudden Deafness**
Take **mouse gallbladder**, instill into the ear—**no more than three drops**—and recovery follows.

Another account states: If one tilts the head outward and exhausts a single gallbladder’s contents, the bile will soon seep from the lower ear. Initially, hearing may worsen, but by midday, it improves.

**Treatment for Thirty-Year Chronic Deafness**
Take **fourteen croton seeds (bādòu)**, pound them, and mix with **half a *liǎng* of goose fat**, melted over fire. Combine until the consistency of small beans, wrap in cotton, and insert into the ear. Replace daily. **Ma Yao** attests: This cures even **thirty-year deafness**.

If sudden wind afflicts the ear, causing a **whooshing sensation (huánghuáng)**, immediately take **seven *shāng* of salt**, steam in a **zèng (steamer)**, and apply the hot salt to the ear. Replace when cooled. This also treats **sudden ear pain** through steaming and moxibustion.

Another remedy: **Scrape the root of *guōluó* (Trichosanthes kirilowii)* until it fits the ear, then boil in **December pig fat** three times. Insert while warm; repeat daily for **twenty-one days** for full recovery.

**Ma Yao’s Treatment for Ear Pain with Discharge**
Toast **apricot kernels (xìngrén)** until black, pound into a paste, wrap in cotton, and insert into the ear. Replace **three times daily**; recovery follows in **three days**.

**For *Lèng ěr* (Ear Pain with Purulent Discharge)**
Blow **moonlit ash** deep into the ear—it will emerge on its own without discomfort.

**For Chronic Deafness (Cháng Lóng)**
**Chángfú root (Acorus gramineus) pill**:
Take **one *cùn* of chángfú root** and **one croton seed (bādòu, skin and core removed)**, pound and sift into **seven pills**. Wrap in cotton, insert before sleep, and replace nightly. **Ten days** restore hearing; **yellow discharge** clears immediately.

**For Ear Discharge with Blood**
Pound **processed aconite (fúzi)** into a powder, mix with **onion juice (cōngtì)**, and drip into the ear. Alternatively, **onion juice alone** may be tilted into the ear.

**For Persistent Ear Ringing**
Slice **raw rehmannia (shēng dìhuáng)**, insert into the ear, and replace **ten times daily**.

**From *Xiǎo Pǐn* (Small Categories): Treatment for *Lèng ěr* with Purulent Discharge**
Burn **two *liǎng* of alum (fánshí)**, mix with **one *liǎng* of coptis (huánglián)** and **one *liǎng* of cuttlefish bone (wūzé yúgǔ)**, forming pills the size of **date pits**. Wrap in cotton and insert into the ear; replace **twice daily**. Adding **dragon bone (lónggǔ)** enhances efficacy.

**Croton Seed Pill for Deafness**
Take **one croton seed (bādòu, core removed)** and **one *bān māo* (Viverra zibetha, wings and paws removed)**, pound and sift into pills. Wrap in cotton and insert into the ear; replace **twice daily**. **Highly verified** when used as prescribed.

Another remedy: Pound **magnetite (císhí)**, **chángfú root**, **throughwort (tōngcǎo)**, **aloeswood (xiūnlùxiāng)**, **apricot kernels**, **smilax (bìmá)**, and **pine resin (sōngzhī)** into a powder. Mix with **wax and goose fat** to form firm pills, pierced with a hairpin. Remove existing ear obstructions, then insert the pill daily. Initially, itching and noise may occur, but **after a month**, full recovery follows. **Tested by a palace official**.

**Sudden Ear Pain**
Steam salt and apply as a poultice.

**For Unbearable Ear Pain, Seeking Death**
Pound **chángfú root and processed aconite (fúzi), each one *fèn***, mix with **black sesame oil (wūmá yóu)**, and drip into the ear—pain ceases instantly.

**For *Lèng ěr* with Purulent Discharge**
Insert **axle grease (chēzhé zhī)** into the ear until discharge exhausts; recovery follows.

**Additional Remedies**
*(From *Zhǒuhòu Fāng*)* **Treatment for Sudden Ear Swelling with Pus**:
Burn **alum (fánshí)** into powder, blow into the ear with a **pen tube** three or four times daily, or wrap in cotton and insert—**immediate recovery**.

*(From *Jīngyàn Fāng*)* **Treatment for "Root Deafness" (Dǐ Ěr)**:
Toast **one *sāngshūāzhé* (mylabris, *Mylabris phalerata*)** over slow fire until **eight parts cooked**, preserving its essence. Grind finely, add **one *zì* of musk (shèxiāng)**, and dust into the ear (**half a *zì* per dose**). If pus is present, first remove it with cotton, then apply the powder.

Another remedy: **For Sudden Deafness**
Wrap **one croton seed (bādòu)** in **December fat**, pierce with a needle to release its essence, then insert into the ear.

*(From *Méi Shī Fāng*)* **Treatment for Chronic Deafness**
Melt **three *liǎng* of pine resin (sōngzhī)**, mix with **one *liǎng* of croton seeds (bādòu)**, pound until malleable, form pills, wrap in thin cotton, and insert into the ear. Replace **daily**.

*(From *Shèng Huì Fāng*)* **Treatment for Deafness Due to Kidney *Qi* Deficiency**
Use **one pair of deer kidneys**, remove fat and membranes, slice, and simmer in **soy sauce (jīngzhī)** with **two *hé* of glutinous rice**, forming a gruel. Season with **the Five Flavors Method (wǔwèi zhī fǎ)**, serve on an empty stomach as both **soup and wine**.

*(From *Dù Rèn Fāng*)* **Treatment for Deafness from Kidney Deficiency (Cured Within Ten Years)**
Take **forty-nine small scorpions** and **forty-nine slices of ginger (size of a *jié*)**, parch in a **copper vessel** until the ginger dries. Grind into powder for **one dose**. Take with **warm wine at night until the second watch (èr gèng)**, drinking **to full intoxication**. The next day, the ear will sound like **panpipes (shēnghuáng)**—**immediate effect**.

*(From *Shèng Jīn Fāng*)* **Instantly Effective Treatment for Deafness**
Soak **dried earthworms (dìlóng)** in **salt**, store in **onion stems**, and use the liquid to drip into the ear.

*(From *Qiān Jīn Fāng*)* **Treatment for Deafness**
Mix **equal parts of realgar (zhōnghuáng) and sulfur (liúhuáng)**, wrap in cotton, and insert into the ear.

Another remedy: Steep **one *shāng* of broken *mùjīngzi* (Vitex negundo)** in **three *shāng* of wine** for seven days, strain, and drink freely. **Thirty-year deafness** is cured.

Another remedy: Simmer **processed aconite (fúzǐ)** in **aged vinegar (chún cù)** over low heat until pointed, then insert into the ear—**effective**.

*(From *Wàitái Mìyào*)* **Treatment for Deafness**
Pound **mustard seeds (jièzi)**, mix with **human breast milk**, wrap in cotton, and insert into the ear—**recovery follows**.

**From *Yáng Shì Chǎn Rǔ Fāng*:**
**Treatment for Chronic Ear Buzzing (Day and Night)**
Burn **aconite (wútóu)** to ash, mix with **calamus (chāngpú)** in equal parts, grind to powder, wrap in cotton, and insert into the ear—use twice daily for effectiveness.

---
**Section 48: Treatments for Insects Entering the Ear**

**Boǎ Shì’s Method for General Insect Infestation**
Pour **good wine** into the ear; the insect will emerge upon movement.

Another method: Hold breath while someone blows through a reed into one ear.

Another method: Stuff **peach leaves** into both ears—the insect will exit immediately.

**For Centipede (Wúgōng) in the Ear**
Wrap **salt ash** in tree leaves, heat, and cover the ear; replace when cooled—the centipede will emerge.

**For Earwig (Shìtíng) in the Ear**
Roast **sesame (húmá)**, store in a **Bohea tea bag (gě náng)**, and use as a pillow—the insect will follow the scent and exit.

**For Ant (Yǐ) in the Ear**
Fry **pork fat (zhūzhī)** with fragrant substances near the ear canal—the ant will emerge.

**Miraculous Method for Earwig (Shìtíng) in the Ear**
Fill the ear with **cow curd (niúnǎi)**, and the earwig will exit, half dissolved. If it enters the abdomen, fast and consume **one to two *shāng* of fine curd**—it will liquefy into yellow water and pass. If not expelled, repeat. This method is infallible and recently obtained.

Another method: Fry a **young chicken** (plucked, feet removed) in oil until golden, pierce holes, and use as a pillow.

Another method: Place **earthworms (dìlóng)** inside **onion stems (cōngyè)**, crush into liquid, and drip into the ear—the earwig will dissolve into water.

**Supplementary Prescriptions**
From *Shèng Jīn Fāng*:
**For Insects Entering the Ear and Refusing to Exit**
Drip **rooster’s comb blood (jīguān xuè)** into the ear—the insect will emerge.

From *Qiān Jīn Fāng*:
Pound **garlic juice (jiǔ zhī)**, pour into the ear—effective.

Another method:
**For Foreign Objects in the Ear That Won’t Exit**
Cut **hemp rope (má shéng)** into frayed strands, coat with **good glue (hǎo jiāo)**, apply to the object in the ear, let dry until adhered, then gently pull it out.

From *Méi Shī Fāng*:
Apply **carnauba wax (chēzhàng zhī)** to the ear canal—the object will exit.

From *Xù Shí Quán Fāng*:
**For Insects Entering the Ear**
Grind **one *qián* of Sichuan pepper (qín jiāo)** in **half a bowl of vinegar**, steep for a long time, then drip sparingly into the ear—the insect will emerge.

From *Wàitái Mìyào* (adapted from *Zhǒuhòu Fāng*):
**For Ants in the Ear**
Burn **carp scales (lǐlǐ jiǎ)**, grind to powder, mix with water, and pour into the ear—the ant will exit.

From *Chuán Xìn Fāng* by **Liú Yǔxī**:
**For Earwigs in the Ear**
Make a **sesame oil cake (máyóu jiān bǐng)**, use as a pillow—the earwig will emerge within moments.

**Li Yúchún’s Account (Formerly River Yang Governor)**
An earwig entered his ear, and no remedy worked. After half a month, his head throbbed with a deep, resonant sound, and he grew dizzy, striking his head against doorposts in agony. He submitted a desperate illness report, but even imperial medicines failed. Desperate, he forgot survival and was about to perish when someone presented this remedy—he recovered.

From *Bīngbù Shǒují*:
**For Earwigs in the Ear**
**Garlic juice (suàn zhī)** dissolves all insects in the ear—universally effective.

From **Qián Xiànggōng’s *Gé Zhōng Fāng***:
**For Earwigs and Ants in the Ear**
Pour **sour vinegar (kǔ cù)** into the ear—they will emerge upon movement.

From *Shèng Huì Fāng*:
**For Moths Flying into the Ear**
Pour **soy sauce (jiàng zhī)** into the ear—the moth will exit.
Alternatively, strike a **copper vessel** beside the ear.

From *Jīngyàn Fāng*:
**For Water in the Ear**
Drip **mint juice (bòhé zhī)** into the ear—immediate effect.

---
**Section 49: Treatments for Sudden Food Impaction (Yē)**

**Boǎ Shì’s Method**
Hold a small amount of **honey (shǎo mì)** in the mouth—it will pass immediately.

Another method:
Collect **old cow saliva (lǎo niú tián)** the size of a **date pit (zǎo hé)**, place in water, and drink—prevents future impaction.

**Supplementary Prescriptions**
From *Wàitái Mìyào*:
**For Impaction (Yē)**
Grind **antelope horn shavings (língyáng jiǎo xiè)** (quantity flexible), swallow with a **square-inch spoonful** of water—effective.
Alternatively, rub the horn directly on the impaction—excellent.

From *Shí Yī Xīn Jìng*:
**For Sudden Food Impaction**
Steep **one *liǎng* of dried tangerine peel (chén pí)** in hot water, remove seeds, dry-fry, grind to powder. Simmer **one large bowl of water**, reduce to half, and drink warm.

From *Shèng Huì Fāng*:
**For Stagnant *Gě* Qi (Blocked Diaphragm), Throat Constriction, and Inability to Swallow**
Pound **fine bran (xì jiāng)** from the **mortar’s upper edge (duì zhuī)**, roll into **honey pills (mì wán)** the size of **gunpowder pellets (dànzi)**, suck between meals, and swallow saliva.

From *Guǎng Wǔ Xíng Jì*:
During the **Yǒngxuē era**, a monk in **Jiàngzhou** suffered chronic impaction. Before dying, he instructed his disciples: *"After my death, open my chest and throat to see what obstructs me."* Upon dissection, they found a creature resembling a fish with two heads and fleshy scales. Placed in a container, it leapt wildly; when fed various flavors, it dissolved entirely. In summer, when **blue-green algae (lán)** formed scum, a monk placed some in a container—this creature circled and dissolved into water within moments.

---
**Section 50: Treatments for Sudden Foreign Object Impaction (Jīng Bù Xià)**

**For Fish Bones Stuck in the Throat**
Press the **fish bone (yú gǔ)** against the **head**—it will pass immediately, emerging with a *clink*.

Another method:
Chew **green onions (xièbái)** until soft, thread onto a string, swallow to the obstruction, then pull—the bone will follow.

**For Bone Impaction**
Take the remaining bone fragment, toss it between **left and right hands** repeatedly over the back—it will exit immediately.

**For General Foreign Object Impaction**
Loosen the **girdle (yīdài)**, peer downward at the obstruction—it will descend if not already expelled.

Another method:
Use a **spoon (cháo)** to scoop **honey (hǎo mì)** gradually into the throat—the obstruction will pass.

**For Fish Bones Stuck in the Throat (Resistant to Other Methods)**
Roll **molasses (fèi táng)** into a pill the size of a **chicken yolk (jī zǐ huáng)**, swallow. If ineffective, roll a larger pill and repeat—eventually effective.

**Supplementary Prescriptions**
From *Dòu Mén Fāng*:
**For Bone Impaction**
Grind **deer horn (lù jiǎo)** to powder, moisten with saliva, and swallow—miraculous.

「From *Wàitái Mìyào*:
**For Foreign Object Impaction (General)**
Take **tiger bone (hǔ gǔ)** as powder, swallow with water in a dose of a **finger-width spoon (fāngcùn cháo)**—effective immediately.

Another method:
Use the **brain of the mole cricket (zhōugū nǎo)**—swallow, and it will also treat impaled objects that refuse to emerge. Apply the brain externally, and the impaled object will emerge.

Another method:
Recite the word **"cormorant (lúndí)" aloud**, and the obstruction will descend.

From *Gǔjīn Lùyàn*:
**For Fish Bones Lodged Horizontally in the Throat**
Take **carp fish scales (lǐ yú línpí)**, fold and burn into ashes, swallow with water—it will emerge. If not expelled, take another dose.

From *Shèngjīn Fāng*:
**For All Cases of Bone or Bamboo/Wooden Splinter Impaction (Children and Adults)**
In the twelfth month (December), take the **mandarin fish bile (guìyú dǎn)**, suspend it beneath the **northern eave (běi yán)**, and let it dry. For each case of impaction, take a portion the size of a **walnut (zǎozǐ)**, decoct with wine until dissolved, sip warmly. If regurgitation occurs, spit it out—**the obstruction will then exit with the phlegm (wán xiàn)**. If regurgitation does not occur, consume more warm wine until it does. The wine dosage should be adjusted according to the individual’s constitution and strength. If the obstruction remains, decoct another piece—**no case will fail**. This remedy is particularly effective for lodged objects that have remained in the **viscera (zàngfǔ)** for a long time, causing severe pain, yellowing of the skin, and emaciation.

If mandarin fish bile cannot be obtained, **crucian carp bile (lǐyú dǎn)**, **squid bile (yòuyú dǎn)**, or **roach bile (jiéyú dǎn)** may be used instead. Collect them in the twelfth month—**this is optimal**.

**Maó Shì’s Prescription (for Sudden Impaction)**
Take **three parts apricot kernel (xìngrén, *Prunus armeniaca*)**, remove the skin and tip, roast until soft, then pound separately. Add **one part cassia bark (guì)**, mix into a paste. Wrap a **plum pit (lǐ hé)** in cotton, hold it in the mouth, and swallow the paste slowly—**five times daily and three times at night**.

**For Accidental Ingestion of Various Objects (Chapter Fifty)**
**Bo’s Prescription (for Swallowed Hairpins)**
Take **dried chives (*Allium tuberosum*)**, let them wilt, then boil until soft without cutting. Consume a large bundle—**the hairpin will emerge with the stool**.

**For Swallowed Nails, Arrows, Needles, or Iron Coins**
Consume copious amounts of **mutton fat (féiyáng zhī)** and **various fatty meats (zhūbān zhīróu)**—they will envelop the object, ensuring its expulsion.

**For Swallowed Beads Lodged as an Iron Obstruction**
Burn **crossbow copper (nǔ tóng)** until red, immerse in water, and drink the liquid—**immediate cure**.

**For Swallowed Coins**
Burn **charcoal (huǒtàn)** into powder, swallow a dose of a **finger-width spoon (fāngcùn cháo)**—the coin will emerge.

**From *Xiǎopǐn Fāng* (same as above).**

Another method:
Take **three sheng (升) of honey (mì)**, swallow—**the coin will emerge**.

**Yáo’s Prescription (for Hair Lodged in the Throat)**
Take **hair from a comb (shū tóu fà)**, burn into ashes, swallow a dose of **one qián (钱) spoon (cháo)** with water.

**For Swallowed Rings or Strongly Lodged Beads**
Burn **several goose feathers (é yǔ)**, grind into powder, and drink—**effective**.

**For Swallowed Coins (Alternative Method)**
Take **December rice molasses (làyuè mǐtáng)**, swallow half a sheng at once—**effective**.
Another method:
Decoct **strongly concentrated mugwort juice (nóng jiāng ài zhī)**, swallow—**effective**.

**From *Shènghuì Fāng* (Supplementary Prescriptions):**
**For Swallowed Silver Rings or Hairpins**
Take **half a liǎng (两) of mercury (shuǐyín)**, swallow. Repeat once more—**the objects will emerge**.

**For Children Who Swallow Needles**
Use a **magnetite stone (císhí)** the size of a **date pit (zǎo hé)**, polish until smooth, drill a hole, thread with silk, and have the child hold it in the mouth—**the needle will emerge by itself**.

**For Children Who Swallow Copper or Iron Objects Lodged in the Throat**
Take **root of the southern wax plant (*Styrax tonkinensis*) (nántóu gēn)**, burn, and finely grind. Mix with warm water to a dose of **one qián (钱) spoon (cháo)**, swallow—**effective**.

**From Tiěxiànggōng’s *Qièzhōng Fāng* (Prescriptions from a Case):**
**For Swallowed Coins**
Take a **magnetite stone (císhí)** the size of a **walnut (zǎozǐ)**, have the patient hold it in the mouth—**the coin will emerge immediately**.

Another method:
Take **one handful of mugwort (*Artemisia vulgaris*) and chaste tree (*Vitex negundo*) (àihāo)**, finely chop, decoct with **five sheng (升) of water**, reduce to **one sheng (升)**, swallow at once—**the obstruction will descend**.

**From *Wàitái Mìyào* (again):**
Take **one jīn (斤) of molasses (fèi táng)**, swallow gradually—**the ring or hairpin will emerge**.

**From *Yángshì Chǎnrǔ* (Yáng’s Prescriptions for Lactation):**
**For Ear Obstruction**
Take **one handful of ear head (ér tóu)**, steep in **one sheng (升) of water**, sip the water **ten or more times**—**cure achieved**.

**From *Sūn Yònghé Fāng* (Prescriptions of Sūn):**
**For Swallowed Gold or Silver, or Coins Lodged in the Abdomen**
Take **lime (shíhuī)** the size of an **apricot pit (xìng hé)**, and **sulfur (liúhuáng)** the size of a **walnut (zǎozǐ)**. Grind together into powder, mix with wine, and swallow—**regardless of timing**.

**Yáo’s Prescription (for Hair Lodged in the Throat)**
Take **hair from one’s own head (jǐ tóu luàn fà)**, burn into ashes, swallow a dose of **one qián (钱) spoon (cháo)** with water.

**From Chén Cángqì’s Notes:**
**For Impaction of Bamboo or Wooden Splinters (Unable to Pass)**
Burn **sawdust (gǔjīn)** until red, steep in wine, and drink while hot—**both methods ensure expulsion**.

**For Facial Sores and Baldness (Chapter Twelve)**
**Bo’s Prescription (for Young Men with Excess Qi and Facial Sores)**
Mix **yellow ochre (húfěn)**, **mercury (shuǐyín)**, and **December pig fat (làyuè zhū zhī)** into a paste. Let the mercury fully disperse, then apply the paste to the face **just before dusk (xiàngmíng)**. Wipe it off in the morning **without washing with water**. Repeat before dusk again—**three applications will cure**.

**Yáo’s Prescription (same as above).**

Another method:
Apply **muntjac deer fat (mí zhī)**—**effective**.

Another method:
Take **three-year-old vinegar (sǎnsuì jiǔ)**, steep **three nights in chicken eggs (jīzǐ)**. Remove the softened egg whites and apply to the sores—**effective**.

**From *Yǐnjū Xiàofāng* (Prescriptions of the Recluse):**
**For Facial Sores**
Grind **turmeric (huánglián)** and **oyster shell (mǔlì)**—**two liǎng (两) each**—through a sieve, mix with water to form a paste, and seal over the sores. Apply a **concentrated decoction (nóngzhī)** as powder—**divinely verified**.

**Winter Malva Powder (Dōngkuí Sǎn)**
Take **winter malva seed (dōngkuí zǐ)**, **cypress seed (bǎizǐ rén)**, **slimy spleen (xiálí)**, and **bottle gourd peel (guābiàn)**—**one liǎng (两) each**. Make into a powder, swallow a **finger-width spoon (fāngcùn cháo)** after meals, **three times daily**, with wine—**effective**.

**For Facial and Nasal Sores (Alcohol-Based Prescription)**
Mix **equal parts pearl (zhēnzhū)**, **yellow ochre (húfěn)**, and **mercury (shuǐyín)**, apply with **pig fat (zhū zhī)**—**effective**.

Another method:
Mix **cormorant excrement (lúndí shǐ)** with **December pig fat (làyuè zhū zhī)** and apply—**also highly effective**.

**For Excessive Facial Scarring or Sores Resembling Sparrow Eggs in Color**
Take **three-year-old vinegar (sǎnsuì jiǔ)**, decoct with **turmeric (*Curcuma longa*) (shù)**, and **constantly wipe the face** with it—**the scars will gradually vanish**.

Another method:
Take **one fresh chicken egg (xīnshēng jīzǐ)**, pierce and remove the yolk, fill with **one liǎng (两) of cinnabar (dānshā)**, and seal with lacquer. **A separate prescription states:** Stuff the egg with **goose down (é rǔ)**, let a **rooster brood (bùzhū)** upon it, then remove and apply the contents to the face—**the sores will vanish and the skin turn white immediately**.

**Alternative Prescription (from Western Queen Mother’s Pillow):**
**For Facial Sores (Prescription Used by Empress Zāng Guìzhuàng of the Chén Dynasty)**
Take **one chicken egg (jīzǐ)**, crush **two liǎng (两) of red cinnabar (dānshā)** into powder, mix with the egg, and let a **rooster brood (bùzhū)** beneath it—**the rest follows the same method**.」

「Yet another method:
To make the face skin swift and smooth while imparting a red hue, crush **cinnabar (dānshā)** into powder and apply it to the face no more than five times—**the face will become as white as jade, luminous and supple, a most excellent result**. **For those with lingering sores after illness**, apply the powder like **rice flour (mǐfěn)**.

**For refining the skin with alum (fángshí):**
Boil **alum (fángshí)**, mix with wine, and apply—**Maopu (姚) claims it works within three applications**.

**Another prescription:**
Take **white arum (báixiān) two liǎng (分)**, **apricot kernel (xìngrén) half a liǎng (分)**, and **chicken dung (jīshǐ) one liǎng (分)**, pound into a paste, mix with **honey (mì)**, and apply with water to the face—**this is effective**.

**Prescription for treating facial and scalp eruptions (lièyáng):**
Pound **realgar (xiónghuáng)**, **sulfur (liúhuáng)**, and **alum (fángshí)** into powder, mix with **boar fat (zhūzhī)**, and apply—**a proven method**.

**Another prescription:**
