Apply **juice from fresh tree bark (shēngshù kǒngzhōng zǐ zhī)** to the affliction, then crush **cinnamon (guì)**, mix and apply—**do this twice or thrice daily**.

**Another prescription:**
Use **snake shed skin (shé tuì)**, roast and grind it repeatedly until heated, then discard the herb and apply the residue—**do not expose it to the wind**.

**For treating dark, coarse, and thickened facial skin:**
Pound **ram’s leg bone (yáng tǐ)** into fine powder, mix with **egg white (jīzǐbái)**, and apply to the face. Once dry, wash with **white glutinous rice gruel (báiliáng mǐ guāng zhī)**. **Within three days, the skin becomes pure white—**a miraculous effect**.

**Another prescription:**
Take **turnip seed (wújīng zǐ) two liǎng (两)**, **apricot kernel (xìngrén) one liǎng (两)**, pound them together. Remove the seeds from **purslane (qiànlì)**, place **five pig pancreas (zhūyín)** in a pouch, and mix with **undiluted wine (chúnjiǔ)**. Apply at night—**this is used in cold months as a hand and face ointment**. **An alternative states:** It benefits the elderly by reducing spots and whitens dark skin. **If added with one liǎng (两) of **Chinese yam (tǔguā gēn)** and **seven jujubes (dàzǎo)**, the skin will gradually brighten—**Maopu’s method (姚方)**, highly verified.

**From *Hidden Residence’s Verified Prescriptions (Yǐnjū Xiàoyàn Fāng)*:**
**Prescription for removing dark facial pigmentation (yīn):**
Pound **cuttlefish bone (wūzé yú gǔ)**, **Asarum (xìsīn)**, **dried squill (kūróng)**, **dried ginger (gānjiāng)**, and **pepper (jiāo)** each into two liǎng (两). Cut the five ingredients, soak in **bitter wine (kǔjiǔ)** for three days, then boil with **refined beef marrow (chéngliàn niúsuǐ) four jīn (斤)** until the wine’s aroma dissipates—**the medicine is ready**. Apply the powder to the face—**this is a divine and wondrous prescription for unsightly skin**.

**Another prescription for attaining jade-like whiteness:**
Take **mutton fat (yángzhī) one shēng (升)**, **dog fat (gǒuzhī) one shēng (升)**, **white cockscomb (báizhǐ) half a shēng (升)**, **licorice (gāncǎo) seven chǐ (尺)**, **Pinellia (bànxià) half a liǎng (两)**, **Chinese yam (shānyào) one liǎng (两)**, and **Angelica (dāngguī) one liǎng (两)**. Also, **white arum (báixiān) and **white cockscomb (báizhǐ)** each one liǎng (两), **Akebia stem (kuòróng) one liǎng (分)**, and **woodland magnolia bark (mùlán pí) one liǎng (分)**. Boil **refined boar fat (chéngliàn zhūzhī) two shēng (升)** with the eleven ingredients wrapped in cloth, using a small amount of wine to soak overnight. Then, simmer the mixture seven times, each time removing and re-adding a piece of **white cockscomb (báizhǐ)** until it turns yellow—**the medicine is complete**. Strain, squeeze, and apply the juice to the face—**this is a prescription worth more than a thousand gold pieces**. This ointment also treats **golden sores (jīnchuāng)** and **hemoptysis (tǔxuè)**.

**For making the face skin thin and delicate like flower petals:**
Take the **pure white tip of deer antler (lùjiǎo jiān)**, grind it on a flat stone until thick. Mix with **dried ginger (gānjiāng) two liǎng (两)**, pound into a fine powder, and sift through **silk gauze (mìjuàn)**. Combine with deer antler juice, stir until smooth. Before applying, wash the face with warm water at night, pat dry with soft cloth, then coat with **white honey (báimì)** and rub until the hands no longer stick—**this indicates completion**. Apply the medicine, and at dawn, wash again with warm water. **After twenty to seventy days, the complexion will astonish all**. **Do not expose the treated face to wind or sun—**be cautious.

**For sudden dark patches appearing on the face:**
Pound **fresh apricot kernels (shēngxìngrén)**, remove the skin, and mix with **egg white (jīzǐbái)** into a paste like **pan-fried dumplings (jiān bǐng miàn)**. Apply at night after washing the face, dry, and apply. Wash with water in the morning—**the condition will heal immediately**. **Maopu’s method (姚方) states:** The patches will disappear after one night.

**For treating dark facial pigmentation (lièyáng) and restoring smooth, supple skin:**
Pound **Chinese yam (tǔguā gēn)** and sift it. Mix with water into a smooth paste. Wash the face with water at night, apply the medicine, and wash again in the morning. **After a hundred days, the radiance will dazzle all, and even spouses will fail to recognize each other**.

**Bo’s (葛氏) prescription for attaining whiteness through ingestion:**
Take **three trees’ worth of peach blossoms (táohuā)**, dry in shade, and pound into powder. Take **one cùn (寸)** of the powder before meals, three times daily—**Maopu states:** It also slims the waist**.

**Another prescription:**
Take **white gourd seed (báiguā zǐ) kernel (zhōngrén) five liǎng (分)**, **white poplar bark (báiyáng pí) two liǎng (分)**, and **peach blossom (táohuā) four liǎng (分)**, pound into powder. Take **one cùn (寸)** of the powder after meals, three times daily. **For further whitening, add white gourd seed**. **For a rosy hue, add peach blossom**. **In thirty days, the face becomes white; in fifty days, hands and feet are all white**. **Another version omits poplar bark and includes three liǎng (分) of tangerine peel (jú pí)**.

**Another prescription:**
Take **Chinese yam (rú yuán) three liǎng (分)** and **lead cinnabar (qiāndān) one liǎng (分)**, pound into powder. Take **one knife-cut (yī dāo guī)** of the powder with **vinegar gruel (cù jiāng)** before meals, three times daily. **After ten days, the stool turns black; on the eighteenth or nineteenth day, it appears like lacquer (qī)**. **By the twenty-first day, the body becomes entirely white—**then discontinue. **Beyond this point, excessive whiteness is difficult to cure, especially for those over thirty**. **Avoid consuming the five pungent spices (wǔxīn) while taking this medicine**.

**Another prescription:**
Take **cinnabar (Jūdān) five liǎng (两)** and **peach blossom (táohuā) three liǎng (两)**, pound into powder. Take **one cùn (寸)** of the powder with **morning well water (jǐng zhāo shuǐ)** before meals, three times daily. **After ten days, one will know the effect; after twenty days, the skin becomes overly white, and black urine will be expelled**.

**Another prescription for whitening the face like jade:**
Take **white pine resin (báisōng zhī) ten liǎng (分)**, **dried Rehmannia (chán dìhuáng) nine liǎng (分)**, and **dried lacquer (gān qī) five liǎng (分)**, roast them. Take **processed Aconite (fāo fúzi) one liǎng (分)** and **cinnamon bark (guìxīn) two liǎng (分)**, pound into a paste, sift, and form into **honey pills (mì wán)**. Take **ten pills (shí wán)**, three times daily—**all parasites will be expelled, and the body will become plump and white**.

**Further Prescriptions:**

**Another prescription for whitening the face:**
Dried ginger, cinnamon bark, and licorice root—equal parts—ground into powder. Take one fresh chicken egg, place it in a *shēng* of wine, stir and warm, then ingest with a square-inch spoonful of the powder. After ten days, one will know the effect; after a month, the complexion will be white and luminous.

**Another prescription for removing blackness:**
Sheep gallbladder, pig pancreas, and *xiànxīn* (細辛) in equal parts, decocted three times to boiling. Apply to the face and swallow the liquid. Wash with vinegar water in the morning.

**Another prescription:**
Poria and white stone resin in equal parts, mixed with honey and applied to the face, three times daily. Take one type of medicine, and in a month, the face will become plump and white.

**Prescription for yellow soybeans:**
Parboil yellow soybeans until they resemble fermented bean paste, then extract one *dàshēng* of pure yellow residue. Grind and sift, mix with refined lard until fully cooked, form into pills. Ingest twenty pills with wine, twice daily, gradually increasing to thirty or forty. After consuming five *shēng*, within a month, one’s appetite will greatly improve, and the body will become plump and white. This method has been tested.

**Prescription for regrowing mustache and beard:**
**For baldness or stunted growth:**
Three *shēng* of hemp seeds, two *hé* of Sichuan pepper, soaked in lees overnight, strained, and used as a daily wash. After a month, growth will extend two *chǐ*.

**Another prescription:**
Three parts *mànjīngzi* (蔓荆子), two pieces of processed aconite, seven *shēng* of wine, boiled together, sealed in a vessel for forty-nine days, then used as a wash. After ten days, growth will extend one *chǐ*. Do not apply near the face, lest hair grow there.

**Another prescription:**
Three to four *shēng* of *sāngbáipí* (桑白皮), chopped, soaked in water and boiled five or six times, strained, and used to wash the mustache and beard repeatedly. It will then stop falling out.

**Another prescription:**
Three *shēng* of hemp seeds, one handful of white *tóngyè* (桐叶), boiled in lees five or six times, strained, and used as a wash. Repeated application will promote growth.

**Another prescription:**
A three-*chǐ* long *dōngxíngsāng* (东行桑) root, steamed over rice in a *dèng* (甑), with the juice from both ends collected and applied to the mustache and beard. It will cure immediately.

**Prescription for yellowing mustache and beard:**
Burn *wútóng* (梧桐) wood into ash, mix with milk, and apply to the skin and mustache and beard. Excellent.

**Prescription for dyeing hair black from white:**
Boil soybeans in vinegar water, then coat the hair. It will turn as black as lacquer.

**Another prescription:**
First, wash the hair until cold. Mix equal parts quicklime and *húfěn* (胡粉) with water, warm, and apply before bed, wrapping with an oil cloth. Wash off the next morning—it will turn black, and the result is excellent.

**Prescription for removing white hair and regrowing black hair:**
Pluck out the white hair. Apply pure honey to the follicles—black hair will grow. If eyebrows lack hair, prick them with a needle to cause slight injury, then apply honey—hair will grow. I have also seen people collect stones from water, grind them into *dīngxiāng* (丁香) juice, pluck the hair, and immediately apply the juice to the follicles—black hair will grow. This method is highly effective.

**For dandruff caused by wind:**
Refer to the *Fēngtiáo Zhōng Fāng* (风条中方) and *Zhīzé Fāng* (脂泽等方) at the end of this section.

**Maoyao’s Prescription for [unclear condition]:**
Mix honey with poria and apply for seven days—it will cure.

**Prescription for facial acne from *húfěn*:**
Pound fresh *túsī* (菟丝子) to extract juice and apply. No more than three to five applications will suffice.

**Prescription for blackening the face:**
Goat gallbladder and cow gallbladder, three *shēng* of pure wine, decocted three times to boiling. Apply to the face—excellent.

**Prescription for facial sores:**
Three *liǎng* each of *huánglián* (黄连), *huángbài* (黄檗), and *húfěn*, sifted and applied as powder to the sores. All prescriptions for sores are listed in their respective sections—use as needed.

**Ge’s Prescription for Body and Axillary Foxy Odor:**
On the first day of the month, wash the armpits with urine—odor will disappear. Maoyao attests to its great efficacy.

**Another prescription:**
Burn high-quality *fánshí* (矾石) into powder, store in silk, and frequently apply as powder to the armpits.

**Another prescription:**
Burn *mǎchǐfán* (马齿矾) until all liquid is gone, then apply as powder—it will cure.

**Another prescription:**
Two *liǎng* of *qīngmùxiāng* (青木香), one *liǎng* each of processed aconite and quicklime, ground into fine powder, applied to the armpits. When liquid exudes, reapply as powder.

**Maoyao’s Prescription:**
Half a *liǎng* of *fánshí*, burned.

**Another prescription:**
Wipe the armpits with freshly cooked rice balls while still warm to remove odor. Also feed the rice to a dog. Repeat every seven days—it will cure.

**Another prescription:**
Boil two eggs until fully cooked, remove shells, place one in each armpit, discard after cooling. Do not look back three times. Repeat three times—excellent.

**Maoyao’s Prescription:**
Mix cow tallow, *húfěn*, and pepper, apply to the armpits. It will cure in one night. Repeat two or three times for permanent relief.

**Prescription for odor in armpits, palms, soles, and inner thighs:**
Half a *liǎng* each of dried *gǒuqǐ* (枸杞) root, *gānchù* (干畜) root, and licorice; one *liǎng* each of *gānzhānglù* (干章陆), *húfěn*, and talc. Mix the six ingredients with sour wine and apply to the armpits. When liquid exudes, change clothes and reapply. No more than three applications will suffice. If odor recurs, reapply—but do not overuse, as it may harm the skin. Also apply to other affected areas.

**For persistent moisture and odor in inner thighs and groin, or if sores develop:**
Apply one part *húfěn* as powder—it will cure. A consistently effective method.

**Hidden Dwelling’s Effective Prescription for Foxy Odor:**
Two *liǎng* each of *jīshé* (鸡舌), *huòxiāng* (藿香), *qīngmùxiāng*, and *húfěn*, made into a powder. Apply to the armpits, wrapped in cotton. Repeat as needed—it will cure.

**Prescription for making the body fragrant:**
Equal parts *báizhí* (白芷), *xiūncǎo* (熏草), *dúruò* (杜若), *dúhuáng* (杜蘅), and *gǎoběn* (稿本), formed into honey pills. Take three pills in the morning and four in the evening. After twenty days, the soles will emit fragrance—highly effective.

**Another prescription:**
Two *fèn* each of *guāzǐ* (瓜子), *xiōngwú* (芎藭), *gǎoběn*, *dāngguī* (当归), *dúhuáng*, and *xiànxīn*; five *fèn* each of *báizhí* and cinnamon bark. Grind and sift, take a square-inch spoonful after meals, three times daily. After five days, the breath will be fragrant; after ten days, the body will emit scent—truly divine.

**From *The Minor Recipes* of *Xiaopin*:**

**Recipe for Clarity and Memory:**
Equal parts licorice root, pine tree root and bark, jujubes, and sweet melon seeds, ground into powder. Take a square-inch spoonful three times daily. After twenty days, effects will manifest; after fifty days, the body will emit fragrance; after a hundred days, even clothing and bedding will scent divine. —*Yao Tong’s method.*

**Treatment for a Clouded Mind and Forgetfulness:**
On the seventh day of the seventh month, take a spider’s web and place it secretly at the collar, without others knowing—this will ensure lasting memory. —*Yao Tong’s method.*

**Another Recipe:**
On a *Dingyou* day (丁酉), secretly purchase *wánzhì* (远志) at the market, tuck it into a cloth corner, and grind it into powder to ingest—without others knowing. —*Yao Tong’s method.*

**Another Recipe:**
On a *Bingwu* day (丙午), attach a tortoiseshell fragment to one’s belt—effective.

**Another Recipe:**
Dry and powder the hearts of oxen, horses, pigs, and chickens. Take with wine in a square-inch spoonful three times daily—ask one question, know ten answers.

**Confucius’ Divine Wisdom Pillow Recipe** (already recorded in Volume Nine)—*Yao Tong’s method.*

**Another Recipe for Memory:**
Five *fèn* each of *fúlíng* (茯苓), *fúshén* (茯神), and ginseng; seven *fèn* of *wánzhì*; two *fèn* of *chángpú* (菖蒲), ground into powder. Take a square-inch spoonful three times daily and once at night.

**Recipe for Dream Revelation:**
Dry *zhānglùhuā* (章陆花) for a hundred days, grind into powder, and take with water in a square-inch spoonful before bed while meditating on what you wish to know—you will awaken with clarity in your dreams.

**Recipe for Precognitive Dreams:**
Half a *jīn* of *shàngdāng rénshēn* (上党人参) and one *shēng* of *mábó* (麻勃), combined and pounded, then steamed until the *qi* permeates fully. Take one *dāoguī* (刀圭) before bed to dream of future events.

**Treatment for Excessive Sleepiness:**
Burn *mǎtóugǔ* (马头骨) into ash, grind, and take a square-inch spoonful three times daily and once at night.

**Another Recipe:**
Burn a *fùshǔmù* (父鼠目) into crumbs, mix with fish oil, and apply to the outer corner of the eye—this will prevent sleep. Additionally, wrap the two inner eyelids in red silk and wear as a pendant.

**Another Recipe:**
Five *fèn* each of *máhuáng* (麻黄) and *zhú* (术); three *fèn* of licorice root. Pound into powder at noon while facing south, taking a square-inch spoonful three times daily. —*Yao Tong’s method for memory.*

**Recipe for Swift Memory:**
Three *fèn* of *chángpú*; five *fèn* each of *fúlíng*, *fúshén*, and ginseng; seven *fèn* of *wánzhì*, ground into powder. Take a square-inch spoonful three times daily and once at night—effects will appear in five days. Truly divine.

**Recipe for Lustrous Hair (Làzé Prescription):**
One *fèn* each of *qīngmùxiāng* (青木香), *báizhí* (白芷), *línglíngxiāng* (零陵香), *gānsōngxiāng* (甘松香), and *zélán* (泽兰). Wrap in cotton, steep in wine for two nights, then simmer in oil for two more. Add *làzé* (腊泽) to adjust consistency, then rapidly boil, sprinkle lightly with *húfěn* (胡粉) and *yānhúzhī* (烟脂), simmer gently until nearly dry, strain, and apply as a pomade to hair—divinely effective.

**Recipe for Fragrant Hair Oil:**
Follow the *làzé* method, steeping in oil and simmering, then apply directly to hair or wrap in cotton before boiling.

**Method for Hand Cream:**
One set of pig pancreas; one *liǎng* each of *báizhí* and crushed *táorén* (桃人); two *fèn* each of *xīnyí* (辛夷) and *dōngguārén* (冬瓜人); half a *fèn* of *xìnsīn* (细辛); three *fèn* each of *huángguā* (黄瓜) and *guāluórén* (栝篓人). Simmer in one *dàshēng* (大升) of oil with *báizhí* et al. until two or three boils, strain, knead the pancreas thoroughly, then mix in *dōngguā* and *táorén* powders. Apply to palms for radiance.

**Recipe for *Huádòu Xiāngcǎo* (华豆香藻):**
One *shēng* of *huádòu* (华豆); two *liǎng* each of *bái fú* (白附), *xiōngwú* (芎藭), *bái sháo* (白芍药), *shuǐ guāluó* (水栝篓), *dānglù* (当陆), *táorén*, and *dōngguārén*. Pound and sift, mix, and apply as powder after washing the face and hands.

**Six-Flavor Clothing Perfume:**
One piece of *chénxiāng* (沉香); one *liǎng* each of *shèxiāng* (麝香) and *sūhéxiāng* (苏合香); honey-coated and gently roasted over low fire until slightly discolored; one *liǎng* of *bái jiāoxiāng* (白胶香), pounded until *chénxiāng* breaks into pea-sized pieces; one *liǎng* of *dīngxiāng* (丁香), also pounded into three segments. Mix remaining aromatics with honey to form incense sticks. Burn to perfume clothing—use half a *liǎng* per application. Alternatively, add one *liǎng* of *huòxiāng* (藿香) for enhanced effect.

—*Ge Shi’s* methods already include ointments for facial application and hair dyeing, thus omitting redundant *zhīzé* (脂泽) techniques here, as they serve ornamental purposes.

**Recipe for Hair Regrowth:**
Three *fèn* of *mànjīngzǐ* (蔓荆子); two whole *fúzi* (附子, fresh). Pound both with seven *shēng* of wine, seal in a ceramic vessel for forty-nine days until the medicine is complete. First, wash hair and beard with lime water, dry thoroughly, and apply *wūjīzhī* (乌鸡脂) three times daily for seven days. Then apply the medicine three or four times daily. After forty days, hair will grow one *chǐ* (尺)—do not apply elsewhere.

**Additional Recipes from *Zhǒuhòu Fāng*:**
—*Yao Shi’s* treatment for [unclear condition] (□):
Grind *fúlíng* into powder, mix with white honey, and apply for seven days—cure achieved.

**Recipe for Mottled Skin (Resembling Quail Eggs):**
Boil one *jīyángdǎn* (羖羊胆) in two *shēng* of wine until three boils, then apply daily—three treatments will improve.

**From *Qiān Jīn Fāng*: Treatment for Blood-Stained, Wrinkled Skin:**
Mash *mànjīngzǐ* (蔓菁子) into a paste, mix into regular facial cream—effective.

**From *Cuī Yuànliàng’s Sea Shore Prescriptions*: *Mièbān Gāo* (灭瘢膏) for Scar Removal:**
Eight *fèn* each of roasted *huángfánshí* (黄矾石, until juice flows) and fried *húfěn* (until yellow). Grind finely, mix with December pig fat, and re-grind into a paste. First, scrub the area with raw cloth until tender, then apply the ointment five times.

**Alternative Scar Removal:**
Equal parts *yīngshǐbái* (鹰屎白) and ash from *yànkē zhōngcǎo* (燕窠中草), mixed with human breast milk and applied—scars will vanish, leaving skin smooth as before.

**Recipe for Facial Dark Spots:**
Remove the kernel from a *lǐhé* (李核), peel, and grind finely. Mix with egg white into a thin paste, apply, and rinse with diluted vinegar before bed. Later, dust with *húfěn*—within five or six days, results will be divine.

**On Cautions Against Wind and Skin Blemishes**

From *Sun Zhēnrén’s Food Taboos*: **Removing Dark Spots**
Take quicklime, heat it over charcoal until hot, then place glutinous rice atop the lime. Once the rice melts, use it to dab the affected area.

From *Wàitái Mìyào*: **Emergency Treatment for Black Spots**
At night, wash the face with warm rice-water, then scrub the dark spots with cloth until they turn red and tender. Grind *báitiánxiāng* (white sandalwood) into a paste, apply the concentrated juice, and in the morning, wash the face again with rice-water. Then, dust the spots with *yīngfèn* (eagle dung) powder.

**To Make the Face Glow**
Use *mìtuó sēng* (a medicinal fungus) boiled in milk, then apply it to the face—excellent results.

**Also Treats Nasal and Facial Sores**
From *Shènghuì Fāng*: **Removing Skin Blemishes**
Take two *liǎng* of *mìtuó sēng*, grind finely, and mix with breast milk to apply nightly.

**Alternative for Black Moles on Face or Body**
Take five *liǎng* of *lìlú* (blue lily) ash and one large bowl of water, straining the ash juice into a copper vessel. Boil with strong broth until it thickens like black paste. Prick the mole with a needle and apply the paste—cure achieved in no more than three applications.

**To Regrow Eyebrows**
Use *wūmá huā* (black sesame flowers) dried in shade, ground into powder, and soaked in black sesame oil. Apply nightly.

From *Qiānjīn Yì*: **For Aging Faces to Regain Luster**
Take one whole pig’s trotter, clean and prepare as for eating, then boil into a gelatinous broth. Apply at night, wash with rice-water in the morning—skin tightens.

From *Tánshì Xiǎo’ér Fāng*: **Healing Bean Sores and Facial Scars**
Grind *mìtuó sēng* finely, mix with water, apply at night, and wash off in the morning—skin restores smoothly.

**Three Remedies for Wind-Related Sores (detailed in the Wind section).**

From *Qiānjīn Fāng*: **Treating All Armpit Odor**
Apply *fúlóng gān* (a medicinal herb) as a paste—immediate cure.

From *Wàitái Mìyào*: **Treating Fox Odor, or Persistent Dampness and Sores in Groin/Genitals**
Soak *qīngmùxiāng* (green wood aromatic) in good vinegar, then apply to the armpits—cure achieved.

**Alternative for Fox Odor**
Mix aged vinegar with quicklime and apply.

From *Jīngyàn Fāng*: **Effective Treatment for Fox Odor**
Rub fresh ginger on the armpits—eliminates the root cause.

**Comprehensive Remedy for:**
- Regrowing beard and eyebrows
- Preserving youthful complexion
- Strengthening sinews and bones
- Sharpening hearing and vision
- Dispelling wind
- Moisturizing skin
*(Long-term use makes one light and agile.)*

Take *cāngshù* (Atractylodes) in any quantity, soak in rice-water for three days, changing water daily. On the fourth day, scrape off the blackened skin, slice thinly, dry in the sun, then roast over slow fire until golden. Grind into powder. For every *jīn* of powder, mix with half a *jīn* of steamed *fúlíng* (Poria) and honey into pills the size of *wútóng* seeds. Take fifteen pills with warm water on an empty stomach and before meals. Additionally, mix six *liǎng* of *cāngshù* powder with one *liǎng* of *gāncǎo* (licorice) powder, brew as tea, and take with the pills—miraculous.

**Avoid:** Peaches, plums, sparrows, clams, and all "three whites."

From *Qiānjīn Fāng*: **Treating Hair Loss and Promoting Growth**
Roast one *shèng* of *mázǐ* (hemp seeds) until black, press out the oil, and apply to the scalp—hair grows long.

**Alternative for Hair Loss**
Use *yángshǐ huī* (sheep dung ash), strain the juice, and wash the scalp every three days—no more than ten washes needed.

**For Falling Eyebrows and Beard**
Take three *shèng* of quicklime, mix evenly with water, and parch over flame until charred. Store in silk, soak in one *dǒu* of strong wine for fourteen days in winter, seven days in spring/autumn. Take one *hé* daily, ensuring continuous wine vapor exposure. After a hundred days, new beard grows and does not fall again.

From *Sun Zhēnrén’s Food Taboos*: **Hair Growth Remedy**
Dry *cèbǎi yè* (Chinese juniper leaves) into powder, mix with oil, and apply.

**For Black, Lustrous Hair**
Boil black soybeans in vinegar, remove the beans, and reduce the liquid to a thick paste. Apply to hair.

**For Baldness**
Grind *wújīng zǐ* (charred rape seeds) into powder, mix with wine, and apply three times daily.

From *Méi Shī Fāng*: **Treating Premature Gray Hair and Removing White Hair**
Apply honey to hair follicles—new black hair grows.

For hair loss, crush *wútóng zǐ* (Chinese parasol seeds) into juice and apply—black hair regenerates.

From *Qiānjīn Yì*: **Treating Yellow Hair**
Apply *xióngzhī* (bear fat) to hair, comb to distribute, then lie on the floor with head under the bed for one meal’s time. Upon rising, hair turns entirely black—no more than one *shāng* of fat needed.

From *Yángshì Chǎnrǔ*: **Healing White Bald Patches and Scalp Ringworm**
Apply *xióngbái* (bear bile).

**Alternative for Bald Patches**
Apply *hǔgāo* (tiger fat).

From *Shènghuì Fāng*: **Treating White Bald Spots**
Pound *báigē fèn* (white pigeon dung) into fine powder, sieve, wash the scalp with vinegar and rice-water, then apply—immediate cure.

**For Red, Bald Scalp**
Burn *báimǎ tí* (white horse hoof) into ash, grind, and mix with December pig fat to apply.

From *Jiǎnyào Jìzhòng*: **Treating Scalp Sores**
Burn *dà sǔn kě yè* (large bamboo leaf sheath) into ash, adjust quantity to sore size, mix with raw oil, and add a touch of *nìfěn* (fat powder)—excellent.

**Bo Ge’s *Emergency Remedies from the Sleeve* – Volume Seven**

**Treatment for Wounds from Bear or Tiger Claws and Teeth (Poisonous Pain) – Fifth Thirty-Third Prescription**

*Ge’s Prescription:*
Burn green cloth to fumigate the wound; the poison will emerge. Then boil *gé gēn* (kudzu root) into a thick decoction to wash the wound. Pound dry *gé gēn* into powder, mix with the boiled *gé gēn* juice, and administer in a square-inch spoonful—five times daily, once at night, for optimal results.

*Alternative Prescription:*
Chew *sù* (millet) and apply it to the wound.

*Maopeng agrees.*

*Another Prescription:*
Boil raw iron until it emits a scent, then use it to wash the wound.

*Maopeng agrees.*

**General Precautions Against Ferocious Beasts and Poisonous Creatures:**
All wild beasts and venomous creatures are subject to human *qi* restraint. Before entering mountains or grasslands, one must first restrain them. The ritual method states:

*"Upon reaching the mountain’s base, hold your breath for thirty-five breaths. Visualize the divine spirit summoning a tiger to stand before you, then store it within your lungs. A White Emperor emerges, sealing the tiger’s eyes. Your lower *dantian* then expels lung *qi*, and the White Crown ascends above the forest canopy.*

*After a long pause, hold your breath again for thirty-five breaths. With both hands, pinch the tiger’s eyes in three steps—each step taken with the right foot leading. Then halt and recite:*

*'Li Er, Li Er—are you not Li Er? You stole the Yellow Emperor’s hound. The Yellow Emperor commands me to question you: How do you answer?'*

*Then proceed; no tiger in the mountain will be seen.*

*If encountered, stand firm, extend your left hand’s five fingers fully, and leap with all your strength—three upward-downward motions while shouting, ‘#1 *Zhuó!* Tiger, North Dipper Star commands you to depart!’ The tiger will flee. Even when camping, first dig four depressions in the ground as above."*

*Another Method:*
Burn cow or sheep horns—tigers will not dare approach humans.

*Another Method:*
Pound *xiónghuáng* (realgar) and *zǐshí* (purple stone), sew into a pouch, and wear it.*

---
**Appendix: *Mei Shi’s Prescription***
**Treatment for Tiger Bites on Humans:**
Drink alcohol until heavily intoxicated; the hair will be vomited out.

**Treatment for Sudden Rabies from Mad Dog Bites – Fifth Thirty-Fourth Prescription**

**Prescription to Cure Mad Dog Bites:**
First, suck out the foul blood. Moxibustion at the wound site ten times. The next day, reduce to one moxa cone daily until reaching one hundred.

*Maopeng warns:* Avoid alcohol.

*Another Prescription:*
Grind *dìyòu* (sanguisorba root) into powder, take one square-inch spoonful daily, once or twice. Also apply the powder to the wound. Pounding fresh roots and applying them is even better.

*Another Prescription:*
Scrape tiger teeth or tiger bone into powder, take one spoonful. If rabies symptoms appear as from a mad dog, this medicine will cure it.

*Maopeng agrees.*

*

---
**If the Patient Refuses to Eat the Gruel:**
If they refuse to eat the gruel, sprinkle salt near their nose—once they sniff it, coat their nose with the same salt. After licking it, they will then desire to eat. This method is miraculously effective.

**Appendix Prescriptions from *Mei Shi Fang* [Master Mei’s Recipes]:**
**Treatment for Mad Dog Bites:**
Take one handful of *táobáipí* (white peach bark), three *shēng* (升) of water, and decoct to one *shēng* for ingestion.

**From *Food Therapy* [食疗]:**
**Treatment for Dog Bites:**
Pound fresh *xìngrén* (apricots) into a paste and apply it to the wound—this will improve the condition.

**Fifty-Fifth Prescription for Sudden Poisoning and Fox Urine/Thorn Poisoning**

**For Poisonous Wounds from a Horse Biting:**
If a horse bites a person, causing a poisonous wound with intense heat and pain—**Prescription for Severe Heat and Pain (#4):**
Extract blood from a *crown-comb* (rooster’s comb) and drip it onto the wound three times.
If the horse is a *mǎ* (驳, dappled) type, use a hen’s blood; if it is a *grass* (草, plain-colored) type, use a rooster’s blood.
*Maopeng agrees.*

**Another Prescription:**
Moxibustion over the wound and swelling—this will improve the condition.
If the wound remains unhealed for a long time:
Take the tip of a horse’s whip (two *cùn* long), burn it along with 27 pieces of rat dung, grind into powder, mix with grease, and apply—this is highly effective.

**Another Prescription:**
Apply menstrual blood from a woman to the wound—this is the most effective.
*Maopeng says:* It is miraculously effective.
If a person already has a wound and rides a horse, and the horse’s sweat or hair enters the wound, or if their body is simply exposed to the *horse’s qi* (馬氣), this will cause swelling, pain, and fever. If the poison enters the abdomen, it will kill them.
Burn the horse’s whip skin, grind into powder, mix with grease, and apply to the wound.
**Another Prescription:**
Drink copious amounts of pure alcohol until heavily intoxicated—this will cure them.

**Another Prescription for Poisoning from a Dead Horse’s Bone:**
If a person is injured by the bone of a dead horse, and the poison attacks fiercely, threatening death:
Take the dung from the dead horse’s abdomen and apply it—this will improve the condition.
*Maopeng agrees.*

**Another Prescription:**
Insert the hand into a woman’s vagina—this will cure it.
*Note:* This is forbidden for those with a pregnancy, as it may cause a miscarriage.

---
**For Fox Urine/Thorn Poisoning Causing Swelling and Pain, Threatening Death:**
Break open a chicken’s nest (or coop) and apply it—this will improve the condition.
**Another Prescription:**
Dip the wound in hot *mùguī* (mulberry leaf ash) juice, then reapply cold juice repeatedly—this will lead to recovery.

**From *The Minor Formulas* (*Xiǎopǐn Fāng*):**
Apply hot wax directly to the wound, or fumigate with smoke until fluid drains—immediate cure follows.
*This is the urine-soaked wood of a fox, resembling a snake’s nest, beneath which lies fishbone that wounds a person.*

**Additional Prescriptions from *Tújīng*:**
For malignant thorns and fox-urine stings:
Pound *púgōngcǎo* (knotweed) roots and stems to extract the white juice, apply liberally—swelling ceases at once.
*This formula appears in Sun Simiao’s *Thousand-Gold Prescriptions* (*Qīanjīn Fāng*). His preface states:*
*"On the fifteenth night of the fifth month of Zhengguan’s fifth year, my left middle finger accidentally brushed against a courtyard tree. By dawn, unbearable pain set in. For ten days, the pain deepened, the wound swelled and darkened like ripe black beans. I recalled an elder’s remedy and applied it. The pain subsided, the wound healed, and within a decade, I recovered fully. Yang Yan’s *Southern Expedition Formulas* (*Nánxíng Fāng*) also attests to its efficacy."*

**Effective Prescription for Fox-Urine Sting Pain:**
Grind *xìngrén* (apricot kernels) finely, boil one *liǎng* until scalding, then immerse the sting repeatedly in the hot liquid—rapid relief follows.

**From *Wàitái Mìyào*:**
For injuries from dead horse bones breaking the skin, poisoning imminent:
Take dung from the horse’s abdomen and urine to wash the wound, then apply the dung—proven effective.
*Strain the dung juice and drink it—equally efficacious.*

**From *Shènghuì Fāng*:**
For horsebites penetrating to the heart:
Consume *mǎchǐxiàn* (horse-hoof herb) in decoction—condition improves.

**From *Língyuán Fāng*:**
For horse sweat entering a wound, causing swelling and worsening pain—treat urgently, or the poison deepens irreparably:
Apply powdered *shēng wūtóu* (raw aconite) to the wound; after some time, yellow fluid will drain—immediate cure follows.

**From *Wángshì Bóji*:**
For injuries from donkey saliva or horse sweat—divinely effective:
Fly *báifán* (aluminum potassium sulfate) and roast *huángdān* (cinnabar) until purple, mix equal parts, and apply as a poultice to the affected area.

**Prescriptions for Sudden Snakebites and Venomous Serpents (Section 56):**
**Ge Shi’s Prescription for Bamboo-Dwelling Green Wasps:**
Powder *zhōnghuáng* (realgar), *shèxiāng* (musk), and *gānjiāng* (dried ginger) equally, sift, and mix with *shèwǎng* (musk pouch). Load into a small bamboo tube and carry it. In an emergency, apply directly to the wound—equally effective against all venomous snakes.

**Alternative Prescription:**
Crush a black chicken, apply hot to the wound.

*Green snakes, glossy and tree-dwelling, rarely exceed four *chǐ* in length—all called "green-stripe snakes"—their bite is fatal.*

**Ge Shi’s Prescription for Venomous Snakebites:**
Dig a pit immediately, bury the wound, and firmly pack the soil above. The venom drains into the earth; within moments, pain eases, and the victim may be unearthed.

**Xu Wang’s Prescription for Snake Venom:**
Pound *dìyòu* (knotweed root) to extract juice, drink it, and apply to the wound.

**Alternative Prescriptions:**
1. Crush garlic, drink the juice, and apply the residue to the wound.
2. Apply *zhū ěr gòu* (pig ear wax) or *niú ěr gòu* (cow ear wax) to the wound—effective.
3. Chew salt, spit onto the wound, then moxibust three times. Rinse, spit again—pain ceases.
4. Pound *xiè* (onion) and apply.
5. Burn *wúgǔ* (centipede), powder, and apply to the wound.
6. Place a jointless bamboo tube over the wound, melt equal parts *là* (wax) and *mì* (honey), and pour into the tube. If honey is unavailable, use wax alone.
7. Urinate into the wound, then pinch the nose shut for three steps while holding breath. Dig a small pit, pour boiling water onto the soil to form a pill the size of a *wúzi* (Chinese date) seed, swallow it. Seal the wound with a dab of mud—excellent.
8. Powder *guìxīn* (cinnamon bark) and *guāluó* (trichosanthes fruit) equally, pack tightly into a bamboo tube, and carry it. In a snakebite emergency, apply immediately—effective against all venom. *If the tube is not sealed, the qi dissipates and the remedy fails.*

**General Snake Venom Treatment:**
Moxibust the wound three to five times—venom cannot spread.

**Snake Venom:**
Pound *guǐzhēncǎo* (devil’s claw) and apply—pain ceases at once.

**Alternative Prescriptions:**
1. Enclose *jīngyè* (mugwort leaves) in a pouch and press onto the swelling.
2. Apply *shèwǎng* (musk pouch) to the swelling until blood drains—condition improves.
3. Crush *hékǒu jiāo* (black peppercorns with leaves), apply—pain stops without fail.
4. Heat a blade red-hot, sear the wound.

**From *Méi Shī Fāng*:**
For snake or viper bites:
Pound *dútóu suàn* (garlic) and *suāncǎo* (sourgrass), apply to the bite.

**From *Guǎnglì Fāng*:**
For snakebites:
Crush *hēidòu yè* (black soybean leaves), apply three times daily—effective.

**From *Guǎngjì Fāng*:**
For venomous snakebites:
Seal the wound with ash from *jùjiāngcǎo* (a grass resembling swallowtail)—*its leaves resemble a swallow’s tail.*

**From *Bīngbù Shǒují*:**
For snake, lizard, and spider venom:
Gently tap a chicken egg to make a small hole, press it over the bite—immediate relief.

**From *Liú Yǔxī’s Chuánxìn Fāng*:**
For snakebites and scorpion stings:
Burn *dàozǐ tóu* (safflower heads) until red, place *báifán* (aluminum potassium sulfate) on the hot blade. When juice forms, drip it onto the bite—*instant cure.* This method has saved countless lives. In *Zhēnyuán* 32, two monks traveling south to Dengzhou were both bitten by snakes. This remedy saved them instantly—no further suffering.

**Prescriptions for Unhealed Snake Wounds and Snakebone Injuries (Section 57):**
**Ge Shi’s Prescriptions:**
For any unhealed snakebite, avoid hot foods—ingestion causes flare-ups. Treat as initially prescribed.

**Snakebite Causing Bleeding from All Orifices:**
Collect *zhūchóng* (horsefly) engorged with cow or horse blood (27 insects), burn, and ingest.

*Above are treatments for severe snakebites, swelling, and deep venomous injuries.*
**Snakebite with Fractured Fang Embedded in Flesh, Causing Unbearable Pain:**

**Ge Shi’s Prescriptions (Continued):**

For a snakebite with a fractured fang embedded in the flesh, causing unbearable pain:
Apply the liver of a toad (*xiāmá*) to the wound—it will emerge immediately.

Another method: First secretly gather *miǎoyīng* (water shield) leaves, pierce them while covering the wound so that no one sees, then place the pierced leaves over the wound’s opening. When the venom reaches the pierced leaves, the fang will break and emerge.

**Prescriptions for Snakebone Injuries and Poisonous Pain:**

For snakebone injuries causing poisonous, unbearable pain:
Take *tiějīng* (iron filings) the size of large soybeans and blow them into the wound with a tube. **Same method as above.**

Another method: Burn a dead rat, grind it into a paste, and apply it to the wound.

For snakebites where the wound has already closed but lingering venom remains in the flesh, causing persistent itching and pain:
Take garlic (1 *shēng* of large and 1 *shēng* of small), mix and grind them, then strain the juice with hot water and pour it into the wound. **Same method as above.**

For cases where a snake coils around a person and refuses to release:
Bathe the person in hot water—this will cause the snake to loosen. Alternatively, make the person urinate upon the snake.

For a snake entering a person’s mouth and not exiting:
Moxibustion (*áijiǔ*) on the snake’s tail will cause it to leave. If no fire is available, cut the snake’s tail in a circular motion until the skin is severed, then pull the skin downward—this will force the snake to exit. **Same as in *Xiǎopǐn*.**

During the seventh and eighth months (July–August), all snakes’ venom is at its peak and should not be expelled. They bite grasses and trees, causing them to wither and die—a condition called *shéchǐ* (snake-withered wood). This substance harms people more severely than snake venom itself; treat it using the same methods as for snakebites.

**Additional Prescriptions:**

From *Guǎnglì Fāng*: For snakebite wounds, wash them with warm *jiǔ* (alcohol) three times daily.

From *Shènghuì Fāng*: For a snake entering the mouth or any of the seven orifices, cut the tail of a sow and let its blood drip into the mouth—the snake will leave.

---
**Prescriptions for Avoiding and Treating All Snakes in Mountainous Regions and General Snake-Related Remedies (Section 58):**
**Method for Warding Off All Snakes:**

**Prescriptions for Avoiding and Treating All Snakes in Mountainous Regions and General Snake-Related Remedies (Section 58):**
**Method for Warding Off All Snakes:**

As before, following Master Yao’s Daoist method for entering mountainous regions.

Though many remedies exist to repel snakes, *wǔdū xiónghuáng* (realgar from Wudu) is supreme. Carry a piece with you, and if you weigh five *liang* (ounces) on your right arm at the elbow, no snake’s venom will dare approach. If others are bitten, grind it and apply it as a remedy. Also, carrying five *wǔgǔ huáng* (realgar pills) is effective. Since these pills contain *wúgǒng* (centipede), the full prescription appears in *Bèijí* (Emergency Remedies). Below is a prohibition: if one does not observe the ritual, the effect will fail.

Do not cross water after a snakebite—doing so will worsen the pain beyond the initial sting. Before crossing, visualize a giant centipede ahead of you, then proceed. If traveling by boat without performing this ritual, it will be fatal.

When entering mountains, never speak the word *"snake."* Instead, refer to the bitten as *"one struck by a snake."* This caution is all the more important to observe.

**Method to Repel Snakes:**
Burn *yángyáng* (ram) horns wherever you go, letting the smoke rise from the ground—the snakes will depart.

**Additional Prescriptions:**

From *Guǎnglì Fāng*: To treat snakebites where the victim is near death and to repel snakes,
grind equal parts *gānjiāng* (dried ginger) and *xiónghuáng* (realgar), store in a small silk pouch, and tie it on the left arm for men, right for women. The scent of the medicine will repel snakes, and the venom can be applied directly to the wound.

---
**Prescriptions for Sudden Centipede and Spider Bites (Section 59):**

From *Gě Shì’s Prescriptions*: Cut a rooster’s comb and apply its blood to the wound.

Another method: Seal the wound with salt—it will heal immediately. It is said that if the centipede flees far enough, it will not return.

Another method: Apply hot saltwater compresses.

Another method: Chew *dàsuàn* (garlic) or *xiǎosuàn* (small garlic) or *sāngshù bái zhī* (white sap of the mulberry tree) and apply it.

Also, rub the sole of a hemp sandal on the wound—this is effective.

Though *yúgǒng* (scorpions) bite fiercely, their venom is far lighter than that of bees. The pain is slight and subsides quickly. For spider bites:

Grind *shēng tiě yī* (raw iron armor) with vinegar to make a thick paste and apply it.

Another method: Mix *wūmá yóu* (black sesame oil) with *húfěn* (barite powder) and apply it. Once dry, reapply until recovery.

Apply *yángtáo yè* (wolfberry leaves) to the wound—it will heal instantly.

**Additional Prescriptions for Earthworm, Mole Cricket, Silkworm, and Other Pest Bites:**

From *Méi Shī’s Prescriptions*: For centipede bites where the pain does not cease,
rub the wound with *dútóu suàn* (single-clove garlic).

Another method, from *Jīngyàn Hòu Fāng*: Burn chicken dung, mix with alcohol, and apply it—this is excellent.

Another method: Mix chicken dung with vinegar and apply it.

From *Shènghuì Fāng*: To treat centipede bites,
extract juice from a *wōniú* (land snail) and drip it onto the bite.

From *Bīngbù Shǒují*: To treat spider bites where the entire body breaks out in sores,
drink fine spring wine until intoxicated, then lie still on your back—do not move. The alcohol’s toxicity will force the pests from the flesh, emerging like grains of rice. (Note: Be cautious, as the alcohol’s poison may otherwise harm the body.)

From *Tán Shì Xiǎo’ér Fāng*: Take a stalk of *cōng* (green onion), remove the tip, and pierce a hole at the base. Insert an earthworm into the stalk, pinch both ends tightly to prevent escape, and shake vigorously—it will liquefy. Drip the liquid onto the bite for relief.

From *Liú Yǔxī’s Chuánxìn Fāng*: To treat injuries from venomous creatures,
take one bowl of *dàlán zhī* (great indigo root juice), add *xiónghuáng* (realgar) and *shèxiāng* (musk), grinding them finely. Stir into the juice and apply to the bite. If the venom is severe, also ingest a small amount of the liquid—its efficacy is miraculous.

In the past, *Zhāng Yuánwài* served as a judge under *Zhāng Yánshǎng* in Sichuan. Suddenly, a striped spider bit his neck. By the next morning, two red marks, as thin as chopsticks, circled his neck from chest to heart meridian. By the second night, his face and head swelled to the size of several bowls, his abdomen followed, and he nearly perished. *Zhāng Xiàng* (the official) valued his recommendation highly and, in gratitude, donated five hundred thousand (cash) from his personal wealth, along with additional family funds numbering hundreds of thousands more, to seek a cure.

Suddenly, a man stepped forward and declared, *"I can cure him."* Zhang Xiang initially doubted him but, wishing to test his method, ordered him to prepare the medicine on the spot. The man replied, *"I care nothing for the formula—what matters is saving this man’s life."* He then took a porcelain bowl of *dàlán* (great indigo) juice, dropped a spider into it, and after a long while, it emerged from the liquid in great distress, barely able to move. He then crushed more *dàlán* juice, added powdered musk, and placed another spider into it—this one died upon immersion. Finally, he took fresh *dàlán* juice, musk, and added *xiónghuáng* (realgar), then dropped yet another spider into the mixture, where it dissolved into water.

Zhang Xiang and the others were astonished. They applied the liquid to the bite, and within two days, the swelling completely subsided—though a small sore remained at the wound. Once the scab fell off, the skin healed as before.

**From *Jīngyàn Fāng* (Experiential Prescriptions):**
To treat spider bites causing itchy threads across the body—drink one *shēng* (升) of sheep’s milk.

In the *Zhēnyuán* decade of the 10th year (794 CE), *Cuī Yuànwài* reported from *Zhì* (modern Sichuan): *"I witnessed a man bitten by a spider, his abdomen swelling like that of a pregnant woman. His family abandoned him, and he begged for food along the road. A monk encountered him and instructed him to drink sheep’s milk. Within days, he recovered."*

**Another Prescription:**
To treat *qiūyǐn* (earthworm) bites—immerse the body in a concentrated salt bath several times; this will alleviate the condition.

Zhang Shào, a military officer from *Zhèxī* (modern Zhejiang), was bitten by such a creature. Its form was vast as a *fēng* (wind demon), causing his eyebrows and beard to fall out. Each night, the earthworms would writhe within his body, emitting sounds. A monk taught him this remedy, and he recovered.

**Another Prescription:**
To treat *qiūyǐn* (earthworm) bites, where the victim’s form swells like a *fēng* (wind demon) and their eyebrows and beard fall out—immerse the body in lime water; this is also effective.

**From *Shènghuì Fāng* (Sacred Benevolence Prescriptions):**
To treat *gūnyǐ* (mole cricket) bites—apply chicken dung to the wound.

**Another Prescription:**
To treat *lónggū* (mole cricket) bites—mix lime with vinegar and apply it.

**From *Guǎnglì Fāng* (Expanded Benefit Prescriptions):**
To treat silkworm bites—grind musk finely, mix with honey, and apply; this will cure it.

**From *Qiānjīn Fāng* (Thousand-Gold Prescriptions):**
To treat *mòyú* (assassin bug) urine sores—burn *liàn* (melia) tree bark and skin into ash, mix with pig fat, and apply. Alternatively, pound fermented soybeans and apply them. Or mix vinegar with powder and apply. Another method: to treat *mòyú* (assassin bug) urine marks, where the victim develops sores at the point of contact, resembling clusters of millet grains, causing intense pain—if they cluster, the pain spreads like needles beneath the skin, as if stung by a venomous insect, forming small sores in groups like *zhūyú* (Chinese date) seeds, with red edges and white pus at the center. The skin tightens, the body shivers with cold, and a fever rises. In severe cases, the sores merge, spreading across the waist, ribs, and chest.

**Treatment:** Upon first contact, grind rhinoceros horn and apply it to stop the spread.

**From *Bówù Zhì* (Compendium of Curiosities):**
To treat *mòyú* (assassin bug) urine marks, which also cause sores where they touch—apply *jīchángcǎo* (chicken gizzard herb) juice; this is effective.

**From *Wàitái Mìyào* (Essentials of the Imperial Library):**
To treat *mòyú* (assassin bug) urine sores, which encircle the body and may be fatal—mix swallow’s nest soil with pig fat and sour wine, then apply. Another method: burn deer antlers into powder, mix with sour wine, and apply.

**Money Minister’s Prescription:**
To treat *mòyú* (assassin bug) urine sores with yellowish discharge—chew pear leaves and apply; renew as it dries.

**From *Shèngjīn Fāng* (Victorious Gold Prescriptions):**
To treat *mòyú* (assassin bug) urine sores, which first resemble scattered millet, then grow as large as beans, eventually swelling like a branded wound, causing extreme pain—immediately apply *cǎotú* (grass tea) or *làchá* (aged tea), mixed with raw oil. The pain ceases instantly; this is miraculous.

**From *Shènghuì Fāng* (Sacred Benevolence Prescriptions):**
To treat bites from malevolent insects—apply *zǐcǎo* (purple grass) oil. Alternatively, mix ghee with salt and apply.

**Prescriptions for Sudden *bì* (wasps) Stings (60):**
Apply *Yùhú Wán* (Jade Bottle Pills) or *Wǔgū Wán* (Five Armor Pills) to the sting site; these are found in *Bèijí Wán Sǎn Fāng* (Emergency Pill and Powder Prescriptions). Another method: take soil from beneath eaves, mix with water, and apply.

**Prescriptions for Sudden Bee Stings (61):**
If a bee stings—wash the site with human urine. Alternatively, apply the white sap of *gǔshù* (millet tree) or *sāngshù* (mulberry tree); both are effective. Another method: scrape tooth tartar and apply. Also, crush a spider and apply, or boil bee’s nest in water and apply. Burn cow horn into ash, mix with sour wine, and apply. Or cut open a gourd and rub the juice on it. Another method: chew *qīnghāo* (wormwood) and apply.

**Additional Prescriptions from *Qiānjīn Fāng* (Thousand-Gold Prescriptions):**
To treat bee stings—grind *lùfēngfáng* (bee’s nest) into powder, mix with pig fat, and apply.

**From *Yángshì Sǎnrǔ* (Yang’s Breastfeeding):**
Boil bee’s nest in water for washing; this is also effective.

**From *Wàitái Mìyào* (Essentials of the Imperial Library):**
Pound *bóhé* (mint) and apply; this will cure it.

**From *Shènghuì Fāng* (Sacred Benevolence Prescriptions):**
Apply ghee; this will heal it.

Shen Cúnzhōng’s *Bǐtán* (Talks on Calligraphy and Miscellany) records: *"The recluse Liú Tāng lived in seclusion on Wūshān. Once in Qí (modern Shandong), he saw a large rat bound by spider silk, which a wasp stung, causing it to fall to the ground. Soon, its belly swelled as if ready to burst. Slowly, it entered the grass and gnawed on a taro stalk, breaking it slightly. It then rubbed the broken stalk against its wound. After some time, its belly shrank, and it moved lightly as before. Afterward, if anyone was stung by a wasp, they would pound taro stalk and apply it, and the pain would subside."*

**Prescriptions for Sudden Scorpion Stings (62):**
If a scorpion stings—immerse the site in warm water. Another method: pound *mǎmiáo* (horseweed) and garlic. Or chew dried ginger and apply; this is excellent. Yao’s method: soak the sting in cold water, and the pain will not arise. If the water grows slightly warm, the pain returns—change the water immediately. Another method: soak old cloth in cold water and press it against the sting, changing it several times.

**Newly Effective Prescriptions:**
Take equal parts of *shùkuíhuā* (hibiscus flower), *shíliúhuā* (pomegranate flower), and *àixīn* (mugwort core), all harvested on the fifth day of the fifth month at noon, dried in the shade, ground together, and mixed with water to apply to the sting—this will instantly alleviate the pain. If these two flowers are unavailable, use *guǐzhēncǎo* (devil’s needle), pound its juice, and apply; this will cure it immediately. Another method: apply yellow cinnabar mixed with vinegar.

**Treatment for Scorpion Stings (Continued)**

Again, powder fresh *wūtóu* (aconite) and apply with saliva.
Chew dried ginger and spread it on.

Another method: seal with *shèwàng* (a type of adhesive), then soak with warm wine—it will heal immediately.

**Supplementary Prescriptions:**
Sun Zhēnrén’s *Food Taboos*: Treats scorpion stings.
Take one *liǎng* (20g) of alum (*fánshí*) and half a *shēng* (180ml) of vinegar, decocting them. Add alum powder to the vinegar and apply to the sting.

Another, from *Victorious Gold Prescriptions*: A small amount of aconite powder, mixed with head vinegar and applied.

Another, from *Money Minister’s Pocket Prescriptions*: Take *bànxià* (pinellia), grind with water, and apply—pain stops immediately.

Another, from *Food Physician’s Mirror*: Grind *fūzi* (processed aconite) with vinegar and apply.

Another, from *Empirical Prescriptions*: Apply donkey ear wax—it will cure.

Transmitted by Cui Jìshì.

From *Broad Benefit Prescriptions*: Treats scorpion stings where pain does not cease.
Apply the white sap of *chǔshù* (paper mulberry)—it will cure immediately.

**Treatment for Internal Hex Poison (Section 63)**

**Ge’s Prescription:** Cures hex-induced bleeding.
Take three *cùn* (9cm) of *jīyángpí* (goat or sheep skin, or even rotten drumskin), two *liǎng* (40g) each of *lǚlùyè* (lotus leaf), *kǔshēncāo* (soverign vine), *huánglián* (coptis), and *dāngguī* (angelica), seven *shēng* (1.2L) of water, decoct to two *shēng*, and divide into three doses.
One variation adds three *liǎng* each of *xījiǎo* (rhinoceros horn) and *shēngmá* (cimicifuga). If *lǚlùgēn* (lotus root) is unavailable, substitute four *liǎng* of *qiàn* (madder root)—this is superior.

**Diagnosing Hex Poison:**
If someone raises hex creatures to harm others, the symptoms are:
Internal hex causes sharp abdominal pain, as if something is gnawing, or vomiting blood. If untreated, it will consume the five *zàng* (viscera)—death follows.
To distinguish true hex from false: Have the patient spit into water. If the saliva sinks, it is hex; if it floats, it is not.

*—From Small Brand and Yao’s Methods.*

**Revealing the Hex Practitioner’s Name:**
Take a small piece of drumskin, burn it to ash, and give it to the patient to drink. The patient will soon call out the hex practitioner’s name. If they speak, the illness will leave.

Sometimes, snakes and centipedes combine to create hex poison in food, causing *jū* (abdominal masses). This type kills over years—each requires separate treatment.

Another method: Place *lǚlùyè* (lotus leaf) secretly under the patient’s outer mat. The patient will call out the hex practitioner’s name.

**Treating Internal Hex Poison with Vomiting or Bleeding:**
All follow the *Lán Gān* (Rotten Liver) Prescription.
Take three *liǎng* each of *qiàn* (madder root) and *lǚlùgēn* (lotus root), finely chopped, decoct with four *shēng* (720ml) of water to two *shēng*, strain, and serve warm in one dose—it will cure immediately.
The patient will also call out the hex practitioner’s name.
*—From Small Brand and Yao’s Methods.*

**Another Prescription:**
Take one *bādòu* (croton seed), remove its husk, roast, and mix with three *dòu* (soybeans) and a square-inch of ink from the bottom of a pot. Form into three pills. One pill will purge the poison; if ineffective, take another—it will act.

**Another Prescription:**
Take one *shāng* (30ml) of *kuì* (alkali solution) and mix with pure *kǔjiǔ* (strong liquor). One dose will induce vomiting—it will cure.
*—Same as Small Brand.*

**Zhī’s Prescription:**
Decoct one *shēng* (180ml) of *kǔjiǔ* until dissolved, then serve—divinely effective.

**Another Prescription:**
Take fourteen *qiūyǐn* (earthworms), soak in three *shēng* (540ml) of *kǔjiǔ*. When the worms die, drink only the liquid. Even the dead can be revived.

**Another Prescription:**
Take one *kǔhuā* (bitter gourd), decoct with two *shēng* (360ml) of water to one *shēng*, and serve. It will induce vomiting immediately—it will cure.
*—Same as Small Brand.*

**Zhī’s Prescription:**
Decoct one *shēng* of *kǔjiǔ* until dissolved, then serve—divinely verified.

**Another Prescription:**
Take three *zàojiá* (soapberry pods), roast, remove the seeds, and soak in five *shēng* (900ml) of wine overnight. Strain and divide into three doses.
*—Same as Small Brand.*

**Treating Hex Poison in Drink:**
Causes abdominal rigidity, facial greenish-yellow hue, and exposed bones from *línlù* (urinary dysfunction). Symptoms vary unpredictably.
Take *tiějīng* (iron filings), pound into powder, sift finely. Separately, pound *wūjīgān* (black chicken liver) and mix. Form into pills the size of *wúzǐ* (schisandra berries). Take three pills; severe cases may require up to ten days, mild cases will cure immediately.

**Alternative Iron Filings Prescription:**
Take one *jīgān* (pig liver) and one *shēng* (180ml) of honey, decoct until done, divide into twenty doses—secret prescription.
*—Same as Small Brand.*

Zhī’s variation: Can also be made into pills.

**Another Prescription:**
Take the pith of *zǎomù* (jujube wood), grind to one *hú* (5L), place in a pot with three *cùn* (9cm) of water, decoct to two *dǒu* (20L), strain for clarity, and simmer to five *shēng* (900ml) over low heat. Take one *hé* (10ml) daily on an empty stomach—it will purge hex poison.

*—Same as Small Brand and Yao’s Methods.*

**Another Prescription:**
Take one *liǎng* (20g) each of *xiónghuáng* (realgar), *dānshā* (cinnabar), and *lílú* (hemlock), pound to powder. In the morning, take with *jǐnghuá shuǐ* (dew water) the size of a knife-blade—it will induce vomiting and expel the hex creatures.

**Another Prescription:**
Drink one to two *shēng* (180–360ml) of *yǐnyǐngcǎo* (hidden-scented grass, *Platycladus orientalis* sapling) juice.
*—This grass is *zhègēng* (orange-hued *Platycladus*), commonly eaten.*

**Treating Hex Poison That Has Descended to the Lower Abdomen, Causing Perforation:**
Take one *chánggǔ* (long-legged toad) with a green back, and one *jīgǔ* (chicken bone). Zhī’s method: Burn one part to ash, mix, and insert deeply into the lower abdomen.
*—Same as Small Brand. Zhī’s method is frequently verified; Yao’s method agrees.*

**Another Prescription:**
Drip *zhūdǎn* (pig bile) into the lower abdomen, then pack with cotton deeply inserted.

**Another Prescription:**
*Wǔhuáng Huáng Wán* (Five-Yellow Pill) —the most essential for treating hex.
*—Its formula is in the Urgent Conditions section.*

There is also *natural flying hex*, appearing like ghostly mist—difficult to treat.
These varieties respond best to true *xījī* (rhinoceros horn) and *shèxiāng* (musk). Carrying these on one’s person also prevents hex.

**Yao’s Method for Hex-Induced Bleeding Like Chicken Liver, with Stone Residue, and Five *Zàng* (Visceral) Decay—Only the Heart Remains Intact, or the Nose Breaks:**
**Prescription for the Dying:**
Powder *zhègēng* (orange-hued *Platycladus*), serve with wine, one *sháo* (10ml) twice daily.
*—Ge’s Prescription.*

Zhī’s Imperial Physicians have transmitted over ten verified prescriptions.
Take *mǎdōulíng* (Aristolochia) root, pound to powder, serve with water, one square-inch dose. Follow vomiting to expel the poison—extremely effective.

This substance resembles the shoots of *kèmiàn* (Pueraria), grows along fences, and bears fruit like a tangerine. **For those already afflicted by hex:**

If one fears having been struck by hex and wishes to take **licorice juice** (*gāncǎo zhī*), it should be **freshly prepared and ingested**, which will induce vomiting and expel the illness.

**For those who habitually take it to prevent hex poisoning,** it should be **roasted and ingested**—once taken internally, it neutralizes the poison without causing vomiting, and the effect is miraculously verified.

**Another prescription:** Roast licorice and swallow the juice in each dose. If hex poisoning from food induces reverse toxicity, it will cause spontaneous vomiting, and the effect is extremely beneficial. **Constantly swallowing the juice** ensures that water will not be contaminated by either medicine or hex poison.

**Additionally, there is the Universal Poison-Dispelling Powder** (*Jiěbǎidú sǎn*), listed in the later *Yàodú* (Medicinal Poisons) section, which also serves as a remedy. **Serve one *hé* (100ml) of mulberry bark juice** (*sāngbáizhī*), and within moments, vomiting and purging will occur, expelling the hex.

**Chairman Shi’s Imperial Physicians** have transmitted over ten verified prescriptions, including these two, both of which have been tested and proven miraculously effective.

**Prescription with Spotted Cat Insects (*bānmāochóng*):**
Take four **spotted cat insects** (*bānmāochóng*), remove their legs and wings, and roast them. **Use peach bark** (*táopí*) collected on the fifth day of the fifth lunar month, remove the black outer layer, and dry it in shade. **Take *dàjí* (Canthium)**—these three ingredients are pounded separately and then sifted. Mix **one part spotted cat insect** (*bānmāochóng*), **two parts peach bark** (*táopí*), and **two parts *dàjí* (Canthium)** into pills the size of jujube kernels, and take them with **clear rice wine** (*mǐ qīngyǐn*). Upon completion, the hex will be expelled through vomiting. If one dose does not work, repeat after ten days, and the condition will improve. **This hex is most prevalent in Hongzhou**—an elderly woman cured one person and received twenty bolts of silk (*jiān*) as payment; her secret prescription could not be passed down, and her descendants faced legal punishment. **Yellow Flower Public** (*Huánghuā Gōngruò*) served as the **Prefect of Military Affairs** (*Dūdú*), and thus the method spread, but the elderly woman no longer received silk. **Shi states:** He has already cured over ten people with this method.

**Another prescription:**
Take **one square-inch dose of goat-sheep skin** (*yīpí*), **four *liǎng* (120g) of lotus root** (*liánhuā gēn*), **two *liǎng* (60g) each of *kǔcān* (Sophora) and **turmeric** (*huánglián*), and **three *liǎng* (90g) each of *dāngguī* (Angelica), **rhinoceros horn** (*xījǐ*), and **gentian** (*shēngmá*). **Simmer these seven ingredients in nine *shēng* (900ml) of water**, reduce to three *shēng* (300ml), and divide into three doses. The hex will be expelled immediately. **Shi states:** He once administered this to a person, who promptly vomited several *shāng* (60ml) of **wasps** (*fēngxiōng*), and the condition improved right away. **This is Yao’s Imperial Physician’s prescription.**

**Supplementary Prescriptions.**

**《Thousand-Gold Prescriptions》 (《Thousand-Gold Wing Prescriptions》):**
To treat **snake-witch poisoning** (*wùdú*), take **one handful of the white bark from the northern shade of *bìngmù* (Betula albosinensis)**), five *cùn* (15 cm) long, simmer in three *shēng* (300 ml) of water until reduced to one *shēng* (100 ml), and take on an empty stomach in divided doses—**the hex will be expelled immediately.**

**Another prescription:**
For **snake-witch poisoning with bleeding**, burn **hedgehog skin** (*wèipí*) into ash, grind finely, and take with water in a **one-square-inch dose** (*fāngcùn bǐ*). **The wasps will be vomited out immediately.**

**《Essentials of External Taiyi’s Prescriptions》 (《External Taiyi’s Secret Essentials》):**
To **urgently treat snake-witch poisoning**, burn **white goose feathers and droppings** into ash, mix with water, and ingest.

**《Yang’s Lactation Treatises》:**
To treat **internal snake-witch poisoning**, take **raw tortoiseshell** (*shēngdàimào*), grind with water into a thick paste, and consume **one bowlful** (*yīzhǎn*). **The condition will resolve itself.**

**《Sacred Benevolent Prescriptions》:**
To treat **children afflicted by snake-witch poisoning with bleeding, near death**, extract **Indigo plant** (*qīnglán*) juice and administer **half a small spoonful** (*bàn hé*) repeatedly.

**Prescription for Sudden Snake-Witch Poisoning (from *Diseases of the River Poison*)), No. 64**
**Yao’s Secret Prescription for Snake-Witch Poisoning (中水毒):**
Take **dried duckweed** (*shuìpíng*), ingest with wine in a **one-square-inch dose** (*fāngcùn bǐ*). **The condition will improve immediately.**
**Yao further states:** If **fingers are cold**, this is the condition. If **warmness returns**, it is not. **Mild cases** affect only the fingertips, while **severe cases** may extend to the elbows or knees—**if the cold reaches the elbows or knees, the condition is critical.**

**Snake-witch poisoning** (*shuǐdú*), also called **river poisoning** (*zhòngxī*), or **poisoning from water exposure** (*zhòngshǎdōng*), is known in some regions as **Su-hai** (蘇骇切). It resembles **arrow-witch poisoning** (*shègōng*) but lacks the projectile. **Its diagnostic signs:**
At the onset, the afflicted feel **chill** (*èhán*), with **slight headache** (*tóuzhù téng*), **eye discomfort** (*mùzhù téng*), **restlessness** (*xīnzhōng fán’ào*), **shivering limbs** (*sìzhī zhènzè*), **stiffened joints** (*gǔjié jiānqiáng*), **tense sinews** (*jīnjí*), and **excessive drowsiness** (*dàn yù shuì*). Symptoms worsen in the evening, with **coldness in the hands**. By the third day, **parasites reappear**, and **ulcers form in the intestines**—**painless, itchless, and without cold sensation**, but visible upon inspection. If untreated, **after six or seven days**, **abscesses rupture in the lower abdomen**, **parasites consume the viscera**, and **fever and toxins surge downward uncontrollably**. By the **eighth or ninth day**, even **skilled physicians cannot cure** the patient. **To diagnose urgently**, examine the lower abdomen for ulcers: **if the ulcer is bright red like fresh meat**, it is **yang-type poisoning** (*yángdú*), the most critical. **If the ulcer resembles the scales of a carp** (*lǐyú chǐ*), it is **yin-type poisoning** (*yīndú*), though slightly less severe. **All cases are fatal unless treated within twenty days.**

To **confirm snake-witch poisoning**, prepare **several *shēng* (liters) of warm water**, add **five *cùn* (15 cm) of minced garlic** (□), and **do not let it boil excessively**—**excessive heat weakens its effect**. Strain out the residue, adjust the temperature to **lukewarm**, and use it for **immersion therapy**. If **red patches or rashes appear on the body** and **no other symptoms are present**, treat it as another ailment.

**Prescription for Snake-Witch Poisoning:**
Take **leaves of plum or peach**, crush and extract **three *shēng* (300 ml) of juice**, dilute with a small amount of water, and drink. **Yao states:** For **children who cannot drink**, apply the juice to the **nipples** (*rǔtóu*) and let them ingest it.

**Another prescription:**
For **persistent infestation with snake-witch**, crush **common reed** (*chángsī cǎo*), extract **two *shēng* (200 ml) of juice**, and **soak a cotton swab in the juice**, inserting it into the **anus** (*xiōng*) to **guide the parasites downward**. Repeat **three times daily**—**the condition will improve immediately.**

**Another prescription:**
Extract **Indigo plant** (*lánqīng*) juice, mix with a small amount of water, and **apply thoroughly to the head, face, and body**.

**Another prescription:**
Take **one handful of pear leaves**, crush until soft, mix with **one cup of wine**, and ingest. **The condition will resolve within three days.**

**Another prescription:**
Take **roots of *shèméi cǎo* (snakeberry)**, grind into a fine powder, and ingest. **Alternatively, use the juice as a guide downward** or drink **one to two *shēng* (100–200 ml)**.

**In summer, if one must walk in water or bathe:**
Before entering, **sprinkle a small amount of the powder into the water**. **This wards off the hex without fear.**

**To prevent arrow-witch poisoning:**
Even if **water is stored in containers for bathing**, **sprinkle a small amount of the powder into the water**—**this is highly effective.** **Raising white geese or white ducks is also beneficial**, as is **wearing raw rhinoceros horn** (*shēngxījǐ*).

---

**In the eastern regions, such as the counties of Dongxiang and the surrounding mountains, snake-witch poisoning is rampant.**
**It occurs in spring**, much like **damp-heat disorders** (*shānghán*), and is called **river fever** (*xīwēn*). **Not all cases stem from arrow-witch poisoning**, yet **all suffer from dysentery** (*liànlì*). **The symptoms—chill, fever, restlessness, and pain—persist until death.**

**Prescriptions for snake-witch poisoning** resemble those for **damp-heat disorders** (*shānghán wēnjí*). **Administer the same single-method treatments.**
**Powdered *wǔjiā* (Acaanthopanax) root**, taken with **wine or fermented water** (*jiāngshuǐ*).

**Mulberry leaf juice** (*jīngyè zhī*) is also effective.
**These prescriptions are not publicly shared; keep them secret.**

**Another prescription:**
Extract **juice of *liáocǎo* (a type of rush)**, drink **one to two small spoonfuls** (*yī èr hé*), and **apply it thoroughly to the body**.

Take **one handful of *niúxī* (Achyranthes bidentata) stems**, steep in **one cup of water and wine combined**, strain, and drink the juice **three times daily**. **Use the male *niúxī* (雄牛膝), whose stems are purple.**

**If ulcers form in the lower abdomen and have already ruptured:**
Take **one *shēng* (100g) of *jùmǐ* (millet) and **five *shēng* (500g) of salt**, boil in **one *dàn* (10 liters) of water** into a gruel, and **sit in it**—**the condition will improve immediately.**

**Another prescription:**
Take **peach leaves and bark**, crush until soft, steep in water until concentrated, strain, and **sit in the liquid**—**parasites will emerge.**

**Another prescription:**
Burn **soapberry pods** (*zàojiá*) into ash, wrap in cotton, and **insert to guide the parasites out**—**this is also effective.**

Take **one-square-inch dose of *mǔdān* (Peony)**, ingest **three times daily.**
