**Prescription for Sudden Arrow-Witch Poisoning (No. 65):**
In the **southern Jiangnan region**, there exists a **poisonous arrow-witch parasite** (*shègōng dúchóng*), also called **short fox** (*duǎnhú*) or **moth** (*é*). It lurks in **mountain streams and water**, and **when people walk or bathe**, this parasite **uses its cross-shaped bony mouthpiece** (*hénɡgǔ jiǎo shè*) to **fire arrows into their shadows**, causing illness. **Its diagnostic signs:**
At the onset, symptoms may resemble **damp-heat disorders** (*shānghán*), **poisonous affliction** (*zhòng’è*), **loss of speech**, **chill and fever**, **stiffened limbs** (*sìzhī jūjí*), with **symptoms worsening by evening**. In **severe cases**, by the **third day**, **blood appears between the teeth**, and **if untreated, death follows immediately.**

**There are four types of infestation:**
Upon inspection, **one type appears as black spots like ink encircled by four edges** (囗囗囗), **resembling needle pricks**. **Another type forms ulcers**, which **persist and eventually perforate**. **A third type rises like a stone** (囗囗囗), and **the fourth type burns like fire**, causing **blistering skin and ulcers**—**this is the most critical**, and **all types are fatal**.

**The parasite thrives in regions where** (囗囗囗).
**During heavy rains or when people are driven by floods**, it **invades homes and shoots arrows at residents**. **It also preys on geese and ducks** (囗囗). **Raising white geese or white ducks can ward it off**, as can **wearing raw rhinoceros horn** (*shēngxījǐ*).

「If one observes these four types of sores on the body, **immediate treatment is essential**.

**For the first method**, encircle the sore thoroughly, **at a distance of one inch from its edge**, then cauterize (*jiǎ*) the area around it **a hundred times** (*bǎi zhàng*). The sore itself should also be cauterized **a hundred times**—this will cure the ailment.

**Another remedy**: crush and squeeze the stems and leaves of *red amaranth* (*chìxiāng*), **extract its juice for drinking**, and **apply the residue to the sore**. Maoyun states: **"Administer seven *hè* measures, four or five times daily."**

**Yet another remedy**: use *garlic chives* (*húsuàn*), **apply them warm to the sore**, and **moxibustion over the garlic chives a thousand times** (*qiān zhàng*)—this will cure it.

**Another remedy**: take **two white excrement pellets of a rooster** (*bái jīshǐ*), **mix them with honey** (*xiǎo táng*), and **apply the paste to the sore**.

**Another remedy**: combine **seven *hè* measures each of *woodlice* (*shǔfú chóng*) and *fermented broad beans* (*zhǐ*), three *bā* measures of *croton seeds* (*bādòu*), **with the heart removed**, and **melted with pig fat** (*zhūzhī*). **Apply this medicine directly to the sore**—this will cure it.

**Another remedy**: take **one *mǔ* parasite** (*mǔ chóng*)—**a black, bean-sized creature floating and moving on water**—**place it in the mouth**, and the ailment will subside.

**Another remedy**: take **one *zhàojiá* pod** (*zhàojiá*), **preferably two *chǐ* long**, **pound it into pieces**, and **simmer with bitter wine** (*kǔjiǔ*) until it thickens like syrup (*yí*). **Remove the dregs** (*qùzhì*) and **apply it to the painful area**—this will cure it.

**Another remedy**: pound *toothache amaranth* (*mǎchǐxiāng*), **drink its juice in two *shēng* measures**, and **apply the residue to the sore**. **Repeat four or five times daily**—this is highly effective.

**Another remedy**: take **two *liǎng* measures each of *ascending heartvine* (*shēngmá*) and *black bindweed* (*wūxī*), boil with **three *shēng* measures of water**, **reduce to one *shēng* measure**, and **consume it all**. **Apply the residue to the sore**; if no improvement, repeat. **Maoyun’s variation**: add **two *liǎng* measures of rhinoceros horn** (*xījǐ*).

**It states that this parasite** (*sandòu*) **shoots sand at a person’s shadow**, causing illness. **If one wishes to cross water**, first **cast a stone into it**; from the edges, **it fires arrows** (*yùshè*)—**its jaws can flex and extend like a crossbow** (*kǒuxiān*). In winter, **it lies dormant**. **Some have a long horn protruding before the mouth**; when the crossbow’s nock (*nǔyǎn*) aligns with the tip of this horn, **it bends like a raised crossbow**, using **its *qi* as an arrow**, and **propelled by water force**, it strikes people. **If struck**, the person **loses speech**, **and the rest of the symptoms resemble those described by Ge**.

**Remedies for sudden sand-flea poisoning (66th method)**:
Sand-fleas (*shāpí*) are **common in mountainous streams and rivers**; they are **extremely fine and nearly invisible**. When people **enter the water for bathing or washing**, these parasites **attach to the body while submerged**. On **rainy, overcast days**, they also **cling to people in grass**, then **burrow into the skin**.

**Diagnostic signs**:
**Initially**, the skin **turns bright red**, with **sores resembling small beans, millet grains, or foxtail millet seeds**. **When rubbed**, the reddened area **hurts like a needle prick**. After **three days**, the patient **feels stiff in every joint**, with **pain, cold, heat, and sores developing on the reddened skin**. The parasite **gradually penetrates to the bone**, **leading to death**.

**Preventive measures**:
After bathing in mountain streams, **dry the body with cloth several times**, then **wipe once with an old piece of silk** (*gǔbó*), and **apply powder** (*fěn*) to it.

**Another remedy for sand-flea poisoning**:
Take **ten slices of raw garlic** (*dàsuàn*), **place them in hot ashes**, and **warm them until hot**. **Cut the garlic and press the hot slices onto the sore**, using all ten slices. Then **apply moxibustion to the sore**, **seven times** (*qī zhàng*)—this is highly effective.

**Another remedy**:
Take **two *mù* measures of *leopard-spotted amaranth* (*bān māo*)**, roast one measure into a powder**, and **ingest it**. **Burn the other measure** until the smoke dissipates (*lìng juéyān*), then **apply the powdered residue to the sore**—this will cure it. **It is also effective if transmitted by arrows** (*yúshèwǎng*).

**Another remedy**:
Pound **raw musk** (*shèxiāng*) and **raw garlic** (*dàsuàn*) together, **mix with sheep fat** (*yángzhī*), and **carry it in a small tube** (*xiǎo gǔnzi*) while traveling.

**In the eastern regions**, sand-fleas are **found in all waters**. After bathing, **if tiny, hair-like needle pricks** (*rú máomáo zhēn cì*) are felt, **examine closely**—they will be visible. **Use bamboo leaves to scrape and remove them**. In **Lingnan**, when people **first notice this**, they **scrape with *ma* grass leaves** (*máo yè*) or **tea leaves** (*míngyè*). **Even slight skin damage is beneficial**; afterward, **repeatedly apply bitter gourd juice** (*kǔqùcài zhī*) is also effective.

**For deep infestations**, **use a needle to prick and extract the parasites**, **just like scabies mites** (*jiěchóng*). **Hold them under a light** (*yǐng guāng*) to observe their movement—**if extracted**, **apply moxibustion three or four times** (*sān sì zhàng*), **and the parasites will die, curing the illness**.

**If the patient still feels drowsy** (*hūn hūn*), **it indicates the infestation has gone too deep**. **Follow local customs** (*tǔsú*) for remedies, **rubbing out the parasites** (*bìchū*), and **then bathe with various decoctions** (*tāng yào*). **Use one or two *shēng* measures per bath**; **when all the medicine is exhausted**, **repeat with this method and other supplementary ones** (*zá fěn*).

**Sand-flea poisoning and arrow-strike methods** require **urgent rescue**. Within **seven days**, the patient should recover. **If not**, **flying parasites** (*fēichóng*) **will then devour the person’s internal organs**, leading to death. **Be extremely cautious and do not treat lightly**.

**Remedies for sudden overdose or poisoning-induced agitation (67th method)**:
**If one overdoses on medicine**, feels **agitated and restless** (*fánmèn*), or **is severely poisoned**, leading to **agitation and impending death**, the following remedies apply:

**Scrape a small amount of soil from the eastern wall**, **mix with one or two *shēng* measures of water**, and **drink it**—this is effective.

**Another remedy**: dig a **rectangular pit** (*zuòkàn*) **two *chǐ* square and three *chǐ* deep** beneath the eaves (*wūliù xià*). Pour **seven *shēng* measures of water** into the pit, **stir it with an object** to create a mist (*lìng mò chū*), and **drink one *shēng* measure of the mist**. If the symptoms persist, **repeat the process**.

**Another remedy**: pound *indigo plant* (*lán*), **extract its juice**, and **drink several *shēng* measures**. If no indigo is available, **wash blue silk** (*qīngguàn*) instead, **extract the juice**, and **drink it**—this also works.

**For overdose-induced agitation**:
Drinking **large amounts of fresh *kudzu root* juice** (*shēnggěrēn zhī*) is **highly effective**. If fresh kudzu is unavailable, **grind dried kudzu into powder**, **mix with water**, and **ingest five *hè* measures**. It can also be **boiled and consumed**.

**Another remedy**: swallow **several raw egg yolks** (*jīzǐhuáng*)—this will cure it. If no improvement, **repeat**.

**For overdose from mineral-based medicines**:
Powdered **white duck droppings** (*báiyāshǐ*), **mixed with water and ingested**, will cure it.

**Another remedy**: take **three *liǎng* measures of *rhubarb* (*dàhuáng*), two *liǎng* measures of *mirabilite* (*mángxiāo*), and **five *shēng* measures of fresh *Rehmannia root* juice** (*shēngdìhuáng zhī*), **boil until reduced to three *shēng* measures**, and **divide into three doses**. **Once vomiting occurs**, the illness will subside.

**If one suddenly overdoses and vomits uncontrollably**:
Drinking **one *shēng* measure of newly drawn water** (*xīnjì shuǐ*) will **stop the vomiting**.

**If the overdose involves *croton seeds* (*bādòu*) and diarrhea persists**:
Powder **dried ginger** (*gānjiāng*) and **turmeric** (*huánglián*), **ingest one *fāngcùn* spoonful**—this will cure it.

**Another remedy**: boil **soybean juice** (*dòuzhī*) to **one *shēng* measure**, and **drink it**—this will cure it.

**Supplementary Remedies (from *Wàitái Mìyào*)**:
**For overdose or poisoning-induced agitation and impending death**:
Burn **rhinoceros horn into powder** (*shāoxījǐ mò*), **mix with water**, and **ingest one *fāngcùn* spoonful**.

**Remedies for sudden poisoning from various medicines (68th method)**.

**Remedies for Poisoning by Wild Kochia (*yěgě*) Already Dead**

**First method**: Open the mouth with an object, then take **three chicken eggs** (*jīzǐ*), mix them with saliva, and swallow. In a short while, the wild kochia will be vomited out.

**Another method**: Warm **pork fat** (*zhūzhī*) to **one *shēng* measure**, and drink it.

**Another method**: Take a live duck, cut its head near the mouth, and let its blood drip into the victim’s mouth. If the blood reaches the throat, the person will revive.

**If the mouth cannot be opened**: Take a large bamboo tube (*dàzhúguǎn*), pierce its joints, and insert its head into the victim’s side. Fill the tube with cold water, repeatedly changing the water. In a short while, the mouth will open, and the antidote can be administered.

**For multiple victims**: Apply the bamboo tube to both sides and the navel (*páizhōng*), which is even more effective.

**Another remedy**: Drink **licorice juice** (*gāncǎo zhī*) in large quantities—this is excellent.

**Maopu’s Remedy (for poisoning by various toxins and wild kochia already dead)**:
Mix **fresh urine** (*xīn xiǎobiàn*) with **human feces** (*rénshǐ*), wring out the juice to **one *shēng* measure**, and ingest it all at once. Once it enters the stomach, the person will revive. No other antidote is as effective for resolving all poisons.

**For poisoning by *Datura* (*dān dú*) already dead**:
Powder **three *hé* measures of licorice** (*gāncǎo*), mix with **three *shēng* measures of water**, and drink.

**If the mouth is clenched shut**: Use a bamboo tube (*zhúguǎn*) to forcefully open the mouth and pour the antidote in.

**For poisoning by *arrowhead* (*shèwǎng*) toxin**:
**Indigo juice** (*lán zhī*), **large soybean juice** (*dàdòu zhī*), and **dog blood** (*zhūquǎn xuè*)—all can resolve it.

**For poisoning by *wolfberry* (*lángdú*) toxin**:
Use **indigo juice** (*lán zhī*) to resolve it.

**For poisoning by *wolf’s claw* (*lángkuí*) toxin**:
Use **wolf’s claw root juice** (*kuí gēn zhī*) to resolve it.

**For poisoning by *Lappula* (*lí lú*) toxin**:
Use **realgar** (*xiónghuáng*) and **onion juice** (*cōng zhī*)—both can resolve it.

**For poisoning by *Dianthus superbus* (*zhízhú*) toxin**:
Use **gardenia fruit juice** (*zhīzǐ zhī*) to resolve it.

**For poisoning by *croton seeds* (*bādòu*) toxin**:
**Turmeric** (*huánglián*), **small soybean juice** (*xiǎodòu zhī*), **mung bean juice** (*huò zhī*), and **large soybean juice** (*dàdòu zhī*)—all can resolve it.

**For poisoning by *realgar* (*xiónghuáng*) toxin**:
Use **stephania root juice** (*fángjǐ zhī*) to resolve it.

**For poisoning by *Sichuan pepper* (*shǔjiāo*) toxin and *centipede* (*wúgōng*) toxin**:
Both toxins can be resolved by **mulberry root juice** (*sāng gēn zhī*) or by boiling **mulberry root** (*sāng gēn*) into juice.

**For poisoning by *alum* (*fán shí*) toxin**:
Use **large soybean juice** (*dàdòu zhī*) to resolve it.

**For poisoning by *datura* (*yánhuā*) toxin**:
Use **saposhnikovia root** (*fángfēng*), **licorice** (*gāncǎo*), and **cinnamon** (*guì*)—all can resolve it.

**For poisoning by *Pinellia* (*bànxià*) toxin**:
Use **fresh ginger juice** (*shēng jiāng zhī*) and **dried ginger** (*gānjiāng*)—both can resolve it.

**For poisoning by *aconite* (*fùzǐ*) and *monkshood* (*wūtóu*) toxins**:
**Large soybean juice** (*dàdòu zhī*) and **polygala root juice** (*yuǎnzhì zhī*)—both can resolve it.

**For poisoning by *apricot seeds* (*xìngrén*) toxin**:
Use **indigo fruit juice** (*lánzǐ zhī*) to resolve it.

**If one has ingested metal and is already dead**:
Take **half a *shēng* measure of chicken feces** (*jīshǐ*), rinse with water to obtain **one *shēng* measure of liquid**, and drink it—**three doses per day**.

**Another method**: Swallow **two *liǎng* measures of mercury** (*shuǐyín*), which will wrap the metal and expel it. For smaller doses, **one *liǎng* measure** is also sufficient.

**Maopu states**: One dose of **one *liǎng* measure**, taken **three times**, while supporting the victim in an upright sitting position, will ensure revival once ingested.

**Another method**: **Duck blood** (*yāxuè*) and **chicken eggs** (*jīzǐ*) can also resolve it.

**The following is a remedy that resolves one type of poison while also addressing many others**:
Take **licorice** (*gāncǎo*), **chew it finely**, boil into a concentrated decoction, and drink the juice in large quantities. Also, eat **raw onions** (*cōng zhōng tì*) in abundance—both are excellent.

**Another method**: Boil **large soybeans** (*dàdòu*), let them overflow, and drink the juice in large quantities. If no large soybeans are available, **fermented soybeans** (*zhǐ*) are also effective.

**Another method**: **Indigo plant** (*lán qīng*) and **indigo fruit** (*lánzǐ*) can also universally resolve all poisons. Keep some stored for constant use.

**Another secret method**: Boil **waterdropwort** (*jìbì*), strain into a concentrated juice, and drink **one to two *shēng* measures**. If none are available, boil and chew the leaves and swallow. It can also be made into a powder and ingested. This remedy is particularly effective among all antidotes.

**Important note**: For all remedies involving boiling antidote juices, **do not drink them hot**. Poisons worsen when exposed to heat; it is best to drink them **slightly cooled**.

**Note from the Prefect of Lingnan (Maopu)**:
The **Lingnan aborigines** (*lǐrén*) often poison people through food. Victims may not immediately notice, but gradually lose their ability to eat. Some may experience **a bloated heart** (*xīn zhòng*), **tightness and suffocation in the back** (*bèi jí mèn*), or **initial coldness resembling malaria** (*chán*). If symptoms are detected early, quickly take a **piece of white silver** (*bái yín*) and hold it in the mouth. After **one night**, if the silver changes color—**green** (*qīngsè*) indicates **indigo poisoning** (*lán yào*), **yellow or red** (*huángchì*) indicates **datura poisoning** (*yánhuā*). If the poisoning progresses further, the eyes may turn **green** (*qīng*) or **yellow/red** (*huángchì*), with **green** (*qīng*) still indicating **indigo poisoning** (*lán yào*) and **yellow/red** (*huángchì*) indicating **mold toxin poisoning** (*jùn yào*).

The aborigines have their own healers, who fear discovery and often **pretend to use three hundred *liǎng* measures of "cowhead" antidote** (*sāniǎo yào*) or **claim three hundred *liǎng* measures of "silver" antidote** (*yín yào*). The local leaders, through prolonged acquaintance, know these antidotes are commonly used, though the aborigines do not recognize the *Bencao* (classical pharmacopeia), so they fabricate these names. Their methods are as follows:

**Initial Remedy (for aboriginal poisoning and to stabilize the patient)**:
**Four *liǎng* measures of fresh ginger** (*shēng jiāng*), **three *liǎng* measures of licorice** (*gāncǎo*), toasted (*zhì*), cut, and decocted with **six *shēng* measures of water** to obtain **two *shēng* measures**. Divide into **three doses** and administer. Once the doses are complete, then search for the specific antidote to treat the poison.

**Antidote Method**:
**Four *liǎng* measures of *dichroa root* (*chángshān*)**, cut, and **four *qián* measures of white salt** (*bái yán*), decocted with **one *dǒu* measure of water** (*yī dǒu shuǐ*). Soak overnight, preferably on the **last day of the lunar month** (*yuè jìn rì*), or at **five o’clock on the first day of the month** (*yuè yī rì wǔ gèng*). Use an **earthenware pot** (*tǔ fǔ*), boil, and ensure **no slaves, dogs, or chickens** (*núpó jīquǎn*) witness the process. Reduce to **two *shēng* measures**, and **administer two doses in the morning** (*dàn fēn èr fú*). After ingestion, the patient will vomit shortly. Store the vomit in a **copper vessel** (*tóng qì*). If the vomit remains **green** (*qīngsè*) and does not break when held aloft with a stick for **five *chǐ* measures**, the poison remains. After **two days**, administer another dose.

**Prefect Maopu’s Experience**:
Once, after drinking alcohol, a patient became poisoned. It took **over a month** before symptoms appeared. The local leader **Liang Fan** (*liáng fán*) prepared **soil-grown *dichroa root* (*tǔ chángshān*)**, calling it a **"three hundred-head cow" antidote** (*sāniǎo yào*). The patient ingested it and recovered. Afterward, for **twenty days**, they must avoid toxic foods. Only **cooked rice** (*zhǔ fàn*) can be consumed. Prefect Maopu has successfully treated **nine such cases** in total.

**Another Method**:
**Ten *liǎng* measures of *yellow vine* (*huáng téng*)**, which is abundant in Lingnan, cut and decocted with **one *dǒu* measure of water** to obtain **two *shēng* measures**. Divide into **three doses**. Once ingested, the internal poison will dissolve. If the poison is from **stephania-based aboriginal toxins** (*fángjǐ lǐrén yào*), regularly ingesting this vine will naturally prevent the poison from taking effect even if consumed.

**Prefect Maopu states**: Regular ingestion of this vine **promotes urination** (*lì xiǎobiàn*). It has also cured many others.

**Another Method**:
**Ten *liǎng* measures of *Vitex trifolia* (*dōulín téng*)**, also abundant in Lingnan, known to all locals. The aborigines call it **"three hundred *liǎng* measures of silver" antidote** (*sānyín yào*). Its leaves are long and slender, with a **three *chǐ* measure creeping vine**. Cut fresh, decoct with **one *dǒu* measure of water** and **two *shēng* measures of wine** (*jiǔ*), to obtain **three *shēng* measures**. Divide into **three doses**. Once ingested, the poison will be expelled through urination. For **ten days**, avoid toxic foods. If symptoms persist, administer another dose, and recovery will follow.

**Further Remedies:**

**Another Method:**
Four *liǎng* of **dried *Laportea decora* fruit** (*gànlán shí*) and four *liǎng* of **white-flowered vine** (*báihuā téng*), with the finest sourced from **Junzhou**. Avoid gathering wild *Pueraria* (*yěgě*) growing alongside it. Chop finely, decoct with **seven *shēng* of water** and **one *shēng* of wine**, reducing to half. Take on an empty stomach in one dose—brief dizziness is normal.

**Single *Laportea decora* powder**, taken whole, also proves effective.

**For internal toxins:**
Two *liǎng* of **creeping *Vitex trifolia* vine** (*dōulín téng*), three *cùn* long, finely shredded. Steep in **three *shēng* of wine** in a sealed jar, then seal tightly and char the edges with husk-fire until three boilings occur. Once cooled, consume warm, ensuring the wine retains its hue. No dietary restrictions apply—results are profound.

If forced to eat aboriginal food:
First chew and swallow **one *cùn* of roasted licorice root** (*gān cǎo*). If poisoned, vomiting follows—this confirms ingestion. Treat as before.

**Maopu’s Note:** Carry ten licorice slices in a pouch as a preventive measure.

---
**Supplementary Prescriptions:**

**From *Victorious Gold Prescriptions* (*Shèngjīn Fāng*):**
**Universal Antidote.** Grind **copper sulfate** (*dǎnzǐ fán*) into powder, mix with glutinous rice paste into pills the size of a rooster’s egg, coating each with **cinnabar** (*zhūshā*). Store with cinnabar to preserve potency. Dissolve one pill in cold water—immediate recovery follows.

**From *Empirical Prescriptions* (*Jīngyàn Fāng*):**
**For ascending drug poison** (like *Shèngsǎn*). Equal parts **bee’s nest** (*lùfēngfáng*) and licorice, toasted with bran until golden. Remove bran, pulverize. Decoct with **two bowls of water** until reduced to **one bowl (eight *shēng*)**. Drink warm before bed—expels toxins by dawn.

**From *Essentials of the Imperial Library* (*Wàitái Mìyào*):**
**For post-medication collapse**, where the patient seeks cold ground and refuses heat:
Decoct **two *liǎng* of *Acanthopanax* bark** (*wǔjiā pí*) in **four *shēng* of water** to **two and a half *shēng***. Administer when symptoms emerge. If unresolved, repeat.

**Sun Simiao’s Commentary:**
For **aconite** (*wūtóu*) or **croton seed** (*bādòu*) poisoning, licorice alone stabilizes the stomach. Though **soybeans** (*dàdòu*) are said to neutralize all toxins, licorice proves more effective in **licorice-soybean decoction** (*gāndòu tāng*).

**From *Master Mei’s Prescriptions* (*Méi Shī Fāng*):**
**Sichuan pepper** (*chùjiāo*) poisoning causes locked jaws, suffocation, or white froth. Decoct **cinnamon juice** (*guì zhī*) or drink **one to two *shēng* of cold water**, then induce vomiting with **thick fermented soybean paste** (*nóng zhī*).

**From *Holy Benevolence Prescriptions* (*Shènghuì Fāng*):**
**For sulfur poisoning** causing suffocation: Drink **one *hé* of sheep’s blood**—immediate relief.

**Another Method:**
For **arrowhead fish poison** (*shèwǎng*) in meat or **leaked salted meat poison** (*lòupú*), take **half a *qián* of crushed abalone shell** (*bèizǐ*), mixed with water—effective. Same for **fermented wheat poison** (*miàn áo*).

**From *Yu Shi’s Secret-Effective Prescriptions* (*Chū Yú Shì Mìxiào Fāng*):**
**For severe drug poisoning:** Remove skin from **croton seeds** (*bādòu*), avoiding oil extraction. Grind with **sodium sulfate** (*mǎyá xiāo*) in equal parts into a paste. Dissolve **one pea-sized dose** in cold water—recovery follows.

---
**Prescription LXIX: For Food Poisoning**

**Sichuan pepper poisoning** causes locked jaws, throat obstruction, suffocation, or white froth. Drink **cinnamon juice or cold water (one to two *shēng*)**, or consume **large quantities of garlic**—immediate cure. **Never drink hot liquids—fatal.**

For **internal pepper poisoning**, chew **garlic or *Isatis tinctoria*** (*jìdí*).

**Misidentified *Heracleum* (*gōuwén*) poisoning** (resembling mustard greens) is lethal:
Decoct **eight *liǎng* of *Isatis tinctoria*** in **six *shēng* of water** to **three *shēng***. Take **five *hé*** daily, five doses.

**For poisoned vegetables causing delirium or suffocation:**
Burn **chicken dung** into ash, take **one *fǔchí* dose**. If unresolved, repeat.

**For *Datura* (*zhēnmáng*) poisoning:**
Decoct licorice juice, mix with crushed *Laportea decora* juice—both effective.

**For bitter gourd (*kǔhuā*) poisoning:**
Boil **glutinous millet** (*níshú*) into a thick paste, drink **several *shēng***—optimal.

**For horse liver poisoning:**
Consume **seven pairs of field mouse droppings** (*mǔshǔ fèn*), selecting those with tapered ends, mixed with water. Repeat if unresolved.

**For poisoning from six domestic animals or black beasts.**

**For headscarf filth (幞头垢):**
Take **one *qián* dose** of ash—*Xiaopin* states: *"It can revive the dead."*

**For fermented soybean poisoning:**
Drink **several *shēng* of soybean juice**—effective.

**General Warning on Liver Consumption:**
Never casually consume any liver. **Self-slaughtered meat is especially forbidden**, as consuming raw liver is poisonous.

**For liver poisoning:**
Pound *Aconitum carmichaelii* (附子) into powder, take **one *dāoguī* dose**, three times daily.

**For arrow poison in meat:**
Use *Indigofera* juice and **soybeans** to neutralize *Strychnos* (射罔) toxicity.

**For spoiled meat poisoning (郁肉):**
Meat stored in honey vessels overnight, or **salted meat contaminated with thatch-house juice (漏脯)**, is toxic. Burn **human feces** into ash, take **one *fǔchí* dose** in wine.

**Alternative remedy:**
Pound *Allium tuberosum* (薤) juice, drink **two to three *shēng***, taken consecutively with minimal water.

**For millet grain with hidden spoiled meat poisoning:**
Boil **soybeans** until just simmered, drink **several *shēng* of the broth**—this resolves it and **neutralizes all spoiled meat toxins**.

**For poisoning from self-slaughtered domestic animals:**
Take **one *fǔchí* dose of *Phellodendron chinense* (黄檗) powder**. If unresolved, repeat after several days.

**Note on self-slaughtered livestock:**
All such meat is tainted by pestilence and toxic. Consumption causes **persistent diarrhea and abdominal blockage**—administer *lìwán* (痢丸) to purge.

**For fish poisoning:**
Simmer **tangerine peel** into a thick decoction, drink the juice.

*Xiaopin* states: **"Winter melon juice is most effective."**

**For undigested pork forming parasitic worms:**
**First remedy:**
Decoct **one *liǎng* each of *Rheum palmatum* (大黄) and *Natrium sulfate* (朴硝)**—*Natrium sulfite* (芒硝) is also effective—reduce to **one *shēng* of liquid**, consume entirely.

**If unresolved:**
Grind **prunes (杏子)** with the skin into a paste, mix with **three *shēng* of hot water**, take in three doses to induce vomiting—**miraculously effective**.

**For cow meat poisoning:**
Decoct **licorice**, drink **one to two *shēng* of the juice**.

**For horse meat poisoning (leading to fatal diarrhea):**
**Two hundred fermented soybeans (豉)**, **twenty prunes (杏子)**, **chew and mix**, steam with **five *shēng* of cooked rice**, mash thoroughly, and take **twice daily until consumed**.

*Note: This applies only to meat from diseased cattle or horses.*

**For poisoning from *Lateolabrax* (鲈鱼) liver or *Siniperca chuatsi* (鯽鮧) fish:**
Shave **lotus root (芦根)**, decoct the juice, drink **one to two *shēng***—effective.

**To neutralize toxins:**
Simmer **Perilla frutescens (香苏)** into a thick decoction, drink **one *shēng* of the juice**.

**For unknown food poisoning:**
As before, **licorice and *Laportea decora* (荠苨)** universally treat such poisoning—**all can be salvaged**.

**For accidentally swallowing leeches while eating pickled vegetables:**
Leeches consume internal organs and blood, causing **abdominal pain and progressive jaundice and emaciation**. Drink **one to two *shēng* of warm cow or sheep blood**, then after a night’s passage, consume **one *shēng* of warm lard**—this will expel the leeches.

**For mushroom poisoning (致死):**
Squeeze **human feces juice**, drink **one *shēng***—**revives the dying**.

**Alternative remedies:**
Administer **any emetic-purgative pill (吐痢丸)**—also effective.
**Or:**
Dig a pit, mix with water to form a slurry, drink **two to three *shēng***—**highly effective**.

**For accidental wild taro poisoning (欲死):**
Treatment follows the **mushroom poisoning method**.

**Note on wild taro:**
If left unharvested for **three years**, it becomes **wild taro—deadly**.

**Additional Prescription (梅师方):**
**Treatment for poisoning from fish, meat, or vegetables.**

**For poisoning by *Kǔcān* (Sophora flavescens):**
Take **three *liǎng* of *kǔcān***, decoct with **one *shēng* of bitter wine** until **three to five boils**, strain and ingest—**vomiting will cure it**.
**Alternatively:**
Boil **rhino horn juice** to **one *shēng***—also effective.

**For undigested dog meat poisoning:**
Symptoms include **abdominal hardness, bloating, dry mouth, fever, and delirium**.
Boil **reed root (Lophatherum)** and drink—**effective**.

**For stubborn meat retention:**
Take **one *shēng* of apricot kernels**, peel, decoct with **three *shēng* of water** until boiling, strain, and divide into **three doses**—**stop when meat passes**.

---
**From *Jīn Guì* (Golden Cabinet):**
**For crab poisoning:**
Boil **perilla (Zǐsū)** into juice and drink **three *shēng***—**effective**.
**Alternatively:**
Drink **perilla seed juice**—also treats poisoning.
**Note:** Crab **not exposed to frost** is **highly toxic**.

**From *Shèng Huì Fāng* (Holy Benevolence Prescriptions):**
Drink **raw lotus root juice**, **boiled garlic juice**, or **winter melon juice**—**all effective**.

**For pheasant meat poisoning (causing vomiting/diarrhea):**
Take **one *fāngcùn* of powdered raw rhino horn**, mix with **freshly drawn water**, and ingest—**immediately effective**.

**Record of Tang Dynasty’s Cui Wei (崔魏公):**
A man suddenly died at night; upon inquiry, he had eaten **bamboo chicken (a type of bird)**.
The physician diagnosed: **"Poison."**
The servant replied: **"He often ate bamboo chicken."**
The physician deduced: **"Bamboo chicken eats *bànxià* (Pinellia) sprouts—this must be *bànxià* poisoning."**
He ordered **fresh ginger juice** to be forced down—**the man revived**.

---
**From *Jīn Guì* (Golden Cabinet):**
In **spring and autumn**, **dragon essence** enters **celery**, causing **"Snake-Dragon Disease"** when consumed.
Symptoms: **hands turn blue, abdominal distension, unbearable pain**.
Treatment: Drink **three to five *shēng* of hard sugar (rock candy)** twice daily—**vomiting three to five serpentine masses** brings relief.

**From *Míng Huáng Zá Lù* (Miscellaneous Records of Emperor Xuanzong):**
A **Yellow Gate official** returned from a mission to **Lingnan (Guangdong/Guangxi)**.
The physician **Zhōu Mò** examined him and declared: **"Your stomach contains a dragon."**
The Emperor was startled and asked: **"Do you have an illness?"**
The official replied: **"While crossing Dàyù Ridge in the heat, I was thirsty and drank water. Suddenly, my stomach felt hard like a cup."**
Zhōu Mò administered **nitre and realgar**, decocted and ingested—**he vomited a creature several *cùn* long, finger-thick, with scales**. When placed in water, it grew several *zhǎng* long. After dousing it with **bitter wine**, it shrank back. Covered overnight, it had **hatched into a dragon**.
The Emperor was astonished.

---
**Section LXX: Treatments and Taboos for Poisoning from Food and Miscellaneous Foods**

**Taboos for Livestock and Poultry:**
- **White sheep** must not be eaten with **rooster meat**.
- **Sheep liver** must not be eaten with **black plum (Umeboshi)** or **pepper**.
- **Pork** must not be eaten with **sheep liver**.
- **Cow intestines** must not be eaten with **dog meat**.
- **Rooster meat** must not be eaten with **raw leeks**.
- **Chicken or duck meat** must not be eaten with **garlic, plums, or turtle meat**.

**Taboos for Livestock Organs:**
- **Fresh liver** dropped on the ground and **untouched by dust** is **forbidden to eat**.
- **Dried meat** that **does not dry properly**, **does not move when roasted**, or **moves when placed in water** is **forbidden to eat**.
- **Carrion** with **closed mouth** is **forbidden to eat**.

**Taboos for Aquatic Foods:**
- **Fish heads** with **pure white spines** are **forbidden to eat**.
- Fish **without intestines or gallbladder**, or **heads without eyes**, are **forbidden to eat**.
- Fish must not be eaten with **black chicken meat**.
- **Raw fish** with **red eyes** is **forbidden to make into sashimi**.
- Fish must not be eaten with **adzuki beans or amaranth**.
- **Salted green fish** must not be eaten with **raw coriander**.
- **Turtle** with **sunken eyes** is **forbidden to eat**.
- **Turtle meat** must not be eaten with **chicken or duck eggs** or **red amaranth**.
- **Pregnant women** must not eat **raw fish (sashimi)**.

**Taboos for Fruits and Vegetables:**
- **Plums** must not be eaten with **eggs** or **near water**.
- **Raw greens** must not be eaten on **May 5th**.
- **Sick individuals** must not eat **raw mustard greens**.
- **Pregnant women** must not eat **mulberry, duck, or croton seeds**.
- **Soups** containing **Pinellia, Acorus, lamb, Asarum, or Platycodon** have **specific vegetable taboos**.
  - **Glycyrrhiza** avoids **Chinese chives**.
  - **Peony** avoids **coriander**.
  - **Wormwood** avoids **leeks**.
  - **Coptis and Platycodon** avoid **pork**.
  - **Poria** avoids **strong vinegar**.
  - **Asparagus root** avoids **carp**.

**Additional Prescriptions from *Shí Yī Xīn Jìng* (Food Physician’s Mirror):**
**Emperor Huangdi’s Warning:**
Eating **melon followed by salt** causes **cholera**.

**Sun Zhēn Rén’s (*Food Taboos*):**
- **Xanthium (cocklebur)** with **pork** is **lethal**.
- **Frost-bitten melons in September** cause **reverse peristalsis (gastroptosis)**.

---
**Section LXXI: Treatments for Sudden Drunkenness and Alcohol Poisoning**

**Warning:** Excessive drinking risks **intestinal perforation**.

**Method:**
Immerse the drunkard in **large containers of warm water**, changing frequently until cool.

**Precautions:**
- **Do not let them lie still**—**keep them moving**.
- Avoid **lying on damp mats**, **washing with cold water**, or **sexual activity**.

**For drunkenness-induced headache:**
Scrape **five *liǎng* of fresh bamboo bark**, boil with **eight *shēng* of water** to **five *shēng***, strain, then add **five eggs**, stir, and boil again—**drink all at once**.
**If diarrhea persists:**
Boil and drink **dragon bone (fossilized bone)**—**or take as powder**.

**For prolonged drinking causing throat/esophagus erosion and tongue ulcers:**
Pound **one *shēng* of hemp seeds**, mix with **two *liǎng* of Phellodendron bark powder**, form **honey pills**, and ingest.

**For alcohol-induced jaundice from heat accumulation:**
Soak **seven eggs** in **bitter wine**, seal in a **honey-coated jar**, bury in a **well for two nights**, then **swallow two eggs daily** until finished—**cure achieved**.

**For persistent drunkenness and discomfort:**
Boil **mallow leaves** with **a little rice**, strain, cool, and drink—**effective**.
**Alternatively:**
Drink **one to two *shēng* of fresh Pueraria root juice** or **boiled dried Pueraria**—**also effective**.

**To resist intoxication (drink more without harm):**
Pound **two *hé* of *Bǎizǐ Rén* (Biota seeds) and **two *hé* of hemp seeds**, take as a dose, then **drink twice the usual amount**.
**Alternatively:**
Grind **kudzu flower and adzuki bean flower** into powder, take **three to four *sháo***—**also effective**.
**Additionally:**
Frequently drink **Pueraria root tea** or **loquat leaf tea**, or mix with **dried coix seeds, hemp seeds, etc.**—**prevents drunkenness**.

Sesame also **stops intoxication**.
First take **one spoonful of salt**, then drink alcohol—**also doubling the amount**.

**Additional prescriptions from *Wàitái Mìyào* [外台秘要]:**
**For intoxication without regaining consciousness:**
Take **September 9th true chrysanthemum flowers**, powdered, and ingest **one square-inch spoonful** with wine.

**Another prescription to curb drinking:**
Burn **donkey foal hide** into ash and consume with wine.

**Another prescription:**
Take **cormorant dung ash**, ingesting **one square-inch spoonful** with water.

**From *Shènghuì Fāng* [圣惠方]:**
**For alcohol poisoning or intoxication-induced drowsiness and thirst—quick recovery method:**
Take **two liang of tangerine peel**, dry-fry into powder, measure **three qian spoons**, boil with **one medium cup of water** until **three to five boils**, add salt, and consume like tea—**wonderfully effective**.

**Another prescription for intoxication without regaining consciousness:**
Grind **two hé of *Sōngcài Zǐ* (Achyranthes bidentata seeds)** finely, mix with **one cup of well-water**, and divide into **two doses**.

**From *Qiānjīn Fāng* [千金方]:**
**Method to curb drinking:**
Place **seven shēng of wine** in a bottle, add **half a liang of fine cinnabar powder**, seal tightly, and place inside a pigpen, letting the pig shake it for **seven days**. Then drink it all at once.

**Another prescription:**
On **New Year’s Day**, pour **five shēng of wine** over a **mortar pestle**, then drink it.

**Another prescription for alcohol-related illness:**
Boil **half a shēng each of fermented black beans and green onions** with **two shēng of water**, reduce to **one shēng**, and consume all at once.

---
(*Bo Géxiān Wēng Zhǒuhòu Bèijí Fāng* [葛仙翁肘后备急方] Volume 7 concludes here.)

---

**Volume 8 begins:**

**Pai Shi’s Five Toxin Divine Ointment** (裴氏五毒神膏), a remedy for sudden **central evil** (中恶) and violent **hundred diseases** (暴百病).
**Realgar** (雄黃), **cinnabar** (朱砂), **Angelica sinensis** (當歸), **pepper** (椒) each **two liang** (兩), **Aconite** (烏頭) **one shēng** (升), steeped in **bitter wine** (苦酒) overnight. **Pork fat** (豬脂) **five jīn** (斤), arranged facing east with **Phragmites communis** (陈芦). Simmer **five times** (五上) and **five times** (五下), strain and remove dregs, then add **realgar** and **cinnabar powder** (雄黃、朱砂末). Stir until fully incorporated. For sudden **hundred diseases** (卒百病), take with **warm wine** (溫酒) like a **date pit** (枣核) in size; if not effective, take again. Once **discharged** (得下), the illness is removed. For diseases of the **four limbs** (四肢), apply as a liniment. For **edematous sores** (廱肿) and **various diseases** (诸病疮), apply as a plaster. For nighttime travel or illness caused by **mist and dew** (冒露雾), apply to the body—excellent.

This formula also treats **seasonal epidemics** (時行溫疫), **noxious *qi*** (毒氣), **malignant sores** (毒核), **golden wounds** (金創), etc.

**Cangwu Daoist Chen Yuan’s Ointment** (苍梧道士陈元膏) for **hundred diseases** (百病).
**Angelica sinensis** (當歸), **Aconite** (天雄), **Aconite** (烏頭) each **three liang** (兩), **Asarum** (細辛), **Ligusticum** (芎藭), **cinnabar** (朱砂) each **two liang** (兩), **dried ginger** (乾姜), **processed Aconite** (附子), **realgar** (雄黃) each **two liang and half** (兩半), **Cinnamomum cassia** (桂心), **Angelica dahurica** (白芷) each **one liang** (一兩), **pine resin** (松脂) **eight liang** (八兩), **raw Rehmannia** (生地黃) **two jīn** (二斤). Pound and strain to extract juice. Grind the **thirteen substances** (十三物) separately; **realgar** and **cinnabar** as powders. The rest are **pounded** (□砠). Steep in **strong bitter wine** (酽苦酒) **three shēng** (三升), combined with **Rehmannia juice** (地黃渍), overnight. Take **pork fat** (豬脂) **eight jīn** (八斤), simmer over **gentle fire** (微火) until **fifteen boiling points** (十五沸)—when the **Angelica dahurica** turns yellow (白芷黃為度)—strain and remove dregs. Add **realgar** and **cinnabar powder**, stir until thick and uniform, and store in a sealed container. For **internal abdominal diseases** (腹內病), apply as a plaster by holding over fire (對火摩病上), **two or three times daily**, for **ten to twenty days**, until the illness **discharges** (取病出) and improves.

For **fat limbs** (四肢肥肉), **epidemic dampness** (風瘴), also take with **warm wine** (酒溫服) like a **plum-sized pill** (如杏子大一枚). It treats **accumulations in the heart and abdomen** (心腹积聚), **numbness and atrophy of the four limbs** (四肢痹躄), **whole-body wind affliction** (舉體風殘), and is a **universally effective remedy** (百病效方).

**Hua Tuo’s Tiger Bone Ointment** (華佗虎骨膏) for **hundred diseases** (百病).
**Tiger bone** (虎骨), **wild Pueraria** (野葛) each **three liang** (三兩), **processed Aconite** (附子) **fifteen pieces** (十五枚) weighing **nine liang** (重九兩), **pepper** (椒) **three shēng** (三升), **apricorn kernels** (杏仁), **croton seeds** (巴豆,去心皮), **Ligusticum** (芎藭) each **one shēng** (一升), **licorice** (甘草), **Asarum** (細辛) each **one liang** (一兩), **realgar** (雄黃) **two liang** (兩). Steep the **ten substances** (十物) in **bitter wine** (苦酒) for **seven days** (周時). Take **pork fat** (豬脂) **six jīn** (六斤), simmer **three times** (三上三下) until **one piece of processed Aconite** (完附子一枚) turns yellow (視黃為度). Strain and remove dregs, then add **realgar**, stir until thick and uniform, and store in a sealed container.

Apply as a plaster for **all hundred diseases** (百病), but **avoid the eyes** (唯不得入眼). If taken internally, consume like a **date-sized pill** (如枣大) in **one small spoonful** (一合) of **hot wine** (熱酒). After a short while (須臾後), **pluck white hair** (拔白發) and apply to the affected area—it will **regenerate** (即生). For **ulcers from toxic wind** (烏猪疮), **edematous sores** (毒風肿), **saddle sores** (馬鞍疮), wash with the ointment—it will improve. The same applies for **cow-leader sores** (牛領).

**Mugwort Ointment** (莽草膏) for **noxious wind afflictions** (诸贼風), **edematous numbness** (肿痹), **wind entering the five *zàng* organs** (風入五藏), and **dizziness** (恍惚).
**Mugwort** (莽草) **one jīn** (一斤), **Aconite** (烏頭), **processed Aconite** (附子), **Cotoneaster** (踯躅) each **three liang** (三兩). Cut the **four substances** (四物), steep in **water and bitter wine** (水苦酒) **one shēng** (一升) overnight. Take **pork fat** (豬脂) **four jīn** (四斤), simmer **three times** (三上三下), strain and remove dregs. Apply by rubbing over fire (向火以手摩病上) **three hundred times** (三百度)—improvement occurs immediately upon application (應手即差). For **ear and nose diseases** (耳鼻病), wrap with cotton and insert.

It also treats **scabies, ringworm, and miscellaneous sores** (诸疥癬、雜疮). **Hidden Residence’s *Efficacy and Verification* Prescriptions** (隱居《效驗方》) state: It also treats **spasms of the hands and feet** (手脚挛) preventing movement, **head wind afflictions** (頭惡風), and **sudden pain in the back and ribs** (背胁卒痛).

**Snake-Bite Ointment** (蛇衔膏) for **edematous sores** (廱肿), **golden wounds with stagnant blood** (金創瘀血), **postpartum blood accumulation** (産後血積), **ear and eye diseases** (耳目诸病), **cow-leader sores** (牛領), and **saddle sores** (馬鞍).
**Snake-bite herb** (蛇衔), **rhubarb** (大黃), **processed Aconite** (附子), **Angelica sinensis** (當歸), **Paeonia lactiflora** (芍藥), **Asarum** (細辛), **Scutellaria baicalensis** (黃芩), **pepper** (椒), **mugwort** (莽草), **Angelica pubescens** (独活) each **one liang** (一兩), **Allium chinense** (薤白) **fourteen stalks** (十四茎). Steep the **eleven substances** (十一物) in **bitter wine** (苦酒) overnight. Take **pork fat** (豬脂) **three jīn** (三斤), combine and simmer over **Seven-Star Fire** (七星火上), until each substance reaches **boiling point** (各沸). Strain and remove dregs. Take internally with **warm wine** (溫酒) like a **small pill** (如彈丸一枚), **twice daily** (日再). For **external diseases** (病在外), apply as a plaster. For **ear diseases**, wrap with cotton and insert.

**Eye diseases**, such as **millet-sized grains lodged in the inner canthus**, with a **saffron-yellow hue**—also called *jiǎng gāo* (缃膏). **Commoners** also use **Dragon’s Bite Vine** (*Lóng yīn téng*) **one liang**, decocted together, naming it **Dragon’s Bite Salve**.

**Divine Yellow Salve**—cures all **malignant sores**, **head sores**, and **various miscellaneous sores**.
**Coptis** (*Huáng lián*), **Magnolia bark** (*Huáng bò*), **Aconite** (*Fù zǐ*), **Realgar** (*Xióng huáng*), **Mercury** (*Shuǐ yín*), **Hellebore** (*Lí lú*), each **one liang**, and **Barite powder** (*Hú fěn*) **two liang**. Grind the **seven substances** finely, then mix with **December pork fat** (*là yuè zhū zhī*) **one jīn**. Seal tightly in a vessel and steam beneath **five dōu of rice**. Once done, add the mercury, grind again until well-mixed, and store securely. For any sores, first wash with **saltwater**, then apply. **No case fails to heal.**
*Hidden Dweller’s* [*Yàojù*] *Verified Prescriptions* say: **One application of this salve cures the ailment instantly—contemporaries call it divine.**

**Azure Dragon Five-Life Salve**—cures **all manner of sores across the land**.
**Cinnabar** (*Dān shā*), **Realgar** (*Xióng huáng*), **Ligusticum** (*Chuān xiōng*), **Pepper** (*Jiāo*), **Tripterygium** (*Fáng jǐ*), each **five fēn**; **Gentian** (*Lóng dǎn*), **Firmiana bark** (*Wú tóng pí*), **Cypress bark** (*Bǎi pí*), **Green bamboo shavings** (*Qīng zhú rú*), **Mulberry bark** (*Sāng bái pí*), **Beehives** (*Fēng fáng*), **Porcupine hide** (*Wèi pí*), each **four liang**; **Snake molting skin** (*Shé tuì pí*) **one set**—**thirteen substances**, sliced, steeped in **bitter wine** for half a month, then simmered briefly over **gentle fire**. Add **December pork fat** (*là yuè zhū zhī*) **three jīn**, decoct **three times up and down**, strain, and apply to sores. **Ingest as much as a date pit**, and it is **divinely efficacious.**
*Hidden Dweller’s* [*Yàojù*] *Verified Prescriptions* say: **It treats carbuncles, hemorrhoids, and malignant sores.** Though earlier **emergency prescriptions** are more critical, this too has **accumulated proven efficacy**, thus listed afterward.

**Bian Que’s Sunken-Ice Pill**—cures **internal distension**, **spirit possession**, **evil afflictions**, as well as **wasp stings, myriad poisons, stream toxins, and arrow wounds**.
**Realgar** (*Xióng huáng*), **true Cinnabar** (*Zhēn dān shā*) ground separately, **Alum** (*Fán shí*) roasted, each **one liang**; **raw Alum** (*Shēng fán shí*) **three liang and a half**, burned; **Rhubarb** (*Dà huáng*) **one liang and a half**; **Centipede** (*Wú gōng*) **one**, red-footed, lightly toasted; **Calico cat** (*Bān māo*) without wings; **Gentian** (*Lóng dǎn*); **Aconite** (*Fù zǐ*) prepared, each **seven**; **Hellebore** (*Lí lú*) **seven fēn**, toasted; **Apricot kernels** (*Xìng rén*) **forty**, deshelled and skinned, roasted. Pound, sift, and mix with **honey**, grinding **a thousand times**.
For **abdominal distension from evil qi**, **possession by malevolent spirits**, or **wandering corpse spirits**, take **two pills the size of small beans**. If **congealed masses** persist, take **four**. It **expels dysentery** and **multicolored parasitic worms**.
For **parasitic infestations**, **evil afflictions**, or **wandering corpse spirits**, take **two or three pills**, and **rub two pills over the painful area**. For **snake/wasp stings** or **stream toxins/arrow wounds**, dosage depends on **strength, size, and severity**—adjust accordingly.

**Salvia Miltiorrhiza Salve**—cures **seasonal colds**, **bandit winds**, and **malignant vapors**.
If **external**, it eases **numbness and pain in limbs**, **sore throat**, and **abdominal colds** manifesting as **heart palpitations, distension, and chest oppression**. **Internally**, take as a remedy; **externally**, apply as a liniment.
It also treats **prolapsed anus**, **wind-damp paralysis**, **hemiplegia**, **stiffness**, **lockjaw**, **deafness**, **toothaches**, **head winds**, **numbness**, **brain wind with throbbing pain**, **carbuncles, fistulas, scrofula, and hard swellings**—**before ulceration**, apply to **dissolve them**. For **malignant, headless growths** resembling **bone carbuncles**, rub until they **vanish**. It also addresses **wandering wind-water edema** throughout the body.
**Dosage**: **date-pit-sized**, for children reduce proportionally. **Five doses daily**; frequent use yields **universal efficacy**.
**Salvia Miltiorrhiza** (*Dān shēn*), **Gardenia** (*Zhì lì*), each **three liang**; **Mugwort leaves** (*Máng cǎo yè*), **Trollius flowers** (*Zhí zhú huā*), each **one liang**; **Cornus bark** (*Qín jiāo*), **Angelica** (*Dú huó*), **Aconite** (*Wū tóu*), **Sichuan pepper** (*Chuān jiāo*), **Forsythia** (*Lián qiào*), **Mulberry bark** (*Sāng bái pí*), **Achyranthes** (*Niú xī*), each **two liang**—**twelve substances**, decocted in **five shēng of bitter wine** and **seven shēng of sesame oil** until the wine evaporates. Strain and apply as before, or **simmer with pork fat**. For **wind-cold toxins**, take with **wine**; for **heat-toxin diseases**, take plain.
For **toothaches**, take alone, and **chew with cotton**—**preferably decocted in pork fat**.
For **children’s ear cysts** behind the ear, **hard as bone**, persisting months—**apply with cloth**, and they **dissolve in twenty days**, with **unmatched efficacy**.
This recipe comes from *The Minor Collection* [*Xiǎo Pǐn*].

**Divine Clear Salve**—cures **a hundred ailments**: **windstroke**, **malignant vapors**, **head and facial diseases**, **green blindness**, **wind-eroded canthi and nostrils**, **deafness**, **cold toothaches**, **carbuncles, hemorrhoids, sword wounds, scabies, and itch**, all under its domain.
**Angelica** (*Dāng guī*), **Asarum** (*Xì sīn*), each **three liang**; **Evodia** (*Wú zhū yú*), **Ligusticum** (*Chuān xiōng*), **Sichuan pepper** (*Shù jiāo*), **Atractylodes** (*Shú*), **Front-thorn root** (*Qián hú*), **Angelica dahurica** (*Bái zhī*), each **one liang**; **Aconite** (*Fù zǐ*) **thirty pieces**—**nine substances**, sliced, decocted in **ten jīn of pork fat** over **charcoal fire** until boiling, then **three times up and down**. When **Angelica dahurica turns yellow** and the salve forms, strain and store securely.
For **internal ailments**, take with **wine like a pill**, **three times daily**. For **external use**, apply as a liniment.
For **eye diseases** with **millet-like grains in the inner canthus**, **fan with upward gaze** to disperse. It also treats **sore eyes, teeth, and ear infections at the base**.
For **chronic wind disorders**, use this **finished salve**.
**Refined sesame oil** (*Qīng má yóu*) **thirteen liang** (or **rape oil**), **Yellow lead** (*Huáng dān*) **seven liang**—simmer in an **iron pot over gentle fire**, stirring continuously with **rough, damp willow twigs** until **blackened**. Increase to **fierce fire**, fan vigorously, and stir **without pause** until **all moisture evaporates** and the salve thickens. **Prepare in a clean place**, away from **chickens and dogs**.
For **tooth sores**, apply as a **plaster**; for **hemorrhoids**, take **internally**.
**Single-ingredient remedy**: **Brahma’s shipwood seeds** (*Pó luó mén*), called *Chuán sū shù zǐ* in Hu lands, **locally named "medicinal seeds"**—**grind finely**, ensuring no coarse particles, and **use the inner kernel**, discarding the husk.

**Remedies for Various Illnesses**

For sudden vomiting, diarrhea, cholera, abdominal colic below the navel, dysentery, abdominal distension, undigested food, snakebites entering the abdomen, or poisoned arrows penetrating the abdomen—**ingest two kernels**, using the inner seed, with **two *ge* of warm water**, finely ground and taken orally.

For **carbuncles, deep-seated abscesses, anthrax, and elephantiasis**—these four afflictions—**measure the size of the sore**, use the inner seed finely ground with warm water, and **mix with pig bile** to seal the wound.

For **boils, swellings, cold abscesses, ringworm, and general sores**—these five afflictions—**grind with vinegar** and seal the wound.

For **snakebites, scorpion stings, centipede bites, sand fleas, and arrow wounds**—these six afflictions—**grind with warm water** and **mix with red amaranth** to seal the wound.

For **postpartum difficulties, abdominal colic, retained lochia, and painful blood clots**—these six afflictions—**use one kernel**, grind with **one cup of wine**, and take warm.

For **leukorrhea and sudden diarrhea**—these two afflictions—**grind with chestnut juice** and take warm.

For **tooth decay caused by worms**—**shave finely** and **insert into the cavity**; it will heal immediately.

**Pulverize and sift**, applying to sores—**especially effective for muscle ailments**.

This method originates from **Zhi Family’s *Great Medical Text***.

---
**Salt Remedy**
For sudden fever, headache, dizziness, sudden abdominal pain, impending cholera, phlegm retention, undigested food, **qi distension with shortness of breath**, prolonged diarrhea with blood or mucus, **accumulations causing vomiting**, weakness, fatigue, **sallow complexion, malaria, or wind disorders**—**administration method**:

Take **high-quality salt**, first **hold a soybean-sized amount in the mouth without swallowing**. Soon, saliva will fill the mouth near the teeth. Then, **use a square-inch spoon** to place salt into the mouth and swallow with saliva at the same time—**otherwise, it may dissolve entirely**.

For **chronic throat ailments** or **long-term use**, take **two to three months**, **first thing in the morning**.

If vomiting occurs or sudden illness strikes, take **three square-inch spoons**; if vomiting persists, **stop until the illness subsides**, then resume. For **newly afflicted malaria**, it will resolve; for **abdominal pain, distension, or vomiting/diarrhea**, it is also effective.

For **chronic illness**, if **internal heat** persists, take it **every three to five days**. Increased dosage **induces vomiting or diarrhea**, but diarrhea is harmless. **Long-term use greatly fortifies the spleen and kidney *qi***—no ailment remains untreated, **only regretting that people do not persist**.

This remedy varies; the *Small Treatise* states:
For **sudden abdominal pain from malevolent *qi*, undigested food, cholera, or abdominal distension from poisoning**, **brew as a decoction** and take **one to two *sheng***—**induce vomiting or defecation**; it is effective.

**Ge’s Ever-Ready Medicine**
**Rhubarb, cinnamon bark, licorice, dried ginger, coptis, pepper, atractylodes, evodia, mugwort, realgar, rhinoceros horn, musk, acorus, ginseng, peony, aconite, croton, pinellia, ephedra, bupleurum, apricot kernel, kudzu root, scutellaria, aconite root, asarum, and donkey-hide gelatin**—these should each be used in **small amounts**.

Previously, these medicines were **primarily used in Lingnan**, but now they are **listed again for clarity**. All should be **prepared as compound formulas**, **mixed and stored** for ready use—**prioritizing daily sustenance**.

**Decoction Ingredients**
**Toxicoscordion (Chángshān) 14 liang**, **lacquer (Shǔqī)**, **gypsum 1 catty**, **donkey-hide gelatin 7 liang**, **oyster shell, cinnabar, indigo 7 liang each**, **softshell turtle 3**, **carp scales 1 catty**, **cuttlefish bone**, **calamus fruit 1 *dou***, **Chinese angelica 14 liang**, **areca nut 50**, **dragon bone, red stone pitch, antelope horn 3 each**, **tangerine peel, corydalis**—those without specified weights, **4 liang each**. **Use 1 *sheng* of mirabilite**; it is effective.

**Compound Formulas**
**Golden Tooth Powder, Jade Bottle Yellow Pill, Three-Medicine Emergency Remedy, Purple Snow, Tangshen Decoction, Yuán Huáng Pill, Malaria-Dispelling Powder, Powdered Medicine, Middle-Reconciling Powder, Dysentery Medicine, Ding-Swelling Medicine**—if **side-annotated**, use as needed.

**Lao Jun’s Divine Clearance Powder**
**Atractylodes and prepared aconite 2 liang each**, **prepared aconite root, platycodon 2 liang**, **asarum 1 liang**—**pound and sift**. Take **five square-inch spoons daily**. If a household has this, **no illness will spread within a mile**. For travelers, **all encountered pathogenic *qi* will be dispelled**.

If others fall ill, **take with warm wine, one square-inch spoon**. If the illness lasts **four to five days**, **use three spoons of powder with three *sheng* of water**, boil to **three simmers**, and take **one *sheng***—**induce sweating to recover**.

It is said to be **constantly used as a preventive powder**.

**Pearl and Musk Powder**
**Pearl and cassia bark 1 *fēn* each**, **fritillary bulb 3 *fēn***, **parched apricot kernel 2 *fēn***, **egg white parched until yellow-black 3 *fēn***—**pound and sift**. Take **one square-inch spoon on New Year’s Day**. If **frequently ill**, take **on the first and fifteenth of each month**.

**Single-Ingredient Remedy**
**Take the eastern-facing branch of the southern community’s cypress**, **dry in the sun**, **pulverize**, and take **one square-inch spoon**.

**Yáo’s Account**: **Prepare in advance during epidemics**, named **Cypress Branch Powder**; it is **divinely effective**.

*The Abbreviated Excessive Treatise* states:
**On the morning of the first day**, **see the cypress in the southern community**, **immediately collect it**.

**Method to Prevent Contagion During Epidemics**
**Parboil soybeans**, **soak in new rice wine**, and **consume regularly**.

*The Small Treatise*’s **Morning Layer’s *Túsu* Wine Method** prevents **warm disease epidemics**.

**Five-Part Decoction**
**Rhubarb 5 *fēn***, **Sichuan pepper 5 *fēn***, **atractylodes and cinnamon bark 3 *fēn* each**, **platycodon 4 *fēn***, **aconite root 1 *fēn***, **arrowroot 2 *fēn***—**finely chop**, **store in silk pouches**. On the **last day of the twelfth month at noon**, **suspend in a well until muddy**, **retrieve at dawn before the New Year celebration**, and **place the medicine in wine**—**drink as *Túsu* wine**.

「When facing east, **place the medicine in a well**, it can **ward off the coming year’s ills** and **ensure this disease never recurs in a lifetime**. This is **Hua Tuo’s** method, as **Emperor Wu**’s *Verified Prescriptions* attest—**from minor to severe**, adjust the dosage accordingly. **Even the weakest may take it**, and **one person’s consumption can protect an entire household**. **Take the medicine for three mornings**.

**Another method**: **Preventing Warm Disease with Powdered Medicine** (by **Maopu**).
**Chuanxiong, Angelica root (Bai zhi), and Peucedanum**—**three equal parts**, sifted and mixed into powder—**apply this powder to the body**, and it will work wonders.

**Appendix: Zhang Zhongjing’s Three-Medicine Emergency Prescription**
**Powdered form** (by **Si Kong Pei Xiu**): **For treating acute abdominal and thoracic disorders**, including **sudden fatal diseases**, **pounding and sieving** **rhubarb, dried ginger, and croton seeds** (each **1 liang**), mixing with **honey**, and further pounding **a thousand times** into **pea-sized pills**. **Take three pills**, adjusting for age—**the pill form is more potent than the powder**. If **poisonous pathogens invade** and cause **abdominal distension, sudden piercing pain like a dagger, breathlessness, and locked jaws**, or if **the patient collapses and dies suddenly**, **administer warm water or wine** to induce vomiting. If **the medicine does not descend**, **lift the patient’s head** and **force-feed it down the throat**—**immediate relief will follow**. If **the condition persists**, **give another three pills**; **abdominal rumbling and expulsion of toxins** will occur, and the patient will recover. If **the jaws remain locked**, **pry them open** and **administer the medicine by force**—**once it reaches the throat, recovery is certain**.

The **Cui Family’s *Sea of Prescriptions*** states:
**Corydalis turtschaninovii (Wei ling xian)** **disperses all pathogenic winds**, **unblocks the twelve meridians**. **Taken in the morning, it takes effect by evening**. It **disperses stagnant cold abscesses and lingering pathogenic fluids**, **harmonizes without draining**—**those who take it will feel lightness in their limbs, warmth in their hands and feet, and relief from colds**. It also **treats frostbite**.

In **Shangzhou**, a man suffered **heavy feet that could not bear weight** for **ten years without improvement**. Then, a **Silla monk** arrived and said:
*"This ailment has a remedy."* The man **went into the mountains to seek it**, and after **administering the medicine for several days**, his condition **settled**. The monk **left behind the name of the medicine** before departing.

This medicine **treats**:
- **Stroke-related aphasia** in men and women,
- **Paralysis of limbs**,
- **Ocular deviation** (eyes squinting),
- **Wind in tendons and bones**,
- **Fetal wind** (congenital disorders),
- **Head wind** (migraine),
- **Obscure wind** (unseen wind disorders),
- **Heart wind** (cardiac-related wind),
- **Wind-induced madness**,
- **Headaches from injury**,
- **Nasal congestion and discharge**—**after two doses, injury-related fevers cease**,
- **Dizziness and vertigo**,
- **Vitiligo**,
- **Severe wind disorders**,
- **Skin itching from wind**,
- **Toxic heat and poisonous heat**,
- **Wind rashes**.

It **deeply treats**:
- **Chronic fatigue disorders**,
- **Lumbar and vertebral wind**,
- **Wrist-wrapping wind** (carpal tunnel-like symptoms),
- **Stiffness in speech**,
- **Phlegm accumulation**.

It **disperses and unblocks the five organs**, treating:
- **Internal stagnation**,
- **Phlegm in the chest**,
- **Lingering bladder abscesses**,
- **Excessive saliva in the mouth**,
- **Craving for tea residue**,
- **Stiffness and numbness in limbs**,
- **Cold and heat stagnation**,
- **Pain in the waist and knees**,
- **Inability to stand for long periods**,
- **Lingering pathogenic vapors and miasmas**,
- **Severe aversion to cold with high fever**,
- **Earaches progressing to abscesses and deafness**,
- **Eye inflammation from pathogenic winds**,
- **Constipation in the large and small intestines**—**immediate relief upon ingestion, and appetite returns**.

It **treats**:
- **Jaundice**,
- **Melasma** (dark spots),
- **Loss of facial color**,
- **Scrofula (luo li) spreading across the neck**,
- **Postpartum constipation and lumbar pain**,
- **Previous trauma or falls**.

It **treats**:
- **Heart pain**,
- **Qi stagnation**,
- **Diaphragmatic wind**,
- **Cold pathogenic winds attacking**.

It **treats kidney wind stagnation**, causing:
- **Abdominal distension**,
- **Facial and head edema**,
- **Toxic heat in the spleen and lungs**,
- **Phlegm-heat coughing**,
- **Breathlessness**,
- **Restlessness and inability to sit still**,
- **Scaly and pruritic rashes**,
- **Women with delayed menstruation**,
- **Prolonged meridian activation with blood and qi surging to the heart**,
- **Night sweats**,
- **Stealing sweats** (spontaneous sweating),
- **Severe body odor**,
- **Unbearable breath**.

**Diligent consumption of Corydalis turtschaninovii**, combined with **frequent hot water baths throughout the day**, **applying the medicine like saliva in the morning**, or **using it to treat body odor**, **applying it internally and externally**, will **bring about recovery**. For **children without fault**, **have their mother hold the medicine in her mouth and feed it to them**.

It **treats hemorrhoids, constipation, and dysenteric tenesmus**.

**Preparation of Corydalis turtschaninovii**:
**Wash and dry-fry** the herb into a powder. **Mix with good wine** to make it slightly moist, **place in a bamboo tube**, and **seal tightly**. **Steam nine times** and **sun-dry into pills**. **Add wine and re-dry**, then **combine with white honey** to form pills the size of **celtis seeds**. **Take twenty to thirty pills per dose**, with **decoction or wine**.

*The Thousand Gold Prescriptions* states:
**Gather on the fifth day of the fifth month at noon**, **cutting the leaves of the plant growing near the ground**. **Wash, dry, pound, and sift**. **Take one *fēn* (cubic inch) with wine or gruel**, **three times a day and three times at night**. If **the patient vomits or has diarrhea**, **mix with honey into pills**, **calculating the dosage based on the sifted powder**. For **mild wind disorders**, **take twice daily**. If **wind appears on the body**—**as small grains or millet-sized bumps**—**this is wind-toxin erupting**. **Puncture with a needle to drain**, until **yellow fluid emerges and stops**.

**Collect on the fifth day of the fifth month**, **dry in the shade**, and **store in a large container**. **Use sparingly as needed**. This herb **wards off evil**. If **one wishes to prevent illness and disease**, **take it regularly**, and **no fear of harm will remain**. If **the seasonal *qi* is imbalanced**, **the whole household may take it**. If **the stomach is bloated with heat and discomfort**, **take it immediately**.

It **kills the three parasitic worms**, **treats intestinal hemorrhoids**, and **stimulates appetite**. **Ideal to take for a full year**.

**Can be gathered on the seventh day of the seventh month and the ninth day of the ninth month**.

**Prescription for Livestock (73rd)**:
**For treating horses with fever, blackened forehead, nasal discharge with pus, and inability to eat water or grass**:
**Cucumber root, Fritillaria, Platycodon, Scutellaria, Gardenia fruit, Indigo naturalis, Swallowwort flower, Rhubarb, White Aster skin, Scutellaria, and Turmeric**—**each 2 *dang liang*** (heavy ounces). **Coptis and Niter**—**each 4 *dang liang***. **Pound and sift**. For **mild cases**, mix with **ash and feed**. For **severe cases**, use **3 *dang liang* of medicine**, **½ *jin* of Rehmannia root**, **2 *ge* of fermented soybean**, **4 *ge* of rape seed oil**, and **administer before fasting**, feeding again at dusk—**highly effective**.

**Prescription for Livestock (73rd, continued)**:

**For horses traveling long distances when reaching a resting place**:
After a long time without food or grass, **brush them thoroughly**, then **feed them**, followed by **watering them**—this must be done before **stabling them**. If **stabled while exhausted**, they will fall ill from **water and grain**.

**For livestock with scabbed sores**:
Apply **wheat dough** to seal the sores; they will **fall off immediately**.

**For horses with sudden jaundice and blackened sweat**:
**Cut off the upper section** as described above. Take **aged, dried sheep hooves**, soak in water, and **extract the juice to irrigate the nostrils**. If this does not resolve the issue, use **Rhubarb and Angelica**—each **2 *dang liang***, and **salt**—½ *sheng*. Boil in **3 *sheng* of water**, reduce to **1.5 *sheng***, and **irrigate the nostrils in two divided doses**. If still unresolved, **pierce the tail tip**, let **blood flow until it stops**—**immediate effect**.

**For horses unable to lie down, with twisted tendons or intestinal blockage**:
Use this same prescription. **Asarum, Saposhnikovia, and Paeony**—each **2 *dang liang***. Boil with **1 *sheng* of salt** and **5 *sheng* of water**, reduce to **2.5 *sheng***, and **irrigate nostrils in two divided doses** (after and before treatment). For another method, use **Mirabilite, Turmeric, Cold Water Stone, and Indigo naturalis**—each **2 *dang liang***. Boil in **5 *sheng* of water**, reduce to **2.5 *sheng***, mix with **½ *sheng* of wine and ½ *sheng* of rape seed oil**, and **irrigate nostrils in two divided doses**.

**For horses with swollen cannon bones**:
Burn **forty-nine sheep hooves**, apply as a **foment** to the swollen area, replacing when **cool**. If sheep hooves are unavailable, use **willow or mulberry branches** of similar thickness, **parch and foment**—**no limit on quantity**.

**For watering horses**:
Do so at **3–9 AM (寅) and 9 AM–3 PM (午)**; in the evening, **reduce water intake**.

**Method for feeding salt**:
Salt must be **dry**, and weather **clear**. For **seven days**, feed **large horses 1 *sheng*** and **small horses ½ *sheng***. Use a **long-handled ladle** to **force-feed deep into the throat**, ensuring **strong digestion and improved water and grain intake**.

**For horses with posterior cold**:
**Fermented soybean, Allium, and Ginger**—each **2 *dang liang***. Boil in **5 *sheng* of water**, reduce to **1.5 *sheng***, mix with wine, and **irrigate nostrils**—**immediate recovery**.

**For horses with nasal botfly infestation (十年虫颡)**:
Use **aged, bitter soybean paste**—½ *ge* in two divided doses, **irrigating nostrils daily**. Do not overuse; excess may **harm the horse**.

**For severe nasal botfly infestation (虫颡重者)**:
**Gua Lou Ren (Trichosanthes Fruit)**—1 *ge*, **parch until purple**, pound into a paste. **Mulberry Root Bark**—1 handful, **large jujubes**—20, **split**. Boil **1 *ge* of medicine** in **2 *sheng* of water**, reduce to **1 *sheng***, strain, add **pounded Gua Lou Ren**, mix evenly, and **irrigate nostrils at a tolerable cool temperature**. Repeat after **one day**; severe cases require **no more than two treatments**—**recovery follows**.

**For horses with nasal botfly infestation where pus oozes from nostrils and swelling appears on the jaw (虫颡马，鼻沬出，梁肿起者)**:
**Untreatable**.

**For donkeys or horses with twisted tendons nearing death (驴马胞转欲死)**:
Pound **garlic**, insert deep **into the urethra**—5 *cun*—**immediate recovery**.
Alternatively, use **child’s feces**, mix with water, and **irrigate nostrils**—**immediate recovery**.
Another method: **Have the rider mount the horse and gallop uphill**, then **rub the belly downwards** to **displace feces** by hand. **First trim nails**, **coat hands with oil** to **prevent intestinal injury**—**highly effective**.

**For spinal sores (脊疮)**:
Apply **realgar (Orpiment)**, **avoid wind**—**immediate recovery**.

**For scabies (疥)**:
Parch **aged soybeans** until **charred**, mix with **raw sesame oil**, pound, and **apply as a poultice**. Wash with **soapberry solution or rice wash water** before application. Leave a **slight gap in the center** to **allow pests to escape**; excessive application may **worsen sores**.

**For secret treatment of scabies (秘疗疥)**:
Use **croton seeds and stearin powder**, grind into **sesame oil**, apply to **affected areas**, then **wash**. Reapply after **several days**; observe further **changes for efficacy**.

**For horses with dizziness (目晕)**:
Use **fine powder of ramie leaves** from **after the frost**, blow **twice daily into the eyes**—**immediate recovery**.

**For horses with hoof maggots (马蛆蹄)**:
Dig a **1 *chi* hole beneath the stable**, bury a **round stone the size of a chicken egg**, ensuring the horse **stands over it**. After **one or two days**, the infestation will **permanently cease**.

**For feeding hemp seeds (啖大麻子)**:
Select **1 *sheng* of clean seeds**, mix into feed. **Treats nasal botfly and scorched hair**—**highly effective**.

**For scabies (疥)**:
Use **powdered Sophora root**, mix with **sesame oil**, and **apply**. First **wash thoroughly with soapberry or rice wash water**, then **apply the mixture**, leaving a **slight gap in the center** to **allow pests to escape**; excessive application may **widen the sores**.

**End of *Jiuzhi Yizong* (九畜医宗) Prescriptions—Volume 8 of *Jingui Yaolan* (急仙方, *Emergency Prescriptions for the Daoist Immortal*).**
